when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是程式設計師 , 她確實做了一些 , 但真正的情況是說 , 未來將會是 , 遠遠超過這個 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	一百年後 , 這傢伙出現了 , alanturing , 1936年 , 又發明了一台電腦 。
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然 , babbage的機器是完全機械化的
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	圖靈的機器完全是理論性的 。
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	這兩位都是從數學的角度來的 , 但turing告訴我們一件非常重要的事 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他為電腦科學奠定了數學基礎 , 說: 「 製造電腦並不重要 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	不管你電腦的機械 , 像babbage的原理或是電子 , 像是今天的電腦 , 或是未來的電腦 , 或是細胞 , 或再一次的機械化 , 一旦我們進入奈米技術 ,
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到babbage的機器讓它變小 , 所有這些東西都是電腦
there is in a sense a computing essence .	一種計算的本質 。
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這叫做 「 教堂 」 論 。
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	突然間 , 你看到了這個連結 , 你說babbage建造的東西真的是一台電腦
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	事實上 , 它能夠做到我們今天用電腦所做的一切 , 只有非常緩慢 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	為了讓你們知道有多慢 , 大概有1k的記憶體 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	它用打孔卡 , 裡面被餵食 , 它跑的速度大約是第一台zx81的一萬倍 。
it did have a ram pack .	它的確有一個ram包 。
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	如果你想的話 , 你可以在額外的記憶加入很多 。
so , where does that bring us today ?	所以 , 今天這帶給我們的是什麼 ?
so there are plans .	所以 , 有計畫 。
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在swindon , 科學博物館的檔案庫中 , 有數百個計畫和數千頁的筆記 , 是由charlesbabbage所寫的 , 關於這個分析引擎 。
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中一組是我們稱之為 「 計劃28 」 的計畫 , 這也是我和doronswaade合作的一個慈善團體的名字 , 他是科學博物館計算機的策展人 , 也是駕駛這個計劃來建立不同引擎的人 , 我們的計劃是建造它 。
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在肯辛頓南部 , 我們將建造分析引擎 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	這個計畫有幾個部分
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	第一是掃描babbage的檔案庫
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	那是已經完成的 。 第二個是所有計劃的研究 , 來決定要建造什麼 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三部分是電腦模擬那台機器的最後一部分 , 就是在科學博物館中實體建造它 。
when it's built , you'll finally be able to understand how a computer works , because rather than having a tiny chip in front of you , you've got to look at this humongous thing and say , " ah , i see the memory operating , i see the cpu operating , i hear it operating . i probably smell it operating . "	當它被建造出來時 , 你終於能夠了解電腦是如何運作的 , 因為與其在你面前裝上一小塊晶片 , 你必須看著這個和諧的東西 , 說: 「 啊 , 我看到記憶體在運作 , 我看到cpu在運作 , 我聽到它在運作 。 我可能聞到它在運作 。 」
but in between that we're going to do a simulation .	但在那之間我們要做一個模擬 。
babbage himself wrote , he said , as soon as the analytical engine exists , it will surely guide the future course of science .	巴貝奇自己寫道 , 他說 , 一旦分析引擎存在 , 它一定會引導未來科學的發展 。
of course , he never built it , because he was always fiddling with new plans , but when it did get built , of course , in the 1940s , everything changed .	當然 , 他從來沒有打造過它 , 因為他一直在搞新計畫 , 但當它真的被打造出來時 , 當然 , 在1940年代 , 一切都改變了 。
now , i'll just give you a little taste of what it looks like in motion with a video which shows just one part of the cpu mechanism working .	現在 , 我來稍微說明一下它的樣子 , 用影片來呈現cpu機制的其中一部分 。
so this is just three sets of cogs , and it's going to add . this is the adding mechanism in action , so you imagine this gigantic machine .	所以這只是三組齒輪 , 它會加上 。 這是加法的機制 , 所以你想像這台巨大的機器 。
so , give me five years .	所以 , 給我五年的時間 。
before the 2030s happen , we'll have it .	在2030年代發生之前 , 我們將擁有
thank you very much .	非常謝謝 。
in this imagefilled talk , yann arthusbertrand displays his three most recent projects on humanity and our habitat stunning aerial photographs in his series " the earth from above , " personal interviews from around the globe featured in his web project " 6 billion others , " and his soontobereleased movie , " home , " which documents human impact on the environment through breathtaking video .	在這個圖像填充的演講中 , 雅南•亞瑟伯特特最近展出了他近期對人類的三個項目 , 以及我們的棲息地拍攝了他的系列 「 地球 」 的照片 , 來自世界各地的個人訪問 , 標記了他的網站 「 其他六十億人 」 , 以及他即將拍攝的電影《家》 , 這部影片記錄了人類對環境的影響 , 透過呼吸的影片 。
art , climate change , environment , film , future , humanity , media , photography	藝術、氣候變遷、環境、電影、未來、人類、媒體、攝影、攝影 。
yann arthusbertrand captures fragile earth in wideangle	yannarhusbertrand捕捉到很脆弱的地球 , 以寬的角度捕捉 。
i have a big impact on the planet to travel here by plane .	我對地球有很大的影響力 , 可以靠飛機來到這裡 。
i emitted , in the atmosphere , nine tons of co2 ; that is the weight of two elephants .	我在大氣中排放了九噸的二氧化碳 ; 那是兩隻大象的重量 。
i came here to speak about ecology , and i emitted as much co2 as a frenchman in one year .	我來這裡談到生態學 , 一年內我排放的二氧化碳和法國人一樣多 。
so what do i have to do ?	那我該怎麼辦呢 ?
i have to kill a frenchman when i come back at home ?	當我回到家時 , 我必須殺一位法國人 ?
i have to do my carbon offset in another way , like i do every time .	我必須用另一種方式減碳 , 像我每次一樣 。
in fact my work is to show our impact on our planet .	事實上我的工作是展現我們對地球的影響 。
i'm going to show you some examples of the last pictures i've done in the last year .	我要給你們看一些我過去一年所拍攝的照片的例子 。
alberta sand oil , a lot of pollution .	亞伯達省的沙石油 , 很多污染
you know the problem ; we don't want to believe what we know .	你知道問題 , 我們不想相信我們所知道的事 。
in alberta people work nonstop , 24 hours by seven to extract as much oil as they can .	在亞伯達省 , 人們不停工作 , 24小時到7小時 , 盡可能提煉石油 。
we know about the end of oil .	我們知道石油的終點
oil sand is not a longterm solution .	石油沙不是個長期的解決方案
but we use three times more oil than we find every year .	但我們每年使用比我們發現的石油多了三倍 。
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信我們所知道的
coral reef in new caledonia .	新克里多尼亞的珊瑚礁
100 percent of the coral may be wiped out before 2050 because of global warming .	百分之百的珊瑚可能在2050年因為全球暖化而消失 。
and you know how coral are very sensitive to temperature , and are very important for the biodiversity of the sea .	你知道珊瑚對溫度非常敏感 , 對海洋的生物多樣性也非常重要 。
north pole . i've done this picture last summer .	北極 。 我去年夏天拍的這張照片
it was impossible to do this picture 15 years ago .	15年前這張照片是不可能的 。
now there is a new way open between atlantic and pacific .	現在大西洋和太平洋之間有了新的開放方式 。
the thickness of the arctic decreased more than 40 percent since 1960 .	從1960年起 , 北極的厚度減少了超過40% 。
there is a new face of kilimanjaro without ice .	在沒有冰的情況下 , 吉利馬扎羅是有新面孔的 。
it lost 80 percent of its ice .	它失去了80%的冰 。
according to scientists , in 100 years all the mountain glacier will be gone .	根據科學家的說法 , 在100年內 , 所有山上的冰川都會消失 。
glaciers are very important for the life on earth .	冰河對地球上的生命非常重要 。
like al gore told you , two billion people live on the water from the glacier of himalaya .	就像艾爾•高爾說的 , 有二十億人住在來自喜馬拉雅冰河的水上 。

here in america , 90 percent of the corn cultivated is used to feed animals or to do oil .	在美國這裡 , 百分之九十的玉米是用來餵養動物或做石油的 。

video: this earth is four and a half billion years old .	影片:地球已經有四十五億年了 。
these plants , several hundred million years old .	這些植物 , 有好幾億年的歷史
and we humans have been walking upright for only 200 thousand years .	而我們人類僅有20萬年直立行走 。
we've managed to adapt , and have conquered the whole planet .	我們已經成功地適應 , 並且已經征服了整個地球 。
for generations , we've been raising our children , not unlike millions of other species living beside us .	數世代以來 , 我們一直在養育我們的孩子 , 不像其他數百萬個物種住在我們身邊 。
for the past 30 years i've been closely watching the earth and its dwellers from high up in the sky .	在過去的30年裡 , 我一直很仔細地觀察地球和它的居住者 , 來自天上高處 。
our life is tied to the wellbeing of our planet .	我們的生活和我們星球的福祉綁在一起 。
we depend on water , forests , deserts , oceans .	我們依賴水、森林、沙漠、海洋
fishing , breeding , farming are still the world's foremost human occupations .	捕魚、繁殖、養殖 , 至今仍然是世界上最重要的人類職業 。
and what binds us together is far greater than what divides us .	而把我們結合在一起的 , 遠遠大於我們分裂的東西 。
we all share the same need for the earth's gifts the same wish to rise above ourselves , and become better .	我們都有同樣的需求 , 對於地球的禮物 , 和我們自己上升的願望相同 , 變得更好 。
and yet we carry on raising walls to keep us apart .	然而 , 我們卻繼續築起圍牆來讓我們分崩離析 。
today our greatest battle is to protect the natural offerings of our planet .	現今 , 我們最大的戰役就是要保護地球的自然提供 。
in less than 50 years we've altered it more thoroughly than in the entire history of mankind .	不到50年 , 我們更徹底地改變了它 , 整個人類歷史 。
half of the world's forests have vanished .	世界上有一半的森林已經消失
water resources are running low .	水資源正在經營得很低 。
intensive farming is depleting soils .	密集耕作正在耗盡土壤 。
our energy sources are not sustainable .	我們的能源來源並不永續 。
the climate is changing .	氣候正在改變 。
we are endangering ourselves .	我們自己正在瀕臨絕種 。
we're only trying to improve our lives .	我們只想改善生活
but the wealth gaps are growing wider .	但財富差距越來越廣 。
we haven't yet understood that we're going at a much faster pace than the planet can sustain .	我們尚未明白 , 我們的速度比地球能維持的速度要快得多 。
we know that solutions are available today .	我們知道解決方案是現今可行的 。
we all have the power to change this trend for the better .	我們都有能力可以更好地改變這個趨勢 。
so what are we waiting for ?	那我們還在等什麼呢 ?

in this accessible talk from tedxboston , richard resnick shows how cheap and fast genome sequencing is about to turn health care upside down .	在tedxboston的演講中 , 理查德•瑞斯尼克指出 , 基因定序是如何將健康照護顛倒 。
dna , biotech , health care , science , technology	dna , 生物科技 , 健康照護 , 科學 , 科技 。
richard resnick: welcome to the genomic revolution	理查德•雷斯尼克:歡迎來到基因革命 。
ladies and gentlemen , i present to you the human genome .	各位先生女士 , 我給你們看人類基因組 。
chromosome one , top left .	染色體一 , 左上角
bottom right are the sex chromosomes .	右下方是性染色體 。
women have two copies of that big x chromosome ; men have the x and , of course , that small copy of the y .	女人有兩個大x染色體 , 男人有xx染色體 , 當然 , 還有那個小小的y 。
sorry boys , but it's just a tiny little thing that makes you different .	對不起男孩 , 但這只是個小東西 , 讓你有所不同 。
so if you zoom in on this genome , then what you see , of course , is this double helix structure the code of life spelled out with these four biochemical letters , or we call them bases , right: a , c , g and t .	所以 , 如果你放大這個基因組 , 你所看到的 , 當然 , 就是這個雙螺旋結構--生命的編碼與這四個生化字母拼出來 , 或者我們稱它們為基對 , 對了:a , c , g , t 。
how many are there in the human genome ? three billion .	人類基因組中有多少 ? 30億 。
is that a big number ?	這是一個很大的數字嗎 ?
well , everybody can throw around big numbers .	嗯 , 每個人都可以丟出大量的數字 。
but in fact , if i were to place one base on each pixel of this 1280 by 800 resolution screen , we would need 3 , 000 screens to take a look at the genome .	但事實上 , 如果我把每個鹼基放在這個1280到800個解析度螢幕上 , 我們就需要3000個螢幕來檢視基因組 。
so it's really quite big .	所以這真的很大 。
and perhaps because of its size , a group of people all , by the way , with y chromosomes decided they would want to sequence it .	也許因為它的大小 , 一群人 , 順帶一提 , y染色體決定他們會想要定序 。
and so 15 years , actually , and about four billion dollars later , the genome was sequenced and published .	所以 , 事實上 , 15年後 , 大約40億美金後 , 基因組被定序並發表 。
in 2003 , the final version was published , and they keep working on it .	2003年 , 最後的版本被出版了 , 他們繼續努力在其中 。
that was all done on a machine that looks like this .	這一切都是在一個看起來像這樣的機器上完成的 。
it costs about a dollar for each base a very slow way of doing it .	每一塊錢大約需要一塊美金 , 很慢的做法 。
well folks , i'm here to tell you that the world has completely changed and none of you know about it .	各位 , 我來這裡是要告訴各位 , 世界已經完全改變 , 你們都不知道 。
so now what we do is we take a genome , we make maybe 50 copies of it , we cut all those copies up into little 50base reads , and then we sequence them , massively parallel .	我們現在做的是 , 我們拿一個基因組 , 大概50份複本 , 我們把所有複製品剪成50個鹼基 , 然後我們將它們排序 , 大量平行 。
and then we bring that into software , and we reassemble it and we tell you what the story is .	然後我們將它帶入軟體中 , 重新組合起來 , 告訴你故事是什麼 。
and so just to give you a picture of what this looks like , the human genome project: 3 gigabases , right .	給大家看一下這是什麼樣子的 , 人類基因組計劃:3gbs , 對 。
one run on one of these machines: 200 gigabases in a week .	其中一台機器跑了一台 , 一週內就有200gb 。
and that 200 is going to change to 600 this summer , and there's no sign of this pace slowing .	而那200個今年夏天將會改變到600個步調 , 沒有這個步調會慢下來 。
so the price of a base , to sequence a base , has fallen 100 million times .	所以一個鹼基的價格 , 要定序一個鹼基 , 已經下降了一億倍 。
that's the equivalent of you filling up your car with gas in 1998 , waiting until 2011 , and now you can drive to jupiter and back twice .	這相當於你在1998年用氣體把你的車子塞滿 , 等到2011年 , 現在你可以開到木星 , 再回來兩次 。
world population , pc placements , the archive of all the medical literature , moore's law , the old way of sequencing , and here's all the new stuff .	世界人口、pc地點、所有醫學文獻的檔案庫、摩爾定律、定序的舊方法 , 這裡有全新的東西 。
guys , this is a log scale ; you don't typically see lines that go up like that .	各位 , 這是個木質尺度 ; 你通常不會看到像那樣上升的線條 。
so the worldwide capacity to sequence human genomes is something like 50 , 000 to 100 , 000 human genomes this year .	所以 , 全球對人類基因組的定序能力 , 今年大約有5萬到10萬個人類基因組 。
and we know this based on the machines that are being placed .	而我們知道這點基於被放置的機器
this is expected to double , triple or maybe quadruple year over year for the foreseeable future .	預計會在可預期的未來中增加一倍、三倍或四倍 。
in fact , there's one lab in particular that represents 20 percent of all that capacity .	事實上 , 有一個特別的實驗室代表了所有能力的20% 。
it's called the beijing genomics institute .	叫做北京基因組學研究所
the chinese are absolutely winning this race to the new moon , by the way .	中國人絕對贏得這場比賽 , 順便提一下 , 新月球 。
what does this mean for medicine ?	這對醫學意味著什麼 ?
so a woman is age 37 .	所以一個女人年紀是37歲
she presents with stage 2 estrogen receptorpositive breast cancer .	她呈現的是 「 階段2 」 雌激素受性乳癌 。
she is treated with surgery , chemotherapy and radiation .	她接受手術、化療和放射線治療 。
two years later , she comes back with stage three c ovarian cancer .	兩年後 , 她帶著第三期卵巢癌回來 。
unfortunately , treated again with surgery and chemotherapy .	不幸的是 , 再次用手術和化療來治療
she comes back three years later at age 42 with more ovarian cancer , more chemotherapy .	三年後 , 她在42歲時得了更多卵巢癌 , 更多化療 。
six months later , she comes back with acute myeloid leukemia .	六個月後 , 她帶著急性髓性白血病回來 。
she goes into respiratory failure and dies eight days later .	她進入呼吸衰竭 , 八天後她就死了 。
so first , the way in which this woman was treated , in as little as 10 years , will look like bloodletting .	首先 , 這名女子接受治療的方式 , 會是10年後 , 看起來像血腥一樣 。
and it's because of people like my colleague , rick wilson , at the genome institute at washington university , who decided to take a look at this woman postmortem .	正是因為像我的同事rickwilson在華盛頓大學的基因學研究所決定看一看這位女子後研究所
and he sequenced , he took skin cells , healthy skin , and cancerous bone marrow , and he sequenced the whole genomes of both of them in a couple of weeks , no big deal .	他做了測序 , 取出皮膚細胞 , 健康的皮膚 , 以及癌症的骨髓 , 在幾週內 , 他將兩者的整個基因組排序 , 都沒有大不了 。
and then he compared those two genomes in software , and what he found , among other things , was a deletion , a 2 , 000base deletion across three billion bases in a particular gene called tp53 .	然後他在軟體中比較了這兩組基因 , 他在其它事情上發現 , 其中有兩千個鹼基耗損 , 在一個叫做tp53的基因中 , 有三十億個鹼基 。
if you have this deleterious mutation in this gene , you're 90 percent likely to get cancer in your life .	如果你在這個基因中有這種極端的突變 , 你一生中有90%的機率會罹患癌症 。
so unfortunately , this doesn't help this woman , but it does have severe , profound if you will , implications to her family .	所以 , 不幸的是 , 這對這位女士沒有幫助 , 但它的確有嚴重、深刻的影響 , 如果你願意 , 影響她的家庭 。
i mean , if they have the same mutation , and they get this genetic test , and they understand it , then they can go and get regular screens , and they can catch cancer early and potentially live a significantly longer life .	我的意思是 , 如果他們有相同的突變 , 他們得到了這個基因檢測 , 然後他們了解它 , 那麼他們可以去取得一般的螢幕 , 並且可以提早抓到癌症 , 並且可能過著明顯更長壽的生活 。
let me introduce you now to the beery twins , diagnosed with cerebral palsy at the age of two .	現在讓我向各位介紹啤酒雙胞胎 , 在兩歲時被診斷出腦性麻痺 。
their mom is a very brave woman who didn't believe that the symptoms weren't matching up , and through some heroic efforts and a lot of internet searching , she was able to convince the medical community that , in fact , they had something else .	他們的母親是個非常勇敢的女人 , 她不相信症狀不符合我們 , 透過一些英雄式的努力和許多網路搜尋 , 她能夠說服醫學界 , 事實上 , 他們還有別的東西 。
what they had was doparesponsive dystonia .	他們有的是預防反應的肌張力不全症 。
and so they were given ldopa , and their symptoms did improve , but they weren't totally asymptomatic .	所以他們得到了烏托邦 , 他們的症狀確實有所改善 , 但他們並沒有完全症狀 。
turns out the gentleman in this picture is a guy named joe beery , who was lucky enough to be the cio of a company called life technologies .	結果 , 這張照片裡的先生是一位叫joebeery的傢伙 , 他很幸運能成為一家名為 「 生命科技 」 的公司 。
they're one of the two companies that makes these massive whole genome sequencing tools .	它們是兩家製造這些大量基因序列工具的公司之一 。
and so what he did was he got his kids sequenced .	他的做法是讓他的孩子進行排序 。
and what they found was a series of mutations in a gene called spr , which is responsible for producing serotonin , among other things .	他們發現一系列突變基因在一個叫做spr的基因中 , 負責製造血清素 , 其中還有其他東西 。
so on top of ldopa , they gave these kids a serotonin precursor drug , and they're effectively normal now .	所以 , 在左上方 , 他們給了這些孩子一種血清素前驅的藥 , 現在他們很正常 。
guys , this would never have happened without whole genome sequencing .	沒有完整的基因序列 , 絕對不可能發生 。
and at the time this was a few years ago it cost $100 , 000 .	幾年前 , 花費十萬美金 。
today it's $10 , 000 . next year it's $1 , 000 .	今天是一萬美金 。 明年是一千美金
the year after it's $100 , give or take a year .	在它100元後的一年 , 給或一年 。
that's how fast this is moving .	這就是這個動作的速度
so here's little nick likes batman and squirt guns .	這裡有個小尼克喜歡蝙蝠俠和松鼠槍 。
and it turns out nick shows up at the children's hospital with this distended belly like a famine victim .	結果尼克出現在兒童醫院 , 帶著這種不幸的肚子 , 像飢荒的受害者一樣 。
and it's not that he's not eating , it's that when he eats , his intestine basically opens up and feces spill out into his gut .	不是說他沒有吃東西 , 而是當他吃的時候 , 他的腸子基本上會打開 , 糞便就會流出他的腸子 。
so a hundred surgeries later , he looks at his mom and says , " mom , please pray for me . i'm in so much pain . "	所以一百次手術後 , 他看著他的媽媽說: 「 媽媽 , 請為我祈禱 。 我非常痛苦 。 」
his pediatrician happens to have a background in clinical genetics and he has no idea what's going on , but he says , " let's get this kid's genome sequenced . "	他的小兒科醫生剛好有臨床遺傳學的背景 , 他完全不知道發生了什麼事 , 但他說: 「 我們來把這個孩子的基因序列做好 。 」
and what they find is a singlepoint mutation in a gene responsible for controlling programmed cell death .	而他們發現 , 在一個控制細胞死亡的基因突變中 , 有一個單點突變 。
so the theory is that he's having some immunological reaction to what's going on to the food essentially , and that's a natural reaction , which causes some programmed cell death .	所以這個理論是他對食物本質上所產生的免疫反應那是一種天然的反應這會造成一些程式化的細胞死亡
but the gene that regulates that down is broken .	但調節它的基因卻斷裂了 。
and so this informs , among other things , of course , a treatment for bone marrow transplant , which he undertakes .	當然 , 這也說明了骨髓移植手術的治療方法 。
and after nine months of grueling recovery , he's now eating steak with a1 sauce .	經過九個月的辛苦復原後 , 他現在用a1醬吃牛排了 。
the prospect of using the genome as a universal diagnostic is upon us today .	用基因組當作通用診斷方法的前景 , 今天就在我們身上了 。
today , it's here .	今天 , 就在這裡 。
and what it means for all of us is that everybody in this room could live an extra five , 10 , 20 years just because of this one thing .	這對我們所有人的意義是 , 在座的各位可以多活五、十年、二十年 , 只因為這一件事 。
which is a fantastic story , unless you think about humanity's footprint on the planet and our ability to keep up food production .	這是個很棒的故事 , 除非你考慮到人類在地球上的足跡以及我們維持糧食生產的能力 。
so it turns out that the very same technology is also being used to grow new lines of corn , wheat , soybean and other crops that are highly tolerant of drought , of flood , of pests and pesticides .	結果發現 , 同樣的技術也被用來種植玉米、小麥、黃豆 , 以及其他農作物 , 它們對乾旱、洪水、害蟲和殺蟲劑有高度包容性 。
now look , as long as we continue to increase the population , we're going to have to continue to grow and eat genetically modified foods , and that's the only position that i'll take today .	現在 , 看看 , 只要我們繼續增加人口 , 我們就必須繼續種植和食用基因改造的食物 , 這是我今天唯一要取的位置 。
unless there's anybody in the audience that would like to volunteer to stop eating ?	除非觀眾中有人願意自願停止進食 ?
none , not one .	沒有一個 , 沒有一個 。
this is a typewriter , a staple of every desktop for decades .	這是個打字機 , 數十年來每個桌面的釘子 。

daniel kraft demos his marrow miner a new device that quickly harvests lifesaving bone marrow with minimal pain to the donor . he emphasizes that the adult stem cells found in bone marrow can be used to treat many terminal conditions , from parkinson's to heart disease .	danielkraft示範他的骨髓礦工一個新裝置 , 它很快地收集了救命的骨髓 , 給捐贈者最少的疼痛 。 他強調 , 在骨髓中找到的成體幹細胞 , 可以用來治療許多臨終條件 , 從帕金森氏症到心臟病 。

so i am a pediatric cancer doctor and stemcell researcher at stanford university where my clinical focus has been bone marrow transplantation .	我是小兒科癌症醫生 , 也是史丹佛大學的幹細胞研究員 , 我的臨床焦點是骨髓移植 。
now , inspired by jill bolte taylor last year , i didn't bring a human brain , but i did bring a liter of bone marrow .	去年jillboltetaylor的靈感來源 , 我沒有帶來人腦 , 但我的確帶來了一公升的骨髓 。
and bone marrow is actually what we use to save the lives of tens of thousands of patients , most of whom have advanced malignancies like leukemia and lymphoma and some other diseases .	而骨髓實際上是我們用來拯救數萬名病患的生命 , 大部分患有先進的惡性腫瘤 , 如白血病、淋巴瘤 , 及其他一些疾病 。
so , a few years ago , i'm doing my transplant fellowship at stanford .	所以 , 幾年前 , 我在史丹佛做移植研究 。
i'm in the operating room . we have bob here , who is a volunteer donor .	我在手術室 。 我們這裡有bob , 他是志願捐贈者 。
we're sending his marrow across the country to save the life of a child with leukemia .	我們送他的骨髓到全國各地 , 來拯救白血病孩童的生命 。
so actually how do we harvest this bone marrow ?	所以 , 實際上 , 我們要如何採集這種骨髓 ?
well we have a whole o . r . team , general anesthesia , nurses , and another doctor across from me .	我們有一整個o.r團隊 , 麻醉醫師 , 護士 , 還有另一位醫生從我身邊過來 。
bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	bob躺在桌上 , 我們拿著這根小針 , 你知道的 , 沒什麼大不了的 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	我們的做法是 , 把這個放在軟組織中 , 將它打到堅硬的骨頭上 , 進入到tuchus中 , 這是一個技術名詞 , 並且每次用針筒 , 吸出大約十層骨髓 。
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	然後把它交給護士 。 她把它放進一個錫箱裡 。
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	把它交回給我 。 我們一而再 , 再而三地這麼做 。
about 200 times usually .	通常大約200次 。
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	最後 , 我的手臂是sore , 我手上有一通電話 , 更不用說bob , 它的後端看起來像這樣 , 像瑞士起司 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	所以我在想 , 你知道嗎 , 這個程序在大約四十年間都沒有改變 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	或許還有更好的方法 。
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以我想到了一個最小侵入性的方法 , 一個我們稱之為 「 骨髓採取器 」 的新裝置 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	而骨髓採取器 , 這裡的運作方式
our standard seethrough patient .	我們的標準見證病人
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	與其進入骨頭數十次 , 我們只需要進入一次 , 進入臀部前部 , 或臀部後部 。
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有彈性、有力的導管 , 上面有特殊的電線迴圈 , 會留在骨髓的殘酷部分 , 跟著臀部的輪廓 , 隨著它移動 。
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	所以它使你非常迅速地渴望 , 或吸出 , 豐富的骨髓很快地穿過一個洞 。
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們可以多次通過相同的入口
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	所以 , 很快的 , bob只能一次穿刺 , 局部麻醉 , 把這當作病人來收穫 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	所以我做了幾個原型 。 我在史丹佛得到了一個小小的補助 。
and played around with this a little bit .	再來玩一下 。
and our team members developed this technology .	而我們的團隊成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最後我們得到兩種大型動物 , 還有豬的研究 。
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	我們很驚訝地發現 , 我們不僅把骨髓拿出來 , 我們還得到了骨髓中十倍的幹細胞活動 , 相較於一般裝置 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這個裝置在去年剛核准的食品及藥物管理局
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這是個活體病人 。 你可以看到它跟著有彈性的曲線繞著它轉 。
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	在同一個病人中 , 會有兩個通過 , 來自同一個洞 。
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	這是在局部麻醉下進行的 , 身為一個專門病患 。
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	再一次 , 我們得到的幹細胞數量 , 比同一個病人的標準方法多了三到六倍 。
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	所以 , 為什麼你要在乎 ? 骨髓是非常豐富的成人幹細胞來源 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	大家都知道胚胎幹細胞
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	他們很有潛力 , 但還沒進入臨床試驗 。
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成體幹細胞遍佈全身 , 包括我們骨髓內的血液檢查幹細胞 , 我們已經用它作為幹細胞治療的一種形式 , 超過四十年了 。
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	在過去的十年中 , 使用骨髓幹細胞來治療病人的其他疾病例如心臟病、血管疾病、組織工程、甚至神經系統來治療帕金森氏症和糖尿病 。
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	我們剛剛出櫃 , 我們正在商業化 , 今年 , 第二世代的骨髓採礦者 。
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望能得到更多幹細胞 , 轉化成更好的結果 。
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	它可能會鼓勵更多人簽名成為潛在救命的骨髓捐贈者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	甚至可能讓你在更年輕、更健康時 , 去銀行自己的骨髓幹細胞 , 在未來應該要用到它 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最終 , 這張照片是我們的骨髓移植者 , 每年在史丹佛聚集在一起 。
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這項技術能讓我們在未來有更多這樣的倖存者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家和衝浪者garretlisi提出了一個有爭議的新宇宙模型 , 剛剛也許回答了所有大問題 。 如果沒有其他問題 , 它是最美麗的8d立體模型 , 它是你所見過最美麗的8d立體粒子和力 。
physics , science , technology	物理、科學、科技、
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	garrettlisi在他所有東西的理論上
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	哇 , 老兄 。 看看那些殺人方程式 。 甜心 。
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	事實上 , 在接下來的18分鐘裡 , 我會盡力去描述粒子物理的美麗 , 不用方程式 。
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	結果發現 , 我們可以從珊瑚身上學到很多東西 。
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是非常美麗和不尋常的動物 。
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每個珊瑚的頭都是由數千個別的珊瑚群組成的 。
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些珊瑚蟲不斷地發育和分支成基因相同的鄰居 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	如果我們想像這是一個超級聰明的珊瑚 , 我們可以單獨探討一個個體 , 問他一個合理的問題 。
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們可以問他是如何在這個特定的地點相較於他的鄰居是否有機會 , 還是命運 , 又或者如何 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	現在 , 在我們向上指示我們把溫度調高太高之後 , 他會告訴我們 , 我們的問題完全是愚蠢的 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	這些珊瑚可以是相當類似的意思 , 你看 , 我有衝浪疤可以證明這一點 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	但這個 「 波普 」 會繼續告訴我們 , 他的鄰居是相當明顯的一模一樣的 。
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他也在其他的地點 , 但將他們視為獨立的個體 。
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚來說 , 分枝變成不同的複製品是世界上最自然的東西 。
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	和我們不同的是 , 一個超級智慧的珊瑚會獨特的準備去了解量子力學 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學非常準確地描述我們的宇宙是如何運作的 。
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們 , 我們的現實持續分支成不同的可能性 , 就像珊瑚一樣 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	對我們人類來說 , 這是很奇怪的事 , 可以把我們的心思纏繞起來 , 因為我們只能經歷一種可能性 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這種量子力學的怪異性最早是由厄文•薛丁格和他的貓描述的 。
the cat likes this version better .	貓更喜歡這個版本
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	在這個設定中 , 薛丁格在一個有放射性樣本的盒子裡 , 由量子力學定律 , 分支到一種狀態 , 它的輻射和一種狀態 , 並不是 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	在這個樣本放射線的樹枝中 , 它會觸發釋放毒藥和薛丁格的觸發因子死亡 。
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在現實的另一個分支中 , 他仍然活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	這些真實被每個個體分開的經歷 。
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	據我所知 , 另一個不存在 。
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這對我們來說似乎很奇怪 , 因為我們每個人都只經歷一個個體的存在 , 而我們也看不到其他的分支 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	這就好像我們每個人 , 就像薛丁格 , 是一種珊瑚蟲 , 分裂成不同的可能性 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學告訴我們這就是世界如何在微小的尺度下運作的 。
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	可以用單一句子來總結:所有可能發生的事 , 都會做 。
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不表示一切都會發生 。
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	其餘的物理則是描述什麼可以發生 , 以及什麼不能發生 。
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理學告訴我們 , 一切都歸根究底到幾何學 , 以及基本粒子的互動 。
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	只有在這些互動完全平衡的情況下 , 事情才有可能發生 。
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	現在我來描述一下我們對這些粒子的認識 , 它們是什麼 , 以及這個平衡如何運作 。
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這個機器中 , 一束質子和反質子會加速到接近光速的速度 , 並在一個碰撞中聚集在一起 , 產生出一股純能量爆發 。
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這種能量馬上被轉換成亞原子粒子的噴霧 , 有偵測器和電腦用來弄清楚它們的特性 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這個巨大的機器--日內瓦的cern大型強子對撞機有一個圓周長17英里 , 當它在運作時 , 畫出五倍於蒙特雷市 。
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們無法準確預測哪些粒子會在任何個體碰撞中產生
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們所有的可能性都被實現了 。
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理的確告訴我們哪些粒子可以產生
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子的質量和能量就跟質子和反質子一樣多 。
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何比這個能量極限更巨大的粒子都不會產生 , 且對我們來說仍然是看不見的 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這就是為什麼這個新型粒子加速器太興奮了 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	它會把這個能量極限推到前所未有的以上七倍以上 , 所以我們很快就會看到一些新粒子 。
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但在談我們可能看到的東西之前 , 讓我先描述一下我們已經知道的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	有整個亞原子粒子的動物園
most of us are familiar with electrons .	我們大部分人都很熟悉電子
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	現場的許多人 , 都過著好的生活 , 把他們推過來 。
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	但電子也有中性伴侶 , 叫做微中子 , 沒有電荷和很小的質量 。
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相對的 , 上層夸克有非常大的質量 , 結合三者 , 讓原子內的質子和中子成為原子 。
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	所有這些物質粒子都帶有左旋和右旋的品種 , 有反粒子伴侶帶著相反電荷 。
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子也比較不熟悉的第二代和第三代 , 和第一代有相同的載荷 , 但質量也比較高 。
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些物質粒子全都和各種力粒子相互作用
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	電磁力通過稱為光子的粒子產生電荷相互作用
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	還有一種非常微弱的力量 , 叫 「 弱力 」 , 只有左手的物質相互作用 。
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	夸克之間的強力作用 , 會帶有不同的載荷 , 稱為顏色載荷 , 會出現三種不同的品種:紅、綠、藍 。
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	你可以怪罪murraygellmann為了這些名字--他們是他的錯 。
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後 , 還有重力 , 透過質量和旋轉 , 與物質相互作用 。
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	最重要的是 , 這裡有不同的載荷和每一種力量有關 。
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	這四種不同的力量是根據每個粒子所擁有的對應的載荷而相互作用 。
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	一個還沒被看見的粒子 , 但我們很確定存在 , 就是希格斯粒子 , 它給予所有其他粒子的質量 。
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型強子對撞機的主要目的是看到這個希格斯粒子我們幾乎確定它會
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最偉大的謎團是我們可能還能看到的 。
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	我將向你們展示一種美麗的可能性 , 朝這場演說的結尾 。
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	現在 , 如果我們用各式各樣的旋轉和載荷算出這些不同的粒子 , 總共有226種 。
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	那是很多粒子用來追蹤的 。
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	看來 , 大自然會有這麼多基本粒子 。
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果我們根據它們的載荷把它們畫出來 , 有些漂亮的圖案就會浮現出來 。
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的載荷是電荷 。
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子有電荷 , 負電荷 , 夸克有三分之一的電荷 。
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	所以當2個上夸克和1個下夸克結合成質子時 , 它的電荷總和是1 。
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子也有反粒子 , 具有相反的載荷 。
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	結果發現 , 電荷其實是另外兩種載荷的結合:超荷和弱荷 。
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	如果我們散開超荷和弱荷 , 並在這個二度載荷空間中繪製粒子的載荷 , 電荷是這些粒子位於垂直方向的位置 。
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁力和弱力的相互作用 , 根據它們的超荷和弱荷 , 產生這種模式 。
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	這被稱為 「 統一伊萊克模式 」 , 它在1967年被拼湊起來 。
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	大部分人都熟悉電荷而不是兩者都是因為希格斯粒子
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	左邊的希格斯有很大的質量打破了電擊模式的對稱性
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	它會讓弱作用力非常弱 , 通過給弱粒子一個很大的質量 。
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	由於這個巨大的希格斯會沿著水平方向坐著 , 電磁力的光子會保持質量 , 並沿著這個載荷空間的垂直方向與電荷相互作用 。
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	所以電磁力和弱力在二維空間中被描述成粒子電荷的模式
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們能將強力納入 , 透過散播出它的兩個載荷方向 , 並沿這些夸克方向劃出載荷的載荷 。
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有已知粒子的載荷可以在四度載荷空間中被繪製出來 , 然後投射到像這樣的兩度空間中 , 以便我們能看見它們 。
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	每當粒子相互作用 , 大自然都會在四個載荷方向上保持完美的平衡 。
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	如果一個粒子和一個反粒子相撞 , 它會產生能量 , 以及四個載荷方向的總載荷 。
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	此時 , 任何東西都可以產生只要它有相同的能量 , 並且保持總載荷的0 。
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	舉例來說 , 這個弱力粒子和它的反粒子可以在碰撞中產生 。
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	在進一步的互動中 , 載荷必須永遠保持平衡 。
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	其中一個弱粒子可以衰退成一個電子和一個反中微子 , 這三個仍然可以加到零個總載荷 。
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	大自然總是保持完美的平衡
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以這些模式的載荷不只是漂亮的 。
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	他們告訴我們什麼樣的互動是允許發生的 。
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	我們可以在四度空間中旋轉這個載荷空間 , 來更好地觀察強相互作用 , 這個強相互作用的對稱性 。
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	在強力相互作用中 , 一個強力粒子 , 例如這一個 , 和一個有色夸克相互作用 , 例如這個綠色夸克 , 給一個有不同顏色荷荷的夸克 。
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	而強相互作用每秒鐘都發生在我們身體的每一個原子上 , 將原子核放在一起 。
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但這四種載荷相對應三種力量並不是故事的結局
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們還可以再納入兩個載荷對應到重力力 。
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	當我們把這些納入 , 每個物質粒子都有兩個不同的旋轉載荷 , 旋轉和旋轉 。
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以他們都分開了 , 在六度載荷空間中給出了不錯的模式 。
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以在六度空間中旋轉這個模式 , 看到它相當漂亮 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	目前 , 這種模式符合我們目前對大自然的最佳知識 , 以這些微小粒子的規模建造 。
this is what we know for certain .	這是我們肯定知道的 。
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	其中有些粒子是在實驗的極限 。
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個圖案中 , 我們已經知道了這些微小尺度的粒子物理學 。 宇宙運作的方式和這些微小的尺度是非常美麗的 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	但現在我要討論一些新的、舊的想法關於我們還不知道的事情 。
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們想要單單用數學來擴展這個模式 , 看看我們能不能把雙手放在整體的恩基拉達上 。
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們想要找到所有組成我們宇宙的所有粒子和力 。
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們想要用這張圖來預測新粒子 , 當實驗達到更高能量時會看到 。
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	所以 , 在粒子物理學中有一個古老的想法 , 就是這種已知的載荷模式 , 不太對稱 , 可能從更完美的圖案中浮現出來 , 變得和希格斯粒子如何突破電極圖案 。
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了做到這一點 , 我們需要引進有新的載荷方向的新力量 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們導入一個新的方向時 , 我們能猜到 , 是什麼帶電粒子沿這個方向移動 , 然後我們就可以把它和其他粒子一起旋轉 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	如果我們明智地猜想 , 我們就能在六度載荷維度中建構標準的載荷 , 作為七度載荷維度中這個更完美的對稱性 。
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	這個特別的選擇對應於1973年pati和salam推出的一個宏大的統一理論 。
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們看這個新的統一圖案時 , 我們可以看到一些空隙 , 粒子似乎缺少了 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這是統一理論的運作方式 。
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	物理學家尋找更大、更對稱的模式 , 將已建立的模式納入為子集 。
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	更大的模式讓我們能夠預測從未見過的粒子的存在 。
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這個統一模型預測了這兩種新力粒子的存在 , 它應該會作用得很像弱力 , 只有比較弱的力 。
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	現在我們可以在七度空間中旋轉這組載荷 , 並考慮一個奇怪的事實:關於物質粒子的第二代和第三代物質在六度載荷空間中有完全相同的載荷 。
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子並不是獨一無二的由他們六個載荷所辨識出來的 。
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	他們坐在標準載荷空間的頂端 。
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 如果我們在八度載荷空間中工作 , 那麼我們可以把獨特的新載荷分配給每一個粒子 。
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	然後我們可以在八度空間中旋轉 , 看看整個模式是什麼樣子 。
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	這裡我們可以看到第二代和第三代物質與第一個世代的對稱性是 「 試驗性 」 。
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	八度中的這個特殊的載荷圖案 , 其實是數學中最美麗的幾何結構的一部分 。
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	這是最大的例外謊言團體的模式 , e8 。
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	這個謊言團體是一個平滑、彎曲的形狀 , 有248維度 。
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	圖案中的每個點都對應到這個非常複雜且美麗的形狀的對稱性 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	e8形狀的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦廣義相對論的曲線時空 , 解釋重力 。
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	加上量子力學 , 這個形狀的幾何學可以描述宇宙如何在最小的尺度下運作的一切 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	這種形狀存在於八度載荷空間的圖案非常美麗 , 它總結了成千上萬個可能的相互作用 , 在這些基本粒子之間 , 每一個都只是這複雜形狀的一面 。
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	當我們旋轉它時 , 我們可以看到許多其他錯綜複雜的圖案在這個圖案中 。
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	用一個特定的旋轉 , 我們可以向下看這個圖案 , 沿著一個對稱軸 , 八度空間 , 同時看到所有的粒子 。
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	這是一個非常美麗的物體 , 隨著任何統一 , 我們可以看到一些洞 , 新粒子是這個圖案所需要的 。
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	這裡有20個缺口 , 新粒子應該有2個已經被patisalam粒子給填滿 。
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	從他們在這個模式中的位置 , 我們知道這些新粒子應該是像希格斯粒子一樣的疤田 , 但有色荷 , 和強力相互作用 。
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	填入這些新粒子完成這個圖案 , 給我們完整的e8 。
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	這個e8圖案有著非常深層的數學根
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	它被許多人認為是數學中最美麗的結構 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這個偉大數學美的物體可以用最小尺度來描述粒子相互作用的真相 。
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	而這個想法 , 大自然被數學所描述的完全不是新東西 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	在1623年 , 伽利略寫了這句話: 「 大自然的宏偉書 , 代表著持續開放給我們的目光 , 是用數學的語言寫的 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	它的角色是三角形 , 圓形和其他幾何圖形 , 沒有這些 , 是人類無法理解的 ; 若沒有這些 , 一個在黑暗的迷宮中漫遊 。 」
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這是真的 , 我曾試著遵循伽利略的指導 , 以描述粒子物理的數學 , 只用三角形、圓形和其他幾何圖形來描述 。
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 當其他物理學家和我實際在研究這個東西時 , 數學可以像一個黑暗的迷宮 。
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但 , 要確保數學的核心是純粹、美麗的幾何學 。
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	加入了量子力學 , 這個數學把我們的宇宙描述成一個在成長的e8珊瑚 , 粒子在每個地點都在相互作用 , 根據一個美麗的圖案 。
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	隨著更多的圖案用像大型強子對撞機這樣的新機器來看 , 我們或許可以看出大自然是否使用e8圖案或不同圖案 。
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這項發現的過程是一趟美好的探險 , 要參與其中 。
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果lhc找到符合e8圖案的粒子那會非常非常非常酷
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果lhc找到新的粒子但它們不符合這個模式那會非常有趣但對這個e8理論不利
and , of course , bad for me personally .	當然 , 對我個人而言是不好的 。
now how bad would that be ?	那會多糟 ?
well , pretty bad .	嗯 , 相當糟糕 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但預測大自然的運作是很冒險的遊戲 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這個理論和其它類似的 , 都是長槍 。
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	一個人做了很多辛苦的工作 , 知道大部分這些想法可能最後不會對大自然產生影響 。
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	這就是理論物理學的原理:有很多的無線技術 。
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	在這方面 , 新的物理理論很像新創公司 。
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	就如同任何大型投資一樣 , 在不成功時 , 要放棄一行研究是很困難的 。
but in science , if something isn't working , you have to toss it out and try something else .	但在科學上 , 如果有東西不成功 , 你就得要丟棄它 , 再試試別的 。
now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	現在 , 在這種不確定性中 , 唯一能維持理智和達到快樂的方法 , 就是在生活中保持平衡和觀點 。
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我已經盡我所能過著平衡的生活 。
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著在物理、愛和衝浪之間平衡我的人生 。 我試著在三個載荷方向之間取得平衡 。
this way , even if the physics i work on comes to nothing , i still know i've lived a good life .	這麼一來 , 即使我所研究的物理學什麼都沒有 , 我仍然知道我過得很好 。
and i try to live in beautiful places .	我試著生活在美麗的地方 。
for most of the past ten years i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .	過去十年來 , 我住在毛伊島 , 一個非常美麗的地方 。
now it's one of the greatest mysteries in the universe to my parents how i managed to survive all that time without engaging in anything resembling fulltime employment .	現在 , 這是宇宙中最偉大的奧秘之一 , 讓我的父母知道 , 我如何能在那段時間中生存下來 , 卻沒有投入任何與全職工作相似的東西 。
i'm going to let you in on that secret .	我要告訴你們那個秘密 。
this was a view from my home office on maui .	這是我在毛伊島的家裡辦公室的一個景象 。
and you may have noticed that these beautiful views are similar , but in slightly different places .	你可能已經注意到這些美麗的觀點是相似的 , 但在稍微不同的地方 。
that's because this used to be my home and office on maui .	那是因為這曾經是我在毛伊島的家和辦公室 。
i've chosen a very unusual life .	我選擇過非常不尋常的生活 。
but not worrying about rent allowed me to spend my time doing what i love .	但不用擔心房租讓我可以花時間做我所愛的事 。
living a nomadic existence has been hard at times , but it's allowed me to live in beautiful places and keep a balance in my life that i've been happy with .	過著遊牧的存在 , 有時是很困難的 , 但它讓我能住在美麗的地方 , 在我的人生中保持平衡 。
it allows me to spend a lot of my time hanging out with hyperintelligent coral .	它讓我可以花很多時間和超級聰明的珊瑚相處 。
but i also greatly enjoy the company of hyperintelligent people .	但我也很享受超級聰明的人的公司 。
so i'm very happy to have been invited here to ted .	所以我很高興能被邀請來到ted 。
chris anderson: i probably understood two percent of that , but i still absolutely loved it . so i'm going to sound dumb .	克里斯•安德森:我大概明白其中的2% , 但我還是很喜歡 。 所以我會聽起來很笨 。
your theory of everything garrett lisi: i'm used to coral .	你的萬物理論:我習慣了珊瑚 。
ca: that's right . the reason it's got a few people at least excited is because , if you're right , it brings gravity and quantum theory together .	克:沒錯 。 它之所以有少數人至少興奮是因為 , 如果你是對的 , 它會把重力和量子理論結合在一起 。
so are you saying that we should think of the universe , at its heart that the smallest things that there are , are somehow an e8 object of possibility ?	所以 , 你是不是說我們應該把宇宙想成它的心臟 , 那個最小的東西 , 是有某種可能性的e8物體 ?
i mean , is there a scale to it , at the smallest scale , or . . . ?	我的意思是 , 在最小尺度 , 還是...
gl: well , right now the pattern i showed you that corresponds to what we know about elementary particle physics that already corresponds to a very beautiful shape .	格林:現在 , 我給你們看的圖案 , 就是我們所知的基本粒子物理學 , 已經對應到一個非常美麗的形狀 。
and that's the one that i said we knew for certain .	那就是我說我們知道的那個 。
and that shape has remarkable similarities and the way it fits into this e8 pattern could be the rest of the picture .	這個形狀有著驚人的相似性 , 和它符合e8圖案的方式 , 可能是圖片的其餘部分 。
and these patterns of points that i've shown for you actually represent symmetries of this highdimensional object that would be warping and moving and dancing over the space time that we experience .	我給你們看的這些點的圖案 , 其實代表了這個高維物體的對稱性 , 會在我們所經歷的空間中扭曲、移動、跳舞 。
and that would be what explains all these elementary particles that we see .	這就解釋了我們看到的所有這些基本粒子
ca: but a string theorist , as i understand it , explains electrons in terms of much smaller strings vibrating i know you don't like string theory vibrating inside it .	克:但弦理論學家 , 如我所知 , 用更小的弦振動來解釋電子 , 我知道你不喜歡弦理論在裡面振動 。
how should we think of an electron in relation to e8 ?	我們該如何看待電子與e8的關係 ?
gl: no , it would be one of the symmetries of this e8 shape .	格林:不 , 它會是這個e8形狀的對稱之一 。
so what's happening is , as the shape is moving over spacetime , it's twisting . and the direction it's twisting as it moves is what particle we see . so it would be ca: the size of the e8 shape , how does that relate to the electron ?	所以 , 當這個形狀在時空中移動時 , 它會扭轉 。 當它移動時 , 它會扭轉的方向 , 就是我們看到的粒子 。 所以 , 它會是:e8形狀的大小 , 它和電子的大小 , 它是如何與電子連結在一起的 ?
i kind of feel like i need that for my picture .	我覺得我需要這張照片 。
is it bigger ? is it smaller ?	變大了 ? 變小了嗎 ?
gl: well , as far as we know electrons are point particles , so this would be going down to the smallest possible scales .	格林:嗯 , 據我們所知 , 電子是點粒子 , 所以這會降到最小的可能尺度 。
so the way these things are explained in quantum field theory is , all possibilities are expanding and developing at once .	所以 , 這些東西在量子場理論中被解釋的方式是 , 所有的可能性都同時擴張和發展 。
and this is why i use the analogy to coral .	這就是為什麼我用類比來珊瑚的原因 。
and in this way , the way that e8 comes in is it will be as a shape that's attached at each point in spacetime .	如此一來 , e8進來的方式 , 將是一個在時空中每一點都附加在的形狀 。
and , as i said , the way the shape twists the directional along which way the shape is twisting as it moves over this curved surface is what the elementary particles are , themselves .	正如我所說 , 形狀扭曲的方向 , 隨著它移動在曲線表面上扭曲的方向 , 正是基本粒子本身 。
so through quantum field theory , they manifest themselves as points and interact that way .	透過量子場理論 , 他們將自己呈現為點 , 並以此方式互動 。
i don't know if i'll be able to make this any clearer .	我不知道我能不能把這個更清楚 。
ca: it doesn't really matter .	克:這一點都不重要 。
it's evoking a kind of sense of wonder , and i certainly want to understand more of this .	它喚起了一種驚奇感 , 我當然也想了解更多這點 。
but thank you so much for coming . that was absolutely fascinating .	但非常謝謝你來了 。 這真的很吸引人 。
the legendary chimpanzee researcher jane goodall talks about tacare and her other community projects , which help people in booming african towns live sidebyside with threatened animals .	傳奇的黑猩猩研究員珍.古德談到塔卡爾和她的其他社區計畫 , 協助在非洲爆發的小鎮上 , 和受到威脅的動物一起生活 。
africa , animals , biodiversity , environment , global issues , pollution , primates , science	非洲、動物、生物多樣性、環境、全球議題、污染、靈長類、科學 。
jane goodall helps humans and animals live together	珍古德幫助人類和動物一起生活 。
good afternoon , good evening , whatever .	午安 , 晚安 , 等等 。
we can go , jambo , guten abend , bonsoir , but we can also ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh .	我們可以去 , 詹姆波 , 古斯班德 , 邦索爾 , 但我們也可以...噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 。
that is the call that chimpanzees make before they go to sleep in the evening .	這是黑猩猩在晚上睡覺前所製造的叫聲 。
you hear it going from one side of the valley to the other , from one group of nests to the next .	你聽到它從山谷的一端傳到另一邊 , 從一群巢穴傳到下一群 。
and i want to pick up with my talk this evening from where zeray left off yesterday .	今天晚上 , 我想要從昨天zeray離開的地方來聽我的演講 。
he was talking about this amazing , threeyearold australopithecine child , selam .	他當時在談論這個令人驚奇、三歲的奧地匹克兒童賽蘭
and we've also been hearing about the history , the family tree , of mankind through dna genetic profiling .	我們也聽過有關人類的歷史、家族樹 , 透過dna側寫 ,
and it was a paleontologist , the late louis leakey , who actually set me on the path for studying chimpanzees .	那是一位古生物學家 , 已故的路易斯•李克 , 他讓我踏上研究黑猩猩的路徑 。
and it was pretty extraordinary , way back then .	回到以前 , 這相當不尋常 。
it's kind of commonplace now , but his argument was because he'd been searching for the fossilized remains of early humans in africa .	現在這有點常見 , 但他的論點是 , 因為他一直在尋找非洲早期人類的化石 。
and you can tell an awful lot about what those beings looked like from the fossils , from the shape of the muscle attachments , something about the way they lived from the various artifacts found with them .	你可以從化石中得知這些化石的樣子 , 從肌肉依附的形狀 , 得知他們與之共存的各種手工藝品 。
but what about how they behaved ? that's what he wanted to know .	但它們的行為呢 ? 這就是他想要知道的 。
and of course , behavior doesn't fossilize .	當然 , 行為並不會化石 。
he argued and it's now a fairly common theory that if we found behavior patterns similar or the same in our closest living relatives , the great apes , and humans today , then maybe those behaviors were present in the apelike , humanlike ancestor some seven million years ago .	他主張 , 現在這個理論相當普遍如果我們在最接近的生命親戚、大猩猩和人類的近親裡發現了類似的行為模式或許這些行為在七百萬年前就出現了人類的祖先
and therefore , perhaps we had brought those characteristics with us from that ancient , ancient past .	因此 , 也許我們已經把這些特徵從古老的過去 , 帶給我們 。
well , if you look in textbooks today that deal with human evolution , you very often find people speculating about how early humans may have behaved , based on the behavior of chimpanzees .	嗯 , 如果你看看今天處理人類演化的教科書 , 你經常會發現人們推測早期人類的行為方式 , 根據黑猩猩的行為 。
they are more like us than any other living creature , and we've heard about that during this ted conference .	他們比任何其他生物都更像我們 , 在ted大會上我們也聽說過 。
so it remains for me to comment on the ways in which chimpanzees are so like us , in certain aspects of their behavior .	所以對我來說 , 我還是要評論黑猩猩和我們很像的方式 , 在某些方面是如此 。
every chimpanzee has his or her own personality .	每一隻黑猩猩都有他或她自己的個性
of course , i gave them names . they can live to be 60 years or more , although we think most of them probably don't make it to 60 in the wild .	當然 , 我給他們名字 。 他們可以活到60年以上 , 雖然我們認為大部份的人可能不會在野外活到60歲 。
mr . wurzel . the female has her first baby when she's 11 or 12 .	沃茲爾先生 。 雌性在十一或十二歲時就生了她的第一個寶寶 。
thereafter , she has one baby only every five or six years , a long period of childhood dependency when the child is nursing , sleeping with the mother at night , and riding on her back .	如此一來 , 她每五到六年就有一個嬰兒 , 一個長期的童年依賴兒童 , 當孩子在療養 , 晚上和母親一起睡覺 , 然後在背上騎著 。
and we believe that this long period of childhood is important for chimpanzees , just as it is for us , in relation to learning .	我們相信 , 長時間的童年對黑猩猩來說是很重要的 , 就如同對我們來說 , 和學習的關係一樣 。
as the brain becomes ever more complex during evolution in different forms of animals , so we find that learning plays an ever more important role in an individual's life history .	隨著大腦在演化過程中變得更加複雜 , 以不同形式的動物為例 , 所以我們發現 , 學習在個體的生命史中扮演了更重要的角色 。
and young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .	而年輕的黑猩猩花了很多時間看牠們的前輩們在做什麼 。
we know now that they're capable of imitating behaviors that they see .	我們現在知道他們有能力模仿他們所看到的行為 。
and we believe that it's in this way that the different toolusing behaviors that have now been seen in all the different chimpanzee populations studied in africa how these are passed from one generation to the next , through observation , imitation and practice , so that we can describe these toolusing behaviors as primitive culture .	我們相信 , 這種方式就是現在在非洲所有不同黑猩猩族群中所看到的不同的工具行為 , 如何從一個世代傳到下一個世代 , 透過觀察、模仿和練習 , 這樣我們才能把這些工具行為描述成原始文化 。
chimpanzees don't have a spoken language . we've talked about that .	黑猩猩沒有口語語言 , 我們已經談過了
they do have a very rich repertoire of postures and gestures , many of which are similar , or even identical , to ours and formed in the same context . greeting chimpanzees embracing .	牠們的確有非常豐富的姿勢和姿勢 , 很多都很類似 , 甚至相同 , 與我們的相同 , 在相同的背景下形成 。 迎接黑猩猩 。
they also kiss , hold hands , pat one another on the back .	他們也親吻、握手、拍打對方在後面
and they swagger and they throw rocks .	牠們會搖晃 , 也會扔石頭 。
in chimpanzee society , we find many , many examples of compassion , precursors to love and true altruism .	在黑猩猩的社會中 , 我們發現許多許多同情心的例子 , 前導者是愛的 , 也是真正的利他行為 。
unfortunately , they , like us , have a dark side to their nature .	不幸的是 , 他們和我們一樣 , 對他們的本質有著黑暗的一面 。
they're capable of extreme brutality , even a kind of primitive war .	他們有能力極端殘暴 , 甚至是一種原始的戰爭 。
and these really aggressive behaviors , for the most part , are directed against individuals of the neighboring social group .	而這些非常具侵略性的行為 , 大部分的情況下 , 都是針對鄰近社會群體的個體 。
they are very territorially aggressive .	牠們非常具侵略性 。
chimpanzees , i believe , more than any other living creature , have helped us to understand that , after all , there is no sharp line between humans and the rest of the animal kingdom .	我相信 , 黑猩猩 , 比起其他生物 , 已經幫助我們了解 , 畢竟人類和動物王國之間沒有明顯的界線 。
it's a very blurry line , and it's getting more blurry all the time as we make even more observations .	這條線非常模糊 , 隨著我們觀察到的情況越來越模糊 。
the study that i began in 1960 is still continuing to this day .	我從1960年開始的研究至今仍持續到現在 。
and these chimpanzees , living their complex social lives in the wild , have helped more than anything else to make us realize we are part of , and not separated from , the amazing animals with whom we share the planet .	而這些黑猩猩 , 生活在野外複雜的社交生活 , 比起其它任何事情 , 都更能幫助我們意識到我們是其中的一份子 , 而不是分離 , 那些與我們共享這個星球的神奇動物 。
so it's pretty sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures around the world , are losing their habitats .	所以 , 要找到那隻黑猩猩 , 就像世界上許多其他生物一樣 , 都在失去牠們的棲息地 。
this is just one photograph from the air , and it shows you the forested highlands of gombe .	這只是一張從空中拍攝的照片 , 它展示了戈米普的森林高地 。
and it was when i flew over the whole area , about 16 years ago , and realized that outside the park , this forest , which in 1960 had stretched almost unbroken along the eastern shore of lake tanganyika , which is where the tiny , 30squaremile gombe national park lies , that a question came to my mind .	就在我飛越整個區域時 , 大約16年前 , 我了解到 , 在公園外面 , 這片森林 , 在1960年 , 這片森林幾乎沒有被打斷 , 沿著塔哥尼卡湖的東岸 , 那裡小小 , 30平方的戈米國家公園就在那裡 , 這個問題來到我心中 。
" how can we even try to save these famous chimpanzees , when the people living around the national park are struggling to survive ? "	「 我們要如何試著拯救這些有名的黑猩猩 , 當住在國家公園附近的居民在掙扎求生存時 ? 」
more people are living there than the land could possibly support .	比原本的土地還多的人可以支援 。
the numbers increased by refugees pouring in from burundi and over the lake from congo .	難民數量增加 , 來自蒲隆地和剛果湖的難民數量 。
and very poor people they couldn't afford to buy food from elsewhere .	而非常貧窮的人 , 他們買不起從別處買來的食物 。
this led to a program , which we call tacare .	這導致了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為 「 塔卡爾 」 。
it's a very holistic way of improving the lives of the people living in the villages around the park .	用一種全面的方式來改善住在公園附近村莊的人們的生活 。
it started small with 12 villages . it's now in 24 .	由12個村莊開始 , 現在在24個村莊
there isn't time to go into it , but it's including things like tree nurseries , methods of farming most suitable to this now very degraded , almost desertlike land up in these mountains .	沒有時間深入探討 , 但這包括樹木的保育 , 最適合養殖的方法 , 目前這種方法非常退化 , 幾乎像沙漠般的土地在這些山上 。
ways of controlling , preventing soil erosion .	控制、預防土壤侵蝕的方法 。
ways of reclaiming overused farmland , so that within two years they can again be productive .	重新使用過度使用的農地 , 讓兩年內再次變得有生產力 。
working to help the villagers obtain fresh water from wells .	幫助村民從井中取得新鮮水源 。
perhaps build some schoolrooms .	或許建造一些教室
most important of all , i believe , is working with small groups of women , providing them with opportunities for microcredit loans .	最重要的是 , 我相信 , 和一小群婦女合作 , 提供她們提供微型貸款的機會 。
and we've got , as is the case around the world , about 95 percent of all loans returned .	如同世界各地的情況 , 我們有95%的貸款回來 。
empowering women , working with education , providing scholarships for girls so they can finish secondary school , in the clear understanding that , all around the world , as women's education improves , family size drops .	賦予女性能力 , 和教育相關 , 為女孩們提供獎學金 , 這樣她們才能完成中學 , 清楚知道 , 在全世界 , 隨著女性的教育改善 , 家庭規模大幅下降 。
we provide information about family planning and about hiv/aids .	我們提供關於家庭計畫和關於愛滋病的資訊 。
and as a result of this program , something's happening for conservation .	這個計畫的結果是 , 有些事情正在發生 , 發生在保育上 。
what's happening for conservation is that the farmers living in these 24 villages , instead of looking on us as a bunch of white people coming to study a whole bunch of monkeys and by the way , many of the staff are now tanzanian but when we began the tacare program , it was a tanzanian team going into the villages .	保育的現況是 , 居住在24個村莊的農民 , 而不是看著我們一群白人來研究一群猴子──順帶一提 , 很多工作人員現在都是坦尚尼亞人──但當我們開始計劃時 , 坦尚尼亞是個坦尚尼亞團隊進入村落 。
it was a tanzanian team talking to the villagers , asking what they were interested in .	那是坦尚尼亞的團隊和村民談話 , 問他們有興趣什麼 。
were they interested in conservation ? absolutely not .	他們對保育有興趣嗎 ? 絕對不是 。
they were interested in health ; they were interested in education .	他們對健康有興趣 ; 他們對教育有興趣 。
and as time went on , and as their situation began to improve , they began to understand ever more about the need for conservation .	隨著時間的推移 , 當他們的情況開始改善 , 他們開始對保育的需求有更多了解 。
they began to understand that as the upper levels of the hills were denuded of trees , so you've got this terrible soil erosion and mudslides .	他們開始了解 , 隨著山坡的上層被除去樹木 , 所以你得到了這片可怕的土壤侵蝕和泥土 。
today , we are developing what we call the greater gombe ecosystem .	現今 , 我們正在發展我們所謂的更偉大的gmbe生態系統 。
this is an area way outside the national park , stretching out into all these very degraded lands .	這是國家公園以外的一個區域 , 延伸到這些非常惡化的土地上 。
and as these villages have a better standard of life , they are actually agreeing to put between 10 percent and 20 percent of their land in the highlands aside , so that once again , as the trees grow back , the chimpanzees will have leafy corridors through which they can travel to interact as they must for genetic viability with other remnant groups outside the national park .	當這些村落有更好的生活水準時 , 他們其實同意將10%到20%的土地放在高地上 , 所以 , 再一次 , 當樹木長回來時 , 黑猩猩們就會有葉廊 , 通過這條路 , 可以在國家公園外進行基因的可行性交流 。
so tacare is a success .	所以 , tacare是成功的 。
we're replicating it in other parts of africa , around other wilderness areas which are faced with extreme population pressure .	我們在非洲的其他地區複製它 , 圍繞著面臨極端人口壓力的其他荒野地區 。
the problems in africa , however , as we've been discussing for the whole of these first couple of days of ted , are major problems .	然而 , 非洲的問題 , 如同我們這幾天一直在ted討論的 , 是很重大的問題 。
there is a great deal of poverty .	貧窮的問題很大 。
and when you get large numbers of people living in land that is not that fertile , particularly when you cut down trees , and you leave the soil open to the wind for erosion , as desperate populations cut down more and more trees , so that they can try and grow food for themselves and their families , what's going to happen ? something's got to give .	當你在土地上生活的大量人數沒有那麼肥沃 , 尤其是當你砍掉樹木時 , 將土壤開放給風化 , 隨著絕望的族群砍伐越來越多樹木 , 這樣他們就可以嘗試為自己和他們的家人種植食物 , 會發生什麼事 ? 有些事需要給予 。
and the other problems in not only africa , but the rest of the developing world and , indeed , everywhere what are we doing to our planet ?	其他的問題不只在非洲 , 還在發展中國家 , 到處都是 , 我們對地球做了什麼事 ?
you know , the famous scientist , e . o . wilson said that if every person on this planet attains the standard of living of the average european or american , we need three new planets .	你知道 , 著名的科學家 , e.o.wilson說過 , 如果地球上的每一個人都能達到一般歐洲人或美國人的生活水準 , 我們需要三個新的星球 。
today , they are saying four . but we don't have them . we've got one .	現今 , 他們說四個 。 但我們沒有 。 我們只有一個 。
and what's happened ? i mean , the question here is , here we are , arguably the most intelligent being that's ever walked planet earth , with this extraordinary brain , capable of the kind of technology that is so well illustrated by these ted conferences , and yet we're destroying the only home we have .	到底發生了什麼事呢 ? 我的意思是 , 這裡我們是 , 可以說是最有智慧的生物 , 走過地球 , 帶著這個非凡的頭腦 , 能夠利用這些ted會議所描述的科技 , 然而我們卻在破壞我們唯一的家園 。
the indigenous people around the world , before they made a major decision , used to sit around and ask themselves , " how does this decision affect our people seven generations ahead ? "	世界各地的原住民 , 在他們做出重大決定之前 , 常常會坐在一旁問自己: 「 這個決定如何影響我們前後的七代人 ? 」
today , major decisions and i'm not particularly talking about africa here , but the developed world major decisions involving millions of dollars , and millions of people , are often based on , " how will this affect the next shareholders' meeting ? "	現今 , 重大的決策──我在這裡並不是特別談非洲 , 但已開發國家──重大決策包括數百萬美金 , 數百萬人──常常會根據 「 這會如何影響下一個股東的會議 ? 」
and these decisions affect africa .	而這些決策會影響到非洲
as i began traveling around africa talking about the problems faced by chimpanzees and their vanishing forests , i realized more and more how so many of africa's problems could be laid at the door of previous colonial exploitation .	當我開始環遊非洲 , 談論黑猩猩和牠們消失的森林所面臨的問題時 , 我了解到 , 非洲有這麼多問題可以解決之前殖民時代的剝削 。
so i began traveling outside africa , talking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .	所以我開始到非洲外面旅行 , 在歐洲演說 , 在美國演說 , 去到亞洲 。
and everywhere there were these terrible problems .	到處都有這些可怕的問題 。
and you know the kind i'm talking about . i'm talking about pollution .	而你知道我在說的那種 , 我指的是污染 。
the air that we breathe that often poisons us .	我們呼吸的空氣通常會毒害我們 。
the earth is poisoning our foods .	地球正在毒害我們的食物
the water water is perhaps one of the most crucial issues that we're going to face in this century and everywhere water is being polluted by agricultural , industrial and household chemicals that still are being sprayed around the world , seemingly with the inability to profit from past experience .	水資源可能是本世紀最關鍵的議題之一 , 到處都是水 , 被農業、工業 , 和家庭的化學物污染 , 這些化學物仍然遍佈世界各地 , 似乎無法從過去的經驗中獲利 。
the mangroves are being cut down ; the effects of things like the tsunami get worse .	紅樹林正在被砍伐 ; 海嘯的影響越來越嚴重 。
we've talked about the soil erosion .	我們已經談過土壤侵蝕 ,
we have the reckless burning of fossil fuels along with other greenhouse gasses , so called , leading to climate change .	我們和其他溫室氣體一起燃燒化石燃料 , 所以被稱為 , 導致氣候變遷 。
finally , all around the world , people have begun to believe that there is something going on very wrong with our climate .	最後 , 全世界 , 人們開始相信我們的氣候有問題 。
all around the world climates are mixed up .	世界各地的氣候都混雜在一起
and it's the poor people who are affected worse .	而且是那些受影響較差的窮人
it's africa that already is affected .	就是非洲已經受到影響 。
in many parts of subsaharan africa , the droughts are so much worse .	在撒哈拉以南非洲的許多地區 , 乾旱情況更糟糕 。
and when the rain does come , it so often leads to flooding and added distress , and the cycle of poverty and hunger and disease .	當雨量來臨時 , 通常會導致洪水和苦惱 , 還有貧窮、飢餓和疾病的循環 。
and the numbers of people living in an area that the land cannot support , who are too poor to buy food , who can't move away because the whole land is degraded .	而居住在一個土地無法支援的地區的人數 , 他們太貧窮 , 無法購買食物 , 無法搬走 , 因為整片土地都被分解了 。
and so you get desertification creeping , creeping , creeping as the last of the trees are cut down .	所以 , 沙漠化繁衍、令人毛骨悚然、令人毛骨悚然 , 因為最後一棵樹被砍伐了 。
and this kind of thing is not just in africa . it's all over the world .	而這種東西不只在非洲 , 在世界各地
so it wasn't surprising to me that as i was traveling around the world i met so many young people who seemed to have lost hope .	所以 , 我並不意外 , 當我在世界各地旅行時 , 我遇見了許多看似失去希望的年輕人 。
we seem to have lost wisdom , the wisdom of the indigenous people .	我們似乎失去了智慧 , 原住民的智慧 。
i asked a question . " why ? "	我問了一個問題: 「 為什麼 ? 」
well , do you think there could be some kind of disconnect between this extraordinarily clever brain , the kind of brain that the ted technologies exemplify , and the human heart ? talking about it in the nonscientific term , in terms of love and compassion . is there some disconnect ?	嗯 , 你認為在這種極端聰明的大腦之間 , 可能有某種不一致的區別 , 那種被ted科技展現出來的大腦 , 和人類的心臟 ? 用非科學的術語來說 , 用愛和同情的角度來談 , 是否有些斷歧視 ?
and these young people , when i talk to them , basically they were either depressed or apathetic , or bitter and angry . and they said more or less the same thing , " we feel this way because we feel you've compromised our future and there's nothing we can do about it . "	而這些年輕人 , 當我和他們談話時 , 基本上他們是憂鬱的 , 或冷淡的 , 或苦痛和生氣的 。 他們說 , 或多或少是一樣的 , 「 我們有這種感覺 , 因為我們覺得你已經妥協了我們的未來 , 而我們卻無能為力 。 」
we have compromised their future .	我們已經妥協了他們的未來 。
i've got three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them and i think how we've harmed this beautiful planet since i was their age , i feel this desperation .	我有三個小孫子 , 每一次我看著他們 , 我就會想 , 我們如何在自從他們年紀開始 , 傷害這個美麗的星球 , 我就感到絕望 。
and that led to this program we call roots and shoots , which began right here in tanzania and has now spread to 97 countries around the world .	這就導致了我們稱之為根與芽的計畫 , 這計畫始於坦尚尼亞 , 現在已經擴散到全世界97個國家 。
it's symbolic . roots make a firm foundation .	具有象徵意義 , 根建立了堅定的基礎
shoots seem tiny ; to reach the sun they can break through a brick wall .	射擊似乎很小 ; 為了到達太陽 , 它們可以穿過磚牆 。
see the brick wall as all these problems we've inflicted on the planet , environmental and social . it's a message of hope .	把磚牆視為地球上所有的這些問題 , 環境和社交 。 這是希望的訊息 。
hundreds and thousands of young people around the world can break through and can make this a better world for all living things .	全世界有成千上萬的年輕人可以突破 , 可以為所有生物創造出更好的世界 。
the most important message of roots and shoots: every single one of us makes a difference , every single day .	根與芽的最重要的訊息:我們每一個人都會做出改變 , 每一天 。
we have a choice . every one of us in this room , we have a choice as to what kind of difference we want to make .	我們有選擇 。 在座的每一位 , 我們都有選擇要做出什麼樣的改變 。
the very poor have no choice . it's up to us to change things so that the poor have choice as well .	窮人沒有選擇 。 要靠我們去改變事情 , 這樣窮人也能選擇 。
the roots and shoots groups all choose three projects .	根與芽的團體全都選擇三個項目
it depends on how old they are , and which country , whether they're in a city or rural , as to what kinds of projects .	這取決於他們年齡多大 , 以及哪個國家 , 不論他們在哪個城市或鄉村 , 都要看哪些計畫 。
but basically , we have programs now from preschool right through university , with more and more adults starting their own roots and shoots groups .	但基本上 , 我們現在有來自幼兒園的方案 , 透過大學 , 有越來越多的成人開始他們自己的根與芽 。
and every group chooses , between them , three different kinds of project to make this a better world , recognizing that all these different problems are interconnected and impinge on each other .	而每一個團體都選擇 , 在它們之間 , 三種不同的計畫 , 來讓這個世界更美好 , 認識到所有這些不同的問題都是互相關聯的 , 並互相衝突 。
so one of their projects will be to help their own human community .	所以 , 他們的一個計畫將是幫助他們自己的人類社群 。
and then , if they're able , they may raise money to help communities in other parts of the world .	然後 , 如果他們能的話 , 他們可能會籌集資金來幫助世界其他地區的社區 。
one of their projects will be to help animals not just wildlife , domestic animals as well .	他們的其中一個計畫是幫助動物不僅是野生動物 , 家禽也一樣 。
and one of their projects will be to help the environment that we all share .	他們的計畫之一就是幫助我們共同的環境 。
and woven throughout all of this is a message of learning to live in peace and harmony within ourselves , in our families , in our communities , between nations , between cultures , between religions and between us and the natural world .	在這一切中 , 編織出的訊息是:學習生活在和平與和諧中在我們自己、在我們的家庭、在我們的社區中、在國家之間、文化之間、宗教之間、在我們和自然世界之間 。
we need the natural world . we cannot go on destroying it at the rate we are .	我們需要自然世界 。 我們不能以我們現在的速度破壞它 。
we not do have more than this one planet .	我們沒有比這個星球還多 。
just picking one or two of the projects right here in africa that the roots and shoots groups are doing , one or two projects only in tanzania , in uganda , kenya , south africa , congobrazzaville , sierra leone , cameroon and other groups . and as i say , it's in 97 countries around the world .	只要挑選一個或兩個在非洲的項目 , 即根與芽的團體正在進行 , 一兩個項目只有在坦尚尼亞、烏干達、肯亞、南非、剛果巴拉薩克、獅子山共和國、喀麥隆和其他團體中 。 如我所說的 , 它位於世界各地97個國家 。
of course , they're planting trees . they're growing organic vegetables .	當然 , 他們在種植樹木 。 他們在種有機蔬菜 。
they're working in the refugee camps , with chickens and selling the eggs for a little amount of money , or just using them to feed their families , and feeling a sense of pride and empowerment , because they're no longer helpless and depending on others with their vegetables and their chickens .	他們在難民營裡工作 , 帶著雞和賣蛋 , 只用一點點錢 , 或僅僅用它們來餵飽家人 , 感受到一種自豪和賦權的感覺 , 因為他們不再無助 , 依賴他人 , 靠他們的蔬菜和雞隻 。
it's being used in uganda to give some psychological help to exchild soldiers .	它被用在烏干達 , 給予一些心理上的幫助 , 讓士兵外出 。
doing projects like this is bringing them out of themselves .	做像這樣的計畫是把他們從自己身上帶走 。
once again , they're useful members of society .	再一次 , 他們是有用的社會成員 。
we have this program in prisons as well .	我們在監獄也有這個計畫 。
so , there's no time for more roots and shoots now .	所以 , 現在沒有更多根與芽的時間了 。
but oh , they're also working on hiv/aids .	但 , 喔 , 他們也在研究愛滋病 。
that's a very important component of roots and shoots , with older kids talking to younger ones .	那是根與芽的重要成份 , 年紀較大的孩子和較年輕的孩子談話 。
and unwanted pregnancies and things like that , which young people listen to better from other youth , rather than adults .	沒有懷孕之類的事 , 年輕人會傾聽其他年輕人的傾聽 , 而不是成年人 。
hope . that's the question i get asked as i'm going around the world: " jane , you've seen so many terrible things , you've seen your chimpanzees decrease in number from about one million , at the turn of the century , to no more than 150 , 000 now , and the same with so many other animals .	希望 。 這就是我在世界各地被問到的問題: 「 珍 , 你看過這麼多可怕的東西 , 你看到你的黑猩猩數量減少 , 從本世紀開始 , 大約有一百萬隻 , 到現在沒有超過十五萬隻 , 和許多其他動物一樣 。
forests disappearing , deserts where once there was forest .	森林消失 , 曾經有森林的沙漠 。
do you really have hope ? " well , yes .	你真的有希望嗎 ? 」 嗯 , 是的 。
you can't come to a conference like ted and not have hope , can you ?	你不能來參加ted這樣的會議 , 也不能沒有希望 , 你能嗎 ?
and of course , there's hope . one is this amazing human brain .	當然 , 還有希望 。 一個是這個驚人的人類大腦 。
and i mean , think of the technologies .	我的意思是 , 想想科技 。
and i've just been so thrilled , finally , to come to people talking about compost latrines .	我終於很興奮 , 終於 , 來到人們談起堆肥式廁所 。
it's one of my hobbyhorses .	它是我的一個嗜好者 。
we just flush all this water down the lavatory , it's terrible .	我們只是把所有這些水都沖下了廁所 , 很糟糕 。
and then talking about renewable energy desperately important .	接著 , 談到再生能源 , 迫切地重要 。
do we care about the planet for our children ?	我們是否關心孩子的地球 ?
how many of us have children or grandchildren , nieces , nephews ?	有多少人有小孩或孫子、姪子、姪子 ?
do we care about their future ?	我們關心他們的未來嗎 ?
and if we care about their future , we , as the elite around the world , we can do something about it . we can make choices as to how we live each day .	如果我們關心他們的未來 , 我們身為世界各地的菁英 , 我們可以為此做點什麼 。 我們可以為我們每天的生活方式做出選擇 。
what we buy . what we wear .	我們買什麼 。 我們穿什麼 。
and choose to make these choices with the question , how will this affect the environment around me ?	而選擇用問題來做出這些選擇 , 這會如何影響我周遭的環境 ?
how will it affect the life of my child when he or she grows up ?	當他或她長大後 , 會如何影響我孩子的生活 ?
or my grandchild , or whatever it is .	或是我的孫子 , 或不論如何 ,
so the human brain , coupled with the human heart , and we join hands around the world .	所以 , 人類的大腦 , 與人類的心結合 , 我們加入世界各地的手 。
and that's what ted is helping so well with , and google who help us , and esri are helping us with mapping in gombe national park .	這也是ted能幫上忙的 , 還有google幫助我們 , esri也在幫我們繪製gmbe國家公園的地圖 。
all of these technologies we can use .	所有這些我們可以使用的科技
now let's link them , and it's beginning to happen , isn't it ?	現在讓我們把它們連結起來 , 開始發生了 , 不是嗎 ?
you've heard about it this afternoon . it's beginning to happen .	今天下午你已經聽說過了 , 開始發生了
this change , this change . to see change that we must have if we care about the future .	這種改變 , 這種改變 。 要看到我們必須要有的改變 , 如果我們關心未來 。
and the next reason for hope nature is amazingly resilient .	希望大自然的下一個理由是驚人的韌性 。
you can take an area that's absolutely destroyed , with time and perhaps some help it can regenerate .	你可以把一個絕對被破壞的區域 , 隨著時間 , 或許還有一些幫助 , 它可以再生 。
and an example is the tacare program .	其中一個例子是 「 計劃 」 。
