i told you , where a seemingly dead tree stump if you stop hacking them for firewood , which you don't need to because you have wood lots , then in five years you can have a 30foot tree .	我跟你說 , 如果你停止駭進樹木 , 那你就不需要因為你有木材 , 那麼在五年內 , 你就可以有一棵30英尺高的樹 。
and animals , almost on the brink of extinction , can be given a second chance . that's my next book .	而動物 , 幾乎在滅絕的邊緣 , 可以給第二次機會 。 那是我的下一本書 。
it's inspiring . and it brings me to my last category of hope , and we've heard about this so much in the last two days: this indomitable human spirit . this determination of people , the resilience of the human spirit , so that people who you would think would be battered by poverty , or disease , or whatever , can pull themselves up out of it , sometimes with a helping hand , and take their part in society , and take their part in changing the world .	它鼓舞人心 。 它帶給我最後一類的希望 , 我們在過去兩天中都聽說過這一點:這種不屈不撓的人類精神 。 這個人類精神的決心 , 人類精神的恢復力 , 讓那些你認為會被貧窮、疾病所影響的人 , 或其他的人們 , 可以把自己從中拉出來 , 有時用手協助 , 拿走他們在社會中的一部分 , 讓他們成為改變世界的一份子 。
and just to think of one or two people out of africa who are just really inspiring .	想想看 , 在非洲有一兩個人真的很鼓舞人心 。
we could make a very long list , but obviously nelson mandela , emerging from 17 years of hard physical labor , 23 years of imprisonment , with this amazing ability to forgive , so that he could lead his nation out the evil regime of apartheid without a bloodbath .	我們可以列出很長的清單 , 但顯然是納爾遜•曼德拉 , 從十七年辛苦的體力勞動中湧現出來 , 23年的監禁 , 用這種驚人的寬恕能力 , 讓他可以帶領他的國家脫離種族隔離 , 沒有血巴 。
ken sarowiwa , in nigeria , who took on the giant oil companies , and although people around the world tried their best , was executed .	kensarowiwa , 在奈及利亞 , 他們採用巨型石油公司 , 雖然全世界的人都竭盡全力 , 卻被處決了 。
people like this are so inspirational .	像這樣的人是如此鼓舞人心 。
people like this are the role models we need for young africans .	像這樣的人是我們年輕非洲人所需要的榜樣 。
and we need some environmental role models as well , and i've been hearing some of them today .	我們也需要一些環境的榜樣 , 我今天一直聽到其中的一些 。
so i'm really grateful for this opportunity to share this message again , with everyone at ted .	所以我真的很感激這個機會再次分享這個訊息 , 和ted的每個人一起 。
and i hope that some of us can get together and talk about some of these things , especially the roots and shoots program .	我希望我們當中的一些人能聚在一起 , 談談其中的一些事 , 特別是根與芽的計畫 。
and just a last word on that the young woman who's running this entire conference center , i met her today .	最後一個字 , 就是這個經營這整個會議中心的年輕女子 , 我今天遇到了她 。
she came up so excited , with her certificate . she was [in] roots and shoots .	她很興奮 , 帶著她的證書 , 她是根與芽 。
she was in the leadership in dar es salaam .	她在達爾斯薩拉姆的領導階層
she said it's helped her to do what she's doing .	她說這可以幫助她做她正在做的事 。
and it was very , very exciting for me to meet her and see just one example of how young people , when they are empowered , given the opportunity to take action , to make the world a better place , truly are our hope for tomorrow .	我非常非常興奮 , 能見到她 , 能看到其中一個例子 , 說明年輕人是如何被賦予權力 , 因為有機會採取行動 , 讓世界變得更美好 , 真正是我們明天的希望 。
artist dianna cohen shares some tough truths about plastic pollution in the ocean and in our lives and some thoughts on how to free ourselves from the plastic gyre .	藝術家黛安娜•柯恩分享了一些艱難的真相 , 關於海洋中的塑膠污染 , 以及我們生活中的一些思想 , 關於如何解放我們自己 , 脫離塑膠漩渦 。
consumerism , global issues , green , mission blue , oceans , plastic	消費主義、全球議題、綠色、使命藍、海洋、塑膠等 。
dianna cohen: tough truths about plastic pollution	黛安娜•科恩:關於塑膠污染的艱難真相 。
i'm a visual artist , and i'm also one of the cofounders of the plastic pollution coalition .	我是視覺藝術家 , 我也是塑膠污染聯盟的共同創辦人之一 。
i've been working with plastic bags , which i cut up and sew back together as my primary material for my artwork for the last 20 years .	我一直在和塑膠袋合作 , 我把塑膠袋剪起來 , 縫合起來 , 作為我過去二十年來的主要材料 。
i turn them into two and threedimensional pieces and sculptures and installations .	我把它們變成二維三維的片段 , 雕塑和裝置 。
upon working with the plastic , after about the first eight years , some of my work started to fissure and break down into smaller little bits of plastic .	在和塑膠一起工作後 , 大約在前八年 , 我的一些作品開始裂縫 , 分解成更小的一點塑膠 。
and i thought , " great .	我心想: 「 太好了 。
it's ephemeral just like us . "	和我們一樣是短暫的 。 」
upon educating myself a little further about plastics , i actually realized this was a bad thing .	在我更進一步教育自己塑膠時 , 我發現這是件壞事 。
it's a bad thing that plastic breaks down into smaller little bits , because it's always still plastic .	塑膠分解成小塊的壞東西 , 因為它總是塑膠 。
and what we're finding is that a lot of it is in the marine environment .	我們發現 , 很多都在海洋環境中 。
i then , in the last few years , learned about the pacific garbage patch and the gyre .	接著 , 在過去幾年 , 我學到了太平洋垃圾堆和垃圾桶 。
and my initial reaction and i think this is a lot of people's first reaction to learning about it is , " oh my god !	而我的初步反應我認為這是很多人的第一反應就是 「 天啊 !
we've got to go out there and clean this thing up . "	我們得走出去 , 把這個東西清乾淨 。 」
so i actually developed a proposal to go out with a cargo ship and two decommissioned fishing trawlers , a crane , a chipping machine and a coldmolding machine .	所以 , 我發展出了一個提案 , 要和一艘貨運船和兩艘退役的捕魚拖網、一座起重機、一台洋芋片機和一台冷模機一起出去 。
and my intention was to go out to the gyre , raise awareness about this issue and begin to pick up the plastic , chip it into little bits and cold mold it into bricks that could potentially be used as building materials in underdeveloped communities .	我的意圖是去健身房 , 提高對這個議題的認知 , 開始拿起塑膠 , 將它切成一小塊 , 然後冷模 , 變成磚塊 , 可以用在未開發的社區中 。
i began talking with people who actually had been out to the gyre and were studying the plastic problem in the marine environment and upon doing so , i realized actually that cleaning it up would be a very small drop in the bucket relative to how much is being generated every day around the world , and that actually i needed to back up and look at the bigger picture .	我開始和實際去過健身房的人談話 , 正在研究海洋環境中的塑膠問題 , 並且在做這件事時 , 我意識到 , 將它們清理乾淨 , 相對於全世界每天產出的量 , 會是很小的一滴 , 其實我需要回頭看看更大的圖像 。
and the bigger picture is: we need to find a way to turn off the faucet .	更大的情況是:我們需要找到方法來關掉水龍頭 。
we need to cut the spigot of singleuse and disposable plastics , which are entering the marine environment every day on a global scale .	我們需要切斷單一使用和丟棄的塑膠 , 這些塑膠每天都在全球範圍內進入海洋環境 。
so in looking at that , i also realized that i was really angry .	所以 , 看著這個 , 我也了解到 , 我真的很生氣 。
i wasn't just concerned about plastic that you're trying to imagine out in the middle of the pacific ocean of which i have learned there are now 11 gyres , potentially , of plastic in five major oceans in the world .	我不只關心塑膠 , 你還在想 , 在太平洋中間我所學到的 , 現在有11個塑膠漩渦 , 可能是世界上五大洋的塑膠 。
it's not just that gyre of plastic that i'm concerned about it's the gyre of plastic in the supermarket .	不只是我所關心的塑膠垃圾漩渦是超市裡塑膠的漩渦
i'd go to the supermarket and all of my food is packaged in plastic .	我會去超市 , 我所有的食物都是用塑膠包裝的 。
all of my beverages are packaged in plastic , even at the health food market .	我所有的飲料都包在塑膠中 , 甚至在健康食品市場 。
i'm also concerned about the plastic in the refrigerator , and i'm concerned about the plastic and the toxins that leach from plastic into us and into our bodies .	我也很關心冰箱裡的塑膠 , 我關心的是塑膠和毒素從塑膠滲透到我們體內 , 進到我們體內 。
so i came together with a group of other people who were all looking at this issue , and we created the plastic pollution coalition .	所以我和其他一群人聚在一起 , 他們全都在探討這個議題 , 我們創造了塑膠污染聯盟 。
we have many initiatives that we're working on , but some of them are very basic .	我們有很多我們正在進行的倡議 , 但有些是非常基本的 。
one is: if 80 to 90 percent of what we're finding in the ocean of the marine debris that we're finding in the ocean is plastic , then why don't we call it what it is .	其一是:如果我們在海洋中發現的海洋碎片中 , 有80%到90%都是塑膠 , 那我們為什麼不把它叫做它 。
recycling everybody kind of ends their books about being sustainable and greening with the idea of recycling .	回收每個人的書終結了他們關於永續和綠化的書 , 用的是回收的概念 。
you put something in a bin and you don't have to think about it again .	你把某樣東西放進一個桶子裡 , 不用再想了 。
what is the reality of that ?	真正的現實是什麼 ?
in the united states , less than seven percent of our plastics are recycled .	在美國 , 我們的塑膠回收率不到7% 。
and if you really look into it , particularly when it comes to plastic bottles , most of it is only downcycled , or incinerated , or shipped to china .	如果你真的深入研究 , 尤其是當談到塑膠瓶時 , 大部分只會被下降或被燒掉 , 或被運送到中國 。
it is downcycled and turned into lesser things , while a glass bottle can be a glass bottle again or can be used again a plastic bottle can never be a plastic bottle again .	它被降低 , 被轉化為更少的東西 , 而玻璃瓶可以再次變成玻璃瓶 , 或是再次使用塑膠瓶 , 不能再變成塑膠瓶 。
so this is a big issue for us .	所以這對我們來說是個大問題 。
another thing that we're looking at and asking people to think about is we've added a fourth r onto the front of the " reduce , reuse , recycle , " three r's , and that is refuse .	另一件我們看著並要求人們思考的事是 , 我們在 「 減量、再利用、回收再利用 」 前面加了第四個r , 那就是拒絕 。
whenever possible , refuse singleuse and disposable plastics .	不論何時 , 都拒絕使用和丟棄的塑膠 。
alternatives exist ; some of them are very oldschool .	替代方案存在 ; 有些是很老派的 。
i myself am now collecting these cool pyrex containers and using those instead of glad and tupperware containers to store food in .	我現在正在收集這些很酷的pyrex容器 , 並用那些取代玻璃和tupupware容器來儲存食物 。
and i know that i am doing a service to myself and my family .	我知道我在為自己和我的家人做服務 。
it's very easy to pick up a stainlesssteel bottle or a glass bottle , if you're traveling and you've forgotten to bring your stainlesssteel bottle and fill that up with water or filtered water , versus purchasing plastic bottled water .	很容易撿起一瓶不銹鋼瓶或玻璃瓶 , 如果你在旅行時 , 卻忘了帶著不銹鋼瓶 , 裝滿水或過濾水 , 而不是用塑膠瓶裝水 。
i guess what i want to say to everybody here and i know that you guys know a lot about this issue is that this is a huge problem in the oceans , but this is a problem that we've created as consumers and we can solve .	我猜我想對在座的各位說 , 我知道你們對這個議題了解很多 , 是因為這在海洋中是個很大的問題 , 但這是個我們身為消費者所創造的問題 , 且我們能解決的問題 。
we can solve this by raising awareness of the issue and teaching people to choose alternatives .	我們可以藉由提高對議題的意識 , 來教導人們選擇替代方案 。
so whenever possible , to choose alternatives to singleuse plastics .	所以 , 不論何時 , 若要選擇使用塑膠的替代品 。
we can cut the stem tide the stem of this into our oceans and in doing so , save our oceans , save our planet , save ourselves .	我們可以把幹細胞的潮汐切割成海洋 , 這樣 , 拯救海洋 , 拯救我們的地球 , 拯救我們自己 。
this demo from pattie maes' lab at mit , spearheaded by pranav mistry was the buzz of ted . it's a wearable device with a projector that paves the way for profound interaction with our environment . imagine " minority report " and then some .	這個例子來自麻省理工學院的帕蒂梅斯的實驗室 , 由帕納•佛特利所製作的 , 是ted的公牛 。 它是一個可穿戴的裝置 , 和一個投影機一起鋪設了深刻與我們環境互動的路 。 想像一下 「 少數報告 」 , 接著 , 一些 。
demo , design , interface design , technology	展示、設計、介面設計、科技
pattie maes and pranav mistry demo sixthsense	派蒂夫•梅斯和帕納•米瑞•狄摩爾第十六感 。
i've been intrigued by this question of whether we could evolve or develop a sixth sense a sense that would give us seamless access and easy access to metainformation or information that may exist somewhere that may be relevant to help us make the right decision about whatever it is that we're coming across .	我對這個問題很感興趣:我們能否進化或發展出第六感──一種能讓我們無縫接觸 , 容易取得新陳代謝或資訊 , 可能存在於某處 , 協助我們做出正確的決策 , 決定我們要面對的是什麼 。
and some of you may argue , well , don't today's cell phones do that already ?	你們之中有些人可能會爭論 , 嗯 , 今天的手機還沒做到嗎 ?
but i would say no .	但我會說不 。
when you meet someone here at ted and this is the top networking place , of course , of the year you don't shake somebody's hand and then say , " can you hold on for a moment while i take out my phone and google you ? "	當你在ted這裡遇見一個人 , 這是最頂尖的網絡 , 當然 , 在那一年裡 , 你不會和某人握手 , 然後說: 「 你能在我拿出手機的時候 , 緊緊握住一會兒嗎 ? 」
or when you go to the supermarket and you're standing there in that huge aisle of different types of toilet papers , you don't take out your cell phone , and open a browser , and go to a website to try to decide which of these different toilet papers is the most ecologically responsible purchase to make .	或者 , 當你去超市的時候 , 你站在那兒 , 用不同類型的衛生紙 , 你不會拿出你的手機 , 然後打開瀏覽器 , 然後去一個網站 , 試著決定這些不同的衛生紙是哪一個最環保的購買方式 。
so we don't really have easy access to all this relevant information that can just help us make optimal decisions about what to do next and what actions to take .	所以 , 我們不太容易取得這些相關的資訊 , 只能協助我們做出最佳的決定 , 決定下一步該做什麼 , 以及該採取什麼行動 。
and so my research group at the media lab has been developing a series of inventions to give us access to this information in a sort of easy way , without requiring that the user changes any of their behavior .	所以 , 我在媒體實驗室的研究小組正在研發一系列的發明 , 讓我們能用很簡單的方式取得這些資訊 , 不需要使用者改變他們的行為 。
and i'm here to unveil our latest effort , and most successful effort so far , which is still very much a work in process .	我是來揭開我們最新的努力 , 到目前為止 , 最成功的努力 , 這還是很有用的過程 。
i'm actually wearing the device right now and we've sort of cobbled it together with components that are off the shelf and that , by the way , only cost 350 dollars at this point in time .	我現在正穿著這個裝置 , 我們將它和架子外面的零件一起組合 , 順便說一下 , 目前只需350美元 。
i'm wearing a camera , just a simple webcam , a portable , batterypowered projection system with a little mirror .	我戴著攝影機 , 只是一個簡單的網路攝影機 , 一個可攜帶的電池動力投影系統 , 帶著一面小鏡子 。
these components communicate to my cell phone in my pocket which acts as the communication and computation device .	這些零件向我口袋裡的手機溝通 , 作為溝通和計算設備 。
and in the video here we see my student pranav mistry , who's really the genius who's been implementing and designing this whole system .	在影片中 , 我們看到我的學生panavmetry , 他是真正在執行和設計這整個系統的天才 。
and we see how this system lets him walk up to any surface and start using his hands to interact with the information that is projected in front of him .	我們看到這個系統如何讓他走到任何表面 , 開始用他的手和他面前投射的資訊互動 。
the system tracks the four significant fingers .	系統追蹤了四個重要手指
in this case , he's wearing simple marker caps that you may recognize .	在這個例子中 , 他戴著你可能認得的簡單標記帽 。
but if you want a more stylish version you could also paint your nails in different colors .	但如果你想要一個更時髦的版本 , 你也可以把你的指甲塗上不同的顏色 。
and the camera basically tracks these four fingers and recognizes any gestures that he's making so he can just go to , for example , a map of long beach , zoom in and out , etc .	相機基本上追蹤了這四個手指並且辨認出他製作的任何手勢 , 這樣他就可以直接去舉例來說 , 一張長灘的地圖 , 放大和放大等等 。
the system also recognizes iconic gestures such as the " take a picture " gesture , and then takes a picture of whatever is in front of you .	系統也會辨識出有代表性的手勢例如 「 拍照 」 手勢 , 然後拍下你面前的任何東西 。
and when he then walks back to the media lab , he can just go up to any wall and project all the pictures that he's taken , sort through them and organize them , and resize them , etc . , again using all natural gestures .	當他走回媒體實驗室時 , 他可以走到任何一面牆上 , 投影出他所拍攝的所有照片 , 分析它們 , 整理它們 , 再次利用自然的手勢 , 將它們重新調整 。
so , some of you most likely were here two years ago and saw the demo by jeff han or some of you may think , " well , doesn't this look like the microsoft surface table ? "	所以 , 你們當中有些人可能兩年前就在這裡 , 看到傑夫•漢的示範 , 或你們有些人可能會想: 「 這不是看起來像微軟的表面桌子嗎 ? 」
and yes , you also interact using natural gestures , both hands , etc .	是的 , 你也用自然的手勢來互動 , 雙手等等 。
but the difference here is that you can use any surface , you can walk to up to any surface , including your hand if nothing else is available and interact with this projected data .	但這裡的不同是 , 你可以用任何表面 , 你可以走到任何表面 , 包括你的手 , 如果沒有其他東西可以取得 , 和這個投影的資料互動 。
the device is completely portable , and can be . . .	裝置是完全可攜式的 , 而且可以是...
so one important difference is that it's totally mobile .	一個重要的不同點是 , 它完全是移動式的 。
another even more important difference is that in mass production this would not cost more tomorrow than today's cell phones and would actually not sort of be a bigger packaging could look a lot more stylish than this version that i'm wearing around my neck .	另一個更重要的不同是 , 在大量生產中 , 明天不會比現在的手機費用高出許多 , 實際上不是一個更大的包裝 , 看起來會比我戴在脖子上的這個版本更時髦 。
but other than letting some of you live out your fantasy of looking as cool as tom cruise in " minority report , " the reason why we're really excited about this device is that it really can act as one of these sixthsense devices that gives you relevant information about whatever is in front of you .	但 , 除了讓你們其中一些人活出幻想 , 在 「 少數報告 」 中 , 湯姆克魯斯看起來很酷 , 我們對這個裝置感到很興奮的原因是 , 它真的可以扮演這六感裝置之一 , 讓你對眼前的資訊有所相關性 。
so we see pranav here going into the supermarket and he's shopping for some paper towels .	我們可以看到帕納走進超市 , 他在購物一些紙巾 。
and , as he picks up a product the system can recognize the product that he's picking up , using either image recognition or marker technology , and give him the green light or an orange light .	當他拿起產品時 , 系統可以辨認出他拿起的產品 , 使用影像辨識或標記技術 , 然後給他綠光或橘色的光 。
he can ask for additional information .	他可以尋求額外的資訊
so this particular choice here is a particularly good choice , given his personal criteria .	所以 , 這個特別的選擇 , 根據他個人的標準 , 是一個很好的選擇 。
some of you may want the toilet paper with the most bleach in it rather than the most ecologicallyresponsible choice .	有些人可能會想要衛生紙中最白斑的 , 而不是最環保的選擇 。
if he picks up a book in the bookstore , he can get an amazon rating it gets projected right on the cover of the book .	如果他在書店裡拿起一本書 , 他就能得到亞馬遜的評分 , 它會被投射在書的封面上 。
this is juan's book , our previous speaker , which gets a great rating , by the way , at amazon .	這是胡安的書 , 我們之前的演講者 , 順帶一提 , 在亞馬遜 , 得到很好的評分 。
and so , pranav turns the page of the book and can then see additional information about the book reader comments , maybe sort of information by his favorite critic , etc .	所以 , 帕納把書的頁面翻過來 , 再看到關於書讀者評論的額外資訊 , 也許是他最喜歡的評論家的資訊 , 等等 。
if he turns to a particular page he finds an annotation by maybe an expert of a friend of ours that gives him a little bit of additional information about whatever is on that particular page .	如果他轉到某個特定的頁面 , 他會發現我們朋友的註解 , 給他一些關於那特定頁面上的資訊 。
reading the newspaper it never has to be outdated .	閱讀報紙──它永遠不用過時 。
you can get video annotations of the event that you're reading about you can get the latest sports scores etc .	你可以得到你正在閱讀的事件的影片註解--你可以得到最新的運動分數等等 。
this is a more controversial one .	這是更具爭議性的
as you interact with someone at ted , maybe you can see a word cloud of the tags , the words that are associated with that person in their blog and personal web pages .	當你在ted和某人互動時 , 也許你可以看到一個字的標籤雲 , 和那個人在部落格和個人網頁裡的文字連結在一起 。
in this case , the student is interested in cameras , etc .	在這個例子中 , 學生對攝影機感興趣 , 等等 。
on your way to the airport , if you pick up your boarding pass , it can tell you that your flight is delayed , that the gate has changed , etc .	在你前往機場的路上 , 如果你拿起你的登機證 , 它可以告訴你 , 你的飛行被延遲了 , 大門已經改變了 , 等等 。
and , if you need to know what the current time is it's as simple as drawing a watch on your arm .	而且 , 如果你需要知道現在的時間是什麼 , 就跟在手臂上畫一支手錶一樣簡單 。
so that's where we're at so far in developing this sixth sense that would give us seamless access to all this relevant information about the things that we may come across .	所以 , 這就是我們目前正在發展的第六感 , 讓我們能取得所有我們可能遇到的相關資訊 。
my student pranav , who's really , like i said , the genius behind this .	我的學生帕納 , 他真的像我說的 , 這背後的天才
he does deserve a lot of applause because i don't think he's slept much in the last three months , actually .	他的確應得很多掌聲 , 因為我認為在過去三個月裡他睡的不多 。
and his girlfriend is probably not very happy about him either .	他的女朋友也可能對他不太滿意 。
but it's not perfect yet , it's very much a work in progress .	但還不夠完美 , 進展非常多 。
and who knows , maybe in another 10 years we'll be here with the ultimate sixth sense brain implant .	又有誰知道 , 也許在接下來的十年中 , 我們會帶著終極第六感的大腦植入到這裡 。
phyllis rodriguez and aicha elwafi have a powerful friendship born of unthinkable loss . rodriguez' son was killed in the world trade center attacks on september 11 , 2001 ; elwafi's son zacarias moussaoui was convicted of a role in those attacks and is serving a life sentence . in hoping to find peace , these two moms have come to understand and respect one another .	菲利斯•羅德里格和艾卡•埃爾瓦菲有一個強大的友誼 , 誕生於難以想像的損失中 。 羅德里茲的兒子在世貿中心被殺害 , 在2001年9月11日的世貿攻擊中 , 埃爾瓦菲的兒子穆薩洛伊被定罪 , 在這些攻擊中扮演著一種生活句子 。 希望能找到和平 , 這兩位母親來互相了解和尊重 。
culture , global issues , politics	文化、全球議題、政治、
9/11 healing: the mothers who found forgiveness , friendship	911療癒:找到原諒的母親 , 友誼的母親 。
phyllis rodriguez: we are here today because of the fact that we have what most people consider an unusual friendship .	菲莉斯•羅德里格斯:我們今天在這裡 , 是因為我們有多數人認為不尋常的友誼 。
and yet , it feels natural to us now .	然而 , 現在對我們來說 , 這感覺很自然 。
i first learned that my son had been in the world trade center on the morning of september 11th , 2001 .	我第一次得知我兒子在2001年9月11日的世貿中心
we didn't know if he had perished yet until 36 hours later .	我們不知道他是否已經死了 , 直到36小時後 ,
at the time , we knew that it was political .	當時 , 我們知道那是政治的 。
we were afraid of what our country was going to do in the name of our son my husband , orlando , and i and our family .	我們害怕我們的國家要做什麼 , 以我們的兒子之名──我的丈夫 , 奧蘭多 , 還有我們的家人 。
and when i saw it and yet , through the shock , the terrible shock , and the terrible explosion in our lives , literally , we were not vengeful .	當我看到它 , 然而 , 透過震驚 , 恐怖的震驚 , 以及我們生命中可怕的爆炸 , 真的 , 我們並沒有被復仇 。
and a couple of weeks later when zacarias moussaoui was indicted on six counts of conspiracy to commit terrorism , and the u . s . government called for a death penalty for him , if convicted , my husband and i spoke out in opposition to that , publicly .	幾週後 , zacariasmoussaoui被指控有六個陰謀要犯恐怖主義 , 而美國政府要求對他判處死刑 , 如果被定罪 , 我和我的丈夫公開反對 。
through that and through human rights groups , we were brought together with several other victims' families .	透過這些和透過人權團體 , 我們和其他幾個受害者的家人聚在一起 。
when i saw aicha in the media , coming over when her son was indicted , and i thought , " what a brave woman .	當我看到aicha在媒體上 , 出現在她兒子被指控時 , 我心想: 「 多麼勇敢的女人啊 。
someday i want to meet that woman when i'm stronger . "	有一天 , 我更強壯的時候 , 我想見見那個女人 。 」
i was still in deep grief ; i knew i didn't have the strength .	我還在深深的悲慟中 ; 我知道我沒有那份力量 。
i knew i would find her someday , or we would find each other .	我知道有一天我會找到她 , 或者我們會找到彼此 。
because , when people heard that my son was a victim , i got immediate sympathy .	因為 , 當人們聽到我的兒子是受害者時 , 我得到了立即的同情 。
but when people learned what her son was accused of , she didn't get that sympathy .	但當人們知道她的兒子被指控了什麼 , 她沒有得到那個同情 。
but her suffering is equal to mine .	但她的苦難與我是平等的
so we met in november 2002 , and aicha will now tell you how that came about .	我們在2002年11月見面 , aicha會告訴你這是怎麼來的 。
aicha elwafi: good afternoon , ladies and gentlemen .	aichaelwafi:午安 , 女士們先生們
i am the mother of zacarias moussaoui .	我是zacariasmoussaoui的母親 。
and i asked the organization of human rights to put me in touch with the parents of the victims .	我要求人權組織讓我與受害者的父母聯絡 。
so they introduced me to five families .	所以他們介紹我給五個家庭
and i saw phyllis , and i watched her .	我看到phyllis , 我看著她
she was the only mother in the group .	她是群體中唯一的母親 。
the others were brothers , sisters .	其他的則是兄弟姊妹
and i saw in her eyes that she was a mother , just like me .	我在她眼中看到她是母親 , 就像我一樣 。
i suffered a lot as a mother .	我身為母親所苦許多 。
i was married when i was 14 .	我十四歲時結婚
i lost a child when i was 15 , a second child when i was 16 .	我在十五歲時失去了一個孩子 , 一個十六歲時的第二個孩子 。
so the story with zacarias was too much really .	所以zacarias的故事實在太多了
and i still suffer , because my son is like he's buried alive .	而我仍然受苦 , 因為我的兒子就好像他活著一樣 。
i know she really cried for her son .	我知道她真的為兒子哭了 。
but she knows where he is .	但她知道他在哪裡 。
my son , i don't know where he is .	我的兒子 , 我不知道他在哪裡 。
i don't know if he's alive . i don't know if he's tortured .	我不知道他是否活著 。 我不知道他是否受過折磨 。
i don't know what happened to him .	我不知道他發生了什麼事 。
so that's why i decided to tell my story , so that my suffering is something positive for other women .	所以這就是為什麼我決定要說我的故事 , 這樣我的苦難對其他女性來說是很正面的 。
for all the women , all the mothers that give life , you can give back , you can change .	對所有的女性 , 所有賦予生命的媽媽 , 你可以回饋 , 你可以改變 。
it's up to us women , because we are women , because we love our children .	取決於我們女性 , 因為我們是女性 , 因為我們愛我們的孩子 。
we must be handinhand and do something together .	我們必須親自動手做點什麼 。
it's not against women , it's for us , for us women , for our children .	不是反對女性 , 而是對我們、對我們女性、對我們的孩子 。
i talk against violence , against terrorism .	我反對暴力 , 反對恐怖主義 。
i go to schools to talk to young , muslim girls so they don't accept to be married against their will very young .	我去學校和年輕的穆斯林女孩談 , 讓他們不接受很年輕的意志結婚 。
so if i can save one of the young girls , and avoid that they get married and suffer as much as i did , well this is something good .	所以 , 如果我能拯救其中一個年輕女孩 , 避免她們跟我一樣結婚和受苦 , 嗯 , 這是好事 。
this is why i'm here in front of you .	這是我在你們面前的原因 。
pr: i would like to say that i have learned so much from aicha , starting with that day we had our very first meeting with other family members which was a very private meeting with security , because it was november 2002 , and , frankly , we were afraid of the superpatriotism of that time in the country those of us family members .	pr:我想說我從aicha身上學到了很多 , 從那天開始 , 我們和其他家庭成員有了第一次會面 , 那是一場非常私人的會議 , 和安全有關 , 因為那是2002年11月 , 坦白說 , 我們害怕那個時代的超級善良主義 , 那些我們家庭成員 。
but we were all so nervous .	但我們都好緊張 。
" why does she want to meet us ? "	「 她為什麼想和我們見面 ? 」
and then she was nervous .	接著她很緊張 。
" why did we want to meet her ? "	「 我們為什麼想和她見面 ? 」
what did we want from each other ?	我們從彼此之間想要什麼 ?
before we knew each others' names , or anything , we had embraced and wept .	在我們知道彼此的名字或任何東西之前 , 我們已經擁抱並哭泣 。
then we sat in a circle with support , with help , from people experienced in this kind of reconciliation .	接著 , 我們圍成一圈 , 有支援 , 有助人 , 從人們經歷到這種和解 。
and aicha started , and she said , " i don't know if my son is guilty or innocent , but i want to tell you how sorry i am for what happened to your families .	然後aicha開始了 , 她說: 「 我不知道我兒子是不是有罪 , 還是無辜 , 但我想告訴你們 , 我有多麼抱歉 , 為了你們家人發生的事 。
i know what it is to suffer , and i feel that if there is a crime , a person should be tried fairly and punished . "	我知道什麼是苦難 , 我覺得如果有犯罪 , 一個人就應該被公平地審視和懲罰 。 」
but she reached out to us in that way , and it was , i'd like to say , it was an icebreaker .	但她用那樣的方式向我們伸出援手 , 我想說 , 那是個冰箱 。
and what happened then is we all told our stories , and we all connected as human beings .	接著發生的是 , 我們都說了自己的故事 , 我們都以人類的身分來連結 。
by the end of the afternoon it was about three hours after lunch we'd felt as if we'd known each other forever .	下午結束時 , 午餐後大約是三小時 , 我們覺得好像永遠認識彼此一樣 。
now what i learned from her , is a woman , not only who could be so generous under these present circumstances and what it was then , and what was being done to her son , but the life she's had .	我從她身上學到的 , 是一個女人 , 不僅可以在這些當下的情況下如此慷慨 , 和當時的狀況 , 以及她對兒子所經歷的 , 更是如此 。
i never had met someone with such a hard life , from such a totally different culture and environment from my own .	我從來沒有遇過這麼艱難的生活 , 從一個完全不同的文化和環境中 ,
and i feel that we have a special connection , which i value very much .	我覺得我們有一種特別的聯繫 , 我非常重視它 。
and i think it's all about being afraid of the other , but making that step and then realizing , " hey , this wasn't so hard .	我想 , 重點是要害怕對方 , 但做出那一步 , 然後意識到: 「 嘿 , 這沒那麼難 。
who else can i meet that i don't know , or that i'm so different from ? "	我還能遇見哪些人 , 我不知道 , 還是跟我有這麼大的不同 ? 」
so , aicha , do you have a couple of words for conclusion ?	所以 , aicha , 你有幾個字可以做結論嗎 ?
because our time is up .	因為我們的時間到了 。
aw: i wanted to say that we have to try to know other people , the other .	艾瑞克:我想說我們必須試著認識其他人 , 另一人 。
you have to be generous , and your hearts must be generous , your mind must be generous .	你必須慷慨 , 你的心一定很慷慨 , 你的心一定很慷慨 。
you must be tolerant .	你一定要寬容 。
you have to fight against violence .	你必須對抗暴力 。
and i hope that someday we'll all live together in peace and respecting each other .	我希望有一天我們都能和平共存 , 尊重彼此 。
this is what i wanted to say .	這是我想說的 。
too much of the world lacks access to clean drinking water . engineer michael pritchard did something about it inventing the portable lifesaver filter , which can make the most revolting water drinkable in seconds . an amazing demo from tedglobal 2009 .	太多的世界缺乏乾淨的飲用水 。 工程師michaelpritchard做了什麼 , 發明了可攜式的lifes濾水器 , 它可以在幾秒鐘內製造出最耐用的水 。 一個驚人的示範 , 來自2009年的tedglobal 。

the first thing is water .	第一件事是水 。
now i see you've all been enjoying the water that's been provided for you here at the conference , over the past couple of days .	現在我看到你們都很享受在會議上為你們提供的水 , 在過去的幾天裡 。
and i'm sure you'll feel that it's from a safe source .	我相信你們會覺得這是來自一個安全的來源 。
but what if it wasn't ?	但如果不是呢 ?
what if it was from a source like this ?	如果它是來自這樣的源頭呢 ?
then statistics would actually say that half of you would now be suffering with diarrhea .	根據統計 , 在座有一半人現在正在腹瀉受苦 。
i talked a lot in the past about statistics , and the provision of safe drinking water for all .	過去我談了很多統計數據 , 提供所有人安全的飲用水 。
but they just don't seem to get through .	但它們似乎無法通過 。

it's because , using current thinking , the scale of the problem just seems too huge to contemplate solving .	這是因為 , 使用目前的思考 , 問題的規模似乎太大了 , 無法思考解決問題 。

by the way , since i've been speaking , another 13 , 000 people around the world are suffering now with diarrhea .	順道一提 , 自從我開始演講以來 , 世界各地有一萬三千人正在受痢疾所苦 。

i invented lifesaver bottle because i got angry .	我發明了lifesaver濾水瓶 , 因為我生氣了 。
i , like most of you , was sitting down , the day after christmas in 2004 , when i was watching the devastating news of the asian tsunami as it rolled in , playing out on tv .	我和你們大部份人一樣 , 在2004年聖誕節後的一天 , 當時我在看亞洲海嘯毀滅性的消息 , 當它滾進來時 , 在電視上演出 。
the days and weeks that followed , people fleeing to the hills , being forced to drink contaminated water or face death .	隨後的日子 , 人們逃到山丘上 , 被迫喝下被污染的水或面對死亡 。
that really stuck with me .	那真的困住了我 。
then , a few months later , hurricane katrina slammed into the side of america .	然後 , 幾個月後 , 卡崔娜颶風滑入美國的一邊 。
" okay , " i thought , " here's a first world country , let's see what they can do . "	「 好吧 , 」 我心想: 「 這裡是第一個世界國家 , 讓我們看看他們能做什麼 。 」
do you know it took five days to get water to the superdome ?	你知道要花五天才能把水送到超級室嗎 ?
people were shooting each other on the streets for tv sets and water .	人們在街上互相射殺 , 為了電視機和水 。
that's when i decided i had to do something .	那時我決定要做點什麼 。
now i spent a lot of time in my garage , over the next weeks and months , and also in my kitchen much to the dismay of my wife .	現在我花了很多時間在我的車庫裡 , 在接下來的幾週、幾個月 , 還有在我廚房裡 , 對於我妻子感到很沮喪 。
however , after a few failed prototypes , i finally came up with this , the lifesaver bottle .	然而 , 在幾次失敗的原型之後 , 我終於想出了這個 , lifesaver濾水瓶 。
okay , now for the science bit .	好 , 現在來談談科學 。
before lifesaver , the best hand filters were only capable of filtering down to about 200 nanometers .	在lifesaver之前 , 最好的手部過濾器只能過濾到大約200奈米 。
the smallest bacteria is about 200 nanometers .	最小的細菌大約是200奈米 。
so a 200nanometer bacteria is going to get through a 200nanometer hole .	所以一個200奈米的細菌將會通過一個200奈米的洞 。
the smallest virus , on the other hand , is about 25 nanometers .	另一方面 , 最小的病毒大約是25奈米 。
so that's definitely going to get through those 200 nanometer holes .	所以這絕對會穿過那200奈米的洞 。
lifesaver pores are 15 nanometers .	lifesaver濾水孔是15奈米
so nothing is getting through .	所以 , 沒有任何事情要經過 。
okay , i'm going to give you a bit of a demonstration .	好 , 我要給你們一些示範
would you like to see that ?	你願意看看嗎 ?

but i got to thinking , you know , if we were in the middle of a flood zone in bangladesh , the water wouldn't look like this .	但我在想 , 如果我們在孟加拉的一個洪區中間 , 水不會像這樣 。

the lifesaver bottle works really simply .	lifesaver濾水瓶的功用很簡單 。

okay , so i'm going to take this really filthy water , and put it in here . do you want a drink yet ?	好吧 , 我會帶著這塊很骯髒的水 , 把它放到這裡 。 你還想喝杯飲料嗎 ?
okay . there we go .	好了 , 開始了 。
give it a few pumps . okay ?	給它一些幫浦 。 好嗎 ?
that's all that's necessary .	那都是必要的 。
now as soon as i pop the teat , sterile drinking water is going to come out .	一旦我抽出了有氣體、無菌的飲用水 , 就會出來 。

there you go chris .	來了克里斯
what's it taste of ?	它的味道是什麼 ?

okay . lifesaver bottle is used by thousands of people around the world .	好的.lifesaver濾水瓶被全世界數以千計的人使用
it'll last for 6 , 000 liters .	它會持續6000公升 。
and when it's expired , using failsafe technology , the system will shut off , protecting the user .	而當它過期時 , 使用失敗的科技 , 系統會關閉 , 保護使用者 。
pop the cartridge out . pop a new one in .	把貨車趕出去 , 把新的東西塞進去 。
it's good for another 6 , 000 liters .	對另外一萬六千公升有利 。
so let's look at the applications .	我們來看看應用程式 。
traditionally , in a crisis , what do we do ?	傳統上 , 在危機中 , 我們該怎麼做 ?
then , after a few weeks , we set up camps .	然後 , 幾個星期後 , 我們設立營地 。
and people are forced to come into the camps to get their safe drinking water .	人們被迫來到難民營 , 取得他們的安全飲用水 。
what happens when 20 , 000 people congregate in a camp ?	當兩萬人聚集在一個營區時 , 會發生什麼事 ?
diseases spread . more resources are required .	疾病擴散 。 需要更多的資源 。
the problem just becomes selfperpetuating .	問題只會變成自我延續 。
but by thinking differently , and shipping these , people can stay put .	但藉由不同的思考 , 運送這些 , 人們可以留在
they can make their own sterile drinking water , and start to get on with rebuilding their homes and their lives .	他們可以自己製造無菌的飲用水 , 開始重建家園和生活 。
now , it doesn't require a natural disaster for this to work .	這並不需要天然災害才能成功 。
using the old thinking , of national infrastructure and pipe work , is too expensive .	使用舊思維、國家基礎建設和管道工作 , 實在太貴了 。
when you run the numbers on a calculator , you run out of noughts .	當你在計算機上執行數字時 , 你就快沒了 。

instead of shipping water , and using manmade processes to do it , let's use mother nature . she's got a fantastic system .	與其運送水 , 和使用人造過程來做這件事 , 讓我們用母親的本質 。 她有一個很棒的系統 。
she picks the water up from there , desalinates it , for free , transports it over there , and dumps it onto the mountains , rivers , and streams .	她從那裡取水 , 免費淡化水 , 運送到那裡 , 然後把水丟到山上 , 河流和溪流上 。

the same technology , in a jerry can .	同樣的科技 , 在一個jerry罐子裡
this will process 25 , 000 liters of water ; that's good enough for a family of four , for three years .	這將要處理25 , 000公升的水 ; 這足夠一個四、三年的家庭 。
and how much does it cost ?	而且要花多少錢 ?
about half a cent a day to run .	一天要跑半分錢 。
so , by thinking differently , and processing water at the point of use , mothers and children no longer have to walk four hours a day to collect their water .	所以 , 用不同的方式思考 , 並在使用時處理水 , 母親和孩子不再需要每天走四小時才能收集他們的水 。
they can get it from a source nearby .	他們可以從附近的源頭取得
so with just eight billion dollars , we can hit the millennium goal's target of halving the number of people without access to safe drinking water .	只要八十億美元 , 我們就能達到千禧目標的目標 , 讓無法取得安全飲用水的人數減半 。
to put that into context , the u . k . government spends about 12 billion pounds a year on foreign aid .	若要把這件事情納入考量 , 英國政府每年花大約120億英鎊在國外援助上 。
but why stop there ?	但為什麼要停在那裡呢 ?
with 20 billion dollars , everyone can have access to safe drinking water .	有了200億美元 , 每個人都能取得安全的飲用水 。
so the threeandahalf billion people that suffer every year as a result , and the two million kids that die every year , will live .	所以每年受苦的三十五億人 , 每年死去的兩百萬名孩童 , 將會活下去 。
paddy ashdown claims that we are living in a moment in history where power is changing in ways it never has before . in a spellbinding talk at tedxbrussels he outlines the three major global shifts that he sees coming .	帕迪阿什唐宣稱我們正處於歷史的一刻 , 權力從來沒有改變過 。 在tedxbrussels的一個拼字演講中 , 他發現了三項重大的全球轉變 。

there's a poem written by a very famous english poet at the end of the 19th century .	有一首詩是由一位非常有名的英文詩人在十九世紀末寫的
it was said to echo in churchill's brain in the 1930s .	據說在30年代 , 在邱吉爾的大腦中迴盪 。
and the poem goes: " on the idle hill of summer , lazy with the flow of streams , hark i hear a distant drummer , drumming like a sound in dreams , far and near and low and louder on the roads of earth go by , dear to friend and food to powder , soldiers marching , soon to die . "	這首詩是這麼說的: 「 在夏天的偶像山丘上 , 懶得帶著溪流的流動 , 哈克我聽到遙遠的鼓聲 , 鼓鼓聲在夢中發出聲音 , 距離越來越近 , 越來越大聲 , 地球的道路經過 , 親愛的朋友和食物傳遞給粉末 , 士兵很快就會到死去 。 」
those who are interested in poetry , the poem is " a shropshire lad " written by a . e . housman .	那些對詩有興趣的人 , 這首詩是 " shropshirelad " , 由a.e.豪斯曼寫的 。
but what housman understood , and you hear it in the symphonies of nielsen too , was that the long , hot , silvan summers of stability of the 19th century were coming to a close , and that we were about to move into one of those terrifying periods of history when power changes .	但 , 豪斯曼所了解的 , 你也在尼爾森的交響曲中聽過 , 那就是 , 十九世紀的漫長、熱帶的、非凡的夏天正要靠近 , 我們即將邁向歷史上最可怕的時期之一 , 當權力改變時 。
and these are always periods , ladies and gentlemen , accompanied by turbulence , and all too often by blood .	這些都是月經 , 女士們 , 先生們 , 伴隨著動盪 , 經常是血液 。
and my message for you is that i believe we are condemned , if you like , to live at just one of those moments in history when the gimbals upon which the established order of power is beginning to change and the new look of the world , the new powers that exist in the world , are beginning to take form .	我的訊息是 , 我相信我們會被譴責 , 如果你願意 , 只能在歷史上的那些時刻 , 生活在那一刻 , 建立了權力的限制開始改變 , 以及世界的新面貌 , 世界上存在的新勢力開始形成 。
and these are and we see it very clearly today nearly always highly turbulent times , highly difficult times , and all too often very bloody times .	這些是──我們今天看得很清楚──幾乎總是有高度動盪的時刻、高度難度的時代 , 及時常非常血腥的時代 。
by the way , it happens about once every century .	順帶一提 , 它每世紀都會發生一次 。
you might argue that the last time it happened and that's what housman felt coming and what churchill felt too was that when power passed from the old nations , the old powers of europe , across the atlantic to the new emerging power of the united states of america the beginning of the american century .	你可能會主張 , 最後一次發生了 , 那就是豪斯曼所感受到的 , 以及邱吉爾的感覺 , 就是當權力從舊國、歐洲的舊勢力 , 跨越大西洋到美國的新興權力──美國是美國最初的時代 。
and of course , into the vacuum where the tooold european powers used to be were played the two bloody catastrophes of the last century the one in the first part and the one in the second part: the two great world wars .	當然 , 以前那些過時的歐洲大國強權在上個世紀的兩場血腥的災難中 , 第一部份和第二部分的那一場:二次大戰 。
mao zedong used to refer to them as the european civil wars , and it's probably a more accurate way of describing them .	毛澤東曾經把他們當作歐洲內戰來稱呼他們 , 這可能是比較準確的形容方式 。
well , ladies and gentlemen , we live at one of those times .	各位先生女士 , 我們生活在這樣的時代 。
but for us , i want to talk about three factors today .	但對我們來說 , 我今天想談談三個因素 。
and the first of these , the first two of these , is about a shift in power .	第一 , 前兩項 , 是關於權力的轉變 。
and the second is about some new dimension which i want to refer to , which has never quite happened in the way it's happening now .	第二個是關於一些我想要參考的新維度 , 這從來沒有像現在這樣發生過 。
but let's talk about the shifts of power that are occurring to the world .	但讓我們來談談權力的轉移 , 正發生在世界各地 。
and what is happening today is , in one sense , frightening because it's never happened before .	現今的情況是 , 在某種意義上 , 令人害怕的 , 因為它從來沒有發生過 。
we have seen lateral shifts of power the power of greece passed to rome and the power shifts that occurred during the european civilizations but we are seeing something slightly different .	我們看到了希臘的權力轉移 , 轉移到羅馬 , 以及在歐洲文明期間發生的權力轉移 , 但我們看到了一些稍微不一樣的東西 。
for power is not just moving laterally from nation to nation .	權力的發展不僅僅是從國家轉移到國家 。
it's also moving vertically .	它也垂直移動 。
what's happening today is that the power that was encased , held to accountability , held to the rule of law , within the institution of the nation state has now migrated in very large measure onto the global stage .	現今的情況是 , 權力被縮減到負責任的程度 , 被牽扯到法治之中 , 在國家國家的機構內 , 現在已經移居到全球的極大措施上 。
the globalization of power we talk about the globalization of markets , but actually it's the globalization of real power .	全球化的權力我們談到市場的全球化 , 但事實上是真正的權力全球化 。
and where , at the nation state level that power is held to accountability subject to the rule of law , on the international stage it is not .	在國家的層級 , 權力受到法律的指責 , 在國際舞台上 , 沒有 。
the international stage and the global stage where power now resides: the power of the internet , the power of the satellite broadcasters , the power of the money changers this vast moneygoround that circulates now 32 times the amount of money necessary for the trade it's supposed to be there to finance the money changers , if you like , the financial speculators that have brought us all to our knees quite recently , the power of the multinational corporations now developing budgets often bigger than mediumsized countries .	國際舞台和全球舞台現在都在:網路的力量、衛星廣播的力量、金錢改變者的力量──這巨大的金錢流動的金錢 , 現在的交易所需的金錢數量是現在的32倍──這應該是用來資助金錢改變的改變者 , 如果你喜歡 , 那些近期的金融推理者 , 把我們都帶到我們的膝蓋上 , 多國企業的權力 , 現在發展的預算都比中世紀的國家還要大 。
these live in a global space which is largely unregulated , not subject to the rule of law , and in which people may act free of constraint .	這些居住的全球空間 , 大致上是不規則的 , 不受法治規範的限制 , 也不受法律限制 。
now that suits the powerful up to a moment .	這就適合了強大的一刻 。
it's always suitable for those who have the most power to operate in spaces without constraint , but the lesson of history is that , sooner or later , unregulated space space not subject to the rule of law becomes populated , not just by the things you wanted international trade , the internet , etc . but also by the things you don't want international criminality , international terrorism .	總是適合那些擁有最大權力的人在沒有限制的空間中運作 , 但歷史的教訓是 , 遲早 , 不受規範的空間空間空間空間 , 不受法律規範 , 不只受制於你想要的國際貿易 , 網路等等 。 還有你不想要國際犯罪 , 國際恐怖主義 。
the revelation of 9/11 is that even if you are the most powerful nation on earth , nevertheless , those who inhabit that space can attack you even in your most iconic of cities one bright september morning .	9/11事件的啟示是 , 即使你是地球上最強大的國家 , 儘管如此 , 那些居住空間的人 , 甚至可以在你最具代表性的城市裡攻擊你 , 一個明亮的九月早晨 。
it's said that something like 60 percent of the four million dollars that was taken to fund 9/11 actually passed through the institutions of the twin towers which 9/11 destroyed .	據說 , 約有60%的四百萬美金被帶到資金911事件中 , 實際上是通過雙子星大樓的機構 , 911摧毀了 。
you see , our enemies also use this space the space of mass travel , the internet , satellite broadcasters to be able to get around their poison , which is about destroying our systems and our ways .	要知道 , 我們的敵人也用這個空間──大眾旅行、網路、衛星廣播 , 來繞過他們的毒藥 , 也就是破壞我們的系統和方式 。
sooner or later , sooner or later , the rule of history is that where power goes governance must follow .	遲早 , 歷史的規則是 , 權力的治理必須遵守 。
and if it is therefore the case , as i believe it is , that one of the phenomenon of our time is the globalization of power , then it follows that one of the challenges of our time is to bring governance to the global space .	如果是這樣 , 如我所相信的 , 我們這個時代的其中一個現象就是權力的全球化 , 那麼我們這個時代的挑戰之一就是把統治權帶到全球的空間 。
and i believe that the decades ahead of us now will be to a greater or lesser extent turbulent the more or less we are able to achieve that aim: to bring governance to the global space .	我相信 , 未來的數十年 , 會是更大或更少的動盪 , 我們能做到那樣的目標:把統治權帶到全球 。
now notice , i'm not talking about government .	現在請注意 , 我不是在說政府
i'm not talking about setting up some global democratic institution .	我不是指設立一些全球民主制度
my own view , by the way , ladies and gentlemen , is that this is unlikely to be done by spawning more u . n . institutions .	我自己的看法 , 順帶一提 , 女士們先生們 , 就是這不太可能透過推出更多聯合國機構來完成 。
if we didn't have the u . n . , we'd have to invent it .	如果我們沒有聯合國 , 我們就必須發明它 。
the world needs an international forum .	世界需要一個國際論壇
it needs a means by which you can legitimize international action .	它需要一種手段 , 可以合法化國際行動 。
but when it comes to governance of the global space , my guess is this won't happen through the creation of more u . n . institutions .	但 , 談到全球空間的治理 , 我的猜測是 , 這不會發生在更多聯合國機構的創建上 。
it will actually happen by the powerful coming together and making treatybased systems , treatybased agreements , to govern that global space .	強大的力量會集結在一起 , 建立以條約為基礎的系統、以條約為基礎的協議 , 來治理全球的空間 。
and if you look , you can see them happening , already beginning to emerge .	如果你看 , 你可以看到他們正在發生 , 已經開始出現了 。
the world trade organization: treatybased organization , entirely treatybased , and yet , powerful enough to hold even the most powerful , the united states , to account if necessary .	世界貿易組織:以條約為基礎的組織 , 完全以條約為基礎 , 然而 , 強大到連最強大的美國 , 都可以考量到如果必要的話 。
kyoto: the beginnings of struggling to create a treatybased organization .	京都:努力創造一個以條約為基礎的組織 。
the g20: we know now that we have to put together an institution which is capable of bringing governance to that financial space for financial speculation .	二十號g20:我們現在知道 , 我們必須組建一個機構 , 這個機構能夠把統治權帶到金融的空間 , 來做財務上的推測 。
and that's what the g20 is , a treatybased institution .	那就是g20是以條約為基礎的機構 。
now there's a problem there , and we'll come back to it in a minute , which is that if you bring the most powerful together to make the rules in treatybased institutions , to fill that governance space , then what happens to the weak who are left out ?	現在有一個問題 , 我們等一下再回來談 , 就是如果你把最有權力的規則集合起來 , 在以條約為基礎的機構中 , 來填補那個治理空間 , 那麼 , 剩下的弱者會發生什麼事 ?
and that's a big problem , and we'll return to it in just a second .	這是個大問題 , 我們只要一秒鐘就可以重回它 。
so there's my first message , that if you are to pass through these turbulent times more or less turbulently , then our success in doing that will in large measure depend on our capacity to bring sensible governance to the global space .	所以 , 我的第一個訊息是 , 如果你要更常經過這些動亂的時代 , 那麼我們的成功就會取決於我們的能力 , 取決於我們的能力 , 把合理的治理帶到全球 。
and watch that beginning to happen .	看著那開始發生 。
my second point is , and i know i don't have to talk to an audience like this about such a thing , but power is not just shifting vertically , it's also shifting horizontally .	我的第二點是 , 我知道我不需要跟這麼一個觀眾談類似的事情 , 但是權力不只是垂直地轉移 , 權力也是橫向的轉移 。
you might argue that the story , the history of civilizations , has been civilizations gathered around seas with the first ones around the mediterranean , the more recent ones in the ascendents of western power around the atlantic .	你可能會爭辯說 , 故事、文明的歷史 , 一直以來 , 文明聚集在海上 , 和最早圍繞地中海的海洋 , 近期 , 在西方國家大西洋的後裔中 , 越是近期 。
well it seems to me that we're now seeing a fundamental shift of power , broadly speaking , away from nations gathered around the atlantic [seaboard] to the nations gathered around the pacific rim .	嗯 , 在我看來 , 我們現在看到的是權力的基本轉變 , 廣泛來說 , 遠離聚集在大西洋棋周圍的國家 , 到太平洋邊緣聚集的國家 。
now that begins with economic power , but that's the way it always begins .	這是從經濟力量開始的 , 但它一直都是這樣開始的 。
you already begin to see the development of foreign policies , the augmentation of military budgets occurring in the other growing powers in the world .	你已經開始看到外交政策的發展 , 軍事預算的擴增發生在世界上其他成長的權力中 。
i think actually this is not so much a shift from the west to the east ; something different is happening .	我認為這其實不是什麼從西方移轉到東方 , 不一樣的事情正在發生 。
my guess is , for what it's worth , is that the united states will remain the most powerful nation on earth for the next 10 years , 15 , but the context in which she holds her power has now radically altered ; it has radically changed .	我的猜測是 , 值得一提的是 , 美國在接下來的十年 , 十五年 , 仍然是地球上最強大的國家 , 但在她掌握權力的背景下 , 現在已經徹底改變了 , 徹底地改變了 。
we are coming out of 50 years , most unusual years , of history in which we have had a totally monopolar world , in which every compass needle for or against has to be referenced by its position to washington a world bestrode by a single colossus .	我們來到五十年 , 最不尋常的歷史中 , 我們有一個完全獨立的世界 , 每個指南針對或反對的指南針都得要參考它的位置 , 來到華盛頓 , 一個由單一羅馬群體所組成的世界 。
but that's not a usual case in history .	但這不是歷史上常見的案例 。
in fact , what's now emerging is the much more normal case of history .	事實上 , 現在出現的是更正常的歷史案例 。
you're beginning to see the emergence of a multipolar world .	你開始看到一個多極世界的出現
up until now , the united states has been the dominant feature of our world .	到目前為止 , 美國一直是我們世界的主導特徵 。
they will remain the most powerful nation , but they will be the most powerful nation in an increasingly multipolar world .	他們會留住最強的國家 , 但他們會是越來越多世界中最強大的國家 。
and you begin to see the alternative centers of power building up in china , of course , though my own guess is that china's ascent to greatness is not smooth .	你就會開始看到中國的權力替代中心 , 當然 , 我自己的猜測是 , 中國的利益不光滑 。
it's going to be quite grumpy as china begins to democratize her society after liberalizing her economy .	相當可惜 , 中國在自由化她的經濟後 , 開始民主化她的社會 。
but that's a subject of a different discussion .	但那是不同的討論對象 。
you see india , you see brazil .	看到印度 , 看到巴西
you see increasingly that the world now looks actually , for us europeans , much more like europe in the 19th century .	你可以看到 , 現在這個世界看起來 , 對我們歐洲人來說 , 很像十九世紀的歐洲 。
europe in the 19th century: a great british foreign secretary , lord canning , used to describe it as the " european concert of powers . "	歐洲在19世紀:一個偉大的英國外交部長 , 大主教坎寧 , 曾將其形容為 「 歐洲權力協會 」 。
there was a balance , a fivesided balance .	有一個平衡點 , 一個五度平衡點 。
britain always played to the balance .	英國總是玩到平衡點 。
if paris got together with berlin , britain got together with vienna and rome to provide a counterbalance .	如果巴黎和柏林結合 , 英國和維也納和羅馬合作 , 來提供反平衡 。
now notice , in a period which is dominated by a monopolar world , you have fixed alliances nato , the warsaw pact .	現在請注意 , 在一個單一世界被支配的時期 , 你有固定的同盟國 , 北約 , 華沙特協會 。
a fixed polarity of power means fixed alliances .	固定的權力對立意謂著固定的盟友 。
but a multiple polarity of power means shifting and changing alliances .	但多方對立的權力 , 意味著轉移和改變盟友 。
and that's the world we're coming into , in which we will increasingly see that our alliances are not fixed .	這就是我們正在進入的世界 , 我們會逐漸看到我們的同盟國沒有固定不變 。
canning , the great british foreign secretary once said , " britain has a common interest , but no common allies . "	坎寧 , 偉大的英國外交部長曾說: 「 英國有共同的利益 , 但沒有共同的盟友 。 」
and we will see increasingly that even we in the west will reach out , have to reach out , beyond the cozy circle of the atlantic powers to make alliances with others if we want to get things done in the world .	我們會看到即使我們西方國家也會伸出援手 , 必須伸出援手 , 超越大西洋的舒適圈 , 才能與他人結盟 , 只要我們想要把事情做好 。
note , that when we went into libya , it was not good enough for the west to do it alone ; we had to bring others in .	注意 , 當我們進入利比亞的時候 , 西方國家不夠好 , 不夠好 , 我們得要把其他人帶進來 。
we had to bring , in this case , the arab league in .	我們必須把阿拉伯聯盟帶進來 。
my guess is iraq and afghanistan are the last times when the west has tried to do it themselves , and we haven't succeeded .	我的猜測是伊拉克和阿富汗 , 是西方最後一次嘗試自己做的時候 , 我們還沒成功 。
my guess is that we're reaching the beginning of the end of 400 years i say 400 years because it's the end of the ottoman empire of the hegemony of western power , western institutions and western values .	我的猜測是 , 我們到達了400年後的開始-我說400年-因為它是歐特曼帝國的終點-西方權力、西方制度和西方的價值觀 。
you know , up until now , if the west got its act together , it could propose and dispose in every corner of the world .	你知道 , 直到現在 , 如果西方國家團結起來 , 它可以在世界的每個角落提出和散播 。
but that's no longer true .	但這已經不是事實了 。
take the last financial crisis after the second world war .	以第二次世界大戰後最後一次的金融危機為例 。
the west got together the bretton woods institution , world bank , international monetary fund the problem solved .	西方國家聚集了布雷頓森林機構世界銀行國際貨幣基金組織解決了問題
now we have to call in others .	現在我們必須打電話到其他人
now we have to create the g20 .	現在我們必須創造g20
now we have to reach beyond the cozy circle of our western friends .	現在我們必須超越西方朋友的舒適圈 。
let me make a prediction for you , which is probably even more startling .	讓我為各位做個預測 , 這可能更讓人驚訝 。
i suspect we are now reaching the end of 400 years when western power was enough .	我懷疑現在已經達到400年的終點 , 西方的權力已經足夠了 。
people say to me , " the chinese , of course , they'll never get themselves involved in peacemaking , multilateral peacemaking around the world . "	人們對我說: 「 中國人 , 當然 , 他們永遠不會讓自己參與到世界各地的調停、多邊性的調停 。 」
oh yes ? why not ?	有嗎 ? 為什麼不呢 ?
how many chinese troops are serving under the blue beret , serving under the blue flag , serving under the u . n . command in the world today ?	有多少中國軍隊在藍色貝雷特下服役 , 在藍色旗幟下服役 , 在當今世界聯合國指令下服役 ?
how many americans ? 11 .	有多少美國人 ? 11個人 。
what is the largest naval contingent tackling the issue of somali pirates ?	對於解決索馬利海盜問題 , 最大的海軍陸戰隊是什麼 ?
the chinese naval contingent .	中國海軍的內容
of course they are , they are a mercantilist nation .	當然 , 他們是商人 。
they want to keep the sea lanes open .	想要保持海道開放
increasingly , we are going to have to do business with people with whom we do not share values , but with whom , for the moment , we share common interests .	漸漸地 , 我們得要和我們不共享價值觀的人做生意 , 但當下 , 我們要分享共同利益 。
it's a whole new different way of looking at the world that is now emerging .	這是一種全新的角度來看現在所出現的世界 。
and here's the third factor , which is totally different .	第三個因素是完全不同的
today in our modern world , because of the internet , because of the kinds of things people have been talking about here , everything is connected to everything .	今天在我們的現代世界 , 由於網路 , 由於人們在此討論過的種類 , 一切都與一切息息相關 。
we are now interdependent .	我們現在是互相依賴的
we are now interlocked , as nations , as individuals , in a way which has never been the case before , never been the case before .	我們現在是以國家 , 以個人的身分 , 以以前從未如此的身分相互連結 , 從來沒有如此過 。
the interrelationship of nations , well it's always existed .	國與國之間的關聯性 , 總是存在的 。
diplomacy is about managing the interrelationship of nations .	外交就是管理國家之間的關聯性 。
but now we are intimately locked together .	但現在我們密不可分 。
you get swine flu in mexico , it's a problem for charles de gaulle airport 24 hours later .	墨西哥的豬流感 , 是24小時後查爾斯•德高爾機場的問題 。
lehman brothers goes down , the whole lot collapses .	雷曼兄弟的數量下降 , 整體的崩潰 。
there are fires in the steppes of russia , food riots in africa .	在俄羅斯的步伐、非洲的糧食暴動中有火災 。
we are all now deeply , deeply , deeply interconnected .	我們現在都很深、很深、很深的相互連結 。
and what that means is the idea of a nation state acting alone , not connected with others , not working with others , is no longer a viable proposition .	這意味著 , 一個國家單獨行動的概念 , 不和他人連結 , 不和他人合作 , 不再是可行的提議 。
because the actions of a nation state are neither confined to itself , nor is it sufficient for the nation state itself to control its own territory , because the effects outside the nation state are now beginning to affect what happens inside them .	因為一個國家的行動 , 不受限於自己 , 也不足以讓國家自己去控制自己的領土 , 因為國家外部的影響已經開始影響他們內部的狀況 。
i was a young soldier in the last of the small empire wars of britain .	我還是個年輕的士兵 , 在英國的最後一個小帝國大戰中 ,
at that time , the defense of my country was about one thing and one thing only: how strong was our army , how strong was our air force , how strong was our navy and how strong were our allies .	那時 , 我國家的防衛措施大約是一件事 , 還有一件事:我們的軍隊有多強壯 , 我們的空軍有多強壯 , 我們的海軍有多強 , 以及我們的盟友有多強壯 。
that was when the enemy was outside the walls .	那是敵人在外牆的時候 。
now the enemy is inside the walls .	現在敵人在牆內
now if i want to talk about the defense of my country , i have to speak to the minister of health because pandemic disease is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of agriculture because food security is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of industry because the fragility of our hitech infrastructure is now a point of attack for our enemies as we see from cyber warfare i have to speak to the minister of home affairs because who has entered my country , who lives in that terraced house in that inner city has a direct effect on what happens in my country as we in london saw in the 7/7 bombings .	如果我想要談談我的國家的防禦 , 我得和健康部談談 , 因為大流行疾病對我的安全造成威脅 , 我得和農業部談談 , 因為糧食安全對我的保障是威脅 , 我得要和工業部談 , 因為現代的基礎設施很脆弱 , 對於我們的敵人來說 , 正如我們從網路戰場看到的攻擊 , 我得要和國務部談談 , 因為在我的國家 , 在我們的房子裡 , 誰會發生在我的國家 , 直接攻擊我的國家 。
it's no longer the case that the security of a country is simply a matter for its soldiers and its ministry of defense .	一個國家的安全不再是對士兵和國防部而言重要的事 。
it's its capacity to lock together its institutions .	能夠封鎖它的機構的能力
and this tells you something very important .	這告訴了你一件非常重要的事
it tells you that , in fact , our governments , vertically constructed , constructed on the economic model of the industrial revolution vertical hierarchy , specialization of tasks , command structures have got the wrong structures completely .	它告訴你 , 事實上 , 我們的政府 , 垂直建構 , 建構在工業革命的經濟模式垂直化階級制度 , 專門處理任務 , 指令結構已經完全出錯了 。
you in business know that the paradigm structure of our time , ladies and gentlemen , is the network .	你在企業知道我們這個時代的典範結構 , 各位先生女士 , 就是網絡 。
it's your capacity to network that matters , both within your governments and externally .	網路的能力很重要 , 不論是在你的政府或外部 。
so here is ashdown's third law .	這是ashdown的第三定律 。
by the way , don't ask me about ashdown's first law and second law because i haven't invented those yet ; it always sounds better if there's a third law , doesn't it ?	順道一提 , 不要問我有關阿什佛第一及第二定律因為我還沒發明這類定律 ; 如果有第三定律 , 聽起來總是比較好嗎 ?
ashdown's third law is that in the modern age , where everything is connected to everything , the most important thing about what you can do is what you can do with others .	ashdown的第三定律是 , 在現代 , 所有事物都與萬物相連的地方 , 最重要的是你能做的事 , 就是你能和他人做些什麼 。
the most important bit about your structure whether you're a government , whether you're an army regiment , whether you're a business is your docking points , your interconnectors , your capacity to network with others .	最重要的是關於你的結構--不論你是政府 , 不論你是軍事人員 , 不論你是生意的 , 是你的告別點 , 你的互聯網 , 你和他人的能力 。
you understand that in industry ; governments don't .	你明白在工業界 , 政府沒有 。
but now one final thing .	但現在是最後一件事 。
if it is the case , ladies and gentlemen and it is that we are now locked together in a way that has never been quite the same before , then it's also the case that we share a destiny with each other .	如果是這樣 , 女士們先生們--而我們現在被鎖在一起 , 以一種從來不太一樣的方式 , 那也是我們彼此分享命運的方式 。
suddenly and for the very first time , collective defense , the thing that has dominated us as the concept of securing our nations , is no longer enough .	突然間--而且這是第一次集體防禦 , 那個已經主導我們國家安全的概念 , 已經不夠了 。
it used to be the case that if my tribe was more powerful than their tribe , i was safe ; if my country was more powerful than their country , i was safe ; my alliance , like nato , was more powerful than their alliance , i was safe .	以前 , 如果我的部落比他們的部落更強大 , 我更安全 ; 如果我的國家比他們的國家更強大 , 我就更安全 ; 我的聯盟 , 如北約 , 比他們的同盟更強大 , 我就更安全了 。
it is no longer the case .	不再是如此了 。
the advent of the interconnectedness and of the weapons of mass destruction means that , increasingly , i share a destiny with my enemy .	大規模毀滅性的關聯性和武器的出現 , 意味著 , 漸漸地 , 我和我的敵人分享了命運 。
when i was a diplomat negotiating the disarmament treaties with the soviet union in geneva in the 1970s , we succeeded because we understood we shared a destiny with them .	當我還是外交官 , 和蘇聯的蘇聯在1970年代協商時 , 我們成功了 , 因為我們了解我們與他們共享一個命運 。
collective security is not enough .	集體安全是不夠的
peace has come to northern ireland because both sides realized that the zerosum game couldn't work .	和平來到了北愛爾蘭 , 因為雙方都意識到零和遊戲無法運作 。
they shared a destiny with their enemies .	他們與敵人共享命運 。
one of the great barriers to peace in the middle east is that both sides , both israel and , i think , the palestinians , do not understand that they share a collective destiny .	中東和平的一個很大的障礙就是以色列與巴勒斯坦人的雙方都不明白他們共同的命運
and so suddenly , ladies and gentlemen , what has been the proposition of visionaries and poets down the ages becomes something we have to take seriously as a matter of public policy .	所以突然間 , 各位先生女士們 , 一直以來 , 關於有遠見和詩人在這個時代的主張 , 變成了我們必須認真看待的東西 , 成為公共政策的問題 。
i started with a poem , i'll end with one .	我從一首詩開始 , 以一首詩作結 。
the great poem of john donne's .	約翰•多恩的偉大詩作
" send not for whom the bell tolls . "	「 不要把鐘鈴給誰 。 」
the poem is called " no man is an island . "	這首詩叫做 " 沒有男人是孤島 "
and it goes: " every man's death affected me , for i am involved in mankind , send not to ask for whom the bell tolls , it tolls for thee . "	上面寫著: 「 每個男人的死亡都會影響我 , 因為我涉及到人類 , 不會去要求鈴聲響是誰 , 它會為該死 。 」
for john donne , a recommendation of morality .	對約翰•多恩來說 , 推薦道德
for us , i think , part of the equation for our survival .	對我們來說 , 我認為 , 方程式的一部分是為了我們的生存 。
to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	為了尋找漫長壽命和健康的道路 , danbuetner和團隊一起研究世界的 「 藍色區塊 」 , 他們的長老與vigor一起生活 , 來紀錄年齡 。 在tedxtc , 他共享9個共同飲食和生活習慣 , 讓他們在100歲時過世 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物學、文化、探索、食物、健康、生活、科學、科學、
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	danbuetner:如何活到一百歲以上 ?
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	丹麥雙胞胎研究發現 , 在某些生物限制下 , 人人平均壽命只有百分之十 。
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	其他90%都被我們的生活方式所主導 。
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	所以 , 藍寶地的前提是:如果我們能找到長壽的最佳生活方式 , 我們就能找出長壽的事實公式 。
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問美國人平均壽命最佳的公式是什麼 , 他們可能無法告訴你 。
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	他們可能聽說過南海灘飲食 , 或阿特金斯減肥法 。
you have the usda food pyramid .	你有美國農業食物金字塔 。
there is what oprah tells us .	歐普拉告訴我們的是
there is what doctor oz tells us .	奧茲博士告訴我們
the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	事實是 , 對於真正幫助我們活得更好的東西 , 有許多困惑 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你應該跑馬拉松嗎 ? 還是做瑜伽 ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	你應該吃有機肉 , 還是要吃豆腐 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	談到補給品時 , 你是否該把它們
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	那這些荷爾蒙或斯脊椎呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	目的在其中演奏嗎 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	靈性 ? 我們該如何社交呢 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	嗯 , 我們尋找長壽的方法是與國家地理雜誌合作 , 和國家老化研究院合作 , 找出四個人口統計學確認的領域 , 這些區域是地理定義的 。
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	然後帶進一個專家團隊 , 來很明確地通過這些人的所作所為 , 來分解跨文化的干擾 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	最後我要告訴你們那是什麼 。
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但首先 , 談到長壽 , 我想破解一些常見的迷思 。
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一個迷思是 , 如果你很努力 , 你可以活到100歲 。
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 美國的5000人中只有1人活到100歲 。
your chances are very low .	你的機會非常低 。
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	即使是美國成長最快的人口結構 , 還是很難達到100 。
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題在於我們不是為了長壽而設計的 。
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們為所謂的 「 繁衍成功 」 設計 。
i love that word .	我很喜歡這個字 。
it reminds me of my college days .	這讓我想起我的大學日子 。
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家稱之為 「 成功 」 , 意思是你有孩子的年齡 , 接著是另一個世代 , 當你的孩子有了孩子時 , 年齡 。
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	在那之後演化的效應完全消失了 。
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	如果你是哺乳類 , 如果你是老鼠或大象 , 或人 , 在兩者之間 , 是同一個故事 。
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	要到一百歲 , 你不僅要有非常好的生活方式 , 你還得贏得基因彩票 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個迷思是 , 有治療可以幫助緩慢、反轉 , 甚至停止老化 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	當你這麼想的時候 , 有99件事情可以讓我們老化 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	剝奪你的腦袋氧氣只花了幾分鐘 , 那些腦細胞就死了 , 它們永遠不會再回來 。
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	打網球太硬了 , 在你的膝蓋上 , 破壞了你的軟骨 , 軟骨從不回來 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的動脈可以堵塞 。 我們的大腦可以用斑塊來槍 , 我們可以得到阿茲海默症 。
there is just too many things to go wrong .	有太多事情要出錯了 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有35兆個細胞 , 數兆個有 「 t 」 。 我們在這裡談的是國家債務數字 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	那些細胞每八年一次轉變一次
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每當他們把自己轉到那邊時 , 都會造成一些損害 。 損害會加劇 。
and it builds up exponentially .	並且以指數的方式建造 。
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	這有點像當時我們都有披頭四的專輯或老鷹的專輯 , 我們會在錄音帶上複製一份 , 讓我們的朋友在錄音帶上複製 , 很快地 , 一代又一代的錄音帶 , 聽起來像是垃圾 。
well , the same things happen to our cells .	嗯 , 同樣的事情也發生在我們的細胞上 。
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼一個65歲的人老化速度比一個12歲的人快了125倍 。
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果沒有任何事情可以做來減緩老化或停止老化 , 我在這裡做什麼 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	嗯 , 事實上 , 最好的科學告訴我們 , 人體的能力 , 我的身體 , 你的身體 , 大約是九十年 , 多一點女性 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但這個國家的預期壽命只有78歲 。
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	所以 , 在這條線的某處 , 我們在桌子上留下了大約12年的美好年份 。
these are years that we could get .	我們能得到這些年 。
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究顯示 , 它們會大大免於慢性病、心臟病、癌症和糖尿病 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為 , 要讓這些失落的最好的方法 , 就是看看世界各地的文化 , 實際上正在經歷它們的文化 , 在這裡 , 人們的壽命比我們年齡高出100倍 , 比我們大上10倍 , 平均壽命多了十多年 , 中年死亡率的比例是這個國家的一小部分 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們發現我們的第一個藍色區大約125英里在義大利海岸外 , 在薩丁尼亞島 。
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	不是整個島嶼 , 島嶼大約有一百四十萬人 , 但只在高地上 , 一個叫做努羅省的區域 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	這裡我們有一個地區 , 男人的壽命最長 , 比我們在美國這裡的百歲人瑞還要長十倍 。
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	這裡的人不只能活到一百歲 , 還能活得不凡 。
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	那些102歲的老人仍然騎著腳踏車去工作 , 砍木頭 , 還能打敗一個比他們年輕60歲的人 。
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史實際上可以追溯到大約基督的時代 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	其實是青銅時代文化已被孤立
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為土地是如此的不穩定 , 大部份是牧羊人 , 這種動物偶爾會被定期、低強度的身體活動 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	他們的飲食主要是以植物為基礎的 , 以他們能帶到田裡的食物為主 。
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	他們想出了一個未發酵的全麥麵包 , 叫做carta音樂麵包 , 用全麥麵包做成的一種乳酪 , 用草製成的動物 , 這種乳酪在omega-3脂肪酸中 , 而不是omega-6脂肪酸 , 來自玉米餵養的動物 , 還有一種葡萄酒 , 比世界上任何已知的葡萄酒都要高三倍 。
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但我認為真正的秘密是他們組織社會的方式 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	而薩丁尼亞社會最突出的一個元素就是他們如何對待老年人 。
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你有沒有注意到 , 在美國 , 社會平等似乎在24歲時達到高峰 ?
just look at the advertisements .	只要看看那些廣告
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在薩丁尼亞 , 你得到的平等越大 , 你得到的智慧就越多 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	你進到薩丁尼亞的酒吧 , 而不是看到運動插畫的泳裝日曆 , 而是看到百歲人瑞的月曆 。
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	結果發現 , 這不只對你的老年父母親有益 , 讓他們與家人親近 , 還會有四到六年的預期壽命研究顯示 , 對那些家庭的孩子也有好處 , 他們的死亡率比較低 , 疾病率也比較低 。
that's called the grandmother effect .	也就是所謂的祖母效應 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們發現地球另一邊的第二個藍色區 , 大約在東京南邊800英里 , 在琉球的阿基比拉哥 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	琉球其實是161個小島
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	而在主島的北部 , 這是世界長壽的基礎零 。
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這是最古老的女性族群被找到的地方 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	在這個地方 , 人們有著世界上最長的無障礙壽命預期 。
they have what we want .	他們有我們想要的 。
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	他們活得很久 , 往往在睡眠中死去 , 很快 , 通常 , 我可以在性交後告訴你 。
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們比一般美國人多活七年 。
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	美國百歲人瑞的五倍
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	結腸癌和乳癌的比率是五分之一 , 美國這裡的大殺手 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	以及心血管疾病的六分之一 。
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	事實上 , 這種文化已經產生了這些數字 , 意味著他們有很強的能力可以教我們 。
what do they do ?	他們會怎麼做 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	再一次 , 以植物為基礎的飲食 , 裡面裝滿了許多顏色的蔬菜 。
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	而他們吃大約八倍於美國人的豆腐 。
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	比他們所吃的更重要 , 就是他們如何吃它 。
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各式各樣的小策略可以避免過度食用 , 如你所知 , 這是美國的一個大問題 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察到的幾個策略:它們會從較小的盤子上進食 , 所以它們在座的每一位攝取的卡路里會比較少 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	與其服務家庭風格 , 你可以在談話時無意吃東西 , 他們會在櫃台上服務 , 把食物帶走 , 然後帶到桌子上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們還有一段三千年的格言 , 我認為這是有史以來最偉大的飲食建議 。
it was invented by confucius .	是由孔子所發明的
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	而那種飲食就是所謂的 「 哈特奇 」 、 「 野牛飲食 」 。
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	簡單地說 , 這些人在吃飯前會說 , 提醒他們 , 在他們的胃部長度為80%時停止吃飯 。
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	整體的感覺需要半小時才能從肚子傳到大腦 。
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	藉由記住要停止百分之八十 , 就能幫助你不去做這件事 。
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但 , 就像薩丁尼亞 , 琉球有少數的社會建構可以讓我們與長壽聯繫在一起 。
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道孤立會殺害
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	十五年前 , 美國人平均有三個好朋友 。
we're down to one and half right now .	我們現在已經降到一半了 。
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你幸運地在琉球出生 , 你生在一個系統 , 你自動有半個朋友 , 和你在人生中旅行 。
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱之為moai 。 如果你在moai , 你被期待分享的就是如果你碰到運氣 , 如果事情不好 , 孩子會生病 , 父母會死去 , 總是有人會背負你的背 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這個特別的摩艾 , 這五位女士已經在一起九十七年了 。
their average age is 102 .	他們的平均年齡是102歲 。
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	通常在美國 , 我們把成人生活分成兩部分 。
there is our work life , where we're productive .	我們的工作是有生產力的 。
and then one day , boom , we retire .	然後有一天 , 砰 , 我們退休了 。
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	通常這意味著要退休到簡單的椅子上 , 或下降到亞利桑那州去打高爾夫 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在琉球語中 , 甚至沒有退休的字眼 。
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	反而有一個詞會讓你一生充滿活力 , 而那個字就是 「 生生生生生生生生的 」 。
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	而且 , 大概是翻譯的意思是 「 早上醒來的理由 」 。
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	對這位102歲的karate大師而言 , 他的ikigai正在帶著這項武器藝術 。
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	對這位一百歲的漁夫來說 , 這隻漁夫持續為他的家人捕魚 , 一週三次 。
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	這是個問題 。 國家老化研究院實際上給了我們一個問卷 , 給這些百歲人瑞 。
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	其中一個問題 , 他們在文化上很常見 , 他們是那些把問卷放在了的人 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你的ikigai是什麼 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們馬上就知道為什麼早上醒來
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	對這位102歲的女人來說 , 她的ikigai就是她的曾曾孫女 。
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩個女孩在101年半的時候分開了
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她 , 拿著一個曾曾孫女的感覺是怎樣的 。
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	她把頭放回去 , 說: 「 感覺就像跳上天堂一樣 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我以為那是個很棒的想法 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我在地理雜誌的編輯希望我能找到美國的藍寶地 。
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	有一陣子 , 我們看著明尼蘇達的金字塔 , 那裡的確有很高的百歲人瑞 。
but that's because all the young people left .	但那是因為所有的年輕人都離開了 。
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們又轉向數據 。
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們發現美國最長壽的族群 , 位於第七天的冒險家集中在加州的洛馬林達市附近 。
adventists are conservative methodists .	先驅者是保守的方法論者 。
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	他們在星期五從日落上慶祝他們的安息日 , 直到星期六日 。
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	一個 " 24小時的避難所 " , 他們稱之為
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	他們遵循五個小習慣 , 來傳達給他們非凡的長壽 , 相對來說 。
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	在美國 , 一般女性的平均壽命是80 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但對一個冒險的女人來說 , 他們的預期壽命是89 。
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	不同之處在於 , 在男性中更明顯 , 他們預期的壽命會比美國人的住所要長達11年 。
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	現在 , 這個研究追蹤了約七萬人三十年 。
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	史特林研究 。 而我認為它非常能說明這個藍色區域計畫的前提 。
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是一個異型社區 。
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	是白人、黑人、西班牙人、亞洲人 。
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	他們唯一的共同點就是一組非常小的生活習慣 , 他們大半輩子都遵循儀式式 。
they take their diet directly from the bible .	直接從聖經上拿走他們的飲食 。
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	gensis:第一章 , 上帝說過29 , 上帝講到的樂高和種子 , 再來談談綠色植物 , 很可能缺乏肉類 。
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們認真看待這個庇護所 。
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每週有24小時 , 不論他們多忙 , 工作壓力多大 , 孩子們需要被驅使 , 他們停止一切 , 專注在他們的上帝、他們的社交網路上 , 然後 , 在宗教裡 , 天生就是走路 。
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	這種力量並不是偶爾完成 , 力量是每週一次都在進行 。
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	一點都不難 。 沒有一個花錢 。
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	冒險家也傾向與其他的冒險家共處 。
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去找一位冒險家的派對 , 你不會看到有人在游吉姆貝姆 , 或滾動一個關節 。
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	取而代之的是他們在談他們的下一個自然步行 , 交換食譜 , 是的 , 他們祈禱 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但它們會以很深刻且可衡量的方式影響彼此 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這個文化讓埃爾斯•沃爾斯•哈雷姆受益 。
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	埃爾斯沃雷斯•厄姆九十七歲 。
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是千萬富翁 , 但當一個包商要六千美金來蓋一座隱私柵欄時 , 他說: 「 為了那種錢我會自己做 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	所以接下來的三天 , 他出去擠壓水泥 , 到處跑 。
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	可預測的是 , 也許在第四天 , 他最後進到手術室 。
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不是像桌子上的那個人 , 而是開心手術的那個人 。
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	九十七歲時 , 他每個月仍然做二十次開心手術 。
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	艾德•羅林斯 , 103歲 , 一個活躍的牛仔 , 用游泳開始他的早晨 。
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	在週末 , 他喜歡貼在板子上 , 丟出羅斯特的尾巴 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她的孫子其實住在這裡的雙胞胎城市 。
she starts her day with lifting weights .	她從升起體重開始一天 。
she rides her bicycle .	她騎腳踏車
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	然後她穿上了牠的羅盤 , 1994年凱迪拉克塞維爾 , 沿著聖柏納迪諾高速公路撕下去 , 在那裡 , 她仍自願為七個不同的組織做志工 。
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我曾參加過19次艱難的探險
i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我大概是你會遇到的唯一一個人 , 他騎腳踏車穿過撒哈拉沙漠 , 沒有防曬霜 。
but i'll tell you , there is no adventure more harrowing than riding shotgun with marge deton .	但我要告訴各位 , 沒有任何冒險比騎馬克•戴頓時更具殺傷力 。
" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	「 一個陌生人是我還沒見過的朋友 ! 」 她會對我說:
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	那麼 , 在這三個文化中 , 共有的是什麼 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	他們都在做些什麼 ?
and we managed to boil it down to nine .	我們成功地把它歸為9 。
in fact we've done two more blue zone expeditions since this and these common denominators hold true .	事實上 , 我們已經完成了兩次藍寶地探險 , 自從這之後 , 這些常見的探險家才是真的 。
and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	首先 , 我將要說出一個這裡 , 沒有一個是運動 , 至少我們認為運動的方式 。
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	相反地 , 他們設立了自己的生活 , 這樣他們不斷被推進身體活動 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這些百歲的琉球婦女正在起身離開地面 , 她們坐在地板上 , 每天30或40次 。
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	薩丁尼亞人住在垂直的房子裡 , 上下樓梯 。
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每次旅行到商店 , 或去教堂 , 或去朋友家裡偶爾會散步 。
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有任何便利性 。
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	沒有按鈕來推動做院子工作或房子工作 。
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們想要混合蛋糕 , 他們用手做 。
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	燃燒的熱量和跑步機一樣多 。
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們做有意願的身體活動時 , 就是他們喜歡的東西 。 他們傾向會走路 , 唯一證明可以脫離認知衰退的方法 , 他們都傾向於擁有一個花園 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何用正確的方式來設定他們的生活 , 這樣他們才有正確的視野 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	每一種文化都需要時間去往下移 。
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	薩丁尼亞人祈禱 。 第七天的冒險家祈禱 。
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	琉球人有這種祖先的移情
