but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你匆促或有壓力時 , 會觸發一種叫做 「 發炎反應 」 的東西 , 和所有東西都有關 , 從阿茲海默症到心血管疾病 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你每天慢下來15分鐘 , 你會把那個發炎狀態轉變成更抗炎的狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	他們有詞彙 , 可以用來感知目的、ikigai , 就像琉球人一樣 。
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你知道你生命中最危險的兩年是你出生的那一年 , 因為嬰兒死亡率 , 以及你退休的那一年 。
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道他們人生的目的感 , 並且活躍起來 , 這價值約七年的額外壽命 。
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽飲食
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	相反地 , 這些人每天都喝一點點 , 不是很難賣給美國人口 。
they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	他們傾向於以植物為主的飲食
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	不代表他們不吃肉 , 而是大量的豆子和堅果 。
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	他們有策略不讓它們過度食用 , 小東西會在適當的時間把它們推離桌子 。
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	這一切的基礎是它們如何連結在一起 。
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們把家人放在第一 , 照顧他們的孩子和老年父母 。
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們都傾向於以信仰為基礎的社群 , 這個社群值四到十四年的預期壽命如果你一個月做四次 ,
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	這裡最大的是他們也屬於正確的部落 。
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	他們要麼生來就要不就是主動與對的人圍在一起 。
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從弗林漢研究中得知 , 如果你三個最好的朋友都過胖 , 你就有50%的機會過重 。
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 如果你和不健康的人在一起 , 這會隨著時間產生很大的影響 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	相反地 , 如果你朋友的休閒理念是身體活動、保齡球、打曲棍球、騎腳踏車或園藝 , 如果你的朋友喝了一點 , 但不多 , 他們吃得對 , 他們很投入 , 信任和可信 , 這會隨時間產生最大的影響 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	飲食是行不通的 。 世界歷史上沒有任何飲食對超過百分之二的人口都行得通 。
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	運動計畫通常從一月開始 ; 通常是十月份完成 。
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	長壽沒有短期固定在藥丸或其他東西上 。
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但當你仔細想想 , 你的朋友是長期的冒險 , 因此 , 或許是最顯著的事 , 你能做的事 , 以增添多年的生活 , 並且延續幾年的生活 。 非常謝謝你 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	墨水會導電 ; 一扇窗戶會從開關的清晰轉向不透明的開關 ; 一種讓音樂存在的水母 。 所有這些東西都存在 。 卡塔娜莫塔說:是時候該玩了 。 莫塔帶領我們踏上驚喜和酷炫的新材料之旅 , 建議我們找出它們的好方法 , 就是要實驗、改裝、讓它們有樂趣 。
creativity , design , technology	創造力、設計、科技、
catarina mota: play with smart materials	catarinamota:玩弄智慧型材料
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我有個在葡萄牙的朋友 , 他的祖父用腳踏車和洗衣機建造了一台車 , 讓他可以運送他的家人 。
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他這麼做是因為他買不起車子 , 也因為他知道如何建造一台車 。
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	曾經有一段時間 , 我們了解事物如何運作 , 以及它們是如何被製造出來的 , 這樣我們才能建造、修復它們 , 或最少針對該購買什麼 , 做出資訊的決策 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	許多這些做法在二十世紀後半就已經失去了 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 自造者社群和開源模型正把這種知識帶到我們的生活中 , 關於事物如何運作 , 以及它們是什麼組成的 , 我相信我們需要把它們帶到下一個層級 , 到組成的元件上 。
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	大部分的情況下 , 我們仍然知道紙張和紡織品的傳統材料是什麼組成 , 以及它們是如何生產的 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有了這些令人驚奇、具體的複合材料 , 可以改變形狀、會導電的油漆、會改變顏色的顏料、會發光的布料 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我給你們看一些例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	所以導電油墨讓我們可以畫電路而不是用傳統印刷電路板或電線
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	在我舉的這個小例子中 , 我們用它來創造一個觸控感應器 , 透過打開這個小燈 , 來對我的皮膚做出反應 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	導電油墨已經被藝術家使用了 , 但最近的發展顯示 , 我們很快就能在雷射印表機和筆上使用 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這張圖是用無色光分散的粒子所注入的油晶體 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	這意味著 , 雖然一般的丙烯酸鹽只會散射到邊緣的光 , 這會照亮整個表面 , 當我打開周圍的燈時 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	這項材料的兩項已知應用包括室內設計和多點觸控系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	而熱色素會在特定溫度下改變顏色 。
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	我要把這個放在一個熱板上 , 溫度比環境稍高一點 , 你可以看到會發生什麼事 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	所以 , 這種材料的其中一項原則是 , 在嬰兒奶瓶裡 , 其它東西 , 在嬰兒奶瓶裡 , 它表示 , 當內容物夠酷時 , 可以飲用 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	這些只是眾所皆知的智慧型材料中的一些 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	幾年後 , 它們會成為我們每天使用的許多物品和技術 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們可能還沒有科幻小說裡的飛天車承諾過我們 , 但我們可以有改變顏色的牆壁 , 依據溫度變化 , 會捲起來的鍵盤 , 窗戶會變得不透明 , 在開關的一閃而過 。
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	所以 , 我是社會科學家 , 透過訓練 , 所以 , 為什麼我今天在這裡談智慧型材料 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是製造家 。
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我很好奇事物如何運作 , 以及它們如何被製造 , 也因為我相信我們應該要對構成我們世界的元件有更深的了解 , 而現在 , 我們對於這些高科技複合體的了解 , 我們的未來將不足以組成 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	智慧型材料很難在小量中取得 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	幾乎沒有任何相關資訊可以用在如何使用它們上 , 很少有人說它們是如何生產的 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	所以 , 目前 , 它們大多存在於這個貿易秘密和專利的領域中 , 只有大學和企業才能取得 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	三年前 , 克莉絲蒂男孩和我開始了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為開放材料 。
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	這是一個網站 , 我們和其他任何想加入我們的人 , 分享實驗 , 發表資訊 , 鼓勵其他人隨時都可以貢獻 , 並且集合資源 , 像是其他像我們一樣的自造者的研究論文和課程 。
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們希望它能成為一個大型、集體的資料庫 , 以智慧型材料為出發點 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但我們為什麼要在乎智慧型材料是如何運作的 ? 以及它們是由什麼組成的 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法塑造我們不了解的東西 , 而我們不了解和使用的東西 , 最後會塑造我們 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們使用的物品、穿的衣服、我們所居住的房子 , 都對我們的行為、健康和生活品質有著深遠的影響 。
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以 , 如果我們生活在一個由智慧型材料組成的世界 , 我們應該要知道並了解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	其次 , 同樣重要的是 , 創新一直都是由tinker所推動的 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	許多次 , 業餘演員 , 而非專家 , 一直是發明家和改進者 , 從登山腳踏車到半導體、個人電腦、飛機 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是 , 材料科學是複雜的 , 且需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但事實並非總是如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	伊利諾州大學的兩位科學家了解這一點 , 當時他們用更簡單的方法發表了一篇論文 , 來製造導電墨水 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	喬登•布恩克對化學毫無經驗直到那時 , 他才讀這篇論文 , 並在他的自造者空間中重製出實驗 , 只用現成的物質和工具 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用烤麵包機 , 甚至做出自己的旋渦混合器 , 根據另一位科學家的課輔 。
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	約旦接著在網路上發表了他的成果 , 包括所有他曾經嘗試過、沒有用的東西 , 讓其他人可以研究、繁殖它 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	所以 , 約旦的創新主要形式是把一個實驗在一所熟練的大學實驗室裡進行 , 並在芝加哥的車庫中重現它 , 只使用廉價的材料和工具 , 他自己製作的工具 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在他發表了這個作品 , 其他人可以拿起他離開的地方 , 想出更簡單的流程和改善 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另一個例子我想提一下她的計畫的目標是強調材料的表達特質同時專注於建造者的創造力和技巧
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子裝置非常強大 , 它們教導我們事物的運作方式 , 但它們設計的限制會影響我們學習的方式 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	所以漢娜的做法 , 另一方面 , 是要制定一系列的技術 , 來創造出不尋常的物品 , 讓我們免於預先設計的限制 , 來教導我們關於材料本身的知識 。
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	所以在漢娜的許多令人印象深刻的實驗中 , 這是我最喜歡的一個 。
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	[紙喇叭]我們現在看到的只是一張紙上面有一些銅膠帶連接著一個mp3播放器和磁鐵
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	所以根據麻省理工學院的marcelocoelho的研究漢娜創造了一系列的紙喇叭 , 用各式各樣的材料 , 從簡單的銅膠帶 , 到導電布和墨水 。
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像約旦和其他許多製造者一樣 , 漢娜發表了她的食譜 , 讓任何人可以複製、繁殖它們 。
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙電子產品是最有前景的材料科學分支 , 讓我們能創造出更便宜、更靈活的電子產品 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	所以漢娜的手工藝作品 , 以及她分享她的發現的事實 , 打開了一扇門 , 通往一系列新的可能性 , 兩者都是美學和創新的 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	所以 , 製造者有趣的地方在於我們用熱情和好奇心創造出來 , 我們不怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們經常從不規則的角度來處理問題 , 在過程中 , 最後發現替代方案 , 或甚至更好的方法來做事 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以 , 越多人用材料做實驗 , 就越多研究人員願意分享他們的研究 , 製造商他們的知識 , 我們就越有機會創造出真正為我們服務的科技 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	我覺得有點像泰德納爾森在1970年代早期 , 他寫道: 「 你現在一定要了解電腦 。 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	那時 , 電腦是只有科學家在乎的大型主機 , 沒有人想過要在家裡裝一個 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以 , 這有點奇怪 , 我站在這裡說: 「 你現在必須要了解智慧型材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	請記住 , 取得關於新興科技的先驅知識 , 是確保我們在未來能有發言權的最佳方式 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們會進入一個玻璃泡 , 鎖上門 , 按下加速器 , 仰賴我們的眼睛來指導我們 , 即使我們只能看到前面和後面的少數車輛 。 但如果汽車能彼此分享他們的位置和速度 , 以及可預測的模型 , 來計算路上每個人最安全的路線 ? 珍妮佛•海耶想像一個沒有意外的世界 。
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	珍妮佛•海利:如果車子能說話 , 意外可能會被避免 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	讓我們面對現實:開車是危險的 。
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	這是我們不喜歡去思考的事情之一 , 但事實上 , 宗教圖像和好運氣charm出現在世界各地的儀表板上 , 我們知道這個事實是真的 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍是美國16到19歲死亡人數的主因 , 導致死亡的主因 , 其中75%的意外與毒品或酒精無關 。
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒有人能肯定地說 , 但我記得我的第一個意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	我當時是高速公路上的年輕駕駛員 , 前面的車子 , 我看到煞車燈亮了起來 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我說: 「 好吧 , 好吧 , 這傢伙慢下來了 , 我也會慢下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我踩煞車 。
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但不 , 這傢伙並沒有慢下來 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這個人在高速公路上停下來 , 死了 , 死了 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	剛好是65比0 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我踩煞車 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我感受到abs的踢進去 , 車子還在 , 它不會停下來 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 空氣袋子部署 , 車子完全沒有人受傷 。 幸好 , 沒有人受傷 。
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我完全不知道車子停了下來 , 我想我們能做得更好 。
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我認為我們可以藉由讓我們的車子彼此交談 , 轉變駕駛體驗 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我只是想讓你們稍微想一下開車的經驗是怎樣的 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	進入你的車 , 關上門 。 你在玻璃泡裡 。
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你無法真正直接感受到周遭的世界 。
you're in this extended body .	你在這個延伸的身體裡 ,
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你的任務是將它導入部份的路徑中 , 在其他的金屬巨人中 , 在超人的速度下 。
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	好嗎 ? 而你只需要指導你是你的兩隻眼睛 。
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好吧 , 這就是你所有的眼睛 , 不是為了這個任務而設計的 , 但是人們要你做一些事 , 像是 , 你想做一個車道的改變 , 他們最先要你做的事是什麼 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	把你的眼光從路上移下來 。 沒錯 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	別再看你要去哪了 , 轉身 , 檢查你的盲點 , 然後開車下去 , 不看你要去哪裡 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	你和其他人 。 這是安全的駕駛方式 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	我們為什麼要這麼做 ? 因為我們必須 , 我們必須做出選擇 , 我看這裡還是看這裡 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常我們會做一份很棒的工作 , 選擇我們在路上的目的 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾我們會錯過一些事 。
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾我們會感覺到一些不對或太晚的事 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	在無數的意外中 , 司機說: 「 我沒看到它來了 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我相信這點 , 我相信
we can only watch so much .	我們只能看這麼多 。
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但現在科技的存在可以幫助我們改善這一點 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	在未來 , 有了汽車互相交換資料 , 我們將能看到的不只是前面三台車 , 還有後面三台車 , 左邊和左邊 , 同時 , 鳥類的眼睛視野 , 我們將能夠看見那些車子 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們將能看到前面車輛的速度 , 看看那傢伙走得多快或多快 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那傢伙下降到零 , 我會知道 ,
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	透過計算和演算法和預測模型 , 我們將能夠看到未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你可能覺得那不可能 。
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你要如何預測未來 ? 這真的很難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	實際上 , 沒有 。 有了汽車 , 並不是不可能的 。
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	汽車是三維的物體有固定的位置和速度
they travel down roads .	沿著道路旅行
often they travel on prepublished routes .	通常他們會在預先出版的路上旅行 。
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	要合理地預測車子在不久的將來的位置 , 並不難 。
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	就算你在車子裡 , 摩托車騎士來了 ! 時速85英哩 , 車道平衡--我知道你有過這種經驗--那傢伙不是 「 無處可去 」 。
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	那傢伙在路上可能已經半小時了 。
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	對吧 ? 我的意思是 , 有人見過他 。
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	10、20、30英里前 , 有人看過那個傢伙 , 一旦有一輛車看到那個傢伙 , 把他放在地圖上 , 他的地圖位置、速度、很好的估計他會以每小時85英里的速度持續下去 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你會知道 , 因為你的車會知道 , 因為其他車會在他耳邊低語一些東西 , 比如: 「 順便一提 , 五分鐘 , 摩托車騎士 , 小心 。 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以合理的預測汽車的行為 。
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 他們是牛頓的物品 。
that's very nice about them .	那對他們是很棒的 。
so how do we get there ?	所以 , 我們要如何達到目的 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從簡單的東西開始 , 就像在車子之間分享我們的位置資料一樣 , 只是分享gps 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我車上有gps和攝影機 , 我有一個很精確的概念 , 知道我在哪裡 , 以及我走得多快 。
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	有了電腦視覺 , 我可以估計我身邊的車子在哪裡 , 有點像是 , 及它們要往哪裡去 。
and same with the other cars .	其他車也一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	他們可以很精確地知道他們在哪裡 , 並且有點模糊地知道其他車子在哪裡 。
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩部車共享這些數據 , 如果它們彼此交談 , 會發生什麼事 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以告訴你的確切結果 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	bobwang教授和他的團隊做了電腦模擬當fuzy估計結合時會發生什麼事即使是輕型交通工具 , 當車子只分享gps數據我們也將這項研究從電腦模擬中移到機器人測試床上這些設備現在在這些機器人上有實際的感應器:s音響攝影機、gps還有2d立體雷射測量器在系統中很常見
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們還附著一個短距離的短距離通訊收音機 , 機器人彼此交談 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些飛行器互相靠近時 , 它們會精確地追蹤彼此的位置 , 它們就能避開彼此的距離 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	我們現在在混搭中加入越來越多的機器人 , 我們遇到了一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	其中一個問題 , 當你收到太多的聊天器時 , 你很難處理所有的包裝 , 所以你必須優先順序 , 而這就是預測模型幫助你的地方 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機器人車都在追蹤被預測的軌跡 , 你不會去注意那些包裝 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	優先順序一位看似有點離譜的人 。
that guy could be a problem .	那傢伙可能是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	而且可以預測新的軌跡
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他怎麼下去了 , 你知道的 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	而你知道你需要哪些駕駛才能警示走出去 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	我們想怎麼警告每一個人 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些車子怎麼會悄悄地說: 「 你需要走出去 ? 」
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	嗯 , 這取決於兩件事:第一 , 汽車的能力 , 第二 , 駕駛的能力 。
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果一個人有一輛很棒的車 , 但他們在手機上 , 或者 , 你知道的 , 做點什麼 , 他們不可能會在緊急情況中做出最好的反應 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	所以我們開始了不同的研究線 , 做駕駛者州立模型 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 用一系列的三台攝影機 , 我們可以偵測到駕駛員是否正在往前看 , 往下看 , 在電話上 , 或者喝杯咖啡 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預測意外事故 , 我們可以預測誰 , 哪一輛車在最好的位置 , 可以搬出去計算每個人最安全的路線 。
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	基本上 , 這些技術今天的存在
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為我們面臨的最大問題是我們自己的意願去分享我們的資料 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我覺得這是一個令人不安的概念 , 我們的車子會看著我們 , 和其他車子談話 , 我們會在八卦的大海中走下去 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信 , 它可以用一種方式來保護我們的隱私 , 就像現在一樣 , 當我從外面看你的車時 , 我其實並不清楚你 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	如果我看你的車牌號碼 , 我不知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信我們的車子可以在背後談論我們 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	而我認為這將會是一件很棒的事 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	我希望各位稍微考慮一下 , 如果你不想要讓你後面那個分心的青少年知道你在煞車 , 你來到死胡同 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	透過願意分享我們的資料 , 我們可以為每個人做到最好 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以 , 讓你的車子八卦一下你 。
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	會讓道路安全許多
x prize founder peter diamandis talks about how he helped stephen hawking fulfill his dream of going to space by flying together into the upper atmosphere and experiencing weightlessness at zero g .	xprize的創辦人彼得•戴曼迪斯談到他如何協助史蒂芬•霍金實現太空的夢想 , 通過一起飛入大氣層中 , 體驗到零g的無重力 。
business , flight , science , short talk , space , technology , universe	商業、航班、科學、簡短的演講、空間、科技、宇宙、宇宙、
peter diamandis on stephen hawking in zero g	彼得•戴曼迪斯在零g的stephenhawkings上
those of you who know me know how passionate i am about opening the space frontier .	認識我的人都知道我有多熱衷於打開太空邊境 。
so when i had the chance to give the world's expert in gravity the experience of zero gravity , it was incredible .	所以當我有機會給世界重力專家帶來重力的體驗-無重力的體驗時 , 真是不可思議 。
and i want to tell you that story .	我想告訴各位那個故事 。
i first met him through the archon x prize for genomics .	我第一次見到他透過基因組學的archonxprize
it's a competition we're holding , the second x prize , for the first team to sequence 100 human genomes in 10 days .	這是我們所舉辦的競賽 , 第二個xprize , 為第一個在十天內完成100個人類基因組定序的團隊 。
we have something called the genome 100 100 individuals we're sequencing as part of that .	我們有所謂的 " 基因體 " -100個我們將其定序為其中的一部分
craig venter chairs that event .	克萊格•凡特斯那事件的椅子 。
and i met professor hawking , and he said his dream was to travel into space .	我和霍金教授見面 , 他說他的夢想是要進入太空 。
and i said , " i can't take you there , but i can take you into weightlessness into zerog .	我說: 「 我不能帶你去那裡 , 但我可以帶你進入無重力進入無重力 。
and he said , on the spot , " absolutely , yes . "	他說: 「 絕對可以 。 」
well , the only way to experience zerog on earth is actually with parabolic flight , weightless flight .	嗯 , 地球上唯一能體驗無重力飛行的方法 , 其實是搭乘拋物飛行 , 無重力飛行 。
you take an airplane , you fly over the top , you're weightless for 25 seconds .	你搭飛機 , 飛越頂端 , 體重25秒 。
come back down , you weigh twice as much .	回來 , 你的體重是兩倍 。
you do it again and again .	你一而再、再而三地
you can get eight , 10 minutes of weightlessness how nasa's trained their astronauts for so long .	你可以得到8、10分鐘的無重力nasa如何訓練他們的太空人這麼久
we set out to do this .	我們開始做這件事 。
it took us 11 years to become operational .	我們花了11年才開始營運 。
and we announced that we were going to fly stephen hawking .	然後我們宣布要讓史蒂芬•霍金飛行 。
we had one government agency and one company aircraft operator say , you're crazy , don't do that , you're going kill the guy .	我們有一間政府機關 , 一家公司的飛機操作員說 , 你瘋了 , 不要這樣做 , 你就會殺了那個人 。
and he wanted to go .	而他想去
we worked hard to get all the permissions .	我們努力取得所有的許可 。
and six months later , we sat down at kennedy space center .	六個月後 , 我們在甘迺迪太空中心坐下 。
we had a press conference , we announced our intent to do one zerog parabola , give him 25 seconds of zerog .	我們舉辦了一場媒體大會 , 我們宣佈我們的目的是要做一場無重力拋物線拋物 , 給他25秒的zerog 。
and if it went really well , we might do three parabolas .	如果一切順利的話 , 我們可能會做三個拋物面鏡 。
well , we asked him why he wanted to go up and do this .	我們問他 , 為什麼他要上去做這件事 。
and what he said , for me , was very moving .	他所說的 , 對我來說 , 非常感動 。
he said , " life on earth is at an everincreasing risk of being wiped out by disaster . . .	他說: 「 地球上的生命正冒著越來越多的風險 , 被災難所消滅......
i think the human race doesn't have a future if it doesn't go into space .	我認為 , 如果不進入太空 , 人類就沒有未來 。
i therefore want to encourage public interest in space . "	因此我想要鼓勵公眾對太空的興趣 。 」
we took him out to the kennedy space center , up inside the nasa vehicle , into the back of the zerog airplane .	我們帶他到甘迺迪太空中心 , 在太空總署的車內 , 前往zerog飛機的後面 。
we had about 20 people who made donations we raised $150 , 000 in donations for children's charities who flew with us .	我們大約有20個人做捐款 , 我們募集了150 , 000美元 , 捐贈給那些和我們一起飛行的兒童慈善團體 。
a few tedsters here .	這裡的幾位ted成員
we set up a whole er .	我們設置了一整個er
we had four emergency room doctors and two nurses on board the airplane .	我們有四個急診室醫生和兩位護士登上飛機 。
we were monitoring his po2 of his blood , his heart rate , his blood pressure .	我們在監測他的血液 , 他的心率 , 他的血壓 。
we had everything all set in case of an emergency ; god knows , you don't want to hurt this worldrenowned expert .	萬一緊急情況發生 , 天知道 , 你不想傷害這個世界知名的專家 。
we took off from the shuttle landing facility , where the shuttle takes off and lands .	我們從太空梭降落場起飛 , 太空梭在那裡起飛 , 降落 。
and my partner byron lichtenberg and i carefully suspended him into zerog .	而我和我的夥伴byronlichtenberg , 小心地把他吊成zerog 。
once he was there , [we] let him go to experience what weightlessness was truly like .	一旦他在那裡 , 我們就讓他去體驗無重力真正的樣子 。
and after that first parabola , you know , the doc said everything is great . he was smiling , and we said go .	在那第一個拋物面鏡之後 , 你知道的 , 醫生說一切都很棒 。 他笑了 , 我們說去吧 。
so we did a second parabola .	所以我們做了第二個拋物線飛行 。
we actually floated an apple in homage to sir isaac newton because professor hawking holds the same chair at cambridge that isaac newton did .	我們實際上是向艾薩克•牛頓爵士搭乘一顆蘋果 , 因為霍金教授在劍橋拿著同樣的椅子 , 那是艾薩克•牛頓所做的 。
and we did a fourth , and a fifth and a sixth .	我們做了第四個 , 第五個和第六個 。
and a seventh and an eighth .	和第七個和第八個
and this man does not look like a 65yearold wheelchairbound man .	這位男士看起來不像65歲的輪椅男子 。
he was so happy .	他好高興 。
we are living on a precious jewel , and it's during our lifetime that we're moving off this planet .	我們生活在一個珍貴的珠寶上 , 在我們有生之年 , 我們正在離開這個星球 。
please join us in this epic adventure .	請加入我們在這史詩般的冒險中
medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫學動畫師davidbolinsky提出了3分鐘驚人的動畫 , 顯示細胞內的繁忙生活 。
design , entertainment , film , health , medicine , science , technology , visualizations	設計、娛樂、電影、健康、醫學、科學、科技、視覺化 。
david bolinsky animates a cell	davidbolinsky動畫一個細胞
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是醫學插畫家 , 我來自稍微不同的觀點 。
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	自從我成長以來 , 我一直在看真與美的表達在藝術中 , 真與美的表達在科學中 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	雖然這兩者都是自己權利的美好事物 , 但兩者都有非常美好的美好事物 , 能將科學和數學視為理想的事物 , 幾乎就像是科學家想要約會的理想雙胞胎 。
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些表達真相是令人敬畏的事物 , 意即 , 它們是你能崇拜的事物 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	它們是強而有力的理想 。 它們是不可思議的 。
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	它們是獨一無二的 。 它們有時是有用的 , 通常是之後很長一段時間 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	你現在可以將其中一些照片翻轉過來 , 因為我不想在螢幕上看著我 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	真與美是對不在科學界的人來說常常不透明的事物 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	它們是用來形容美麗的事物 , 通常只有在你了解這個主題的語言和語法中 , 才能理解真與美 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你看數學 , e=mc平方 , 如果你看宇宙常數 , 那裡有一個人類的理想 , 你看到生命必須從描述宇宙的數字中演化出來 , 這些都是非常難理解的 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	自從我以醫學插畫家的身份 , 開始接受我的訓練 , 由我父親教我的動畫 , 他是一位雕塑家和我的視覺導師 , 我想找出一個方法 , 幫助人們了解生物科學的真與美 , 藉由動畫 , 用圖片 , 說故事 , 讓那些不見得是明顯的事物 , 可以被教導 , 並且可以被理解 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	現今的學生常常沉浸在一個環境中 , 他們學習的主題是有真與美 , 深植在其中 , 但他們被教導的方式是相對的 , 被拉到事實和美麗不見得都是明顯的 。
it's almost like that old recipe for chicken soup where you boil the chicken until the flavor is just gone .	幾乎就像是雞湯的舊食譜 , 你把雞煮沸了 , 直到香味消失 。
we don't want to do that to our students .	我們不想對我們的學生
so we have an opportunity to really open up education .	所以我們有機會真正開放教育
and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	幾年前 , 我接到哈佛大學的robertlue打來的電話 , 在分子和細胞生物學部門 , 他問我 , 我和我的團隊是否有興趣 , 並願意真正改變哈佛大學的醫學和科學教育 。
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	所以我們開始進行一個專案 , 探究細胞能夠探索分子和細胞生物學中與生俱來的真與美 , 讓學生能更了解這些事實 。
they could have a mental image of the cell as a large , bustling , hugely complicated city that's occupied by micromachines .	他們可以把細胞的心智圖像當作一個大型、破壞、非常複雜的城市 , 被微機械所佔據 。
and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	這些微機械真的是生命的核心 。
these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微機械 , 正是世界各地的羨慕 , 它們是自我導向、強大、精確、精確、精確的裝置 , 它們是用胺基酸串成的 。
and these micromachines power how a cell moves .	而這些微機械會如何影響細胞的移動 。
they power how a cell replicates . they power our hearts .	它們能供電一個細胞如何複製 。 它們能供給我們的心臟 。
they power our minds .	它們能驅動我們的心靈 。
and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	我們想做的是 , 要想出如何把這個故事變成一個動畫 , 這個動畫是哈佛大學生物顧問的中心 , 這個網站是哈佛大學的 「 分子與細胞生物學 」 學生們 , 除了所有文字訊息以外 , 除了視覺上把所有東西放在一起以外 , 這樣這些學生就會有內視能力去研究細胞的真與美 , 並用這個觀點去研究這些觀點 , 讓他們的想像力能夠被激發 , 讓他們的想像力能夠發揮 , 讓他們的心靈活 。
so we set out by looking at how these molecules are put together .	所以我們開始研究這些分子是如何組合在一起的 。
we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們與一個主題合作 , 也就是說 , 巨噬細胞在微血管內流動 , 它們在觸碰微血管壁的表面 , 它們從毛細管壁上的細胞中取得資訊 , 它們在外面有發炎症 , 無法看見和感知 。
but they get the information that causes them to stop , causes them to internalize that they need to make all of the various parts that will cause them to change their shape , and try to get out of this capillary and find out what's going on .	但它們得到了導致它們停止的資訊 , 導致它們內化 , 它們需要製造出所有造成它們改變形狀的各個部分 , 並試著脫離這種微血管 , 找出到底發生了什麼事 。
so these molecular motors we had to work with the harvard scientists and databank models of the atomically accurate molecules and figure out how they moved , and figure out what they did .	所以這些分子馬達我們必須和哈佛的科學家及數據bank模型合作 , 這些原子上精確的分子 , 找出它們如何移動 , 找出它們做了什麼 。
and figure out how to do this in a way that was truthful in that it imparted what was going on , but not so truthful that the compact crowding in a cell would prevent the vista from happening .	想出如何實現這一點 , 讓它能夠實現 , 但事實並非如此 , 細胞中的緊密擁擠會阻止視覺發生 。
and so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute reader's digest version of the first aspect of this film that we produced . it's an ongoing project that's going to go another four or five years .	接下來我要給你們看的是一個三分鐘的讀者消化版本 , 是我們製作的這部電影的第一面 。 這是一個持續進行的計劃 , 接下來四、五年 。
and i want you to look at this and see the paths that the cell manufactures these little walking machines , they're called kinesins that take these huge loads that would challenge an ant in relative size .	請各位看看這個 , 看到細胞製造這些小步行機器的路徑 , 它們被稱為 「 腎上腺素 」 , 將這些巨大的負荷 , 以相對尺寸來挑戰螞蟻 。
run the movie , please .	拍電影 , 拜託
but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些能驅動細胞內部的機器 , 真的很了不起 , 它們真的是所有生命的基礎 , 因為所有這些機器彼此互動 。
they pass information to each other .	它們會互相傳遞信息 。
they cause different things to happen inside the cell .	它們造成細胞內不同的事情發生 。
and the cell will actually manufacture the parts that it needs on the fly , from information that's brought from the nucleus by molecules that read the genes .	細胞會製造果蠅所需要的部位 , 從讀取基因的分子所取得的資訊中 。
no life , from the smallest life to everybody here , would be possible without these little micromachines .	沒有任何生命 , 從最小的生命到這裡的每個人 , 若沒有這些小微機械 , 就有可能實現 。
in fact , it would really , in the absence of these machines , have made the attendance here , chris , really quite sparse .	事實上 , 在沒有這些機器的情況下 , 它的出席率真的很高 , 克里斯 , 真的很矛盾 。
this is the fedex delivery guy of the cell .	這是細胞的fedex遞送小伙子 。
this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這個小傢伙被稱為 「 腎上腺素 」 , 他把一個裝滿全新的製造蛋白質的袋子拉到細胞所需的任何地方 , 不論是送到細胞膜上 , 不論是送到器官上 , 不論是用來建造東西或修復東西 。
and each of us has about 100 , 000 of these things running around , right now , inside each one of your 100 trillion cells .	我們每個人大約有十萬個這種東西在你一百兆個細胞內運轉 。
so no matter how lazy you feel , you're not really intrinsically doing nothing .	所以 , 不論你有多懶惰 , 你其實什麼都不做 。
so what i want you to do when you go home is think about this , and think about how powerful our cells are .	所以 , 我希望你們回家時 , 能想想這一點 , 想想我們的細胞有多強大 。
and think about some of the things that we're learning about cellular mechanics .	並且思考一些我們正在學習的關於細胞機械的東西 。
once we figure out all that's going on and believe me , we know almost a percent of what's going on once we figure out what's going on , we're really going to be able to have a lot of control over what we do with our health , with what we do with future generations , and how long we're going to live .	一旦我們搞清楚了所有正在發生的狀況 , 相信我 , 我們幾乎知道一旦我們搞清楚到底發生了什麼事 , 我們就真的能夠對我們健康的所作所為有很大的掌控 , 帶著未來的世代 , 和我們將要活多久 。
and hopefully we'll be able to use this to discover more truth , and more beauty .	希望我們能用這個來發現更多的真相 , 和更多的美 。
but it's really quite amazing that these cells , these micromachines , are aware enough of what the cell needs that they do their bidding .	但這真的很神奇這些細胞 , 這些微機械 , 足以察覺到它們所需要的細胞 。
they work together . they make the cell do what it needs to do .	它們同心協力 , 使細胞做該做的事 。
and their working together helps our bodies huge entities that they will never see function properly .	他們一起努力 , 幫助我們的身體龐大的實體 , 他們永遠看不到正常的功能 。
enjoy the rest of the show . thank you .	享受其餘的節目 。 謝謝 。
becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	貝琪•布蘭頓計劃在她的旅行車裡住了一年 , 看到了這個國家 , 但當憂鬱症和她的自由工作結束時 , 她的露營旅程變成無家可歸 。 在這個親密的演講中 , 她描述了她成為美國工作無家可歸者的經驗 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險、快樂、生活、個人成長、貧窮、社會變遷、社會、說故事、故事 。
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	貝琪布蘭頓:那年我無家可歸的日子
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是作家和記者 , 我也是一個很有好奇心的人 , 所以 , 在當記者的22年裡 , 我學到了如何做很多新事 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學到了一件事 , 就是變成隱形 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我成為了工作無家可歸者之一 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	我辭掉我父親同年二月去世後的報紙編輯的工作 , 決定去旅行 。
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的死因讓我很辛苦 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	在我這麼做時 , 我有很多想要感受和處理的事情 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我一輩子都在露營 。 我決定住在旅行車裡一年 , 這樣做會像一趟漫長的露營旅行 。
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	所以我打包了我的貓、我的腐敗者 , 以及我的露營裝備 , 進入1975年雪佛蘭旅行車 , 開到日落 , 完全沒有意識到三件重要的事 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	第一:社會將生活在一個永久的結構中 , 甚至是一件小事 , 以人的價值為基礎 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	二:我沒有意識到別人的負面認知能多快影響我們的現實 , 如果我們讓它發生的話 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	第三:我沒有意識到無家可歸是一種態度 , 而不是生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	一開始 , 住在旅行車很棒 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在營地洗澡 , 定期吃掉
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	我有時間放鬆和悲慟 。
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但接著我父親死後的憤怒和沮喪
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我的自由工作結束了 。 我得要全職工作來支付帳單 。
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	一個溫和的春天變成了一個非常熱的夏天 。
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	在任何地方 , 都不可能停車 , 沒有很明顯我有隻貓和一隻狗 , 牠真的很熱 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	貓來了 , 穿越廂型車的開窗
the doggy went into doggy day care .	狗狗進入烤日照護 。
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	每當我能時 , 我都會用辦公大樓的員工淋浴器和卡車站 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或是我在公共休息室清洗
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	夜間在廂型車內的溫度很少下降到華氏80度以下 , 讓睡眠變得困難或無法睡覺 。
food rotted in the heat .	食物在熱中腐爛
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	我冰胸的冰層在數小時內融化 , 而且相當悲慘 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我買不起公寓 , 或是負擔不起一間公寓 , 讓我能有破爛者和貓咪 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	我拒絕放棄他們 , 所以我待在車廂裡 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當熱氣讓我太生病 , 讓我能走50英尺 , 到我車外的公共廁所時 , 我會用桶子和垃圾袋當廁所 。
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天的天氣開始下降 , 溫度下降到凍結狀態 。 然後他們就停留在那裡 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	而我面臨了全新的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	我每天晚上都停在不同的地方 , 以避免被警察察察察覺及發現 。
i didn't always succeed .	我並不總是成功的 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我感覺到 , 無法掌控我的人生 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道何時、如何發生 , 但我從一個有才華的作家和記者 , 變成了無家可歸的婦女 , 住在旅行車裡 , 把我的呼吸帶走 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我沒有改變 , 我的智商沒有下降 。
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的天份、正直、價值觀、關於我的一切 , 都仍然是一樣的 。
but i had changed somehow .	但我不知怎麼地改變了 。
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我旋轉得越來越深 , 變成憂鬱症 。
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最後有人提到我去了無家可歸的健康診所 。
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	然後我就去了 。 我三天沒洗澡了 。
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我和排隊中的任何人一樣 , 都很臭、很沮喪 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我就是沒喝醉或高醉 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當幾個無家可歸的人意識到 , 包括一位前大學教授 , 他們說: 「 你不是無家可歸者 。 你為什麼真的來這裡 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家可歸的人沒有把我視為無家可歸 , 但我確實這麼做了 。
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	接著 , 教授傾聽我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有工作 , 你有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	真正的無家者沒有希望 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	診所給予我的憂鬱症讓我自殺的反應 。 我記得我當時在想: 「 如果我殺了我自己 , 沒有人會注意到 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	一個朋友在那之後沒多久就告訴我 , 她聽說提姆•羅斯瑟特 , 一位全國知名記者 , 在全國公共電視台上一直提到我 。
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	我寫過一篇關於我父親的論文 , 在他死前的那一年 , 就在提姆的新書裡 。
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	他在做這場演說電路 。 他在談我的寫作 。
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我意識到timrusssert , 《迎接媒體》的前任主持人 , 是在談論我的寫作 , 當時我住在一輛在沃爾瑪停車場的貨車上 , 我開始笑了 。
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑 , 是因為它到達了那個時候 , 我是作家 , 還是無家可歸的女人 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	所以我去了書店 。 然後我找到了提姆的書 。
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	我站在那裡 , 重新讀我的論文 。
because i was a writer .	因為我是個作家 ,
i was a writer .	我是個作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	在那之後不久 , 我搬回田納西 。
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我和朋友一起住在休旅車和沙發衝浪之間 。
and i started writing again .	然後我又開始寫作
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	隔年夏天 , 我擔任工作記者 。
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	我在贏得獎項 。 我住在我自己的公寓裡 。
i was no longer homeless .	我不再無家可歸 。
and i was no longer invisible .	而我不再隱形 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	數以千計的人全職工作和兼職工作 , 住在他們的車裡 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但社會持續汙名化和犯罪化生活在你的車輛或街道上 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以 , 無家可歸者 , 工作無家者 , 主要還是看不見 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你遇到一個 , 讓他們投入 , 鼓勵他們 , 並給他們希望 。
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	人類精神可以克服任何事情 , 如果它有希望的話 。
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我不是來這裡當無家可歸的海報女生 。
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是來鼓勵你們把錢給你遇到的下一個乞討者 。
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	但我在這裡要告訴各位 , 根據我的經驗 , 人不是他們住的地方、睡覺的地方 , 或是他們在任何時間的人生狀況 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前我住在旅行車裡 , 位於沃爾瑪的停車場 , 今天我在ted演講 。
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望總是 , 總是找到一個方法 。 謝謝 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	在tedxchange , 泰國的 「 保險套先生 」 , mechaiviravaya , 帶我們走過全國的大膽計畫 , 來提高它的生活水準 , 從1970年代開始 。 第一步:人口控制 。 這意味著許多法蘭克、好笑且非常有效的談論保險套 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球議題、健康、人口、科學、科學、
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	美西維拉瓦迪亞:保險套先生如何讓泰國成為更好的地方 。
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	現在 , 當我還是個40年前的年輕人時 , 這個國家非常非常貧窮 , 有許多人生活在貧窮之中 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定要做點什麼 , 但我們沒有從福利計畫開始 , 或減少貧窮計畫開始 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	但我們從家庭解釋計劃開始 , 遵循非常成功的孕產兒健康活動 , 一組活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	所以基本上 , 如果他們的孩子沒有存活下來 , 沒有人會接受家庭計劃 。
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	所以 , 第一步:向孩子們 , 到達母親身邊 , 然後跟上家庭計畫 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不僅僅是兒童死亡率 , 你還需要家庭計劃 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	現在讓我帶各位回到為什麼我們需要這麼做 。
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在我的國家 , 那是1974年的案例 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	每個家庭有7個小孩成長率達3.3% 。
there was just no future .	根本沒有未來 。
we needed to reduce the population growth rate .	我們需要降低人口成長率 。
so we said , " let's do it . "	所以我們說: 「 我們來做吧 。 」
the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	婦女們說: 「 我們同意 。 我們會用藥丸 , 但我們需要一個醫生來開藥 。 」 我們有非常非常少的醫生 。
we didn't take no as an answer ; we took no as a question .	我們沒有得到答案 ; 我們沒有提出問題 。
we went to the nurses and the midwives , who were also women , and did a fantastic job at explaining how to use the pill .	我們去找護士和助產士 , 他們也是女性 , 做了一個很棒的工作 , 解釋如何使用藥丸 。

over a quarter of a million were taught about family planning with a new alphabet a , b for birth , c for condom , i for iud , v for vasectomy .	超過25萬人被教導要用新的字母a、b來生、c來保險套、ud、v來做血液切除術 。

if you land on anything profamily planning , you move ahead .	如果你在任何事務所的規劃上降落 , 你就往前走 。

in thailand , for poor people , diamonds don't make it so the condom is the girl's best friend .	在泰國 , 對窮人來說 , 鑽石不會讓它變成保險套 , 所以保險套是女孩最好的朋友 。
we introduced our first microcredit program in 1975 , and the women who organized it said , " we only want to lend to women who practice family planning .	我們在1975年推出我們的第一個微型貸款計畫 , 組織起來的那些婦女說: 「 我們只想借給實踐家庭規劃的婦女 。
if you're pregnant , take care of your pregnancy .	如果你懷孕了 , 照顧你的懷孕
if you're not pregnant , you can take a loan out from us . "	如果你沒有懷孕 , 你可以向我們取出貸款 。 」
and that was run by them .	那是他們所經營的 。
and after 35/36 years , it's still going on .	經過35/36年 , 仍然持續進行著 。
it's a part of the village development bank ; it's not a real bank , but it's a fund microcredit .	它是村落發展銀行的一部分 ; 不是真的銀行 , 而是基金的微型貸款 。
and we didn't need a big organization to run it it was run by the villagers themselves .	我們不需要一個大型組織來運作 , 由村民自己主導 。
and you probably hardly see a thai man there , it's always women , women , women , women .	你可能幾乎看不到一個泰國人 , 總是有女人、女人、女人、女人 。

and this is on the fourth of july .	而這是在七月四日

and the hotel gave us the ballroom for it very appropriate room .	飯店給了我們這間房間非常適合的房間 。

of course , it must be american cola .	當然 , 這一定是美國的可樂 。

obviously , he's had his vasectomy because his hotdog is half eaten , and he was very happy .	很明顯地 , 他有他的血管切除術是因為他的熱狗一半被吃掉了 , 他非常開心 。

these are primary school kids third , fourth grade going to every household in the village , every household in the whole of thailand , giving aids information and a condom to every household , given by these young kids .	這些是小學三、四年級的小朋友 , 到村子裡的每個家庭、整個泰國的每個家庭 , 給予愛滋病的資訊和保險套 , 給這些小朋友用 。

we had condoms in all the refrigerators in the hotels and the schools , because alcohol impairs judgment .	我們在旅館和學校裡都有保險套 , 因為酒精會損害判斷 。

according to the u . n . , new cases of hiv declined by 90 percent , and according to the world bank , 7 . 7 million lives were saved .	根據聯合國 , 新愛滋病例數量下降了90% , 根據世界銀行 , 770萬條性命被拯救了 。

and then we decided to help people out of poverty , now that we got aids somewhat out of the way this time , not with government alone , but in cooperation with the business community .	接著 , 我們決定要幫助人們脫離貧窮 , 現在我們用的方式讓愛滋病變得有點離不開 , 不是單靠政府 , 而是和商業界合作 。
because poor people are business people who lack business skills and access to credit .	因為窮人是商人 , 他們缺乏商業技能 , 取得信用 。
those are the things to be provided by the business community .	那些是要被商業界提供的 。
we're trying to turn them into barefoot entrepreneurs , little business people .	我們試著把他們變成赤腳企業家、小商人 。
the only way out of poverty is through business enterprise .	脫離貧窮的唯一方法就是透過企業
so , that was done .	所以 , 完成了 。
the money goes from the company into the village via treeplanting .	經費從公司進入村落 , 通過種植 。
it's not a free gift .	而不是免費的禮物
they plant the trees , and the money goes into their microcredit fund , which we call the village development bank .	他們種植樹木 , 金錢進入了他們的微型貸款基金 , 我們稱之為村落發展銀行 。
everybody joins in , and they feel they own the bank , because they have brought the money in .	每個人都加入進去 , 他們覺得自己擁有銀行 , 因為他們把錢帶進去 。
and before you can borrow the money , you need to be trained .	在你能借錢之前 , 你需要接受訓練 。
and we believe if you want to help the poor , those who are living in poverty , access to credit must be a human right .	我們相信 , 如果你想要幫助窮人 , 那些生活在貧窮中的人 , 取得信用的人 , 一定是人權 。
access to credit must be a human right .	取得信用權必定是人權 。
otherwise they'll never get out of poverty .	否則他們永遠脫離貧窮 。
and then before getting a loan , you must be trained .	然後在取得貸款之前 , 你一定要受過訓練 。
here's what we call a " barefoot mba , " teaching people how to do business so that , when they borrow money , they'll succeed with the business .	這是我們所謂的 「 赤腳mba 」 , 教導人們如何做生意 , 這樣一來 , 當他們借錢時 , 他們就會成功地與企業合作 。
these are some of the businesses: mushrooms , crabs , vegetables , trees , fruits , and this is very interesting nike ice cream and nike biscuits ; this is a village sponsored by nike .	這些是一些生意:蘑菇、螃蟹、蔬菜、樹木、水果 , 這是非常有趣的nike冰淇淋和nike餅乾 ; 這是由nike贊助的村莊 。
they said , " they should stop making shoes and clothes .	他們說: 「 他們應該停止製造鞋子和衣服 。
make these better , because we can afford them . "	把這些做得更好 , 因為我們負擔得起 。 」
and then we have silk , thai silk .	然後我們有絲 , 泰國絲 。
now we're making scottish tartans , as you can see on the left , to sell to all people of scottish ancestors .	現在我們正在製造蘇格蘭的tartans , 如你們在左邊所看到的 , 賣給所有蘇格蘭祖先的人 。
so anyone sitting in and watching tv , get in touch with me .	所以 , 任何人坐進去看電視 , 跟我聯絡 。
and then this is our answer to starbucks in thailand " coffee and condoms . "	然後這是我們在泰國 「 咖啡和保險套 」 的星巴克的答案 。

your smartphone may feel like a friend but a true friend would give you a smile once in a while . at ted2013 , keller rinaudo demos romo , the smartphonepowered mini robot who can motor along with you on a walk , slide you a cup of coffee across the table , and react to you with programmable expressions .	你的智慧型手機可能感覺像個朋友 , 但真正的朋友會給你微笑一陣子 。 在ted2013年 , 凱勒•里納多•德莫 , 智慧型手機驅動的迷你機器人 , 它能和你一起散步 , 將你一杯咖啡滑過桌子 , 用可程控的表達方式對你做出反應 。
keller rinaudo: a mini robot powered by your phone	kellerrinaudo:一個迷你機器人是由你的手機主導的 。

that's the problem that we're trying to solve at romotive that i and the other 20 nerds at romotive are obsessed with solving .	這就是我們在romotive試圖解決的問題我和其他20位在romotive的書呆子都沉迷於解決問題 。
so we really want to build a robot that anyone can use , whether you're eight or 80 .	所以我們真的很想建造一個任何人都可以用的機器人 , 不管你是八歲還是八十歲 。
and as it turns out , that's a really hard problem , because you have to build a small , portable robot that's not only really affordable , but it has to be something that people actually want to take home and have around their kids .	結果發現 , 這真的是個困難的問題 , 因為你必須建造一個小型、可攜帶的機器人 , 不僅是真正負擔得起的 , 它還必須是人們真的想要帶回家 , 圍繞著孩子 。
this robot can't be creepy or uncanny .	這個機器人不能令人毛骨悚然或不可思議 。
he should be friendly and cute .	他應該要友善且可愛 。
romo's a robot that uses a device you already know and love your iphone as his brain .	romo是一個用你已經知道的裝置來使用的機器人 , 並把你的iphone當作他的大腦 。
and by leveraging the power of the iphone's processor , we can create a robot that is wifi enabled and computer visioncapable for 150 bucks , which is about one percent of what these kinds of robots have cost in the past .	藉由iphone處理器的力量 , 我們就能創造出一種無線網路和電腦視覺化的機器人 , 只要150美元 , 這大約是這類機器人在過去的成本的1% 。

he's wary , so he'll keep his eyes on me .	他很溫暖 , 所以他會把目光留在我身上 。

that girl can take her iphone , put it on the robot , send an email to grandma , who lives on the other side of the country .	那個女孩可以帶著她的iphone , 把它放在機器人上 , 發一封電子郵件給祖母 , 住在該國另一端的祖母 。

so those are a couple of the really cool things that romo can do today .	這些是romo今天能做的一些很酷的事 。
but i just want to finish by talking about something that we're working on in the future .	但我只想透過談未來我們正在努力的一件事來結束我的演講 。
this is actually something that one of our engineers , dom , built in a weekend .	這其實是我們的一位工程師 , dom , 在一個週末就建造出來的 。
it's built on top of a google open framework called blockly .	它是建立在google開放架構上 , 叫做blockly 。
this allows you to drag and drop these blocks of semantic code and create any behavior for this robot you want .	這讓你可以拖曳、丟下這些分號碼的積木 , 為你想要的這個機器人創造任何行為 。
you do not have to know how to code to create a behavior for romo .	你不需要知道如何編寫程式來為romo創造一個行為 。

and then if you have something you like , you can download it onto your robot and execute it in real life , run the program in real life .	如果你有你喜歡的東西 , 你可以把它下載到你的機器人上 , 在現實生活中執行 , 在現實生活中執行 。
and then if you have something you're proud of , you can share it with every other person who owns a robot in the world .	然後如果你有你驕傲的事 , 你可以和世界上所有擁有機器人的人分享 。
so all of these wifi–enabled robots actually learn from each other .	所以 , 所有這些無線網路的機器人 , 其實是彼此學習的 。
the reason we're so focused on building robots that everyone can train is that we think the most compelling use cases in personal robotics are personal .	我們之所以如此專注於打造出每個人都能訓練的機器人 , 是因為我們認為在個人機器人中最引人注目的使用案例是個人的 。
they change from person to person .	它們會因人而改變 。
so we think that if you're going to have a robot in your home , that robot ought to be a manifestation of your own imagination .	所以 , 我們認為 , 如果你要在家裡裝一個機器人 , 那機器人應該是你自己的想像力的呈現 。
so i wish that i could tell you what the future of personal robotics looks like .	所以我希望我能告訴你個人機器人的未來是什麼樣子的 。
to be honest , i have no idea .	老實說 , 我完全不知道 。
but what we do know is that it isn't 10 years or 10 billion dollars or a large humanoid robot away .	但我們確實知道的是 , 它不是10年或100億美金 , 也不是一個大型的人形機器人 。
the future of personal robotics is happening today , and it's going to depend on small , agile robots like romo and the creativity of people like yourselves .	現今個人機器人的未來正在發生 , 它會仰賴小型、敏捷的機器人 , 比如romo , 以及像你自己一樣人的創造力 。
so we can't wait to get you all robots , and we can't wait to see what you build .	所以我們迫不及待想讓你們全部的機器人 , 我們迫不及待想看看你們建造什麼 。
author and activist isabel allende discusses women , creativity , the definition of feminism and , of course , passion in this talk .	作者和活躍的伊莎貝爾•阿言德討論女性、創意、女性主義的定義 , 當然 , 還有這場演說的熱情 。
entertainment , global issues , love , parenting , storytelling , women , world cultures	娛樂、全球議題、愛、家長、說故事、女人、世界文化 。
isabel allende tells tales of passion	伊莎貝爾•阿言德會訴說熱情的故事 。

what is truer than truth ? answer: the story .	什麼比真相更真實 ? 答案是:故事 。
i'm a storyteller . i want to convey something that is truer than truth about our common humanity .	我是一個說故事的人 , 我想傳達一些比我們共同的人性更真實的東西 。
all stories interest me , and some haunt me until i end up writing them .	所有故事都感興趣我 , 有些一直縈繞在我的腦海 , 直到最後我才寫下它們 。
certain themes keep coming up: justice , loyalty , violence , death , political and social issues , freedom .	有些主題不斷出現:正義、忠誠、暴力、死亡、政治和社會議題、自由 。
i'm aware of the mystery around us , so i write about coincidences , premonitions , emotions , dreams , the power of nature , magic .	我意識到我們身邊的謎團 , 所以我寫下關於巧合、預備、情緒、夢想、自然的力量、魔法的力量 。
in the last 20 years i have published a few books , but i have lived in anonymity until february of 2006 , when i carried the olympic flag in the winter olympics in italy .	在過去的20年裡 , 我出版了幾本書 , 但我一直活在匿名中 , 直到2006年2月 , 當我帶著奧運在義大利的冬季奧運時 ,

allow me to tell you about my four minutes of fame .	允許我講述我的名氣的四分鐘
one of the organizers of the olympic ceremony , of the opening ceremony , called me and said that i had been selected to be one of the flagbearers .	奧運會典禮的組織者之一 , 開幕典禮 , 打電話給我 , 說我曾被選為旗幟師之一 。
i replied that surely this was a case of mistaken identity because i'm as far as you can get from being an athlete .	我回答說 , 這肯定是錯誤身份的案例 , 因為我不想成為運動員 。

five women , representing five continents , and three olympic gold medal winners .	五位女性 , 代表五大洲 , 還有三位奧運金牌贏家 。

passion lives here . isn't it always true ?	熱情就活在這裡 。 不是永遠都是真的嗎 ?
heart is what drives us and determines our fate .	心是驅使我們、決定我們的命運的動力 。

i need mavericks , dissidents , adventurers , outsiders and rebels , who ask questions , bend the rules and take risks .	我需要mavericks , 異議者 , 冒險家 , 外人和叛軍 , 他們問問題 , 彎曲規則 , 並承擔風險 。
people like all of you in this room .	像在座各位一樣的人 ,

she replied , " posture . my back is always straight , and i don't make old people's noises . "	她回答: 「 姿勢 。 我的背總是直的 , 我不製造老人的噪音 。 」
