no grunting , no coughing , no wheezing , no talking to yourselves , no farting .	沒有草 , 沒有咳嗽 , 沒有休息 , 沒有對自己說話 , 沒有遙不可及 。
well , she didn't say that exactly .	嗯 , 她並沒有這麼說 。
at some point around midnight , we were summoned to the wings of the stadium , and the loudspeakers announced the olympic flag , and the music started by the way , the same music that starts here , the aida march .	在午夜的某個時點 , 我們被召喚到體育館的翅膀 , 大聲說話者宣佈奧運旗 , 順帶一提 , 音樂從這裡開始 , 和艾達遊行的同一音樂 。
sophia loren was right in front of me she's a foot taller than i am , not counting the poofy hair .	蘇菲雅羅蘭就在我面前 , 她比我高一英尺 , 不計尖頭髮 。
she walked elegantly , like a giraffe on the african savannah , holding the flag on her shoulder . i jogged behind on my tiptoes holding the flag on my extended arm , so that my head was actually under the damn flag .	她優雅地走著 , 像一隻長頸鹿在非洲大草原上 , 肩上拿著旗幟 。 我在背後 , 拿著旗幟在伸展手臂上 , 以致我的頭在該死的旗子下 。
all the cameras were , of course , on sophia .	當然 , 所有的攝影機都在蘇菲雅 。
that was fortunate for me , because in most press photos i appear too , although often between sophia's legs .	這對我來說是很幸運的 , 因為在大部分的媒體照片中 , 我也會出現 , 雖然通常在蘇菲雅的雙腿之間 。
a place where most men would love to be .	一個大部分男人都樂意去的地方 。
the best four minutes of my entire life were those in the olympic stadium .	我一生中最棒的四分鐘是奧運體育館裡的人 。
my husband is offended when i say this although i have explained to him that what we do in private usually takes less than four minutes so he shouldn't take it personally .	我先生很冒犯 , 因為我說過這句話 , 雖然我向他解釋 , 我們私下的做法通常只花不到四分鐘 , 所以他不應該親自承受 。
i have all the press clippings of those four magnificent minutes , because i don't want to forget them when old age destroys my brain cells .	我有那四個壯麗的分鐘 , 全部的報導 , 因為我不想忘記它們 , 因為年紀大時破壞了我的腦細胞 。
i want to carry in my heart forever the key word of the olympics passion .	我想永遠帶著奧運熱情的關鍵字 。
so here's a tale of passion .	以下是熱情的故事 。
the year is 1998 , the place is a prison camp for tutsi refugees in congo .	今年是1998年 , 那個地方是剛果圖西難民營的監獄營 。
by the way , 80 percent of all refugees and displaced people in the world are women and girls .	順道一提 , 世界上80%的難民和流離失所的人都是女性和女孩 。
we can call this place in congo a death camp , because those who are not killed will die of disease or starvation .	我們可以在剛果稱這個地方為死亡集中營 , 因為那些沒有被殺死的人 , 會死於疾病或餓死 。
the protagonists of this story are a young woman , rose mapendo , and her children .	這故事的主角是一位年輕女子 , 蘿絲•瑪德諾 , 還有她的孩子 。
she's pregnant and a widow .	她懷孕和寡婦
soldiers have forced her to watch as her husband was tortured and killed .	士兵迫使她看著她的丈夫被虐待和殺害 。
somehow she manages to keep her seven children alive , and a few months later , she gives birth to premature twins .	不知怎麼地 , 她能讓她七個孩子活著 , 幾個月後 , 她生下了產前的雙胞胎 。
two tiny little boys .	兩個小男孩
she cuts the umbilical cord with a stick , and ties it with her own hair .	她用棍子剪斷臍帶 , 用自己的頭髮把它和它連結起來 。
she names the twins after the camp's commanders to gain their favor , and feeds them with black tea because her milk cannot sustain them .	她以營地的指揮官命名為雙胞胎 , 以獲得他們的喜好 , 並用黑茶餵他們 , 因為她的牛奶無法維持住他們 。
when the soldiers burst in her cell to rape her oldest daughter , she grabs hold of her and refuses to let go , even when they hold a gun to her head .	當士兵闖進她的牢房來強暴她最大的女兒時 , 她會抓住她 , 拒絕放手 , 即使當他們拿著槍抵著她的頭 。
somehow , the family survives for 16 months , and then , by extraordinary luck , and the passionate heart of a young american man , sasha chanoff , who manages to put her in a u . s . rescue plane , rose mapendo and her nine children end up in phoenix , arizona , where they're now living and thriving .	不知怎麼的 , 家庭存活了16個月 , 接著 , 靠著非凡的運氣 , 以及一位年輕美國人的熱情心 , 薩夏•查諾夫 , 他成功地把她放在美國救援飛機上 , 羅斯•馬德諾多和她的九個孩子最後到亞利桑那州鳳凰城 , 他們現在所居住的地方和繁榮的地方 。
mapendo , in swahili , means great love .	斯瓦希里語中 , mapendo代表著偉大的愛 。
the protagonists of my books are strong and passionate women like rose mapendo .	我書裡的主角是堅強且熱情的女性 , 如羅絲•馬迪諾 。
i don't make them up . there's no need for that .	我不把它們做成 , 不需要這樣 。
i look around and i see them everywhere .	我環顧四周 , 到處可見 。
i have worked with women and for women all my life .	我一生都在和女性合作 。
i know them well .	我很清楚他們 。
i was born in ancient times , at the end of the world , in a patriarchal catholic and conservative family .	我出生在遠古時期 , 在世界末日 , 在父權天主教和保守的家庭中 。
no wonder that by age five i was a raging feminist although the term had not reached chile yet , so nobody knew what the heck was wrong with me .	難怪我五歲的時候是個憤怒的女權主義者雖然這個詞還沒達到智利所以沒人知道我到底怎麼了
i would soon find out that there was a high price to pay for my freedom , and for questioning the patriarchy .	我很快就會發現 , 要為我的自由付出很高的代價 , 為了質疑父權制度 。
but i was happy to pay it , because for every blow that i received , i was able to deliver two .	但我很高興能付出代價 , 因為對我收到的每一擊 , 我都能遞出兩擊 。
once , when my daughter paula was in her twenties , she said to me that feminism was dated , that i should move on .	有一次 , 當我女兒保羅在她二十多歲時 , 她對我說女權主義是約會 , 我應該繼續下去 。
we had a memorable fight . feminism is dated ?	我們有一場難忘的戰鬥 , 女權主義是約會 ?
yes , for privileged women like my daughter and all of us here today , but not for most of our sisters in the rest of the world who are still forced into premature marriage , prostitution , forced labor they have children that they don't want or they cannot feed .	是的 , 對於有特權的女性 , 像我女兒和我們今天在場的所有人 , 但不是為了在世界上其他大部分的姊妹 , 她們仍然被迫成為早婚、賣淫、強迫勞工 , 她們有不想要的孩子 , 或無法養活的孩子 。
they have no control over their bodies or their lives .	他們無法控制自己的身體或生活 。
they have no education and no freedom .	他們沒有教育 , 也沒有自由 。
they are raped , beaten up and sometimes killed with impunity .	他們被強暴、毆打 , 甚至有時被懲罰 。
for most western young women of today , being called a feminist is an insult .	對於現今大部分西方年輕女性來說 , 被稱為女權主義者是一種侮辱 。
feminism has never been sexy , but let me assure you that it never stopped me from flirting , and i have seldom suffered from lack of men .	女性主義從來沒有性感過 , 但 , 讓我向各位保證 , 它從來沒有阻止我調情 , 而我已經缺乏男性 。
feminism is not dead , by no means .	女權主義沒有死 , 絕非如此 。
it has evolved . if you don't like the term , change it , for goddess' sake .	它已經進化了 。 如果你不喜歡這個詞 , 改變它 , 對女神來說 。
call it aphrodite , or venus , or bimbo , or whatever you want ; the name doesn't matter , as long as we understand what it is about , and we support it .	稱之為 「 phrodite 」 、 「 金星 」 、 「 bimbo 」 , 或 「 不論你想要什麼 」 ; 這個名字無所謂 , 只要我們了解它的內容 , 我們就能支持它 。
so here's another tale of passion , and this is a sad one .	這是另一個充滿熱情的故事 , 這是令人難過的一個 。
the place is a small women's clinic in a village in bangladesh .	這個地方是孟加拉村裡的一間小型婦女診所
the year is 2005 .	2005年
jenny is a young american dental hygienist who has gone to the clinic as a volunteer during her threeweek vacation .	珍妮是一位年輕的美國牙齒衛生學家 , 她在三週假期時去診所當義工 。
she's prepared to clean teeth , but when she gets there , she finds out that there are no doctors , no dentists , and the clinic is just a hut full of flies .	她準備了乾淨的牙齒 , 但當她到了那裡 , 她發現沒有醫生 , 沒有牙醫 , 診所只是一間滿是蒼蠅的小屋 。
outside , there is a line of women who have waited several hours to be treated .	在外面 , 有一行女性等了好幾個小時才被治療 。
the first patient is in excruciating pain because she has several rotten molars .	第一個病人正在疼痛中 , 因為她有好幾顆腐爛的臼齒 。
jenny realizes that the only solution is to pull out the bad teeth .	珍妮意識到 , 唯一的解決方案就是拔掉壞牙 。
she's not licensed for that ; she has never done it .	她沒有執照 , 她從來沒有做過 。
she risks a lot and she's terrified .	她冒很大的風險 , 她嚇壞了 。
she doesn't even have the proper instruments , but fortunately she has brought some novocaine .	她甚至沒有適當的樂器 , 但幸運的是 , 她帶來了一些革命 。
jenny has a brave and passionate heart .	珍妮有著勇敢且熱情的心 。
she murmurs a prayer and she goes ahead with the operation .	她拍了一段禱告 , 帶著手術前進 。
at the end , the relieved patient kisses her hands .	最後 , 鬆了一口氣的病人親吻她的手
that day the hygienist pulls out many more teeth .	那天衛生專家拉出更多的牙齒
the next morning , when she comes again to the socalled clinic , her first patient is waiting for her with her husband .	隔天早上 , 當她再次來到所謂的診所時 , 她的第一個病人正在和她丈夫一起等她 。
the woman's face looks like a watermelon .	女人的臉看起來像個水匠
it is so swollen that you can't even see the eyes .	它很腫脹 , 你甚至看不到眼睛 。
the husband , furious , threatens to kill the american .	丈夫 , 憤怒 , 威脅要殺死美國人 。
jenny is horrified at what she has done , but then the translator explains that the patient's condition has nothing to do with the operation .	珍妮對她所做的事感到害怕 , 但接著翻譯解釋 , 病人的狀況和手術無關 。
the day before , her husband beat her up because she was not home in time to prepare dinner for him .	前一天 , 她先生打她 , 因為她不在家準備晚餐 。
millions of women live like this today .	今天有數百萬的女性像這樣生活著 。
they are the poorest of the poor .	他們是窮人中最窮的人 。
although women do twothirds of the world's labor , they own less than one percent of the world's assets .	雖然女性從事世界上三分之二的勞動卻擁有不到世界資產的百分之一
they are paid less than men for the same work if they're paid at all , and they remain vulnerable because they have no economic independence , and they are constantly threatened by exploitation , violence and abuse .	他們的薪水低於男性 , 只要他們有薪水 , 就會保持脆弱 , 因為他們沒有經濟獨立 , 且他們不斷受到剝削、暴力和虐待的威脅 。
it is a fact that giving women education , work , the ability to control their own income , inherit and own property , benefits the society .	事實是 , 給予女性教育、工作、控制自己的收入、繼承和產權的能力 , 讓社會受惠 。
if a woman is empowered , her children and her family will be better off .	如果一個女人被賦予能力 , 她的孩子和家人就會更好 。
if families prosper , the village prospers , and eventually so does the whole country .	如果家庭繁榮 , 村落的繁榮 , 最終整個國家也是如此 。
wangari maathai goes to a village in kenya .	wangarimaathai到肯亞的一個村莊
she talks with the women and explains that the land is barren because they have cut and sold the trees .	她和女人談話 , 解釋說 , 土地是貧瘠的 , 因為他們已經砍伐、賣掉樹木 。
she gets the women to plant new trees and water them , drop by drop .	她讓婦女們種植新的樹木 , 澆水 , 滴下來 。
in a matter of five or six years , they have a forest , the soil is enriched , and the village is saved .	在五或六年內 , 他們有一片森林 , 土壤豐富 , 村落也救了 。
the poorest and most backward societies are always those that put women down .	最貧窮和最落後的社會總是那些把女性放下來的人 。
yet this obvious truth is ignored by governments and also by philanthropy .	然而這個顯而易見的事實卻被政府以及慈善事業所忽略 。
for every dollar given to a women's program , 20 dollars are given to men's programs .	給女性的每一塊錢 , 給男性計畫20塊錢 。
women are 51 percent of humankind .	女性是51%的人類 。
empowering them will change everything more than technology and design and entertainment .	賦權他們改變一切 , 勝過科技、設計和娛樂 。
i can promise you that women working together linked , informed and educated can bring peace and prosperity to this forsaken planet .	我可以向各位保證 , 女性們攜手合作 , 連結、知情、受教育 , 能為這個偽造星球帶來和平和繁榮 。
in any war today , most of the casualties are civilians , mainly women and children . they are collateral damage .	在今天的任何一場戰爭中 , 大部分的傷亡都是平民 , 主要是婦女和兒童 。 她們是相對的傷害 。
men run the world , and look at the mess we have .	男人經營這個世界 , 看看我們所擁有的混亂 。
what kind of world do we want ?	我們想要什麼樣的世界 ?
this is a fundamental question that most of us are asking .	這是我們大部分人都在問的基本問題 。
does it make sense to participate in the existing world order ?	是否合理地參與現有的世界秩序 ?
we want a world where life is preserved and the quality of life is enriched for everybody , not only for the privileged .	我們想要一個能保存生命的世界 , 生活品質也能豐富每個人 , 不只能為特權而活 。
in january i saw an exhibit of fernando botero's paintings at the uc berkeley library .	一月份我看到了費南多•波特羅在加州柏克萊圖書館的畫展
no museum or gallery in the united states , except for the new york gallery that carries botero's work , has dared to show the paintings because the theme is the abu ghraib prison .	美國沒有美術館或畫廊 , 除了載著波特羅的作品的紐約畫廊以外 , 都敢於展示畫作 , 因為主題是阿布格萊布監獄 。
they are huge paintings of torture and abuse of power , in the voluminous botero style .	它們是大量的折磨和濫用權力的畫作 , 用的是大量的波特羅風格 。
i have not been able to get those images out of my mind or my heart .	我無法把那些影像從我的腦海或心中
what i fear most is power with impunity .	我最害怕的是有罪惡感的力量 。
i fear abuse of power , and the power to abuse .	我害怕濫用權力 , 以及濫用權力 。
in our species , the alpha males define reality , and force the rest of the pack to accept that reality and follow the rules .	在我們這個物種中 , 雄性領袖定義現實 , 並強迫其餘的群體接受現實 , 並遵守規則 。
the rules change all the time , but they always benefit them , and in this case , the trickledown effect , which does not work in economics , works perfectly .	規則隨時都在改變 , 但它們總是有好處 , 在這個例子中 , 三角函數的效應 , 在經濟上是行不通的 , 完美地工作 。
abuse trickles down from the top of the ladder to the bottom .	虐待騙局從梯子的上到下面 。
women and children , especially the poor , are at the bottom .	婦女和兒童 , 尤其是窮人 , 處於底層 。
even the most destitute of men have someone they can abuse a woman or a child .	即使是男人最多研究所也有一個人他們也可以虐待一個女人或一個小孩
i'm fed up with the power that a few exert over the many through gender , income , race , and class .	我得到的是少數人透過性別、收入、種族、階級的力量 。
i think that the time is ripe to make fundamental changes in our civilization .	我認為時間是成熟 , 要在我們的文明中做出根本的改變 。
but for real change , we need feminine energy in the management of the world .	但對於真正的改變 , 我們需要女性化能源在世界的管理上 。
we need a critical number of women in positions of power , and we need to nurture the feminine energy in men .	我們需要有很關鍵的女性在權力的位置 , 我們需要培養男性內心的女性能量 。
i'm talking about men with young minds , of course .	我指的是有年輕心智的男人 , 當然 ,
old guys are hopeless ; we have to wait for them to die off .	老傢伙是無望的 ; 我們得等他們死掉 。
yes , i would love to have sophia loren's long legs and legendary breasts .	是的 , 我很想有蘇菲雅羅蘭的長腿和傳奇的胸部 。
but given a choice , i would rather have the warrior hearts of wangari maathai , somaly mam , jenny and rose mapendo .	但若要選擇 , 我寧願有位勇士的心 , 來自華加里•馬塔伊、索瑪利的媽媽、珍妮和蘿絲•瑪諾 。
i want to make this world good .	我想讓這個世界變得很好 。
not better , but to make it good .	不是更好 , 而是要把它做得很好 。
why not ? it is possible . look around in this room all this knowledge , energy , talent and technology .	為什麼不呢 ? 這是有可能的 。 看看這個房間裡的周圍 , 所有的知識、能量、才華和科技 。
let's get off our fannies , roll up our sleeves and get to work , passionately , in creating an almost perfect world .	讓我們脫離炫耀 , 捲起袖子 , 熱情地工作 , 創造一個近乎完美的世界 。
every day , in a city the size of london , 30 million meals are served . but where does all the food come from ? architect carolyn steel discusses the daily miracle of feeding a city , and shows how ancient food routes shaped the modern world .	每天 , 在倫敦大小的城市裡 , 有三千萬份餐都是服務的 。 但是所有的食物都來自哪裡 ? 建築師卡羅琳鋼鐵討論餵飽一座城市的日常奇蹟 , 並展現出古老食物路線如何塑造現代世界 。
cities , culture , food , global issues	城市、文化、食物、全球議題
carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities	carolynsteel:食物如何形塑我們的城市
how do you feed a city ?	如何餵飽一座城市
it's one of the great questions of our time .	這是我們這個時代最偉大的問題之一 。
yet it's one that's rarely asked .	但卻很少被問到 。
we take it for granted that if we go into a shop or restaurant , or indeed into this theater's foyer in about an hour's time , there is going to be food there waiting for us , having magically come from somewhere .	我們理所當然地認為如果我們進入一家商店或餐廳 , 或在大概一小時內進入這間劇院的倉庫 , 那裡將會有食物等著我們 , 神奇地從某處來 。
but when you think that every day for a city the size of london , enough food has to be produced , transported , bought and sold , cooked , eaten , disposed of , and that something similar has to happen every day for every city on earth , it's remarkable that cities get fed at all .	但當你認為每一天 , 倫敦大小的城市 , 足夠的食物必須被生產、運送、買、賣、煮、吃、吃、丟 , 每天都要發生同樣的事 , 對於地球上的每個城市而言 , 都很了不起 。
we live in places like this as if they're the most natural things in the world , forgetting that because we're animals and that we need to eat , we're actually as dependent on the natural world as our ancient ancestors were .	我們生活在這樣的地方 , 彷彿牠們是世界上最自然的東西 , 忘記了 , 因為我們是動物 , 我們需要吃東西 , 其實我們和我們古老的祖先一樣依賴自然界 。
and as more of us move into cities , more of that natural world is being transformed into extraordinary landscapes like the one behind me it's soybean fields in mato grosso in brazil in order to feed us .	當更多人搬進城市時 , 更多的自然世界正被轉變為非凡的景觀 , 就像我身後的那一塊黃豆田 , 那是在巴西的馬托格羅索 , 為了餵飽我們 。
these are extraordinary landscapes , but few of us ever get to see them .	這些是非凡的景觀 , 但很少人看過這些景觀 。
and increasingly these landscapes are not just feeding us either .	越來越多的地景 , 不僅僅是餵飽我們 。
as more of us move into cities , more of us are eating meat , so that a third of the annual grain crop globally now gets fed to animals rather than to us human animals .	隨著更多人搬到城市裡 , 更多人都在吃肉 , 所以 , 全球三分之一的年度穀物現在能餵給動物 , 而不是給人類動物吃 。
and given that it takes three times as much grain actually ten times as much grain to feed a human if it's passed through an animal first , that's not a very efficient way of feeding us .	由於它需要三倍的穀物事實上是10倍的穀物來餵飽人類如果它是先經過動物 , 那就不是非常有效率的方式來餵飽我們
and it's an escalating problem too .	這也是一個持續不斷的問題 。
by 2050 , it's estimated that twice the number of us are going to be living in cities .	到2050年 , 估計我們居住城市的數量將會是城市的兩倍 。
and it's also estimated that there is going to be twice as much meat and dairy consumed .	據估計 , 肉類和乳製的消耗量將會是兩倍
so meat and urbanism are rising hand in hand .	所以 , 肉類和都市化手工興起 。
and that's going to pose an enormous problem .	那會造成很大的問題 。
six billion hungry carnivores to feed , by 2050 .	六十億隻飢餓的食肉食動物到2050年
that's a big problem . and actually if we carry on as we are , it's a problem we're very unlikely to be able to solve .	這是個大問題 。 如果我們繼續下去 , 我們不可能解決的問題 。
nineteen million hectares of rainforest are lost every year to create new arable land .	每年有一千九百萬公頃的雨林被丟棄 , 用來創造新的可耕地 。
although at the same time we're losing an equivalent amount of existing arables to salinization and erosion .	儘管我們同時也失去了相當於現有的耕地 , 讓鹽化和侵蝕 。
we're very hungry for fossil fuels too .	我們也非常渴望石化燃料 。
it takes about 10 calories to produce every calorie of food that we consume in the west .	大約需要十卡路里來產生我們西方所消耗的每一卡路里的食物 。
and even though there is food that we are producing at great cost , we don't actually value it .	儘管我們有大量生產的食物 , 但我們卻不重視它 。
half the food produced in the usa is currently thrown away .	美國目前生產的一半食物是被丟棄的 。
and to end all of this , at the end of this long process , we're not even managing to feed the planet properly .	為了結束這一切 , 在這個漫長過程的最後 , 我們甚至沒有適當的管理去餵飽這個星球 。
a billion of us are obese , while a further billion starve .	我們有十億人過胖 , 卻有十億人挨餓 。
none of it makes very much sense .	一點都不合理 。
and when you think that 80 percent of global trade in food now is controlled by just five multinational corporations , it's a grim picture .	當你認為現在全球百分之八十的糧食交易是由五個跨國企業所掌控的 , 這是很嚴峻的照片 。
as we're moving into cities , the world is also embracing a western diet .	隨著我們搬進城市 , 世界也擁抱西方的飲食 。
and if we look to the future , it's an unsustainable diet .	如果我們看向未來 , 這是個不永續的飲食 。
so how did we get here ?	所以 , 我們是怎麼走到這一步的 ?
and more importantly , what are we going to do about it ?	更重要的是 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
well , to answer the slightly easier question first , about 10 , 000 years ago , i would say , is the beginning of this process in the ancient near east , known as the fertile crescent .	首先 , 要回答這個問題稍微簡單一點 , 大約一萬年前 , 我會說 , 是這個過程的開端 , 在東邊的古老時代 , 也就是所謂的肥沃日期 。
because , as you can see , it was crescent shaped .	因為 , 如你所見 , 它是近代的形狀 。
and it was also fertile .	它也很肥沃 。
and it was here , about 10 , 000 years ago , that two extraordinary inventions , agriculture and urbanism , happened roughly in the same place and at the same time .	大約在一萬年前 , 兩項非凡的發明 , 農業和城市化 , 大約在同一個地方和同一個地方發生 。
this is no accident , because agriculture and cities are bound together . they need each other .	這不是偶然的 , 因為農業和城市是互相限制的 。 他們需要彼此 。
because it was discovery of grain by our ancient ancestors for the first time that produced a food source that was large enough and stable enough to support permanent settlements .	因為這是我們古老祖先第一次發現穀物 , 產生了足夠大且穩定的食物來源 , 足以支撐永久定居處 。
and if we look at what those settlements were like , we see they were compact .	如果我們看看那些定居處的狀況 , 我們可以看到它們是很緊密的 。
they were surrounded by productive farm land and dominated by large temple complexes like this one at ur , that were , in fact , effectively , spiritualized , central food distribution centers .	它們被有生產力的農地包圍 , 被大型神廟複雜的土地所支配 , 像烏爾這樣的大型神廟 , 事實上 , 是靈性化的中央食物分配中心 。
because it was the temples that organized the harvest , gathered in the grain , offered it to the gods , and then offered the grain that the gods didn't eat back to the people .	因為是神殿安排了收割 , 聚集在穀物裡 , 提供給了神 , 然後提供了神所不吃的穀物 。
so , if you like , the whole spiritual and physical life of these cities was dominated by the grain and the harvest that sustained them .	所以 , 如果你願意 , 這些城市的精神和實體生活都是由穀物和收成所支配的 。
and in fact , that's true of every ancient city .	事實上 , 每個古老城市都是如此 。
but of course not all of them were that small .	但當然不是全部都那麼小 。
famously , rome had about a million citizens by the first century a . d .	著名的是 , 羅馬在西元前一個世紀 , 大約有一百萬名公民 。
so how did a city like this feed itself ?	所以 , 像這樣的城市如何自食其力 ?
the answer is what i call " ancient food miles . "	答案就是我所謂的 「 古老食物里程 」 。
basically , rome had access to the sea , which made it possible for it to import food from a very long way away .	基本上 , 羅馬能接觸到海 , 這使得它從很遠的地方進口食物 。
this is the only way it was possible to do this in the ancient world , because it was very difficult to transport food over roads , which were rough .	這是在古代世界中唯一有可能做到的 , 因為很難將食物運送到路上 , 很粗糙 。
and the food obviously went off very quickly .	食物很快就消失了 。
so rome effectively waged war on places like carthage and egypt just to get its paws on their grain reserves .	所以羅馬有效地發動戰爭 , 打擊像汽車和埃及這樣的地方 , 只為了讓它的爪子留在穀物的保護區上 。
and , in fact , you could say that the expansion of the empire was really sort of one long , drawn out militarized shopping spree , really .	事實上 , 你可以說帝國的擴張真的有點像軍事化的購物中心 , 真的 。
in fact i love the fact , i just have to mention this: rome in fact used to import oysters from london , at one stage . i think that's extraordinary .	事實上 , 我很喜歡這個事實 , 我只需要提一下:羅馬其實曾經是從倫敦進口牡蠣 , 在一個階段 。 我認為那很不平凡 。
so rome shaped its hinterland through its appetite .	所以羅馬透過它的食慾塑造了它的後塵 。
but the interesting thing is that the other thing also happened in the preindustrial world .	但有趣的是 , 另一件事也發生在工業化前的世界 。
if we look at a map of london in the 17th century , we can see that its grain , which is coming in from the thames , along the bottom of this map .	如果我們看看17世紀的倫敦地圖 , 我們可以看到它的穀物 , 從泰晤士山脈進來 , 沿著這張地圖的下方 。
so the grain markets were to the south of the city .	所以穀物市場就在城市的南方 。
and the roads leading up from them to cheapside , which was the main market , were also grain markets .	道路從它們引領到便宜 , 那是主要的市場 , 也是穀物市場 。
and if you look at the name of one of those streets , bread street , you can tell what was going on there 300 years ago .	如果你看看其中一條街道的名字 , 麵包街 , 你可以知道三百年前那邊的狀況 。
and the same of course was true for fish .	魚也一樣 。
fish was , of course , coming in by river as well . same thing .	當然 , 魚也是由河流進來的 。 同樣的道理 。
and of course billingsgate , famously , was london's fish market , operating onsite here until the mid1980s .	當然 , billingsgate , 著名的是倫敦的魚市場 , 一直到1980年代中期 , 在這裡操作 。
which is extraordinary , really , when you think about it .	想想看 , 這很不尋常 。
everybody else was wandering around with mobile phones that looked like bricks and sort of smelly fish happening down on the port .	其他所有人都帶著像磚塊一樣的手機遊走 , 有點像在港口上聞到的魚 。
this is another thing about food in cities: once its roots into the city are established , they very rarely move .	這是關於城市食物的另一件事:一旦它的根源被建立起來 , 它們很少會移動 。
meat is a very different story because , of course , animals could walk into the city .	肉類是非常不同的 , 因為 , 當然 , 動物可以走進城市 。
so much of london's meat was coming from the northwest , from scotland and wales .	倫敦西北部的大部分肉都來自蘇格蘭和威爾斯 。
so it was coming in , and arriving at the city at the northwest , which is why smithfield , london's very famous meat market , was located up there .	當時正要進入市中心 , 抵達西北部 , 這就是為什麼史密斯菲爾德 , 倫敦非常著名的肉市場 , 位在那邊 。
poultry was coming in from east anglia and so on , to the northeast .	從東安格利亞來到東北部 。
i feel a bit like a weather woman doing this . anyway , and so the birds were coming in with their feet protected with little canvas shoes .	我覺得這有點像天氣女人這樣做 。 總之 , 鳥兒們進來用腳保護著小畫布的鞋子 。
and then when they hit the eastern end of cheapside , that's where they were sold , which is why it's called poultry .	然後當他們碰到便宜的東端時 , 那是他們被賣掉的地方 , 這就是為什麼它叫做 「 流產 」 。
and , in fact , if you look at the map of any city built before the industrial age , you can trace food coming in to it .	事實上 , 如果你看一下任何一個城市的地圖在工業時代之前 , 你可以追溯到食物進來 。
you can actually see how it was physically shaped by food , both by reading the names of the streets , which give you a lot of clues .	你可以看到它是如何被食物所塑造 , 兩者都透過閱讀街道的名字 , 這給了你許多線索 。
friday street , in a previous life , is where you went to buy your fish on a friday .	星期五街 , 在過去的生活中 , 是你星期五去買魚的地方 。
but also you have to imagine it full of food .	但同時你也要想像它充滿了食物 。
because the streets and the public spaces were the only places where food was bought and sold .	因為街道和公共場所是唯一一個購買食物的地方 。
and if we look at an image of smithfield in 1830 you can see that it would have been very difficult to live in a city like this and be unaware of where your food came from .	如果我們看看1830年史密斯菲爾德的圖像 , 你可以看到 , 生活在這樣的城市會非常困難 , 不知你的食物從何而來 。
in fact , if you were having sunday lunch , the chances were it was mooing or bleating outside your window about three days earlier .	事實上 , 如果你吃了星期天的午餐 , 可能性是你在窗外 , 大約三天前就在你的窗外流動 。
so this was obviously an organic city , part of an organic cycle .	顯然這是個有機城市 , 是有機循環的一部分 。
and then 10 years later everything changed .	然後十年後一切都改變了 。
this is an image of the great western in 1840 .	這是1840年大西方國家的影像
and as you can see , some of the earliest train passengers were pigs and sheep .	如你所見 , 一些最早的火車乘客是豬和羊 。
so all of a sudden , these animals are no longer walking into market .	所以突然間 , 這些動物不再走進市場
they're being slaughtered out of sight and mind , somewhere in the countryside .	他們被視力和心靈屠殺 , 在鄉下的某個地方 。
and they're coming into the city by rail .	他們通過欄杆進入城市 。
and this changes everything .	而這會改變一切 。
to start off with , it makes it possible for the first time to grow cities , really any size and shape , in any place .	從頭開始 , 它首次能夠成長城市 , 任何大小和形狀 , 在任何地方 。
cities used to be constrained by geography ; they used to have to get their food through very difficult physical means .	過去 , 城市受到地理限制 ; 他們以前得要透過非常困難的實體手段來取得他們的食物 。
all of a sudden they are effectively emancipated from geography .	突然間它們被有效地從地理上解放了 。
and as you can see from these maps of london , in the 90 years after the trains came , it goes from being a little blob that was quite easy to feed by animals coming in on foot , and so on , to a large splurge , that would be very , very difficult to feed with anybody on foot , either animals or people .	如你所見 , 從倫敦地圖上看的 , 在火車來臨的90年後 , 從一個小小的團體 , 很容易被動物帶進來的動物餵食 , 諸如此類 , 到一個龐然大的水管 , 很難和任何人一起餵飽 , 不論是動物 , 或人 。
and of course that was just the beginning . after the trains came cars , and really this marks the end of this process .	當然這只是個開端 。 火車來了車之後 , 真的是這個過程的結尾 。
it's the final emancipation of the city from any apparent relationship with nature at all .	它是城市最終的解放 , 從任何明顯與自然的關係中 。
and this is the kind of city that's devoid of smell , devoid of mess , certainly devoid of people , because nobody would have dreamed of walking in such a landscape .	而這就是那種沒有氣味的城市 , 沒有亂七八糟 , 沒有人會去做 , 因為沒有人會夢想走在這樣的地景中 。
in fact , what they did to get food was they got in their cars , drove to a box somewhere on the outskirts , came back with a week's worth of shopping , and wondered what on earth to do with it .	事實上 , 他們的做法是 , 他們在車上拿到食物 , 開車到郊區某處的箱子回來 , 帶著一週的購物回來 , 很納悶 , 要怎麼用它 。
and this really is the moment when our relationship , both with food and cities , changes completely .	這就是我們與食物和城市的關係 , 完全改變的時刻 。
here we have food that used to be the center , the social core of the city at the periphery .	這裡我們有曾經是中心的食物 , 城市周圍的社會核心 。
it used to be a social event , buying and selling food .	曾經是社交活動 , 購買和賣食物
we used to cook ; now we just add water , or a little bit of an egg if you're making a cake or something .	我們以前會煮飯 ; 現在我們只加水 , 或是做蛋糕或其他東西的一點點 。
we don't smell food to see if it's okay to eat .	我們聞不到食物看看是否可以吃
we just read the back of a label on a packet .	我們只讀包裝上標籤的背面 。
and we don't value food . we don't trust it .	而我們不珍視食物 , 不信任它
so instead of trusting it , we fear it .	所以 , 我們不信任它 , 而是害怕它 。
and instead of valuing it , we throw it away .	而不是去評價它 , 而是把它丟掉 。
one of the great ironies of modern food systems is that they've made the very thing they promised to make easier much harder .	現代食品系統的一個很諷刺的一點是 , 他們已經做出了他們承諾要更加困難的事 。
by making it possible to build cities anywhere and any place , they've actually distanced us from our most important relationship , which is that of us and nature .	透過讓它能夠在任何地方和任何地方建立城市 , 它們已經讓我們遠離我們最重要的關係 , 那就是我們和大自然的關係 。
and also they've made us dependent on systems that only they can deliver , that , as we've seen , are unsustainable .	此外 , 它們讓我們依賴的是只有它們能傳遞的系統 , 如我們所見 , 它們是不可持續的 。
so what are we going to do about that ?	那我們該怎麼辦呢 ?
it's not a new question .	這不是一個新的問題 。
500 years ago it's what thomas more was asking himself .	五百年前 , 湯瑪斯更多在問自己 。
this is the frontispiece of his book " utopia . "	這是他書《烏托邦》的前身 。
and it was a series of semiindependent citystates , if that sounds remotely familiar , a day's walk from one another where everyone was basically farmingmad , and grew vegetables in their back gardens , and ate communal meals together , and so on .	它是一系列半獨立的城邦 , 如果這聽起來很遙遠 , 一天的步行 , 每個人基本上都是農耕的 , 在他們的後花園種植蔬菜 , 吃了共產餐 , 等等 。
and i think you could argue that food is a fundamental ordering principle of utopia , even though more never framed it that way .	我想 , 你可以主張 , 食物是烏托邦的基本原則 , 即使它從來沒有這麼框架過 。
and here is another very famous " utopian " vision , that of ebenezer howard , " the garden city . "	這是另一個非常有名的 「 烏托邦 」 遠景 , 艾貝茲默斯霍華德 , 《花園城市》 。
same idea: series of semiindependent citystates , little blobs of metropolitan stuff with arable land around , joined to one another by railway .	同樣的想法:一系列半獨立的城市 , 小型的大都市 , 有可耕種的土地 , 加入鐵路 。
and again , food could be said to be the ordering principle of his vision .	再說一次 , 食物可以被說是他視力的訂定原則 。
it even got built , but nothing to do with this vision that howard had .	它甚至被建造出來了 , 但與默斯克韋茲的遠景無關 。
and that is the problem with these utopian ideas , that they are utopian .	這就是這些烏托邦想法的問題 , 他們是烏托邦人 。
utopia was actually a word that thomas moore used deliberately .	烏托邦其實是一個湯瑪斯•摩爾刻意使用的字 。
it was a kind of joke , because it's got a double derivation from the greek .	那是個笑話 , 因為希臘有雙重衍生 。
it can either mean a good place , or no place .	它可以是好的位置 , 或無所不在 。
because it's an ideal . it's an imaginary thing . we can't have it .	因為這是一個理想的 。 這是個想像不到的東西 。 我們不能擁有它 。
and i think , as a conceptual tool for thinking about the very deep problem of human dwelling , that makes it not much use .	我認為 , 作為一個概念 , 用來思考人類居住的深層問題 , 讓它不太有用 。
so i've come up with an alternative , which is sitopia , from the ancient greek , " sitos " for food , and " topos " for place .	所以我想出了一個替代方案 , 就是希托邦 , 來自古希臘 , " sitos " 代表食物 , 還有 " topos " 。
i believe we already live in sitopia .	我相信我們已經住在索比亞了 。
we live in a world shaped by food , and if we realize that , we can use food as a really powerful tool a conceptual tool , design tool , to shape the world differently .	我們生活在一個被食物形塑的世界 , 如果我們意識到 , 我們可以把食物當作一種強而有力的工具 , 一種概念化的工具 , 設計工具 , 以不同的方式塑造世界 。
so if we were to do that , what might sitopia look like ?	所以 , 如果我們要這麼做 , 西索比亞可能會變成什麼樣子 ?
well i think it looks a bit like this .	嗯 , 我想它看起來有點像這樣 。
i have to use this slide . it's just the look on the face of the dog .	我得用這張投影片 。 這只是狗臉上的表情 。
but anyway , this is it's food at the center of life , at the center of family life , being celebrated , being enjoyed , people taking time for it .	但無論如何 , 這是食物在生活的中心 , 在家庭生活的中心 , 被讚頌、被享受 , 人們花時間在它上 。
this is where food should be in our society .	這是我們社會中應該有的食物 。
but you can't have scenes like this unless you have people like this .	但你不能有這樣的場景 , 除非你有這樣的人 。
by the way , these can be men as well .	順帶一提 , 這些也可以是男人 。
it's people who think about food , who think ahead , who plan , who can stare at a pile of raw vegetables and actually recognize them .	而是人們對食物的看法 , 他們認為領先 , 他們計劃 , 他們會盯著一堆生菜 , 真的認得出來 。
we need these people . we're part of a network .	我們需要這些人 , 我們是網路的一部分
because without these kinds of people we can't have places like this .	因為 , 若沒有這類人 , 我們就不能有像這樣的地方 。
here , i deliberately chose this because it is a man buying a vegetable .	在這裡 , 我故意選這個 , 因為它是個人買蔬菜的男人 。
but networks , markets where food is being grown locally .	但是網絡 , 供應食物的市場在當地成長 。
it's common . it's fresh .	很常見 , 很新鮮
it's part of the social life of the city .	成為城市社交生活的一部分
because without that , you can't have this kind of place , food that is grown locally and also is part of the landscape , and is not just a zerosum commodity off in some unseen hellhole .	因為如果沒有這種地方 , 你就不能擁有這種地方 , 當地的食物 , 同時也是地景的一部分 , 而且不只是零和的商品 , 在一些看不見的地獄裡 。
cows with a view .	用景象觀看的牛 。
steaming piles of humus .	蒸汽堆積如山的嗡嗡聲 。
this is basically bringing the whole thing together .	這基本上就是把整件事湊在一起 。
and this is a community project i visited recently in toronto .	這是我最近在多倫多參觀的一個社區計畫 。
it's a greenhouse , where kids get told all about food and growing their own food .	這是一間溫室 , 在那裡 , 孩子們會告訴所有關於食物和種植他們自己的食物 。
here is a plant called kevin , or maybe it's a plant belonging to a kid called kevin . i don't know .	這裡有一株叫凱文的植物 , 或者它是屬於一個叫凱文的孩子 。 我不知道 。
but anyway , these kinds of projects that are trying to reconnect us with nature is extremely important .	但無論如何 , 這類企圖將我們與大自然重新連結的計畫極為重要 。
so sitopia , for me , is really a way of seeing .	所以 , 對我來說 , sitopia真的是一種看法 。
it's basically recognizing that sitopia already exists in little pockets everywhere .	基本上是意識到 , 西索比亞已經存在的小口袋裡到處都是 。
the trick is to join them up , to use food as a way of seeing .	訣竅是要加入他們 , 用食物當作一種看法 。
and if we do that , we're going to stop seeing cities as big , metropolitan , unproductive blobs , like this .	如果我們這樣做 , 我們將不再將城市視為大型、大都市、無生產力的團體 , 就像這樣 。
we're going to see them more like this , as part of the productive , organic framework of which they are inevitably a part , symbiotically connected .	我們會把它們看得更像這樣 , 視為是有生產力、有機體架構的一部分 , 它們無可避免地是一部分 , 共生的連結 。
but of course , that's not a great image either , because we need not to be producing food like this anymore .	但當然 , 這也不是很好的圖像 , 因為我們不需要再這樣生產食物了 。
we need to be thinking more about permaculture , which is why i think this image just sums up for me the kind of thinking we need to be doing .	我們需要更進一步思考永續栽培 , 這就是為什麼我認為這張圖片只是為我做個總結 , 我們需要做的那種思考 。
it's a reconceptualization of the way food shapes our lives .	將食物形塑我們生活的方式重新概念化 。
the best image i know of this is from 650 years ago .	我所知道的最好的圖像 , 是從650年前
it's ambrogio lorenzetti's " allegory of good government . "	是安布羅吉歐•洛倫澤蒂的 「 好政府的寓言 」 。
it's about the relationship between the city and the countryside .	關於城市和鄉村之間的關係
and i think the message of this is very clear .	我認為這個訊息非常清楚 。
if the city looks after the country , the country will look after the city .	如果城市照顧這個國家 , 國家會照顧這個城市 。
and i want us to ask now , what would ambrogio lorenzetti paint if he painted this image today ?	我現在要我們問 , 如果他今天畫出這張圖 , 阿布羅吉歐•羅倫澤蒂會畫什麼 ?
what would an allegory of good government look like today ?	今天好的政府會變成什麼樣子 ?
because i think it's an urgent question .	因為我認為這是一個迫切的問題 。
it's one we have to ask , and we have to start answering .	這是我們必須問的 , 我們必須開始回答 。
we know we are what we eat .	我們知道我們吃的東西
we need to realize that the world is also what we eat .	我們需要意識到 , 世界也是我們所吃的 。
but if we take that idea , we can use food as a really powerful tool to shape the world better .	但如果我們採用這個想法 , 我們可以用食物來當作強大的工具 , 來塑造更好的世界 。
weeks from the charter for compassion launch , karen armstrong looks at religion's role in the 21st century: will its dogmas divide us ? or will it unite us for common good ? she reviews the catalysts that can drive the world's faiths to rediscover the golden rule .	幾週之後 , 卡倫•阿姆斯壯研究宗教在21世紀所扮演的角色:它的教條會分裂我們嗎 ? 還是它會讓我們團結一致利益 ? 她會檢視促進世界的信仰 , 來重新發現黃金法則 。
god , ted prize , global issues , politics , religion , tedglobal2009 , violence	上帝、ted大獎、全球議題、政治、宗教、tedglobal2009年、暴力事件
karen armstrong: let's revive the golden rule	karenarmstrong:讓我們重新審視黃金法則
for years i've been feeling frustrated , because as a religious historian , i've become acutely aware of the centrality of compassion in all the major world faiths .	多年來 , 我一直覺得很沮喪 , 因為身為宗教歷史學家 , 我很敏銳地意識到 , 在所有主要世界的信仰中 , 同情心的核心 。
every single one of them has evolved their own version of what's been called the golden rule .	每一個都已經演化出他們自己對所謂的黃金法則的版本 。
sometimes it comes in a positive version " always treat all others as you'd like to be treated yourself . "	有時它會帶著正面的版本 「 總是把所有其他人對待 , 就像你想要對待自己一樣 。 」
and equally important is the negative version " don't do to others what you would not like them to do to you . "	同樣重要的是負面的版本 「 不要對別人做你不喜歡的事 。 」
look into your own heart , discover what it is that gives you pain and then refuse , under any circumstance whatsoever , to inflict that pain on anybody else .	看看你自己的心臟 , 發現它帶給你痛苦的是什麼 , 然後在任何情況下拒絕 , 在任何情況下 , 將那痛苦打在任何其他人身上 。
and people have emphasized the importance of compassion , not just because it sounds good , but because it works .	而人們強調了同情心的重要性不只是因為它聽起來很好 , 而是因為它有用 。
people have found that when they have implemented the golden rule as confucius said , " all day and every day , " not just a question of doing your good deed for the day and then returning to a life of greed and egotism , but to do it all day and every day , you dethrone yourself from the center of your world , put another there , and you transcend yourself .	人們發現 , 當他們實施了自豪的黃金法則 , 如同孔子所說的: 「 一整天、每天 」 , 不只是一個你做善事的問題 , 接著 , 回到貪婪和自我主義的生活中 , 每天都要實現 , 你將自己從世界的中心中偷走 , 把另一個放在那裡 , 超越你自己 。
and it brings you into the presence of what's been called god , nirvana , rama , tao .	它會帶你進入所謂的上帝、諾凡達、拉瑪、泰羅 。
something that goes beyond what we know in our egobound existence .	超越了我們自大的存在 。
but you know you'd never know it a lot of the time , that this was so central to the religious life .	但你知道你從來都不知道 , 這對宗教生活來說是很重要的 。
because with a few wonderful exceptions , very often when religious people come together , religious leaders come together , they're arguing about abstruse doctrines or uttering a council of hatred or inveighing against homosexuality or something of that sort .	因為有幾個很棒的例外 , 當宗教人士聚集在一起時 , 宗教領袖會聚集在一起 , 他們會爭論關於宗教教義 , 或說出一個充滿憎恨的理事會 , 或是反對同性戀或類似的事情 。
often people don't really want to be compassionate .	通常人們並不真的想要有同情心 。
i sometimes see when i'm speaking to a congregation of religious people a sort of mutinous expression crossing their faces because people often want to be right instead .	我有時會看到 , 當我在和宗教人士說話時 , 一種相互影響的表情 , 穿過他們的臉孔 , 因為人們通常會想對 。
and that of course defeats the object of the exercise .	那當然會打敗運動的物體 。
now why was i so grateful to ted ?	我為什麼對ted這麼感激 ?
because they took me very gently from my booklined study and brought me into the 21st century , enabling me to speak to a much , much wider audience than i could have ever conceived .	因為他們很溫柔地從我的書線研究帶領我進入21世紀 , 讓我和更廣的觀眾交流 , 比我想像中還要廣 。
because i feel an urgency about this .	因為我對此感到急迫
if we don't manage to implement the golden rule globally , so that we treat all peoples , wherever and whoever they may be , as though they were as important as ourselves , i doubt that we'll have a viable world to hand on to the next generation .	如果我們不能在全球實施黃金法則 , 這樣我們就能對待所有人 , 不論他們在哪裡 , 不論他們在哪裡 , 彷彿他們和我們自己一樣重要 , 我懷疑我們會有一個可行的世界 , 可以將下一代交給下一代 。
the task of our time , one of the great tasks of our time , is to build a global society , as i said , where people can live together in peace .	我們這個時代的任務 , 我們這個時代最偉大的任務之一 , 就是建立一個全球化的社會 , 如我所說的 , 人們可以在和平中共同生活 。
and the religions that should be making a major contribution are instead seen as part of the problem .	而應該做出重大貢獻的宗教 , 反而被視為問題的一部分 。
and of course it's not just religious people who believe in the golden rule .	當然不只是宗教人士相信黃金法則
this is the source of all morality , this imaginative act of empathy , putting yourself in the place of another .	這是所有道德的源頭 , 這種充滿同理心的想像力 , 把自己放在另一個地方 。
and so we have a choice , it seems to me .	所以我們有選擇 , 對我來說 ,
we can either go on bringing out or emphasizing the dogmatic and intolerant aspects of our faith , or we can go back to the rabbis . rabbi hillel , the older contemporary of jesus , who , when asked by a pagan to sum up the whole of jewish teaching while he stood on one leg , said , " that which is hateful to you , do not do to your neighbor .	我們可以繼續帶出或強調我們信仰的教條和寬容的面向 , 或者我們也可以回到拉比 。 拉比•希爾 , 較年長的耶穌當代 , 當他在用一條腿站立時 , 總結出整個猶太教義 , 他說: 「 這對你來說很討厭 , 不要對你的鄰人做事 。
that is the torah and everything else is only commentary . "	這是托拉 , 其他的都只是評論而已 。 」
and the rabbis and the early fathers of the church who said that any interpretation of scripture that bred hatred and disdain was illegitimate .	而教堂的拉比人和早期的父親 , 他們說 , 任何對培養憎恨與不利的經文的詮釋都是不合法的 。
and we need to revive that spirit .	而我們需要復甦這種精神 。
and it's not just going to happen because a spirit of love wafts us down .	這不只會發生 , 因為愛的精神讓我們失望 。
we have to make this happen , and we can do it with the modern communications that ted has introduced .	我們必須讓這一切實現 , 我們可以用ted所引進的現代溝通來實現 。
already i've been tremendously heartened at the response of all our partners .	我已經對我們所有伴侶的反應感到極度的期待 。
in singapore , we have a group going to use the charter to heal divisions recently that have sprung up in singaporean society , and some members of the parliament want to implement it politically .	在新加坡 , 我們有一個團體會利用憲章來治癒分歧 , 最近在新加坡社會中出現 , 議會中的一些成員想要在政治上實施 。
in malaysia , there is going to be an art exhibition in which leading artists are going to be taking people , young people , and showing them that compassion also lies at the root of all art .	在馬來西亞 , 將來會有一場藝術展覽 , 主導藝術家將要帶領人們 , 年輕人 , 並向他們展示 , 同情心也屬於所有藝術的根源 。
throughout europe , the muslim communities are holding events and discussions , are discussing the centrality of compassion in islam and in all faiths .	在整個歐洲 , 穆斯林社區正在舉辦活動和討論 , 正在討論伊斯蘭和所有信仰中的慈悲中心 。
but it can't stop there . it can't stop with the launch .	但它不能停在那裡 。 它不能停止發射 。
religious teaching , this is where we've gone so wrong , concentrating solely on believing abstruse doctrines .	宗教教學 , 這是我們出錯的地方 , 單純集中在相信荒誕的教義上 。
religious teaching must always lead to action .	宗教教誨一定會導致行動 。
and i intend to work on this till my dying day .	我打算在我死去的那一天工作 。
and i want to continue with our partners to do two things educate and stimulate compassionate thinking .	而我想要繼續和我們的夥伴一起做兩件事 , 教育和刺激同情的思考 。
education because we've so dropped out of compassion .	教育是因為我們已經退出了同情心
people often think it simply means feeling sorry for somebody .	人們常常認為這只是意味著對某人感到抱歉 。
but of course you don't understand compassion if you're just going to think about it .	但你當然不了解同情心 , 如果你只想著
you also have to do it .	你也要做 。
i want them to get the media involved because the media are crucial in helping to dissolve some of the stereotypical views we have of other people , which are dividing us from one another .	我希望他們能參與媒體 , 因為媒體在協助消除一些我們對其他人的刻板印象 , 把我們從彼此身上分離出來 。
the same applies to educators .	教育家也同樣適用
i'd like youth to get a sense of the dynamism , the dynamic and challenge of a compassionate lifestyle .	我希望年輕人能感受到一種充滿同情心的生活方式的動力和挑戰 。
and also see that it demands acute intelligence , not just a gooey feeling .	同時也看到它需要敏銳的智能 , 不只是一種美好的感覺 。
i'd like to call upon scholars to explore the compassionate theme in their own and in other people's traditions .	我想要呼籲學者 , 去探索他們自己以及他人傳統中的同情心主題 。
and perhaps above all , to encourage a sensitivity about uncompassionate speaking , so that because people have this charter , whatever their beliefs or lack of them , they feel empowered to challenge uncompassionate speech , disdainful remarks from their religious leaders , their political leaders , from the captains of industry .	最重要的是 , 若要鼓勵對不友善的說話有敏感度 , 這麼一來 , 因為人們有這種特殊的信念 , 不論他們的信仰或缺乏他們 , 他們都覺得有能力去挑戰不友善的言論 , 不友善的言論 , 來自於他們的宗教領袖、他們的政治領袖 , 來自工業部隊的領袖 。
because we can change the world , we have the ability .	因為我們可以改變世界 , 我們有能力
i would never have thought of putting the charter online .	我從來沒有想過要把章節放在網路上 。
i was still stuck in the old world of a whole bunch of boffins sitting together in a room and issuing yet another arcane statement .	我還困在舊世界裡 , 一大堆小販坐在一間房間裡 , 說出另一句話 。
and ted introduced me to a whole new way of thinking and presenting ideas .	ted向我介紹了一種全新的思考方式和呈現想法 。
because that is what is so wonderful about ted .	因為這就是ted的精彩之處
in this room , all this expertise , if we joined it all together , we could change the world .	在這個房間裡 , 所有這些專業知識 , 如果我們全部加入 , 我們就能改變世界 。
and of course the problems sometimes seem insuperable .	當然問題有時看起來是不可避免的 。
but i'd just like to quote , finish at the end with a reference to a british author , an oxford author whom i don't quote very often , c . s . lewis .	但我想引述一下 , 結尾是一位英國作家 , 他是一位牛津作家 , 我不常引述 , c.s.路易斯 。
but he wrote one thing that stuck in my mind ever since i read it when i was a schoolgirl .	但他寫了一件事 , 自從我讀到學校主席之後 , 就一直在我腦海中浮現 。
it's in his book " the four loves . "	在他的《四個愛》這本書裡
he said that he distinguished between erotic love , when two people gaze , spellbound , into each other's eyes .	他說 , 他分辨出性愛 , 當兩個人凝視時 , 拼著對方的眼睛 。
and then he compared that to friendship , when two people stand side by side , as it were , shoulder to shoulder , with their eyes fixed on a common goal .	接著 , 他把這和友誼做比較 , 當兩個人站在一起 , 就像是肩並肩 , 雙眼固定在共同目標上 。
we don't have to fall in love with each other , but we can become friends .	我們不需要愛上彼此 , 但我們可以成為朋友 。
and i am convinced .	而我深信 ,
i felt it very strongly during our little deliberations at vevey , that when people of all different persuasions come together , working side by side for a common goal , differences melt away .	在我們在調查期間 , 我強烈感受到 , 當所有不同說服的人聚集在一起 , 同心協力 , 同心協力達成共同目標 , 差異就會融化 。
and we learn amity .	而我們學會了同理心 。
and we learn to live together and to get to know one another .	我們學會一起生活 , 學會彼此認識 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝 。
david macaulay relives the winding and sometimes surreal journey toward the completion of rome antics , his illustrated homage to the historic city .	davidmacaulay重新仰賴風和有時超現實的旅程 , 朝著羅馬反抗的協定前進 , 他對歷史城市的致敬 。
macarthur grant , art , arts , book , cities , communication , culture , design , entertainment , humor , storytelling	麥克阿瑟•格蘭特、藝術、書籍、城市、溝通、文化、設計、娛樂、幽默、說故事 。
i draw to better understand things .	我畫畫的目的是為了更了解事物 。
sometimes i make a lot of drawings and i still don't understand what it is i'm drawing .	有時候我畫了很多圖畫 , 我仍然不明白我在畫什麼 。
those of you who are comfortable with digital stuff and even smug about that relationship might be amused to know that the guy who is best known for " the way things work , " while preparing for part of a panel for called understanding , spent two days trying to get his laptop to communicate with his new cd burner .	在座的各位 , 對於數位化的東西感到很自在 , 甚至對那段關係很有趣 , 可能還會知道 , 最為人所知的 「 事物運作的方式 」 , 同時為 「 理解 」 做準備 , 花了兩天的時間 , 試圖讓他的筆記型電腦和他的新cd燒錄器溝通 。
who knew about extension managers ?	誰知道延伸經理呢 ?
i've always managed my own extensions so it never even occurred to me to read the instructions , but i did finally figure it out . i had to figure it out , because along with the invitation came the frightening reminder that there would be no projector , so bringing those carousels would no longer be necessary but some alternate form of communication would .	我一直在管理我自己的延伸 , 以至於我從來沒有想過要讀取指示 , 但我終於想通了 。 我必須搞清楚 , 因為 , 隨著邀請出現了令人恐懼的提醒 , 沒有投影機 , 所以 , 把這些車子帶回來 , 不再是必要的 , 而是某種形式的溝通方式 。
now , i could talk about something that i'm known for , something that would be particularly appropriate for many of the more technically minded people here , or i could talk about something i really care about .	現在 , 我可以談論一些我所熟知的事 , 一些特別適合在場的許多技術專業的人 , 或者我可以談論一些我真正關心的事情 。
i decided to go with the latter .	我決定帶著後者去
i'm going to talk about rome .	我要談談羅馬 。
now , why would i care about rome , particularly ?	我為什麼要在乎羅馬呢 ? 尤其是 ?
well , i went to rhode island school of design in the second half of the '60s to study architecture .	嗯 , 我到羅德島設計學院在60年代後半 , 去研究建築 。
i was lucky enough to spend my last year , my fifth year , in rome as a student . it changed my life .	我很幸運 , 去年 , 我五年在羅馬當學生 , 這改變了我的人生 。
not the least reason was the fact that i had spent those first four years living at home , driving into risd everyday , driving back .	並不是最不合理的原因是我在家裡度過了前四年的生活 , 每天開車回家 , 開車回家 。
i missed the '60s . i read about them ; i understand they were pretty interesting . i missed them , but i did spend that extraordinary year in rome , and it's a place that is never far from my mind .	我錯過了60年代 。 我讀到他們 , 我知道他們挺有意思的 。 我錯過了他們 , 但我的確在羅馬度過了那不平凡的一年 , 那是一個離我腦海不遠的地方 。
so , whenever given an opportunity , i try to do something in it or with it or for it .	所以 , 每當有機會 , 我就會試著用它或它來做些什麼 。
i also make drawings to help people understand things .	我也畫圖來幫助人們了解事物 。
things that i want them to believe i understand .	那些我希望他們相信我了解的事物
and that's what i do as an illustrator , that's my job .	這就是我作為一個插畫家所做的 , 那是我的工作 。

a book is not only a neat way of collecting and storing information , it's a series of layers .	一本書不僅是一個整齊的收集和儲存資訊的方法 , 它是一系列的層次 。
i mean , you always peel one layer off another ; we think of them as pages , doing it a certain way .	我的意思是 , 你總是把一層拆開 , 我們把它們看成頁面 , 以某種方式做 。
but think of them as layers . i mean , rome is a place of layers horizontal layers , vertical layers and i thought , well just peeling off a page would allow me to if i got you thinking about it the right way would allow me to sort of show you the depth of layers .	但把它們想像成層層 。 我的意思是 , 羅馬是一個層層的層次 , 橫向的層次 , 垂直的層次 , 然後我想 , 只要把頁面剝下來 , 就可以讓我思考一下 , 如果我有正確的思考方式 , 可以讓我向你們展示一些層層次的深度 。
the stucco on the walls of most of the buildings in rome covers the scars ; the scars of centuries of change as these structures have been adapted rather than being torn down .	在羅馬大部分建築物的牆上 , 都是圍繞著疤痕 ; 數世紀以來 , 改變的疤痕一直在適應 , 而不是被拆除 。
if i do a foldout page on the lefthand side and let you just unfold it , you see behind it what i mean by scar tissue .	如果我在左手邊做一個摺疊頁 , 讓你們展開 , 你可以看到它背後的意思 , 疤痕組織 。
you can see that in 1635 , it became essential to make smaller windows because the bad guys were coming or whatever .	你可以看到 , 在1635年 , 做小窗戶是必要的 , 因為壞人要來了 , 或其他東西 。
adaptations all get buried under the stucco .	適應一切都被埋在石頭下 。
i could peel out a page of this palazzo to show you what's going on inside of it .	我可以把這palazzo的一頁拆開 , 讓你們看看它的內部狀況 。
but more importantly , i could also show you what it looks like at the corner of one of those magnificent buildings with all the massive stone blocks , or the fake stone blocks done with brick and stucco , which is more often the case .	但 , 更重要的是 , 我還可以向你們展示那些壯麗的建築物的角落 , 和所有巨大的石塊 , 或是用磚頭和織物磚塊做成的假石塊 , 比較常是這樣 。
so it becomes slightly threedimensional .	所以它會變得稍微立體 。
i could take you down one of those narrow little streets into one of those surprising piazzas by using a double gate fold double foldout page which , if you were like me reading a popup book as a child , you hopefully stick your head into .	我可以帶你們走下一條狹窄的小街道 , 進入其中一個令人驚訝的廣場 , 使用雙層次摺疊頁--如果你像我一樣 , 讀一本彈出式書 , 你會希望把你的頭塞進去 。
you wrap the pages around your head and are in that piazza for that brief period of time .	你在頭上翻頁 , 在那短暫的時期 , 就在那廣場 。
and i've really not done anything much more complicated than make foldout pages .	我沒有做過比做摺疊頁更複雜的事 。
but then i thought , maybe i could be simpler here .	但後來我想 , 也許我可以簡單一點 。
let's look at the pantheon and the piazza della rotonda in front of it .	我們來看看萬神廟和前面的皮亞薩•德拉•羅頓達
here's a book completely wide open .	這是一本完全開放的書 。
ok , if i don't open the book the whole way , if i just open it 90 degrees , we're looking down the front of the pantheon , and we're looking sort of at the top , more or less down on the square .	好 , 如果我不把書全部打開 , 如果我把它打開90度 , 我們就從萬神殿的正面往下看 , 看上方 , 或多或少在正方形上方 。
and if i turn the book the other way , we're looking across the square at the front of the pantheon .	如果我把書翻過來 , 我們會看到萬神殿前方的廣場 。
no foldouts , no tricks just a book that isn't open the whole way .	沒有摺疊 , 沒有戲法只是一本沒有完全開放的書 。
that seemed promising . i thought , maybe i'll do it inside and i can even combine the foldouts with the only partially opened book .	這看起來很有前景 。 我想 , 也許我會在裡面做 , 甚至可以把摺疊物和唯一一部分開放的書結合在一起 。
so we get inside the pantheon and it grows and so on and so forth .	所以我們進入萬神廟 , 它會成長等等 。
and i thought , maybe i'm on the right track , but it sort of lost its human quality .	我想 , 也許我是站在正確的軌道上 , 但它有點失去了它的人類特質 。
so i went back to the notion of story , which is always a good thing to have if you're trying to get people to pay attention to a book and pick up information along the way .	所以 , 我回到故事的概念 , 如果你試圖讓人們注意一本書 , 一路上撿起資訊 , 總是件好事 。
" pigeon's progress " struck me as a catchy title .	「 鴿子的進步 」 把我當成捕捉標題 。
if it was a homing pigeon , it would be called " homer's odyssey . "	假如牠是隻宅鴿 , 牠會被稱為 「 荷馬的奧德修女 」 。
but it was the journey of the . . .	但那是那趟旅程......
i mean , if a title works , use it . but it would be a journey that went through rome and showed all the things that i like about rome .	我的意思是 , 如果一個標題成功了 , 用它 。 但這會是一趟穿越羅馬的旅程 , 展示所有我喜歡羅馬的東西 。
it's a pigeon sitting on top of a church .	是坐在教堂的上方的鴿子 。
goes off during the day and does normal pigeon stuff . comes back , the whole place is covered with scaffolding and green netting and there's no way this pigeon can get home .	白天放假 , 做正常的鴿子東西 。 回來 , 整個地方充滿著支架和綠色網路 , 這樣一來 , 鴿子就無法回家了 。
so it's a homeless pigeon now and it's going to have to find another place to live , and that allows me to go through my catalog of favorite things , and we start with the tall ones and so on .	所以現在是無家可歸的鴿子 , 牠必須找到另一個居住地 , 這讓我得以通過我最喜歡的目錄 , 我們從高處開始 。
maybe it has to go back and live with family members ; that's not always a good thing , but it does sort of bring pigeons together again .	也許牠必須回去和家人同住 ; 那不一定是好事 , 但牠會再次把鴿子集合在一起 。
and i thought , that's sort of interesting , but maybe there's a person who should be involved in this in some way .	我心想 , 這有點有趣 , 但也許有個人應該用某種方式參與這個活動 。
so i kind of came up with this old guy who spends his life looking after sick pigeons .	所以我想出了一個老傢伙 , 他一生都在照顧生病的鴿子 。
he'll go anywhere to get them dangerous places and whatnot and they become really friends with this guy , and learn to do tricks for him and entertain him at lunchtime and stuff like that .	他會到任何地方 , 去找他們危險的地方 , 什麼都不會 , 他們會和這個傢伙交朋友 , 學會為他做技倆 , 在午餐時間和其他類似的東西娛樂他 。
there's a real bond that develops between this old man and these pigeons .	在這個老人和這些鴿子之間發展出真實的鍵結 。
but unfortunately he gets sick . he gets really sick at the end of the story .	但不幸的是 , 他生病了 。 他在故事結束時真的生病了 。
he's taught them to spell his name , which is aldo .	他教導他們拼他的名字 , 也就是aldo 。
they show up one day after three or four days of not seeing him he lives in this little garret and they spell his name and fly around .	他們在三、四天不見他之後 , 出現了一天 , 他住在這個小小的車庫中 , 他們拼出他的名字 , 飛來飛去 。
and he finally gets enough strength together to climb up the ladder onto the roof , and all the pigeons , a la red balloon , are there waiting for him and they carry him off over the walls of the city .	他終於得到足夠的力量 , 把梯子爬到屋頂上 , 所有的鴿子 , la紅氣球 , 都在等著他 , 他們把他帶到城牆上 。
and i forgot to mention this: whenever he lost a pigeon , he would take that pigeon out beyond the walls of the city .	我忘了提到這一點:每當他失去一隻鴿子時 , 他就會把那隻鴿子趕出城牆之外 。
in the old roman custom , the dead were never buried within the walls .	在古羅馬習俗中 , 死者從來沒有被埋在牆內 。
and i thought that's a really cheery story .	我覺得這真的很討喜 。
. that's really going to go a long way .	這真的要走很長的路
so anyway , i went through . . . and again , if packaging doesn't work and if the stories aren't going anywhere , i just come up with titles and hope that a title will sort of kick me off in the right direction .	總之 , 我經歷了......再說一次 , 如果包裝沒用了 , 如果故事沒到哪裡去 , 我就會想出頭銜 , 希望書名能把我推向正確的方向 。
and sometimes it does focus me enough and i'll even do a title page .	有時它會把我聚焦得足夠 , 我甚至會做一個標題頁 。
so , these are all title pages that eventually led me to the solution i settled on , which is the story of a young woman who sends a message on a homing pigeon she lives outside the walls of the city of rome to someone in the city .	所以 , 這些都是標題 , 最終引領我解決方案 , 這是一位年輕女子的故事 , 她在羅馬城外的牆上傳送了一則訊息給羅馬城外的鴿子 。
and the pigeon is flying down above the appian way here .	而鴿子正從這裡飛過 。
you can see the tombs and pines and so on and so forth along the way .	你可以看到墓碑上和松鼠等等 。
if you see the red line , you are seeing the trail of the pigeon ; if you don't see the red line , you are the pigeon .	如果你看到紅線 , 你會看到鴿子的蹤跡 ; 如果你看不見紅線 , 你就是那隻鴿子 。
and it becomes necessary and possible , at this point , to try to convey what that sense would be like of flying over the city without actually moving .	此時 , 它變得有必要和可能性 , 試著傳達出那種飛越城市的感覺 , 而不實際移動的感覺 。
past the pyramid of cestius these will seem very familiar to you , even if you haven't been to rome recently past the gatehouse .	超越了西斯提烏斯金字塔──這些對你來說似乎很熟悉 , 即使你最近沒去過羅馬 , 遠遠超越大門 。
this is something that's a little bit unusual .	這是有點不尋常的事 。
this pigeon does something that most homing pigeons do not do: it takes the scenic route , which was a device that i felt was necessary to actually extend this book beyond about four pages .	這隻鴿子做了一件大部份致致敬鴿子不會做的事:它採取了這條視野路線 , 這個裝置是我覺得必須將這本書延伸到大約四頁以外的書上 。
so , we circle around the coliseum , past the church of santa maria in cosmedin and the temple of hercules towards the river .	所以 , 我們繞過羅馬競技場 , 穿過哥斯坦的聖母瑪利亞教堂 , 以及海克力士的神殿 , 朝著河流前進 。
we almost collide with the cornice of the palazzo farnese designed by michelangelo , built of stone taken from the coliseum narrow escape .	我們與米開朗基羅設計的帕拉佐法蘭基羅公司差不多碰撞 , 由競技場狹窄逃離而建造的石頭 。
we swoop down over the campo de' fiori .	我們俯瞰整個柬埔寨的百葉窗 。
this is one of those things i show to my students because it's a complete bastardization a denial of any rules of perspective .	這是我向學生展示的其中一件事 , 因為它是完全的基礎化 , 否認任何規則的觀點 。
the only rule of perspective that i think matters is if it looks believable , you've succeeded .	我認為唯一重要的觀點規則是 , 如果它看起來是可信的 , 你就成功了 。
but you try and figure out where the vanishing points meet here ; a couple are on mars and a couple of others in cremona .	但你試著找出消失的點在哪裡 ; 一對夫妻在火星上 , 和其他幾位在克雷蒙納州 。
but into the piazza in front of santa maria della pace , where invariably a soccer game is going on , and we're hit by a soccer ball .	但在聖母堂前方的皮雅 , 在那裡 , 不可或缺的足球比賽正在進行 , 我們被足球擊中 。
now this is a terrible illustration of being hit by a soccer ball .	現在這是一個被足球擊中很糟糕的畫面 。
i have all the pieces: there's santa maria della pace , there's a soccer ball , there's a little bit of a bird's wing nothing's happening , so i had to rethink it .	我有所有的碎片:有聖母瑪莉亞德拉步調 , 有足球 , 有一點鳥翅目什麼都沒發生 , 所以我得要重新思考它 。
and if you do want to see santa maria della pace , these books are really flexible , incredibly interactive just turn it around and look at it the other way .	如果你想看到聖母瑪利亞•德拉•步調 , 這些書很有彈性 , 很有互動性 , 只要轉過身來 , 用另一種方式來看它 。
through the alley , we can see the impact is captured in the red line .	透過巷子 , 我們可以看到紅線的影響被捕捉 。
and then bird manages to pull itself together past this medieval tower one of the few remaining medieval towers towards the church of sant'agnese and around the dome looking down into piazza navona which we've already mentioned and seen and flown over a couple of times ; there's the bernini statue of the four rivers and then past the wonderful borromini sant'ivo , stopping just long enough on the 26foot diameter oculus of the pantheon to catch our breath .	接著 , 鳥兒想辦法把自己拉過這個中世紀的高塔 , 只有少數中世紀的塔樓之一 , 朝聖的中世紀塔樓邁進 , 環繞著圓頂向下看 , 向著亞扎那沃納沃納維納納納納納納維納 , 我們已經提過、看到、流過了這四條河流的伯尼亞州雕像 , 接著越過了無比的波羅米米尼聖誕節 , 停止了足足足足足的長度 , 來抵達萬神殿的26英尺寬 , 來捕捉我們的呼吸 。
and then we can swoop inside and around ; and because we're flying , we don't really have to worry about gravity at this particular moment in time , so this drawing can be oriented in any way on the page .	然後我們就可以在內部轉圈 , 因為我們在飛行 , 我們不用在這個特定的時刻擔心地心引力 , 所以這幅畫可以用頁面上的任何方式進行定位 。
we get a little exuberant as we pass gesu ; it's not surprising to sort of mimic the architecture in this way .	當我們通過gesu時 , 我們會變得有點誇張 ; 用這種方式來模仿建築 , 並不讓人驚訝 。
past the wonderful wall filled with the juxtaposition that i was talking about ; beautiful carvings set into the walls above the neon " ristorante " sign , and so on .	經過美好的牆上 , 充滿了我所說的 「 交叉分配 」 ; 漂亮的雕刻在新月球 「 ristorante 」 的標誌上方 , 等等 。
and eventually , we arrive at the courtyard of the palazzo , which is our destination .	最後 , 我們抵達了palazzo的庭院 , 這是我們的目的地 。
straight up through the courtyard into a little window into the attic , where somebody is working at the drawing board .	直接穿過庭院 , 進入閣樓的小窗口 , 在那裡 , 有人在畫板上工作 。
he removes the message from the leg of the bird ; this is what it says .	他把訊息從鳥的腿上移開 ; 這是牠說的 。
as we look at the drawing board , we see what he's working on is , in fact , a map of the journey that the pigeon has just taken , and the red line extends through all the sights .	當我們看著畫板 , 我們看到他正在努力的 , 其實是一張鴿子剛剛拍攝的旅程地圖 , 紅線延伸到所有的視野中 。
and if you want the information , so that we complete this cycle of understanding , all you have to do is read these paragraphs .	如果你想要這些資訊 , 這樣我們就完成了這個循環的了解 , 你只需要讀這些段落 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝 。
mit researcher skylar tibbits works on selfassembly the idea that instead of building something , we can create materials that build themselves , much the way a strand of dna zips itself together . it's a big concept at early stages ; tibbits shows us three inthelab projects that hint at what a selfassembling future might look like .	麻省理工學院的研究員天鵝卵會自行組裝這個想法 , 與其建構一些東西 , 我們還能創造一些材料 , 讓它們自己組裝起來 。 很像一股dna片段本身 。 這是一個很大的概念 。 在初期階段 , tibbits向我們展示了三項進化計劃 , 暗示著自組裝的未來可能是什麼樣子 。
skylar tibbits: can we make things that make themselves ?	天際的tibbits:我們可以做出造就自己的東西嗎 ?
today i'd like to show you the future of the way we make things .	今天我想向各位展示我們製造東西的方式的未來 。
i believe that soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , replicating and repairing themselves .	我相信 , 很快我們的建築物和機器就會自我組裝、複製、修復自己 。
so i'm going to show you what i believe is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare that to some natural systems .	所以我要向你們展示我相信的 , 是目前的製造狀態 , 然後與一些自然系統做比較 。
so in the current state of manufacturing , we have skyscrapers two and a half years [of assembly time] , 500 , 000 to a million parts , fairly complex , new , exciting technologies in steel , concrete , glass .	所以 , 在現有的製造業狀態下 , 我們有摩天大樓 , 兩年半的時間 , 五十萬到一百萬個部分 , 在鋼鐵、混凝土、玻璃上 , 相當複雜、嶄新的、令人興奮的技術 。
we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years [of assembly time] , 2 . 5 million parts .	我們有令人興奮的機器可以帶我們進入太空五年--[組裝時間] , 250萬個零件 。
but on the other side , if you look at the natural systems , we have proteins that have two million types , can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , or dna with three billion base pairs we can replicate in roughly an hour .	但在另一邊 , 如果你看一下自然系統 , 我們有兩百萬種類型的蛋白質 , 可以在一萬奈秒折疊 , 或dna有三十億個鹼基對 , 我們可以在大約一個小時內複製 。
so there's all of this complexity in our natural systems , but they're extremely efficient , far more efficient than anything we can build , far more complex than anything we can build .	所以 , 在我們的自然系統中 , 所有這些複雜性 , 但它們極為有效率 , 遠比我們所能建造的任何東西都更有效率 , 遠比我們所能建造的任何東西都還要複雜 。
they're far more efficient in terms of energy .	它們在能源方面更有效率 。
they hardly ever make mistakes .	他們幾乎不會犯錯 。
and they can repair themselves for longevity .	而且他們可以長壽修復自己 。
so there's something super interesting about natural systems .	所以 , 關於自然系統 , 有個超級有趣的東西 。
and if we can translate that into our built environment , then there's some exciting potential for the way that we build things .	如果我們可以將之轉化為我們的建築環境 , 那就有一些令人振奮的潛力 , 可以讓我們建造東西 。
and i think the key to that is selfassembly .	我認為關鍵在於自我組裝 。
so if we want to utilize selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there's four key factors .	所以 , 如果我們想要在我們的物理環境中利用自我組裝 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。
the first is that we need to decode all of the complexity of what we want to build so our buildings and machines .	第一 , 我們需要解碼所有我們想要建造的東西的複雜性 , 以便我們的建築和機器 。
and we need to decode that into simple sequences basically the dna of how our buildings work .	我們需要將之解碼成簡單的序列基本上就是我們建築物運作的dna
then we need programmable parts that can take that sequence and use that to fold up , or reconfigure .	接著 , 我們需要可編程的部件 , 可以拿這個序列來摺疊 , 或重新配置 。
we need some energy that's going to allow that to activate , allow our parts to be able to fold up from the program .	我們需要一些能讓它活化的能量 , 讓我們的部件能夠從程式中摺疊起來 。
and we need some type of error correction redundancy to guarantee that we have successfully built what we want .	我們需要某種類型的錯誤矯正缺陷 , 來保證我們已經成功地建立了我們想要的 。
so i'm going to show you a number of projects that my colleagues and i at mit are working on to achieve this selfassembling future .	所以我要給你們看一些計畫 , 我和我在麻省理工學院的同事正在努力實現這個自我組裝的未來 。
the first two are the macrobot and decibot .	前兩個是macrobot和decibot
so these projects are largescale reconfigurable robots 8 ft . , 12 ft . long proteins .	所以這些計畫是大規模可重組的機器人--8英尺 , 12英尺 。 長的蛋白質 。
they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .	嵌入機械電器、感應器
you decode what you want to fold up into , into a sequence of angles so negative 120 , negative 120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , negative 120 something like that ; so a sequence of angles , or turns , and you send that sequence through the string .	你把你想要的東西解碼成一連串的角度--那麼負120 , 負120 , 0 , 0 , 0 , 120 , 負120--類似的東西 ; 所以一連串的角度 , 或輪流 , 你把那序列通過了弦 。
each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每個單位都帶著它的負面訊息──它旋轉到那邊 , 檢查它是否到達那裡 , 然後傳遞給它的鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	所以這些是傑出的科學家、工程師、設計師 , 在這個計畫上工作 。
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我認為這真的能帶來光明:這真的可擴展嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 幾千美金 , 許多男生的時間都是為了製造這個八英尺高的機器人 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們可以把這個擴大嗎 ? 我們真的可以把機器人嵌入每個部分嗎 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題 , 和看待被動的自然 , 或被動地嘗試重新配置可編程 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但它更進一步 , 它嘗試著實際的計算 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	它基本上將電腦運算最基本的基礎建構 , 也就是數位邏輯閘 , 直接嵌入到你的零件中 。
so this is a nand gate .	所以這是nandgate
you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	你有一個四面體 , 就是大門要做你的計算 , 你有兩個輸入的四面體 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中之一是使用者的輸入 , 如同你在建構你的磚塊一樣 。
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另外一個是從之前被放置的磚
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	然後它會在3d空間中給你輸出 。
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	這意味著 , 使用者可以開始在他們想要磚塊做的事上 。
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它會計算它之前在做什麼 , 以及你說你想要它做什麼 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它開始在三維空間中移動 , 向上或向下 。
so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	所以 , 在左手邊 , [1]輸入等於0輸出值 , 下降了 。
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	在右手邊 , [0 , 0]輸入是一個輸出值 , 上升 。
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	那真正的意思是 , 我們的結構現在包含了我們想要建造的東西的藍圖 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	所以他們所有的資訊都嵌入其中 , 說明了什麼是建構出來的 。
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	所以這意味著我們可以有某種形式的自我複製 。
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這個例子中 , 我稱它為自給自足的複製 , 因為你的結構包含了精確的藍圖 。
if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果你有錯誤 , 你可以取代一個部分 。
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有的本地資訊都嵌入其中來告訴你如何修復它 。
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	所以你可以有東西爬上去 , 讀它 , 然後在一對一輸出 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	它直接嵌入 ; 沒有外界指示 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	所以 , 我將要展示的最後一個專案叫做偏差鏈 , 它可能是我們現在最令人興奮的例子 , 被動式自組裝系統 。
so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	所以它需要重新配置和可程式化 , 使它成為一個完全被動的系統 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	所以基本上你有一鏈元素 。
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每個元素都是完全相同的 , 它們有偏見 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	所以 , 每一個鏈條 , 或每一個元素 , 都想要左轉或左轉 。
so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	所以當你組裝鏈時 , 你基本上是在編程 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你在告訴每個單位是否應該向右轉或向左轉 。
so when you shake the chain , it then folds up into any configuration that you've programmed in so in this case , a spiral , or in this case , two cubes next to each other .	所以當你搖晃鏈 , 它就會折疊成任何你編程的配置--在這個例子中 , 一個螺旋 , 或者在這個例子中 , 兩個立方體相鄰 。
so you can basically program any threedimensional shape or onedimensional , twodimensional up into this chain completely passively .	基本上你可以編寫任何立體形狀或上維度 , 二維空間完全被動地進入這個鏈子 。
so what does this tell us about the future ?	所以 , 這告訴我們未來什麼 ?
i think that it's telling us that there's new possibilities for selfassembly , replication , repair in our physical structures , our buildings , machines .	我認為 , 它告訴我們 , 自我組裝、複製、修復我們的實體結構、建築物、機器都有新的可能性 。
there's new programmability in these parts .	在這些部分有新的可編程 。
and from that you have new possibilities for computing .	由此可知電腦運算的新可能性
we'll have spatial computing .	我們會有空間計算 。
imagine if our buildings , our bridges , machines , all of our bricks could actually compute .	想像一下 , 如果我們的建築物、橋樑、機器 , 我們所有的磚塊其實都可以計算 。
that's amazing parallel and distributed computing power , new design possibilities .	那是驚人的平行和分散式運算能力 , 新的設計可能性 。
so it's exciting potential for this .	所以這很讓人興奮的潛力 。
so i think these projects i've showed here are just a tiny step towards this future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .	所以我認為我在這裡展示的這些項目只是朝向這個未來邁進的一小步 , 如果我們實行這些新技術 , 為一個新的自我組裝世界 。
we've been to the moon , we've mapped the continents , we've even been to the deepest point in the ocean twice . what's left for the next generation to explore ? biologist and explorer nathan wolfe suggests this answer: almost everything . and we can start , he says , with the world of the unseeably small .	我們去過月球 , 繪製了大陸的地圖 , 我們甚至去過海洋中最深的一點 。 下一代還剩什麼可以探索 ? 生物學家和探險家nathanwolfe提出了這個答案:幾乎所有東西 。 然後我們就可以開始 , 他說 , 與這個不可思議的小世界在一起 。
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	生物多樣性、探索、微生物學、科學
nathan wolfe: what's left to explore ?	nathanwolfe:還有什麼東西可以探索 ?
recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .	最近我拜訪了威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特 ,
and i was there to honor a great 20th century explorer , roy chapman andrews .	我在那裡向一位偉大的20世紀探險家 , roychapmanandrews致敬 。
during his time at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a range of expeditions to uncharted regions , like here in the gobi desert .	在他在美國自然歷史博物館的期間 , 安德魯斯帶領了一系列探險隊去未知的地區 , 就像這裡的戈壁沙漠 。
he was quite a figure .	他是個人物 。
he was later , it's said , the basis of the indiana jones character .	他後來 , 據說是印第安那瓊斯角色的基礎 。
and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市時 , 我給一群中學學生做公開講座 。
and i'm here to tell you , if there's anything more intimidating than talking here at ted , it'll be trying to hold the attention of a group of a thousand 12yearolds for a 45minute lecture .	我來這裡是要告訴各位 , 如果比在ted這裡演講還要嚇人一點 , 它會試著把一群12歲孩童的注意力集中在45分鐘的演講中 。
at the end of the lecture they asked a number of questions , but there was one that's really stuck with me since then .	在演講結束後 , 他們問了幾個問題 , 但其中有一個問題是從那時起就一直困在我身上的 。
there was a young girl who stood up , and she asked the question: " where should we explore ? "	有一個年輕女孩站起來 , 她問了這個問題: 「 我們該去哪探險 ? 」
i think there's a sense that many of us have that the great age of exploration on earth is over , that for the next generation they're going to have to go to outer space or the deepest oceans in order to find something significant to explore .	我想我們之中有很多人認為地球上最偉大的探索時代已經結束了 , 對下一代來說 , 他們得要去外太空或最深的海洋 , 才能找到重要的探索 。
but is that really the case ?	但真的是這樣嗎 ?
is there really nowhere significant for us to explore left here on earth ?	我們在地球上所剩下的土地上是否真的有重要性 ?
it sort of made me think back to one of my favorite explorers in the history of biology .	這有點讓我回想起生物史上我最喜歡的探險家之一 。
this is an explorer of the unseen world , martinus beijerinck .	這是個看不見的世界的探險家 , martinusbeijerinck 。
so beijerinck set out to discover the cause of tobacco mosaic disease .	所以beijerinck開始發現菸草鑲嵌病的起因 。
what he did is he took the infected juice from tobacco plants and he would filter it through smaller and smaller filters .	他所做的是從菸草植物中取出受感染的汁液 , 他會透過越來越小的過濾器過濾 。
and he reached the point where he felt that there must be something out there that was smaller than the smallest forms of life that were ever known bacteria , at the time .	他接觸到一個點 , 他覺得一定有些東西比當時所知的最小型的生命形式還小 。
he came up with a name for his mystery agent .	他為他的神秘代理人提出了一個名字 。
he called it the virus latin for " poison . "	他稱之為 「 毒藥 」 的病毒拉丁文
and in uncovering viruses , beijerinck really opened this entirely new world for us .	在揭開病毒時 , beijerinck真的為我們打開了這個全新的世界 。
we now know that viruses make up the majority of the genetic information on our planet , more than the genetic information of all other forms of life combined .	我們現在知道病毒構成了地球上大多數的基因信息 , 超過所有其他形式生命組合的遺傳信息 。
and obviously there's been tremendous practical applications associated with this world things like the eradication of smallpox , the advent of a vaccine against cervical cancer , which we now know is mostly caused by human papillomavirus .	很明顯地 , 已經有極大的實際應用在這個世界中 , 像是天花的消滅 , 一種疫苗對抗子宮頸癌的出現 , 而我們現在知道的 , 主要是由人類乳腺病毒所造成的 。
and beijerinck's discovery , this was not something that occurred 500 years ago .	而beijerinck的發現 , 這並不是500年前發生的事 。
it was a little over 100 years ago that beijerinck discovered viruses .	大約一百多年前 , beijerinck發現了病毒 。
so basically we had automobiles , but we were unaware of the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	所以基本上我們有了汽車 , 但是我們還沒意識到我們星球上大部分的基因信息的生命形式 。
we now have these amazing tools to allow us to explore the unseen world things like deep sequencing , which allow us to do much more than just skim the surface and look at individual genomes from a particular species , but to look at entire metagenomes , the communities of teeming microorganisms in , on and around us and to document all of the genetic information in these species .	我們現在有了這些驚人的工具 , 讓我們可以探索那些看不見的世界 , 像是深度定序之類的東西 , 它讓我們不僅能跳過表面 , 還能從特定的物種中看出個別的基因組 , 而是去看整個方法 , 這些微生物群落在我們周遭 , 記錄這些物種的所有遺傳信息 。
we can apply these techniques to things from soil to skin and everything in between .	我們可以把這些技巧用在從土壤到皮膚和中間的一切 。
in my organization we now do this on a regular basis to identify the causes of outbreaks that are unclear exactly what causes them .	在我的組織裡 , 我們現在以一般的基礎 , 來確認造成疫情爆發的原因 。
and just to give you a sense of how this works , imagine that we took a nasal swab from every single one of you .	為了讓你們了解這如何運作 , 想像一下 , 我們從你們每一個人身上 , 拿了一把鼻腔 。
and this is something we commonly do to look for respiratory viruses like influenza .	這是我們常做的 , 去尋找呼吸道病毒 , 像是流感病毒 。
the first thing we would see is a tremendous amount of genetic information .	首先我們會看到的是大量的基因信息 。
and if we started looking into that genetic information , we'd see a number of usual suspects out there of course , a lot of human genetic information , but also bacterial and viral information , mostly from things that are completely harmless within your nose .	如果我們開始研究這些基因信息 , 我們會看到一些常見的嫌疑犯 , 當然 , 很多的人類基因信息 , 還有細菌和病毒信息 , 大部分來自你鼻子裡完全無害的信息 。
but we'd also see something very , very surprising .	但我們也看到了一些令人非常驚訝的事 。
as we started to look at this information , we would see that about 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose doesn't match anything that we've ever seen before no plant , animal , fungus , virus or bacteria .	當我們開始研究這些資訊時 , 我們會發現 , 你鼻子裡大約百分之二十的基因信息 , 和我們以前見過的任何東西都不符合 , 沒有植物、動物、真菌、病毒 , 或細菌 。
basically we have no clue what this is .	基本上我們不知道這是什麼 。
and for the small group of us who actually study this kind of data , a few of us have actually begun to call this information biological dark matter .	對於我們這些實際研究這種數據的小團體 , 我們當中有一些人已經開始稱之為資訊生物暗物質 。
we know it's not anything that we've seen before ; it's sort of the equivalent of an uncharted continent right within our own genetic information .	我們知道這不是我們以前見過的任何東西 ; 有點像是我們自己的基因信息中未知的大陸 。
and there's a lot of it .	而且還有很多
if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , if we looked at your gut , up to 40 or 50 percent of that information is biological dark matter .	如果你認為你鼻子裡有20%的基因信息是很多的生物暗物質 , 如果我們觀察你的腸子 , 高達40%或50%的信息是生物暗物質 。
and even in the relatively sterile blood , around one to two percent of this information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be typed or matched with anything we've seen before .	即使在相對抗的血液中 , 大約有1%到2%的資訊是暗物質 , 無法被分類 , 不能被我們看過的任何東西給打字或配對 。
at first we thought that perhaps this was artifact .	一開始我們以為也許這是人造物品 。
these deep sequencing tools are relatively new .	這些深度定序的工具相對是新的 。
but as they become more and more accurate , we've determined that this information is a form of life , or at least some of it is a form of life .	但當它們變得越來越準確時 , 我們已經判斷出這些資訊是一種生命形式 , 或至少有一部分是生命的形式 。
and while the hypotheses for explaining the existence of biological dark matter are really only in their infancy , there's a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that buried in this life , in this genetic information , are signatures of as of yet unidentified life .	雖然解釋生物暗物質存在的假設只存在於嬰兒期 , 但存在著非常令人興奮的可能性:埋藏在生命中 , 在這遺傳信息中 , 都是尚未被辨識出的生命跡象 。
that as we explore these strings of a's , t's , c's and g's , we may uncover a completely new class of life that , like beijerinck , will fundamentally change the way that we think about the nature of biology .	當我們探索一系列的a、t、c、g時 , 我們可能會發現一種全新的生命類型 , 就像beijerinck一樣 , 將會從根本上改變我們對生物學本質的看法 。
that perhaps will allow us to identify the cause of a cancer that afflicts us or identify the source of an outbreak that we aren't familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .	這或許可以讓我們找出一個會衝突我們的癌症的原因 , 或找出我們不熟悉的疫情來源 , 或可能在分子生物學中創造出新的工具 。
i'm pleased to announce that , along with colleagues at stanford and caltech and ucsf , we're currently starting an initiative to explore biological dark matter for the existence of new forms of life .	我很高興能宣佈 , 和史丹佛、加州理工學院和加州大學洛杉磯分校的同事一起 , 我們目前正在開始一項計畫 , 探索生物暗物質 , 為新生命的存在而努力 。
a little over a hundred years ago , people were unaware of viruses , the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	大約一百多年前 , 人們不知道病毒 , 形成我們星球上大部分遺傳信息的生命形式 。
a hundred years from now , people may marvel that we were perhaps completely unaware of a new class of life that literally was right under our noses .	一百年後 , 人們可能會驚嘆我們可能完全不知道在我們鼻子底下的新生命階級 。
it's true , we may have charted all the continents on the planet and we may have discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing left to explore on earth .	這是真的 , 我們可能已經把地球上所有的大陸都描繪出來了 , 我們可能已經發現了所有的哺乳動物 , 但這並不表示地球上沒有任何東西可以探索 。
beijerinck and his kind provide an important lesson for the next generation of explorers people like that young girl from beloit , wisconsin .	beijerinck和他的同類提供了重要的一課 , 給下一代的探險家們 , 像來自威斯康辛州的貝洛特市的年輕女孩 。
and i think if we phrase that lesson , it's something like this: don't assume that what we currently think is out there is the full story .	我認為 , 如果我們把這一課說成這樣:不要假定我們目前認為的都是完整的故事 。
go after the dark matter in whatever field you choose to explore .	去追尋任何你選擇探索的領域中的暗物質 。
there are unknowns all around us and they're just waiting to be discovered .	我們身邊到處都是未知 , 只等著被發現 。
legendary scientist david deutsch puts theoretical physics on the back burner to discuss a more urgent matter: the survival of our species . the first step toward solving global warming , he says , is to admit that we have a problem .	傳說中的科學家大衛•德魯斯奇把理論物理放到背負中 , 來討論更緊迫的物質:我們物種的生存 。 解決全球暖化的第一步 , 他說 , 就是承認我們有問題 。
climate change , cosmos , culture , environment , global issues , physics , science , technology , universe	氣候變遷、宇宙、文化、環境、全球議題、物理、科學、科技、宇宙、宇宙 。
david deutsch on our place in the cosmos	daviddeutsch在我們宇宙中的位置上
we've been told to go out on a limb and say something surprising .	我們被告知要走出肢體 , 說出令人驚訝的事 。
so i'll try and do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone already knows .	我會試著這麼做 , 但我想先從大家都知道的兩件事開始 。
and the first one , in fact , is something that has been known for most of recorded history .	第一個 , 事實上 , 是大部分記錄的歷史上已知的東西 。
and that is that the planet earth , or the solar system , or our environment or whatever , is uniquely suited to sustain our evolution or creation , as it used to be thought and our present existence , and most important , our future survival .	那就是地球、太陽系、環境等等 , 都是獨一無二的 , 能夠維持我們的演化或創造 , 就像以前的思想和現在的存在 , 最重要的是我們未來的生存 。
nowadays this idea has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .	現在這個想法有個戲劇性的名字:太空船地球 。
and the idea there is that outside the spaceship , the universe is implacably hostile , and inside is all we have , all we depend on .	這個想法是 , 在太空船之外 , 宇宙是不可或缺的 , 而內部是我們所擁有的一切 , 我們所仰賴的一切 。
