and we only get the one chance: if we mess up our spaceship , we've got nowhere else to go .	我們只有一次機會:如果我們搞砸我們的太空船 , 我們沒有其他地方可以去 。
now , the second thing that everyone already knows is that contrary to what was believed for most of human history , human beings are not , in fact , the hub of existence .	第二件事 , 大家都已經知道 , 與大多數人類歷史上所相信的相反 , 事實上 , 人類並不是存在的中心 。
as stephen hawking famously said , we're just a chemical scum on the surface of a typical planet that's in orbit around a typical star , which is on the outskirts of a typical galaxy , and so on .	如stephenhawking所說 , 我們只是一個典型的星球表面的化學污垢 , 圍繞著一個典型的恆星軌道 , 位在典型銀河系的外側 , 以此類推 。
now the first of those two things that everyone knows is kind of saying that we're at a very untypical place , uniquely suited and so on , and the second one is saying that we're at a typical place .	大家都知道這兩件事的第一點 , 有點像是在說我們處在一個非常不典型的地方 , 獨一無二的適合性等等 , 第二個是說我們處在一個典型的地方 。
and especially if you regard these two as deep truths to live by and to inform your life decisions , then they seem a little bit to conflict with each other .	特別是 , 如果你把這兩者看成是深刻的真理 , 來了解你的人生決策 , 那麼 , 他們似乎會和彼此有些衝突 。
but that doesn't prevent them from both being completely false .	但這並不能阻止他們完全虛假 。
and they are . so let me start with the second one: typical . well is this a typical place ? well , let's look around , you know , and look in a random direction , and we see a wall , and chemical scum and that's not typical of the universe at all .	它們是 。 所以 , 讓我從第二個開始:這是一個典型的地方嗎 ? 嗯 , 讓我們看看周圍 , 看看一個隨機方向 , 我們看到一面牆 , 化學污垢 , 而這完全不是典型的宇宙 。
all you've got to do is go a few hundred miles in that same direction and look back , and you won't see any walls or chemical scum at all all you see is a blue planet . and if you go further than that , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .	你只需要朝同一個方向走幾百英里 , 再往回看 , 你不會看到任何牆壁或化學污垢--你只能看到一個藍色的星球 。 如果你走得更遠 , 你會看到太陽、太陽系、星星等等 。
but that's still not typical of the universe , because stars come in galaxies .	但那仍然不算典型的宇宙 , 因為恆星在星系中出現 。
and most places in the universe , a typical place in the universe , is nowhere near any galaxies .	宇宙中的大部分地方 , 宇宙中一個典型的地方 , 沒有任何靠近星系的地方 。
so let's go out further , till we're outside the galaxy , and look back , and yeah , there's the huge galaxy with spiral arms laid out in front of us .	所以 , 讓我們再進一步 , 直到我們在銀河之外 , 再回頭看 , 是的 , 有著螺旋手臂的巨大星系 , 擺在我們面前 。
and at this point we've come 100 , 000 light years from here .	此時 , 我們已經從這裡過了十萬光年 。
but we're still nowhere near a typical place in the universe .	但在宇宙中 , 我們仍然沒有接近典型的地方 。
to get to a typical place , you've got to go 1 , 000 times as far as that into intergalactic space .	要到達一個典型的地方 , 你必須走上一千倍的距離 , 進入星系間空間 。
and so what does that look like ? typical .	那看起來是什麼樣子 ? 典型的 。
what does a typical place in the universe look like ?	宇宙中典型的地方是什麼樣子 ?
well , at enormous expense , ted has arranged a highresolution immersion virtual reality rendering of intergalactic space the view from intergalactic space .	嗯 , 在巨大的花費上 , ted已經安排了一個高解析度的虛擬實境 , 從星系間空間來看 。
so can we have the lights off , please , so we can see it ?	所以 , 我們可以把燈關掉嗎 ? 拜託 , 我們能看到嗎 ?
well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	其實 , 不太完美 , 你看 , 在星系間空間是完全漆黑的 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	它是如此的黑暗 , 如果你正看著最近的恆星對你來說 , 那顆恆星就是要爆炸成為超新星 , 而你正要直盯著它 , 當它的光線到達你時 , 你仍然無法看到即使是一顆小點 。
that's how big and how dark the universe is .	這就是宇宙有多大、多黑暗 。
and that's despite the fact that a supernova is so bright , so brilliant an event , that it would kill you stone dead at a range of several light years .	儘管超新星是如此的明亮 , 如此傑出 , 它會在數光年之內殺死你石頭 。
and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	但從星系間的空間來看 , 它是如此遙遠 , 你甚至不會看到它 。
it's also very cold out there less than three degrees above absolute zero .	外面也很冷 , 低於絕對零度的三度 。
and it's very empty . the vacuum there is one million times less dense than the highest vacuum that our best technology on earth can currently create . so that's how different a typical place is from this place .	它是非常空的 。 真空的密度比地球上最好的科技能創造出的最高密度還要少一百萬倍 。 所以這就是一般的地方有多大的不同 。
and that is how untypical this place is .	那就是這個地方是如此的不典型 。
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	請把燈打回來嗎 ? 謝謝 。
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	我們怎麼知道一個離我們這麼遠的環境 , 又這麼不同 , 所以外星人 , 從我們習慣的任何東西都可以知道 ?
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	嗯 , 地球--我們的環境 , 以我們的形式 , 正在創造知識 。
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	嗯 , 這是什麼意思呢 ? 嗯 , 再進一步看看比我們剛才的--我是說 , 用望遠鏡--你會看到看起來像星星的東西 。
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	它們叫做 「 quasars 」 。 quasars原本的意思是 「 量子星體 」 。
which means things that look a bit like stars . but they're not stars .	也就是說 , 有些東西看起來有點像恆星 。 但它們不是恆星 。
and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	我們知道它們是什麼 。 幾十億年前 , 幾十億光年之外 , 銀河系中心的物質崩塌到一個超大質量黑洞 。
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	然後強烈的磁場引導了重力崩塌的一些能量 。 其中一些物質 , 回到了巨大的噴射流束形式 , 照亮了額外的葉子 , 我覺得它是一兆個太陽 。
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	現在 , 人類大腦的物理學幾乎不像這樣一個噴射流的物理 。
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們無法立刻生存下去 。 語言分崩離析 , 試圖描述這些噴射流中會是什麼樣子 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	會有點像經歷超新星爆炸 , 但在超級新星爆炸時 , 以及一次數百萬年 。
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	然而 , 那噴射機發生的確切地 , 幾十億年後 , 在宇宙的另一端 , 一些化學污垢可以準確地描述 , 模型 , 預測 , 並且解釋 , 最重要的是 , 在現實中 , 這裡發生了什麼事 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	一個物理系統 , 大腦 , 包含一個準確的工作模型 , 另外一個是quasar 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	不僅僅是它的超級形象 , 雖然它也包含它 , 還包含了解釋性模型 , 體現了相同的數學關係和相同的因果結構 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	這是知識 。 如果這還不夠驚人的話 , 一個結構的忠實度就跟時間增加一樣 。 這就是知識的增長 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	所以 , 物理定律有這種特殊特性 。
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	實體的物體 , 盡可能不像彼此 , 卻無法體現相同的數學和因果結構 , 隨著時間的推移 , 越來越多 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	所以 , 我們是一個不一樣的化學污垢 。 這個化學污垢有普遍性 。
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它的結構包含了不斷增加的精確度 , 萬物的結構 。 這個地方 , 而不是宇宙中的其他地方 , 包含了整個物理世界的結構和因果本質 。 所以 , 遠離了不可忽略的物理定律 , 甚至是指定這現象 , 是物理學界最重要的事情之一 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	現在 , 太陽系和我們的環境 , 以我們所擁有的這個與宇宙其他地方的特殊關係為何 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	史蒂芬•霍金的論點是真的 , 但它是錯的 , 強調它的確是錯的 。 有一點是事實是 , 它不會用任何特殊的物理學來做這件事 。 沒有特殊的缺陷 , 沒有奇蹟發生 。 它只是用我們這裡有三樣東西來做這件事 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中一個是物質 , 因為知識的增長是一種信息處理的形式 。 信息處理是計算 , 計算需要電腦--沒有任何已知的方法可以製造出沒有物質的電腦 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們也需要能源來製造電腦 , 最重要的是要讓媒體能夠有效地傳播我們所發現的知識 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	第三點 , 比較不有形 , 但對於開放的創造知識、解釋 , 也是很重要的 , 是證據 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	現在 , 我們的環境充滿了證據 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	我們剛好在三百年前就開始做測試 , 假設牛頓的地心引力定律 。
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但過去我們所做的證據是落在地球的每平方米上 , 已經有數十億年了 , 之後數十億年 , 也會持續下降 。 其他科學也是如此 。
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	據我們所知 , 發現所有科學中最基本的真理 , 都只是為了我們星球上發生的真理 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們的位置充滿了證據 , 同時也充滿了物質和能量 。
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	在星系間的空間中 , 知識開放的三項前提是最低可能的供應 。
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	就像我說的 , 它是空的 , 很冷 , 外面是暗的 。 還是它 ?
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	事實上 , 這只是另一個狹隘的誤解 。
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	因為想像一個立方體在星系間的空間 , 和我們家一樣大的太陽系 。 現在那個立方體是人類標準非常空的 , 但這仍然意味著它包含了超過百萬噸的物質 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	一百萬噸足以製造出一個自給自足的太空站 , 那裡有一群科學家 , 致力於創造開放的知識流 , 諸如此類 。
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	現在 , 它已經超越了現有科技 , 甚至從星系間空間中收集氫氣 , 再組成其他元素等等 。
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但 , 重點是 , 在一個全面的宇宙中 , 如果有某樣東西不被物理定律禁止 , 那麼 , 有什麼可能可以阻止我們去做 , 除非知道如何去做 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換句話說 , 這是關於知識的問題 , 而不是資源 。
and the same well , if we could do that we'd automatically have an energy supply , because the transmutation would be a fusion reactor and evidence ?	同樣的 , 如果我們能做到 , 我們會自動產生能源供應 , 因為變異會是核融合反應爐和證據 ?
well , again , it's dark out there to human senses . but all you've got to do is take a telescope , even one of presentday design , look out and you'll see the same galaxies as we do from here .	嗯 , 同樣的 , 它也是人類感官的黑暗 。 但你只需要拿一個望遠鏡 , 即使是現在的設計 , 向外看 , 你會看到和我們從這裡看到的一樣的星系 。
and with a more powerful telescope , you'll be able to see stars , and planets .	有了更強大的望遠鏡 , 你將能夠看見恆星 , 行星 。
in those galaxies , you'll be able to do astrophysics , and learn the laws of physics .	在那些星系中 , 你將能夠做天體物理學 , 並學習物理定律 。
and locally there you could build particle accelerators , and learn elementary particle physics , and chemistry , and so on .	在那裡你可以建造粒子加速器 , 學習基本粒子物理、化學等等 。
probably the hardest science to do would be biology field trips because it would take several hundred million years to get to the nearest lifebearing planet and back .	最困難的科學可能是生物學領域的旅行 , 因為要花上好幾億年才能到達最近的生命維持星球 。
but i have to tell you and sorry , richard but i never did like biology field trips much , and i think we can just about make do with one every few hundred million years .	但是我必須告訴你--對不起 , 理查--但是我從來不喜歡生物學領域的旅行我認為我們可以每隔幾億年就做一次
so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	所以事實上 , 星系間空間的確包含了所有開放的知識創造的先決條件 。 任何這種立方體 , 在宇宙的任何一個角落 , 都可以變成和我們一樣的樞紐 , 只要我們知道該怎麼做的話 。
so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .	所以 , 我們並不是處在一個獨特的安寧之地 。
if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended stream of explanations , then so is almost every other environment . so is the earth . so is a polluted earth .	如果星系間空間能夠創造出一串開放的解釋 , 那麼幾乎所有其他的環境都一樣 。 那麼地球是受污染的地球 。
and the limiting factor , there and here , is not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is scarce .	而有限的因素 , 這裡和這裡 , 不是資源 , 因為資源很充足 , 但知識 , 這很稀少 。
now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	以宇宙為基礎的觀點可能和我認為 , 應該要讓我們覺得非常特別 。 但這也應該讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為這意味著 , 若沒有具體的知識需要在宇宙不斷的挑戰中生存 , 我們就無法生存下去 。
all it takes is for a supernova to go off a few light years away , and we'll all be dead !	只需要讓一個超新星在幾光年之外飛行 , 我們就會死了 !
martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all sorts of things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments gone wrong , and most importantly to terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .	馬丁•里斯最近寫了一本關於我們對各種事物的脆弱性的書 , 從天體物理學 , 到科學實驗都出錯了 , 最重要的是對大規模毀滅性武器的恐怖主義 。
and he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .	他認為文明只有50%的機率存活在這個世紀 。
i think he's going to talk about that later in the conference .	我想他稍後會在會議中談到這點 。
now i don't think that probability is the right category to discuss this issue in .	我不認為機率是正確的分類來討論這個議題 。
but i do agree with him about this . we can survive , and we can fail to survive .	但我確實認同他對此的看法 。 我們可以生存下去 , 而且我們無法生存 。
but it depends not on chance , but on whether we create the relevant knowledge in time .	但這不取決於機會 , 而是我們是否及時創造出相關的知識 。
the danger is not at all unprecedented . species go extinct all the time .	危險並不是前所未有的 。 物種無時無刻都絕種 。
civilizations end . the overwhelming majority of all species and all civilizations that have ever existed are now history .	文明終結了 。 絕大多數的物種和所有存在過的文明現在都是歷史了 。
and if we want to be the exception to that , then logically our only hope is to make use of the one feature that distinguishes our species , and our civilization , from all the others namely , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations , new knowledge to be a hub of existence .	如果我們想成為例外 , 那麼 , 邏輯上我們唯一的希望就是利用一個特徵來區分我們的物種 , 以及我們的文明 , 來自其他所有人 , 我們與物理定律的特殊關係 , 我們創造新解釋的能力 , 新知識成為存在的中心 。
so let me now apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to advocate any particular solution , but just to illustrate the kind of thing i mean .	所以 , 現在讓我把這個應用在當前的爭議上 , 不是因為我想倡導任何特定的解決方案 , 只是為了說明我的意思 。
and the controversy is global warming .	而爭議是全球暖化
now , i'm a physicist , but i'm not the right kind of physicist . in regard to global warming , i'm just a layman . and the rational thing for a layman to do is to take seriously the prevailing scientific theory . and according to that theory , it's already too late to avoid a disaster .	現在 , 我是物理學家 , 但我不是正確的物理學家 。 根據全球暖化 , 我只是一個層人 。 而對於層層人來說 , 合理的做法是認真看待普遍的科學理論 。 根據這個理論 , 這理論已經太晚了 , 無法避免災難 。
because if it's true that our best option at the moment is to prevent co2 emissions with something like the kyoto protocol , with its constraints on economic activity and its enormous cost of hundreds of billions of dollars or whatever it is , then that is already a disaster by any reasonable measure .	因為如果我們當下的最佳選擇是防止二氧化碳排放量和京都議定書等因素 , 在經濟活動上有所限制 , 數千億美元之類的巨大成本 , 那就已經是任何合理的措施所造成的災難 。
and the actions that are advocated are not even purported to solve the problem , merely to postpone it by a little . so it's already too late to avoid it , and it probably has been too late to avoid it ever since before anyone realized the danger .	而被倡導的行動 , 根本無法解決問題 , 只需稍微推延一下 。 所以已經太遲了 , 無法避免它 , 可能在任何人意識到危險之前就已經太遲避免它了 。
it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the best available scientific theory was telling us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age in which billions would die .	在1970年代已經太晚了 , 當時最好的科學理論告訴我們工業排放快要降低數十億人死亡的新冰河時期 。
now the lesson of that seems clear to me , and i don't know why it isn't informing public debate .	對我來說 , 這教訓似乎很清楚 , 我不知道為什麼這不是公開辯論 。
it is that we can't always know . when we know of an impending disaster , and how to solve it at a cost less than the cost of the disaster itself , then there's not going to be much argument , really .	就是我們永遠都不能知道 。 當我們知道一個即將發生的災難 , 以及如何用成本低於災難本身的代價 , 那麼就不會有太多爭論了 , 真的 。
but no precautions , and no precautionary principle , can avoid problems that we do not yet foresee .	但沒有預防措施 , 也沒有預防原則 , 可以避免我們尚未預見的問題 。
hence , we need a stance of problemfixing , not just problemavoidance .	因此 , 我們需要修正問題的立場 , 而不只是修正問題 。
and it's true that an ounce of prevention equals a pound of cure , but that's only if we know what to prevent .	的確 , 一盎司的預防等於一磅解藥 , 但只有我們知道要預防什麼 。
if you've been punched on the nose , then the science of medicine does not consist of teaching you how to avoid punches .	如果你在鼻子上被打了一拳 , 那麼醫學的科學並不是由教導你如何避免被拳頭打到的 。
if medical science stopped seeking cures and concentrated on prevention only , then it would achieve very little of either .	如果醫學不再尋求解藥 , 並只專注在預防上 , 那它也幾乎無法達成 。
the world is buzzing at the moment with plans to force reductions in gas emissions at all costs .	目前世界正在興起 , 隨著計劃在氣體排放量的成本上迫使降低 。
it ought to be buzzing with plans to reduce the temperature , and with plans to live at the higher temperature and not at all costs , but efficiently and cheaply . and some such plans exist , things like swarms of mirrors in space to deflect the sunlight away , and encouraging aquatic organisms to eat more carbon dioxide .	它應該會隨著計劃的計劃而調節 , 以降低溫度 , 隨著計劃以更高的溫度生活 , 不計代價 , 而是有效率又便宜 。 有些計劃存在 , 像是太空中的一群鏡子 , 可以將陽光偏轉 , 並鼓勵水生生物多吃二氧化碳 。
at the moment , these things are fringe research .	目前 , 這些東西都是邊緣研究 。
they're not central to the human effort to face this problem , or problems in general .	他們不是人類努力去面對這個問題 , 或一般來說的問題 。
and with problems that we are not aware of yet , the ability to put right not the sheer good luck of avoiding indefinitely is our only hope , not just of solving problems , but of survival .	我們還沒意識到的問題 , 擺出正確的能力 , 不是無限期的好運 , 是我們唯一的希望 , 不只是解決問題 , 而是生存 。
so take two stone tablets , and carve on them .	拿兩個石板 , 然後在上面刻上雕刻 。
on one of them , carve: " problems are soluble . "	其中之一是雕刻: 「 問題是解決不了的 。 」
and on the other one carve: " problems are inevitable . "	而在另一塊雕刻上: 「 問題是不可避免的 。 」
how can a struggling country break out of poverty if it's trapped in a system of bad rules ? economist paul romer unveils a bold idea: " charter cities , " cityscale administrative zones governed by a coalition of nations .	一個掙扎的國家怎麼能瓦解貧窮 , 如果它被困在惡劣規則的體制中 ? 經濟學家保羅羅羅默揭露出一個大膽的想法: 「 特許城市 」 , 城市管理區 , 由一個國家的聯盟所管理 。
business , culture , economics , global issues , politics	商業、文化、經濟、全球議題、政治、
paul romer's radical idea: charter cities	保羅羅羅默的激進想法:特許城市 。
take a look at this picture .	看一下這張照片 。
it poses a very fascinating puzzle for us .	它為我們帶來了一個非常迷人的謎題 。
these african students are doing their homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have any electricity at home .	這些非洲學生在首都機場的路燈下做功課 , 因為他們家裡沒有電 。
now , i haven't met these particular students , but i've met students like them .	我還沒見過這些特別的學生 , 但我見過像他們一樣的學生 。
let's just pick one for example , the one in the green shirt .	咱們來舉個例子 , 綠色襯衫裡的那個 。
let's give him a name , too: nelson .	我們也給他一個名字:尼爾森 。
i'll bet nelson has a cellphone .	我會打賭尼爾森有支手機 。
so here is the puzzle .	謎題是:
why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼尼爾森能夠接觸到尖端科技 , 像是手機 , 但無法接觸到一百歲的科技 , 讓家裡產生電燈 ?
now , in a word , the answer is " rules . "	現在 , 一句話 , 答案是 「 規則 」 。
bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	不好的規則可以預防雙贏的解決方案 , 當人們能把新科技帶進來 , 讓它們能取得像尼爾森這樣的人 。
what kinds of rules ?	什麼樣的規則 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	這個國家的電力公司在一條規則下運作 , 這條規則說 , 它必須以非常低的、補貼的價格來銷售電力 , 事實上 , 一個價格太低 , 它在賣出的每一個單位上都損失了錢 。
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	所以 , 它既沒有資源 , 也沒有獎勵 , 可以接收其他許多用戶 。
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想改變這個規則
he's seen that it's possible to have a different set of rules , rules where businesses earn a small profit , so they have an incentive to sign up more customers .	他看到有不同的規則 , 規則是有可能讓企業賺取小利潤的 , 所以他們有動機去招募更多客戶 。
that's the kind of rules that the cellphone company that nelson purchases his telephony from operates under .	這就是nelson公司所購買的手機的那種規則 , 從底下運轉來 。
the president has seen how those rules worked well .	總統已經看過那些規則是如何運作的 。
so he tried to change the rules for pricing on electricity , but ran into a firestorm of protest from businesses and consumers who wanted to preserve the existing subsidized rates .	所以他試著改變用電定價的規則 , 但卻遇到一場抗議 , 來自企業和消費者的抗議 , 他們想要保存現有的補助率 。
so he was stuck with rules that prevented him from letting the winwin solution help his country .	所以他卡住了一些規則 , 阻止他讓雙贏解決方案幫助他的國家 。
and nelson is stuck studying under the streetlights .	而尼爾森則卡在街燈下研究
the real challenge then , is to try to figure out how we can change rules .	真正的挑戰是試著找出我們如何改變規則 。
are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	我們是否有一些規則可以用來改變規則 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我認為 , 有一個一般性的抽象洞見 , 可以讓我們實行 , 那就是 , 如果我們能給人們更多選擇 , 且對於許多國家的領導者 , 更多的選擇 , 也是人 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但 , 呈現這兩者之間的對立是很有用的 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為你可能想給某位領袖的那種選擇 , 像是給總統在電力上提高價格的選擇 , 奪走了經濟中人民想要的選擇 。
they want the choice to be able to continue consuming subsidized electric power .	他們希望這個選擇能夠繼續消耗補貼的電力 。
so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	所以如果你只給一邊或另一邊 , 你就會有張力或摩擦力 。
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們能找到給予兩者更多選擇的方法 , 那會給我們一套改變規則的規則 , 讓我們脫離陷阱 。
now , nelson also has access to the internet .	現在 , 尼爾森也能取得網路 。
and he says that if you want to see the damaging effects of rules , the ways that rules can keep people in the dark , look at the pictures from nasa of the earth at night .	他說 , 如果你想看到規則的破壞效應 , 規則能讓人們留在黑暗中 , 看看美國太空總署在夜間的照片 。
in particular check out asia .	特別檢查亞洲
if you zoom in here , you can see north korea , in outline here , which is like a black hole compared to its neighbors .	如果你放大這裡 , 你可以看到北韓 , 這裡的排名就像是黑洞 , 相較於它的鄰居 。
now , you won't be surprised to learn that the rules in north korea keep people there in the dark .	現在 , 你不會驚訝地發現 , 北韓的規則讓人們留在黑暗中 。
but it is important to recognize that north korea and south korea started out with identical sets of rules in both the sense of laws and regulations , but also in the deeper senses of understandings , norms , culture , values and beliefs .	但 , 很重要的是 , 北韓和南韓一開始有一套規則 , 包括法律和法規 , 也有更深層次的了解、規範、文化、價值觀和信念 。
when they separated , they made choices that led to very divergent paths for their sets of rules .	當他們分離時 , 他們做了選擇 , 導致非常多樣化的路徑成為他們一組的規則 。
so we can change we as humans can change the rules that we use to interact with each other , for better , or for worse .	所以 , 我們可以改變我們人類可以改變我們用來和彼此互動的規則 , 更好 , 或更糟 。
now let's look at another region , the caribbean .	現在我們來看另一個區域 , 加勒比海
zoom in on haiti , in outline here .	放大海地這裡
haiti is also dark , compared to its neighbor here , the dominican republic , which has about the same number of residents .	海地也是黑暗的 , 相較於這裡的鄰居 , 多明尼加共和國 , 它的居民數量差不多 。
both of these countries are dark compared to puerto rico , which has half as many residents as either haiti or the dominican republic .	這兩個國家都是黑暗的 , 相較於波多黎各 , 海地或多明尼加共和國有一半的居民 。
what haiti warns us is that rules can be bad because governments are weak .	海地警告我們的是 , 規則可能會是不好的 , 因為政府很弱 。
it's not just that the rules are bad because the government is too strong and oppressive , as in north korea .	不只是規則不好 , 因為政府太強壯和壓迫 , 就像在北韓 。
so that if we want to create environments with good rules , we can't just tear down .	所以如果我們想要創造出有良好規則的環境 , 我們不能就這樣撕下來 。
we've got to find ways to build up , as well .	我們也得找方法來建設 。
now , china dramatically demonstrates both the potential and the challenges of working with rules .	現在 , 中國大大地展示了與規則合作的潛力和挑戰 。
back in the beginning of the data presented in this chart , china was the world's hightechnology leader .	回到資料的一開始 , 在這張圖表中 , 中國是世界上的高科技領導者 。
chinese had pioneered technologies like steel , printing , gunpowder .	中國有先驅性科技 , 像是鋼、印刷、槍枝等 。
but the chinese never adopted , at least in that period , effective rules for encouraging the spread of those ideas a profit motive that could have encouraged the spread .	但中國從未採用 , 至少在那個時期 , 有效的規則來鼓勵那些想法的散播 , 一個能夠獲利的動機 , 可以鼓勵傳播 。
and they soon adopted rules which slowed down innovation and cut china off from the rest of the world .	他們很快就採用了一些規則 , 讓創新慢下來 , 把中國從世界其他地方切下來 。
so as other countries in the world innovated , in the sense both of developing newer technologies , but also developing newer rules , the chinese were cut off from those advances .	所以 , 隨著世界其他國家的創新 , 在發展新科技的同時 , 中國也發展出更新的規則 , 中國的發展也因此被那些進步而切斷 。
income there stayed stagnant , as it zoomed ahead in the rest of the world .	在那裡的收入停滯不前 , 隨著它在世界其他地方縮小 。
this next chart looks at more recent data .	下一張圖表則是比較近期的數據 。
it plots income , average income in china as a percentage of average income in the united states .	它策劃了中國的平均收入佔美國平均收入的百分比 。
in the '50s and '60s you can see that it was hovering at about three percent .	在50年代和60年代 , 你可以看到大約是3%左右 。
but then in the late '70s something changed .	但在70年代後期 , 發生了一些改變 。
growth took off in china . the chinese started catching up very quickly with the united states .	中國的成長起飛了 。 中國人很快就趕上了美國 。
if you go back to the map at night , you can get a clue to the process that lead to the dramatic change in rules in china .	如果你晚上回到地圖上 , 就能得到一個線索 , 來引領中國規則的戲劇性改變 。
the brightest spot in china , which you can see on the edge of the outline here , is hong kong .	中國最明亮的地方 , 你可以看到在線的邊緣 , 就是香港 。
hong kong was a small bit of china that , for most of the 20th century , operated under a very different set of rules than the rest of mainland china rules that were copied from working market economies of the time , and administered by the british .	香港是中國的一小部分 , 在20世紀大部分的時候 , 在中國的一套非常不同的規則下運作 , 比起當時的勞動市場經濟 , 英國的其他部分都還不一樣 。
in the 1950s , hong kong was a place where millions of people could go , from the mainland , to start in jobs like sewing shirts , making toys .	在1950年代 , 香港是一個有數百萬人可以去的地方 , 從大陸開始 , 從縫紉衣服、製作玩具開始 。
but , to get on a process of increasing income , increasing skills led to very rapid growth there .	但 , 為了增加收入的過程 , 越來越多的技能 , 導致那裡的成長非常快速 。
hong kong was also the model which leaders like deng xiaoping could copy , when they decided to move all of the mainland towards the market model .	香港也是領導人像鄧小平可以複製的模式當他們決定將整個大陸都移到市場模式上
but deng xiaoping instinctively understood the importance of offering choices to his people .	但鄧小平直覺地了解為他的人民提供選擇的重要性 。
so instead of forcing everyone in china to shift immediately to the market model , they proceeded by creating some special zones that could do , in a sense , what britain did: make the opportunity to go work with the market rules available to the people who wanted to opt in there .	所以 , 與其強迫中國的每個人立刻轉移到市場模式 , 他們採取的方式是創造一些特別的區塊 , 在某種意義上 , 英國能做的是:讓有機會和市場規則合作 , 讓想要在裡面採取行動的人能有機會 。
so they created four special economic zones around hong kong: zones where chinese could come and work , and cities grew up very rapidly there ; also zones where foreign firms could come in and make things .	所以他們在香港附近創建了四個特別的經濟區域 , 那裡的中國可以來上班的地區 , 都市成長得很快 ; 還有外國企業可以進來製造東西的地區 。
one of the zones next to hong kong has a city called shenzhen .	香港旁邊的一個區域有一個城市叫做深圳
in that city there is a taiwanese firm that made the iphone that many of you have , and they made it with labor from chinese who moved there to shenzhen .	在那城市 , 有一家台灣公司 , 製作了你們當中許多人的iphone , 他們和中國人的勞工合作 , 他們搬到深圳那邊 。
so after the four special zones , there were 14 coastal cites that were open in the same sense , and eventually demonstrated successes in these places that people could opt in to , that they flocked to because of the advantages they offered .	在四個特區之後 , 有14個海岸群體在相同的意義上開放 , 最終在這些地方展現出成功 , 人們可以選擇 , 因為他們提供的優勢而被擺到一邊去 。
demonstrated successes there led to a consensus for a move toward the market model for the entire economy .	證明成功 , 導致整個經濟體向市場模式邁進的共識 。
now the chinese example shows us several points .	現在中國的例子顯示了好幾點
one is: preserve choices for people .	其一是:為人們保存選擇 。
two: operate on the right scale .	二:在正確的尺度上操作 。
if you try to change the rules in a village , you could do that , but a village would be too small to get the kinds of benefits you can get if you have millions of people all working under good rules .	如果你試著改變村子裡的規則 , 你可以這麼做 , 但村落會太小 , 無法取得你能得到的好處 , 如果你有數百萬人都在好的規則下工作 。
on the other hand , the nation is too big .	另一方面 , 國家太大了 。
if you try to change the rules in the nation , you can't give some people a chance to hold back , see how things turn out , and let others zoom ahead and try the new rules .	如果你試著改變國家的規則 , 你不能給一些人一個機會 , 讓一些人拿回來 , 看事情會怎麼樣 , 讓其他人放大 , 試試新規則 。
but cities give you this opportunity to create new places , with new rules that people can opt in to .	但 , 城市能給你這個機會 , 來創造新地方 , 用人們可以選擇的新規則 。
and they're large enough to get all of the benefits that we can have when millions of us work together under good rules .	它們夠大 , 足以獲得所有利益 , 當數百萬人在良好的規則下一起工作時 , 就能得到所有利益 。
so the proposal is that we conceive of something called a charter city .	所以 , 提議是 , 我們構想出所謂的特許城市 。
we start with a charter that specifies all the rules required to attract the people who we'll need to build the city .	我們從一個明確規則開始 , 來吸引我們需要建造城市的人 。
we'll need to attract the investors who will build out the infrastructure the power system , the roads , the port , the airport , the buildings .	我們會需要吸引投資者 , 他們會建立基礎建設 , 電力系統、道路、港口、機場、建築 。
you'll need to attract firms , who will come hire the people who move there first .	你會需要吸引公司 , 他們會先僱用那些先搬過來的人 。
and you'll need to attract families , the residents who will come and live there permanently , raise their children , get an education for their children , and get their first job .	然後你會需要吸引家庭 , 那些將來會永久住在那裡的居民 , 養育他們的孩子 , 為他們的孩子接受教育 , 得到他們的第一份工作 。
with that charter , people will move there .	有了那個憲章 , 人們就會搬到那裡 。
the city can be built .	城市可以建設
and we can scale this model .	而我們可以擴大這個模型 。
we can go do it over and over again .	我們可以一而再、再而三地
to make it work , we need good rules . we've already discussed that .	要讓它運作 , 我們需要好的規則 。 我們已經討論過了 。
those are captured in the charter .	那些在憲章中捕捉到的
we also need the choices for people .	我們也需要人們的選擇 。
that's really built into the model if we allow for the possibility of building cities on uninhabited land .	這真的是建構在這個模型中 , 如果我們能夠在無人居住的土地上建造城市的可能性 。
you start from uninhabited territory .	你從無人居住的領土著手 。
people can come live under the new charter , but no one is forced to live under it .	人們可以在新的章節下生活 , 但沒有人被迫住在下面 。
the final thing we need are choices for leaders .	最後我們需要的是對領導者的選擇 。
and , to achieve the kind of choices we want for leaders we need to allow for the potential for partnerships between nations: cases where nations work together , in effect , de facto , the way china and britain worked together to build , first a little enclave of the market model , and then scale it throughout china .	而且 , 為了達成我們想要領導者的那種選擇 , 我們需要容許國與國之間的合作潛力:國家合作的案例 , 實際上 , 事實是 , 中國和英國的合作方式 , 首先是一項市場模式的大規模競爭 , 然後擴大到整個中國 。
in a sense , britain , inadvertently , through its actions in hong kong , did more to reduce world poverty than all the aid programs that we've undertaken in the last century .	在某種意義上 , 英國 , 無意中 , 透過香港的行動 , 減少了世界貧窮 , 比上個世紀所有的援助計畫都還要多 。
so if we allow for these kind of partnerships to replicate this again , we can get those kinds of benefits scaled throughout the world .	所以如果我們允許這類夥伴合作再次複製這一點 , 我們就能得到那些在世界各地擴展的益處 。
in some cases this will involve a delegation of responsibility , a delegation of control from one country to another to take over certain kinds of administrative responsibilities .	在某些情況下 , 這會涉及到一種責任 , 一種控制權從一個國家傳到另一個國家 , 來掌控某些特定的行政責任 。
now , when i say that , some of you are starting to think , " well , is this just bringing back colonialism ? "	現在 , 當我這麼說時 , 你們有些人開始想: 「 嗯 , 這只是帶回殖民主義嗎 ? 」
it's not . but it's important to recognize that the kind of emotions that come up when we start to think about these things , can get in the way , can make us pull back , can shut down our ability , and our interest in trying to explore new ideas .	並非如此 。 但重要的是要意識到當我們開始思考這些事情時 , 所產生的那種情緒 , 可以走路 , 可以讓我們退後 , 可以關閉我們的能力 , 以及我們對於探索新想法的興趣 。
why is this not like colonialism ?	為什麼這不像殖民主義 ?
the thing that was bad about colonialism , and the thing which is residually bad in some of our aid programs , is that it involved elements of coercion and condescension .	殖民主義不好的地方在於 , 有些援助計畫不好的地方在於它涉及了強制和審解的元素 。
this model is all about choices , both for leaders and for the people who will live in these new places .	這個模式是關於選擇 , 無論是對領導者 , 還是對將來會住在這些新地方的人 。
and , choice is the antidote to coercion and condescension .	而且 , 選擇是強迫和欺騙的解藥 。
so let's talk about how this could play out in practice .	咱們來談談它如何能實踐 。
let's take a particular leader , raul castro , who is the leader of cuba .	讓我們來看看特定的領導人 , 拉爾•卡斯楚 , 他是古巴的領袖 。
it must have occurred to castro that he has the chance to do for cuba what deng xiaoping did for china , but he doesn't have a hong kong there on the island in cuba .	卡斯楚認為他有機會為古巴做些什麼 , 像鄧小平為中國做的那樣 , 但他沒有在古巴島上的香港 。
he does , though , have a little bit of light down in the south that has a very special status .	不過 , 他的確在南方有一點點亮 , 那裡有很特別的地位 。
there is a zone there , around guantanamo bay , where a treaty gives the united states administrative responsibility for a piece of land that's about twice the size of manhattan .	在關塔那摩灣附近有一個地區 , 一個條約讓美國負責一塊土地 , 大約是曼哈頓的兩倍大 。
castro goes to the prime minister of canada and says , " look , the yankees have a terrible pr problem .	卡斯楚前往加拿大總理說: 「 看 , 雅克斯有很糟糕的公關問題 。
they want to get out .	他們想出去 。
why don't you , canada , take over ?	為什麼你不 , 加拿大 , 接手 ?
build run a special administrative zone .	建造一個特別的行政區
allow a new city to be built up there .	允許一個新的城市在上面建設
allow many people to come in .	允許許多多人進來
let us have a hong kong nearby .	讓我們在附近有一個香港
some of my citizens will move into that city as well .	我的一些市民也會搬進那個城市 。
others will hold back . but this will be the gateway that will connect the modern economy and the modern world to my country . "	其他人會回頭 。 但這將會是將現代經濟和現代世界連結到我的國家的大門 。 」
now , where else might this model be tried ?	現在 , 這個模型還能在哪裡被試驗 ?
well , africa . i've talked with leaders in africa .	嗯 , 非洲 。 我和非洲的領導人談過 。
many of them totally get the notion of a special zone that people can opt into as a rule .	當中有許多人完全得到一個特殊區塊的概念 , 讓人們可以選擇成為一個規則 。
it's a rule for changing rules .	是改變規則的規則 。
it's a way to create new rules , and let people optin without coercion , and the opposition that coercion can force .	這是一種創造新規則的方法 , 讓人們在沒有強制的情況下選擇 , 而強制的反對者可以強迫他人 。
they also totally get the idea that in some instances they can make more credible promises to longterm investors the kind of investors who will come build the port , build the roads , in a new city they can make more credible promises if they do it along with a partner nation .	他們也完全了解到 , 在某些情況下 , 他們可以對長期投資者做出更有信心的承諾 , 那種投資者 , 會來建造港口、建造道路 , 在新城市中 , 他們可以做出更有信心的承諾 , 如果他們和另一半國家合作的話 。
perhaps even in some arrangement that's a little bit like an escrow account , where you put land in the escrow account and the partner nation takes responsibility for it .	或許甚至在一些安排有點像escrow帳戶 , 把土地放在escrow帳戶裡 , 伴侶國家也要負起責任 。
there is also lots of land in africa where new cities could be built .	非洲也有許多的土地 , 那裡有新的城市可以建造 。
this is a picture i took when i was flying along the coast .	這是我在沿著海岸飛行時拍的照片 。
there are immense stretches of land like this land where hundreds of millions of people could live .	像這片土地有巨大的延伸 , 數億人可以居住 。
now , if we generalize this and think about not just one or two charter cites , but dozens cities that will help create places for the many hundreds of millions , perhaps billions of people who will move to cities in the coming century is there enough land for them ?	現在 , 如果我們歸納這一點 , 並考慮一下 , 不只是一、二個特許群 , 而是數十個城市 , 能夠為數億人創造地方 , 也許數十億人在未來的世紀會移居到城市 , 為他們帶來足夠的土地嗎 ?
well , throughout the world , if we look at the lights at night , the one thing that's misleading is that , visually , it looks like most of the world is already built out .	嗯 , 在整個世界 , 如果我們晚上看燈光 , 其中一個誤導的是 , 視覺上看來 , 世界上大部分已經建造出來了 。
so let me show you why that's wrong .	所以 , 讓我來說明為什麼這是錯的 。
take this representation of all of the land .	以這片土地為例 。
turn it into a square that stands for all the arable land on earth .	把它變成一個可以代表地球上所有可耕地的正方形 。
and let these dots represent the land that's already taken up by the cities that three billion people now live in .	讓這些點代表已經被三十億人口居住的城市佔據的土地 。
if you move the dots down to the bottom of the rectangle you can see that the cities for the existing three billion urban residents take up only three percent of the arable land on earth .	如果你把點往下移到長方形的底部 , 你可以看到 , 現存的30億城市居民只佔地球上3%的可耕地 。
so if we wanted to build cities for another billion people , they would be dots like this .	所以如果我們想為另外十億人建造城市 , 他們會是這樣的點 。
we'd go from three percent of the arable land , to four percent .	我們會從百分之三的可耕地變成百分之四
we'd dramatically reduce the human footprint on earth by building more cities that people can move to .	我們會大大減少地球上的人類足跡 , 做法是建造更多可以移動的城市 。
and if these are cities governed by good rules , they can be cities where people are safe from crime , safe from disease and bad sanitation , where people have a chance to get a job .	如果這些城市是由良好的規則來管理 , 他們可以是城市 , 人們可以安全地避免犯罪、疾病和不良衛生設施 , 在那裡 , 人們有機會得到工作 。
they can get basic utilities like electricity .	他們可以取得像電力這種基本的公用事業
their kids can get an education .	他們的孩子可以接受教育
so what will it take to get started building the first charter cities , scaling this so we build many more ?	所以 , 要開始建造第一座特許城市 , 要怎麼做才能建造出更多 ?
it would help to have a manual .	能有一本手冊是有幫助的
what university professors could do is write some details that might go into this manual .	大學教授能做的是寫一些細節 , 可能會進入這本手冊 。
you wouldn't want to let us run the cities , go out and design them .	你不會想讓我們經營城市 , 走出去設計它們 。
you wouldn't let academics out in the wild .	你不會讓學者在野外
but , you could set us to work thinking about questions like , suppose it isn't just canada that does the deal with raul castro .	但 , 你可以讓我們開始思考像這樣的問題 , 假設它不只是加拿大用來處理拉爾卡斯楚的問題 。
perhaps brazil comes in as a participant , and spain as well . and perhaps cuba wants to be one of the partners in a fourway joint venture .	或許巴西是參與者 , 西班牙也一樣 。 古巴也想成為四方面關節的夥伴之一 。
how would we write the treaty to do that ?	我們要怎麼寫條約才能做到 ?
there is less precedent for that , but that could easily be worked out .	比較少先例 , 但那很容易解決 。
how would we finance this ?	我們要如何資助這個 ?
turns out singapore and hong kong are cities that made huge gains on the value of the land that they owned when they got started .	新加坡和香港是新加坡的城市 , 都市的價值觀大大提升了他們一開始所擁有的土地 。
you could use the gains on the value of the land to pay for things like the police , the courts , but the school system and the health care system too , which make this a more attractive place to live , makes this a place where people have higher incomes which , incidentally , makes the land more valuable .	你可以利用土地的價值 , 來支付警察、法庭 , 但學校和健康照護體制 , 這讓土地更有吸引力 , 讓土地的收入更高 , 順便一提 , 讓土地更有價值 。
so the incentives for the people helping to construct this zone and build it , and set up the basic rules , go very much in the right direction .	所以 , 為協助建構這區的人提供獎勵 , 並建立基礎規則 , 非常朝正確的方向前進 。
so there are many other details like this .	所以還有許多其他像這樣的細節 。
how could we have buildings that are low cost and affordable for people who work in a first job , assembling something like an iphone , but make those buildings energy efficient , and make sure that they are safe , so they don't fall down in an earthquake or a hurricane .	我們如何能有低成本且負擔得起的建築物 , 對第一份工作的人來說 , 組裝類似iphone的東西 , 但讓那些建築物節能 , 並確保它們是安全的 , 所以它們不會在地震或颶風中落下 。
many technical details to be worked out , but those of us who are already starting to pursue these things can already tell that there is no roadblock , there's no impediment , other than a failure of imagination , that will keep us from delivering on a truly global winwin solution .	許多技術上的細節要想辦法解決 , 但那些已經開始追求這些事情的人 , 已經可以知道 , 沒有路障 , 沒有任何障礙 , 除了失敗的想像力之外 , 還會讓我們無法提供真正的全球雙贏解決方案 。
let me conclude with this picture .	讓我用這張照片做個總結 。
the reason we can be so well off , even though there is so many people on earth , is because of the power of ideas .	我們之所以能做到這麼好 , 儘管地球上有這麼多人 , 是因為想法的力量 。
we can share ideas with other people , and when they discover them , they share with us .	我們可以和其他人分享想法 , 當他們發現它們時 , 他們會和我們分享 。
it's not like scarce objects , where sharing means we each get less .	這不像稀有物品 , 共享意謂著我們每人都得到較少 。
when we share ideas we all get more .	當我們分享想法時 , 我們都會得到更多 。
when we think about ideas in that way , we usually think about technologies .	當我們以那種方式思考想法時 , 我們通常會想到科技 。
but there is another class of ideas: the rules that govern how we interact with each other ; rules like , let's have a tax system that supports a research university that gives away certain kinds of knowledge for free .	但還有另外一類想法:規則是主導我們如何彼此互動的規則 ; 規則如 , 讓我們有一套支援研究大學的稅制 , 免費提供某些知識 。
let's have a system where we have ownership of land that is registered in a government office , that people can pledge as collateral .	咱們來設立一個系統 , 讓土地擁有在政府辦公室註冊的土地 , 人民可以以同事的身份出席 。
if we can keep innovating on our space of rules , and particularly innovate in the sense of coming up with rules for changing rules , so we don't get stuck with bad rules , then we can keep moving progress forward and truly make the world a better place , so that people like nelson and his friends don't have to study any longer under the streetlights . thank you .	如果我們能繼續在規則的空間上創新 , 尤其是創新 , 想出改變規則的規則 , 所以我們不會被不好的規則所困住 , 那麼我們就能繼續前進 , 真正讓世界變得更好 , 讓像尼爾森和他的朋友不用再在路燈下研究任何事 。 謝謝 。
genomics pioneer craig venter takes a break from his epic roundtheworld expedition to talk about the millions of genes his team has discovered so far in its quest to map the ocean’s biodiversity .	基因組學先驅克萊格•凡特從他的史詩般的巡迴探險中休息 , 來探究他的團隊目前數百萬個基因 , 來繪製海洋的生物多樣性 。
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna、生物圈、生物科技、企業家、遺傳學、發明、海洋、科學、科技、科技 。
craig venter on dna and the sea	克萊格•凡特在dna和海上
at the break , i was asked by several people about my comments about the aging debate .	休息時 , 我被幾個人問到我對老化辯論的評論 。
and this will be my only comment on it .	而這將會是我唯一的評論 。
and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	那就是 , 我了解樂觀主義者大幅超越了悲觀主義者 。
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	我18分鐘內要告訴各位的是我們如何從閱讀基因密碼轉換到開始自己寫程式的第一階段 。
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	僅僅在十年前 , 這個月 , 我們發表了第一組免費的有機體 , 也就是流感流行病 。
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	這項計畫從13年下降到4個月 ,
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	我們現在可以在2到8小時內完成同樣的基因組計畫 。
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	所以在過去的十年裡 , 大量的基因組被加入了:大部分的人類病原體、幾株植物、幾種昆蟲和幾種哺乳類 , 包括人類基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	十年前 , 基因組學在這個階段的思考模式是 , 到今年年底 , 我們可能有三到五組基因組定序 ; 數百組定序 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	我們剛從戈登和貝蒂•摩爾基金會得到一份補助 , 今年要完成130組基因組 , 作為環保生物的副程式 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	所以 , 閱讀基因密碼的速率已經改變了 。
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但當我們看 , 外面的東西 , 我們幾乎無法在地球上取得的物體上刮下表面 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大部分人沒有意識到它 , 因為它們是看不見的 , 但微生物組成了地球一半的生物量 , 而所有動物只佔所有生物總量的1/1 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	也許是牛津人不常做的事 , 但如果你曾經到海邊去 , 吞下一口海水 , 請記住每一毫升都有大約一百萬個細菌 , 以及一千萬個病毒的數量 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	兩年前 , 微生物種類不到五千種 , 所以我們決定做點什麼 。
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	我們開始了 「 不足類 」 探險 , 我們在那裡 , 和偉大的海洋探險隊合作 , 每200英里 , 嘗試採集海洋樣本 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們從百慕達開始做我們的測試計畫 , 接著搬到哈利法克斯 , 沿著美國東岸 , 加勒比海 , 巴拿馬運河 , 穿過加拉巴哥群島 , 接著橫越太平洋 , 我們正在穿越印度洋的途中工作 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	非常艱難的職責 ; 我們在帆船上做這件事 , 有部分是要協助讓年輕人興奮地進入科學領域 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	實驗極其簡單 ,
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	我們只用海水過濾它 , 用不同的濾鏡收集不同大小的生物體 , 然後把它們的dna帶回我們在洛克維爾的實驗室 , 在那裡我們可以每24小時完成一億個基因密碼的測序 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	藉此 , 我們做出了一些驚人的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	例如 , 有人認為我們眼中的視覺色素在環境中只有一兩種有機體有相同的色素 。
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果發現 , 幾乎每個在溫暖地區海洋上層的物種都有這些相同的光感接收器 , 利用陽光作為它們能量和溝通的源頭 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	從一個地點 , 從一桶海水中 , 我們發現了一百三十萬種新基因 , 和五萬種新物種一樣多 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	我們已經將此延伸到空氣中 , 現在有來自史隆基金會的贊助 。
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	我們正在測量有多少病毒和細菌 , 我們每天都在內、外面呼吸 , 特別是在飛機上 , 或關閉禮堂上 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	我們透過一些簡單的儀器過濾 ; 我們收集的微生物量量量 , 僅僅一天之內就有十億微生物從紐約市的一棟大樓頂過濾 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	而我們正處於當下的定序過程 。
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	就在數據收集的這一邊 , 就在我們穿過加拉巴哥群島的地方 , 我們發現幾乎每200英里 , 我們在海洋樣本中就可以看到巨大的多樣性 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	有些很合邏輯 , 就不同溫度的梯度而言 。
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	所以這是一張衛星照片 , 根據紅色是溫暖的 , 藍色是冷的 , 我們發現溫水樣本和冷水樣本有極大的差異 , 就豐富的物種而言 。
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另外一點讓我們相當驚訝的是這些光感受體偵測到不同波長的光 , 我們可以根據它們的氨基酸序列來預測 。
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	而這些從地區到地區的巨大變化 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	也許不意外 , 在深海 , 那裡大部分是藍色的 , 感光器通常會看見藍光 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	當周圍有很多葉綠素時 , 他們會看到很多綠光 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但它們的變化還更加不同 , 可能是朝著紅外線和紫外線前進 。
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	為了評估我們的基因修復能力 , 我們組合了所有的資料 , 包括我們目前所在的探險領域 , 這代表了地球上超過一半的基因資料 , 總共大約有兩千九百萬個基因 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試著把這些放到基因家庭中 , 看看這些發現是什麼:我們只是發現已知家庭的新成員 , 還是我們發現了新的家庭 ?
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果發現 , 我們有大約五萬個主要的基因家庭 , 但我們在環境中所採取的每一種新樣本 , 都在這些新家庭中加上線性的時尚 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	所以我們正處於這個星球上最早發現基本基因、元件和生命的階段 。
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們看到所謂的演化樹 , 我們就在右上角和動物一起 。
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	其中大約有2900萬個基因 , 我們的基因組中只有24 , 000個 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果你把所有的動物都聚集在一起 , 我們可能共有不到三萬個 , 也許還會有十多個 , 或幾千個不同的基因家庭 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	我覺得這些基因現在不僅僅是演化的設計元素 ,
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	我們認為以基因為中心的觀點可能回到了理查德•道金斯的想法 , 而不是以基因為中心的觀點 , 這些基因元件的構造是不同的 。
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	合成dna , 合成dna的能力 , 在過去十年或兩年間 , dna定序的步調都改變了 , 且越來越快、非常便宜 。
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	我們首先想到合成基因組學 , 是在1995年我們完成第二組基因組的測序 , 也是來自mycoplasma生殖器 。
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們有很棒的t恤 , 上面寫著: 「 我心臟生殖器 。 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這其實只是一個微生物 。
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但它大約有500個基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	嗜血桿菌有1800個基因 。
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	我們簡單地問一個問題 , 如果一個物種需要800種 , 另一個500種 , 有沒有一組比較小的基因組組成一個最小的操作系統 ?
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	所以 , 我們開始做轉種子突變項目 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	轉換器只是基因密碼中隨機插入的小片段 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	如果他們插入基因的中間 , 就會干擾其功能 。
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以我們做了一張地圖 , 上面有各種基因 , 可以採用跨越器插入 , 我們稱之為 「 無形基因 」 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但事實證明 , 環境對此非常關鍵 , 你只能根據環境中的事物來定義一個必要或非必要的基因 。
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們也嘗試採用更直接的智能方法 , 和13個相關的有機體的基因組做比較 , 我們試著比較 , 看看它們有什麼共同點 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	我們得到了這些重疊的圓形 。 我們發現 , 只有173個基因在所有13個有機體上都很常見 。
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	池塘擴大了一點 , 如果我們忽略了一個細胞寄生蟲 , 它的範圍會更大 。 當我們研究核心基因組時 , 大約有310個左右 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	所以我們認為我們可以擴大或收縮基因組 , 取決於你這裡的觀點 , 到來自500個最少的300到400個基因 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	要證明這些想法的唯一方法 , 就是用那些基因來建構人工染色體 , 我們得要用以錄音為基礎的方式來做這件事 。
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現 , 在大型片斷中合成正確的dna是極其困難的 。
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	hamsmith和clydehutchison , 我這邊的同事 , 開發了一個令人振奮的新方法 , 讓我們能在兩週內合成一個5000個鹼基對的病毒 , 那是100%的準確度 , 以它的序列和它的生物學而言 。
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	那是個相當令人興奮的實驗 , 當我們把合成的dna片段 , 在細菌中注射 , 突然間 , dna開始驅動病毒粒子的生產 , 轉身殺死細菌 。
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這不是第一種合成病毒 , 小兒麻痺病毒在一年前就被製造出來了 , 但它只有十分之一的活躍 , 花了三年的時間 。
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是phix-174的結構的漫畫 。
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	這是一個軟體現在建立了自己的硬體 , 那就是我們對生物學的概念 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	人們立刻跳到關心生物戰 , 我在參議院委員會前有最近的證詞 , 還有美國政府設立的一個特殊委員會審查這個領域 。
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	我認為 , 要讓現實保持在心中是很重要的 , 相較之下 , 人們的想像是怎樣的 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 現今任何已被定序的病毒 , 基因組可以製造出來 。
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	而人們對伊波拉或天花的事物立刻嚇壞了 , 但來自這個有機體的dna並沒有傳染 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以即使有人製造了天花基因組 , dna本身也不會造成感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	真正關心安全部門有的是設計師病毒 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯 , 主要致力於創造生物武器 。
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果那個研究真的被解除了 , 未來應該沒有什麼活動可以製造出設計師病毒 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為單細胞生物在兩年內是有可能的 。
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	而我們這些十年內就有可能存在的真核細胞 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	所以我們現在正在製造數十種不同的構造 , 因為我們可以改變這些人造染色體的膠帶和基因 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵在於 , 如何把所有其他人
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們從這些碎片開始 , 接著我們有一個同源重組系統 , 將這些碎片重新組合成一條染色體 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	這是從一個有機體衍生出來的 , 即deinococcusradiodurans , 它可以承受三百萬次的輻射 , 而且不會被殺死 。
it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	在這個輻射爆發後 , 它的基因組會在12到24小時內重新組合 , 在它的染色體被完全拆開之後 。
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這個有機體在地球上無所不在 , 可能現在就存在於外太空 , 因為我們去過那裡 。
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	這是在大約50萬拉德輻射之後的一個玻璃酒杯 。
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始燃燒和破裂 , 底部的微生物變得越來越快樂 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這裡有一張實際狀況的照片 , 上面顯示出經過一百七十萬雷得輻射後的基因組 。
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	染色體真的被拆開了 。
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	而這是同樣的dna在24小時後自動重新組合 。
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	真的很驚人的是 , 這些生物體可以做到這一點 , 我們可能有成千上萬 , 在這個星球上有能力做到這一點的不同物種 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組被合成之後 , 第一步就是將它們移植到沒有基因組的細胞中 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	所以我們認為合成細胞將會有極大的潛力 , 不僅僅是為了了解生物學的基礎 , 也為了希望環境和社會議題 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	例如 , 從我們定序的第三個有機體 , 甲烷佔據珍納西──它住在沸騰的水溫中 ; 它的能量來源是氫 , 它的所有碳來自於二氧化碳──它從環境中捕捉回來 。
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	所以我們知道許多不同的途徑 , 現在有數千種不同的生物 , 都住在二氧化碳中 , 並且可以捕捉回來 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	所以 , 與其用從石油中取得的碳來製造合成過程 , 我們有機會使用碳 , 並從大氣中捕捉它 , 將它轉換成生物聚合物或其他產品 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有一個生物 , 住在一氧化碳中 , 我們用它來減低水分產生氫氣和氧氣 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	此外 , 還有無數的途徑可以製造出代謝甲烷 。
and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	杜邦在挪威有一項重大的項目 , 用來捕捉和轉換來自瓦斯場的甲烷 , 變成有用的產品 。
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	在短時間內 , 我認為將會有一個新的領域 , 叫做 「 組合基因組學 」 , 因為有這些新的合成能力 , 這些廣大的基因陣列複製品以及同源重組 , 我們認為我們可以設計一個機器人 , 一天可能可以製造出一百萬種不同的染色體 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	因此 , 就像所有生物學一樣 , 你透過篩選 , 不論是篩選氫氣生產 , 或化學生產 , 還是單純的可行性 。
to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	要了解這些基因在接觸中所扮演的角色是很好的 。
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們試著修改光合作用 , 直接從陽光上產生氫氣 。
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	光合作用是由氧氣來調節 , 我們有一種氧氣敏感的氫氣 , 我們認為會完全改變這個過程 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們也在結合纖維酶 , 將複雜糖分解成簡單糖的酵素 , 在同一個細胞中產生乙醇 。
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	藥品生產已經在主要實驗室中使用微生物 。
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	環境中的化合物所產生的化學成份數量比我們最好的化學家所能生產的還要複雜許多 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我認為未來的工程物種可能是食物的來源 , 希望是能源的來源 , 環境的補救措施 , 或許可以取代石化產業 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我用倫理和政策研究來做結尾 。
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	我們在1999年就拖延了實驗的開端 , 直到我們完成了一年半的生物倫理審查 , 我們是否應該嘗試製造一個人造物種 。
every major religion participated in this .	每個主要宗教都參與其中
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	這其實是一項很奇怪的研究 , 因為各宗教領袖用他們的經文作為法律書籍 , 他們找不到任何在禁止製造生命的東西 , 所以一定是沒問題的 。 唯一的顧慮是生物戰事的面向 , 但給了我們這些實驗的前提 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	目前sloan基金會剛剛資助了一項多元機構的研究 , 研究出對社會有哪些風險和利益 , 以及像我自己的科學團隊這些規則 , 在這個領域中 , 我們正試著設立好的例子 。
these are complex issues .	這些都是複雜的議題
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	除了生物恐怖主義的威脅之外 , 它們是很簡單的議題 , 我們能否設計東西來產生乾淨的能源 , 或許改革發展中國家可以做的事 , 並提供各種簡單的過程 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家菲利普•津巴多說快樂和成功根植於一種特徵 , 大部分人都不認同:我們對過去、現在和未來的習慣 。 他建議我們校準時間 , 改善我們生活的第一步 。
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	大腦、商業、快樂、心智、心理、科學、
philip zimbardo prescribes a healthy take on time	菲利浦津巴多開處方健康是準時的 。
i want to share with you some ideas about the secret power of time , in a very short time .	我想和大家分享一些關於時間的秘密力量的想法 , 在很短的時間內 ,
video: all right , start the clock please . 30 seconds studio .	影片:好了 , 請開始時鐘 。 30秒鐘的工作室 。
keep it quiet please . settle down .	保持安靜 。 安靜下來 。
it's about time . end sequence . take one .	時間到了 。 結束序列 。 拿一個 。
10 , nine , eight , seven , six , five , four , three , two . . .	10 , 9 , 8 , 7 , 6 , 5 , 4 , 3 , 2......
philip zimbardo: let's tune into the conversation of the principals in adam's temptation .	菲利浦津巴多:咱們來調整一下亞當的誘惑和校長的對話 。
" come on adam , don't be so wishywashy . take a bite . " " i did . "	「 來吧 , 亞當 , 不要這麼想 , 咬一口吧 。 」 「 我做到了 。 」
" one bite , adam . don't abandon eve . "	「 一口 , 亞當 。 不要放棄夏娃 。 」
" i don't know , guys .	「 我不知道 , 各位 ,
i don't want to get in trouble . "	我不想惹麻煩 。 」
" okay . one bite . what the hell ? "	「 好吧 , 一咬 , 什麼鬼 ? 」
life is temptation . it's all about yielding , resisting , yes , no , now , later , impulsive , reflective , present focus and future focus .	人生是誘惑 。 這一切都和產量有關 , 抗拒 , 是的 , 不 , 現在 , 以後 , 衝動性、反思性、現在的焦點和未來的焦點有關 。
promised virtues fall prey to the passions of the moment .	承諾的美德會讓獵物落入當下的熱情中 。
of teenage girls who pledged sexual abstinence and virginity until marriage thank you george bush the majority , 60 percent , yielded to sexual temptations within one year .	在婚前的十幾歲女生中 , 她們都帶著性慾缺失和貞操 , 直到婚姻結婚 , 謝謝妳布希多數人 , 百分之六十 , 在一年內 , 得到性誘惑 。
and most of them did so without using birth control .	他們大部分都這麼做不用節育 。
so much for promises .	這麼多的承諾 。
now lets tempt fouryearolds , giving them a treat .	現在 , 讓四歲的孩子 , 給他們一個治療 。
they can have one marshmallow now . but if they wait until the experimenter comes back , they can have two .	他們現在可以有一顆棉花糖 。 但如果他們等到實驗員回來 , 他們可以有兩顆 。
of course it pays , if you like marshmallows , to wait .	當然要付錢 , 如果你喜歡棉花糖 , 才能等 。
what happens is twothirds of the kids give in to temptation .	三分之二的孩子給予誘惑
they cannot wait . the others , of course , wait .	他們不能等待 。 其他的 , 當然 , 等等 。
they resist the temptation . they delay the now for later .	他們抗拒誘惑 。 他們延遲到現在 。
walter mischel , my colleague at stanford , went back 14 years later , to try to discover what was different about those kids .	沃爾特.米歇爾 , 我在史丹佛的同事 , 在十四年後 , 試著去發掘那些孩子有什麼不同 。
there were enormous differences between kids who resisted and kids who yielded , in many ways .	在很多方面 , 抗拒的孩子和在很多方面都有很大的差異 。
the kids who resisted scored 250 points higher on the sat .	反抗的孩子在sat上分出了250分 。
that's enormous . that's like a whole set of different iq points .	那是非常巨大的 。 這就像一整組不同的智商點 。
they didn't get in as much trouble . they were better students .	他們沒有遇到很多麻煩 , 他們是更好的學生 。
they were selfconfident and determined . and the key for me today , the key for you , is , they were futurefocused rather than presentfocused .	他們有自信和決心 。 對我來說 , 今天的關鍵是 , 對你來說 , 他們是未來的焦點 , 而不是當下 。
so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about today .	所以 , 時間觀點是什麼 ? 這就是我今天要談的 。
time perspective is the study of how individuals , all of us , divide the flow of your human experience into time zones or time categories .	時間觀點是研究個人、我們所有人 , 如何將你人類經驗的流動分成時間區或時間分類 。
and you do it automatically and nonconsciously .	而且你會自動、無意識地做 。
they vary between cultures , between nations , between individuals , between social classes , between education levels .	它們不同於文化、國家、個人、社會階級、教育水平之間 。
and the problem is that they can become biased , because you learn to overuse some of them and underuse the others .	問題是 , 它們會變得偏見 , 因為你學會了過度使用它們 , 並低估其他的 。
what determines any decision you make ?	是什麼決定了你做的決定 ?
you make a decision on which you're going to base an action .	你做了一個決定 , 你要去做一個動作 。
for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對某些人來說 , 只有在立即的情況下 , 其他人在做什麼 , 以及你感受到的是什麼 。
and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	而那些人 , 當他們以那種形式來做決定時 , 我們會稱他們為 「 現在式 」 , 因為他們的焦點是現在的樣子 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 現在不重要了 。
it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	總是在談 「 我過去經歷過的這種情況是什麼 ? 」
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	所以他們的決定是基於過去的記憶 。
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們將稱這些人為 「 過時的 」 , 因為他們著重的是 「 什麼 」 。
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對其他人來說 , 這不是過去 , 也不是現在 , 只關乎未來 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們的焦點總是關於預期的後果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們將稱它們為 「 未來式 」 。 它們的焦點在於將來會是什麼 。
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	所以 , 時間悖論 , 我想說 , 時間的悖論觀點 , 是影響你所做的每一個決定 , 你完全沒有意識到的 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	換句話說 , 你有一種偏見的時間觀點 。
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	其實有六個 。 有兩種方式可以用 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	有兩種方式可以被當作是未來的兩種方式 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以把焦點放在正面或負面 。
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	你可以是當代主義者 , 也就是你專注於生活的喜悅 , 或是當代主義者──這無所謂 , 你的人生被控制了 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可以是未來的 , 設定的目標 。
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或者 , 你可以是超然的未來:即 , 生命在死亡後才開始 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展出心理靈活性 , 讓時間觀點流暢 , 取決於情況的需求 , 那是你得學會做的事 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	所以 , 很快地 , 最佳的時間檔案是什麼 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	高度積極 。 高度在未來 。
and moderate on presenthedonism .	和現代主義的現代主義 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	總是低於負面和現狀 。
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以 , 最佳的顳葉混合體是從過去的過去式中得到的帶給你的根源 。 你連結你的家庭、身份和自我 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	你從未來得到的 , 是翅膀 , 到達新的目的地 , 新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	你從現在的享樂主義得到的就是能量 , 探索你自己的地方、人、感性 。
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	任何過剩的時光觀點都比正面來得負面 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	未來為了成功犧牲了什麼 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	他們犧牲家庭時間 。 他們犧牲了朋友時間 。
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	他們犧牲樂趣的時光 , 犧牲個人的不屈不撓
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	他們犧牲嗜好 。 然後犧牲睡眠 。 所以這會影響他們的健康 。
and they live for work , achievement and control .	並且為工作、成就和控制
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我相信 , 和一些ted成員產生共鳴 。
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	這對我產生了共鳴 。 我小時候在南布朗克斯貧民窟長大 , 一個西西里亞家庭--所有人都活在過去和現在 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我是以未來的身份來到頂端的人 , 他們做了所有這些犧牲 , 因為老師介入 , 讓我成為未來的方向 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我不要吃那顆棉花糖 , 因為如果你等著你會得到兩顆 , 直到我學會平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我加上了現代主義 , 加上了重視過去式的專注 , 所以 , 在76歲時 , 我比以往更有活力、更有生產力 , 我比以往更快樂 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只是想說 , 我們把這個應用在許多世界的問題上:改變學校孩子的輟學率、結合成癮、增強青少年健康 , 用時間隱喻來治癒vetssd , 用時間隱喻來治療奇蹟的解藥 , 促進永續性和保育 , 減少身體復健 , 讓50%的學校復健率下降 , 改變自殺式恐怖分子的訴求 , 並將家族衝突視為是 「 時尚 」 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	最後我想說:許多人生的謎題 , 都可以透過了解你的時間觀和其他人的時間觀來解決 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	這個想法是如此簡單 , 如此顯而易見 , 但我認為後果真的很深遠 。
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	在一百年後 , 有多少標題會很重要 ? 1000年後 ? 克雷克•克特倫的 「 漫長新聞 」 計畫收集故事 , 不只重要 , 還會有數十年的共鳴 。 在ted2010年 , 他發表了近期的頭條新聞 , 呈現出形塑我們的未來的潛力 。
future , global issues , media , news , science	未來、全球議題、媒體、新聞、科學、
kirk citron: and now , the real news	kirkcitron:而現在 , 真正的新聞
we are drowning in news .	我們淹沒在新聞裡 。
reuters alone puts out three and a half million news stories a year .	光是路透社每年就有350萬則新聞報導 。
that's just one source .	那只是一個來源 。
my question is: how many of those stories are actually going to matter in the long run ?	我的問題是:這些故事長期來看 , 有多少真的會很重要 ?
that's the idea behind the long news .	這就是長遠新聞背後的想法 。
it's a project by the long now foundation , which was founded by tedsters including kevin kelly and stewart brand .	這是一個由長久以來的基金會所創立的專案 , 由tedsters所創立 , 包括凱文凱利和史都華特布蘭德 。
and what we're looking for is news stories that might still matter 50 or 100 or 10 , 000 years from now .	我們要找的新聞可能在50、100或10 , 000年後仍然重要 。
and when you look at the news through that filter , a lot falls by the wayside .	當你透過過濾器看新聞時 , 很多事情都落在一旁 。
to take the top stories from the a . p . this last year , is this going to matter in a decade ?	拿去年a.p.來講最頂尖的故事來講 , 十年內會有什麼影響嗎 ?
is this going to matter in 50 or 100 years ?	這在50或100年後會更加重要嗎 ?
okay , that was kind of cool .	好吧 , 那有點酷 。
but the top story of this past year was the economy , and i'm just betting that , sooner or later , this particular recession is going to be old news .	但 , 過去一年 , 最頂尖的故事是經濟 , 我打賭 , 很快或之後 , 這個特別的衰退將會是老消息 。
so , what kind of stories might make a difference for the future ?	那麼 , 什麼樣的故事可能會為未來帶來改變 ?
well , let's take science .	嗯 , 我們以科學為例 。
someday , little robots will go through our bloodstreams fixing things .	有一天 , 小機器人會經過我們的血液中修復東西 。
that someday is already here if you're a mouse .	若你是老鼠 , 某天就已經在這裡了 。
some recent stories: nanobees zap tumors with real bee venom ; they're sending genes into the brain ; a robot they built that can crawl through the human body .	最近一些故事:奈米生物用真正的蜜蜂毒液將基因送進大腦 ; 一個可以爬過人體的機器人 。
what about resources ? how are we going to feed nine billion people ?	資源呢 ? 我們要如何養活九十億人 ?
we're having trouble feeding six billion today .	現今餵飽60億人的食物 , 我們遇到了麻煩 。
as we heard yesterday , there's over a billion people hungry .	如同我們昨天聽到的 , 有超過十億人挨餓 。
britain will starve without genetically modified crops .	英國將沒有基因改造作物餓死 。
bill gates , fortunately , has bet a billion on [agricultural] research .	很幸運的 , 比爾蓋茲已經賭上十億在[不清楚]研究上 。
what about global politics ?	全球的政治呢 ?
the world's going to be very different when and if china sets the agenda , and they may .	世界將會變得非常不一樣 , 如果中國設立了議程 , 他們也有可能 。
they've overtaken the u . s . as the world's biggest car market , they've overtaken germany as the largest exporter , and they've started doing dna tests on kids to choose their careers .	他們推翻了美國作為世界最大的汽車市場 , 他們推翻了德國成為最大的出口國 。 他們開始在孩子身上做dna檢測 , 來選擇他們的職業 。
we're finding all kinds of ways to push back the limits of what we know .	我們正在尋找各種方法 , 來推回我們所知的極限 。
some recent discoveries: there's an ant colony from argentina that has now spread to every continent but antarctica ; there's a selfdirected robot scientist that's made a discovery soon , science may no longer need us , and life may no longer need us either ; a microbe wakes up after 120 , 000 years .	最近有一些發現:阿根廷有一群螞蟻 , 現在已經散播到每個大陸但南極洲 ; 有一個自導的機器人科學家很快地發現 , 科學可能不再需要我們 , 生命可能不再需要我們 ; 一個微生物在十二萬年後醒來 。
it seems that with or without us , life will go on .	看來 , 有沒有我們 , 生命就會繼續下去 。
but my pick for the top long news story of this past year was this one: water found on the moon .	但我在去年的長篇新聞中 , 選了最頂尖的新聞故事 , 就是這個:月球上的水 。
makes it a lot easier to put a colony up there .	讓蟻群更容易在上面放置 。
and if nasa doesn't do it , china might , or somebody in this room might write a big check .	如果美國太空總署不做 , 中國可能會 , 或是這個房間裡的某個人可能會寫很大的支票 。
my point is this: in the long run , some news stories are more important than others .	我的重點是:長遠來看 , 有些新聞的故事比其他人重要 。
planetary scientist carolyn porco shows images from the cassini voyage to saturn , focusing on its largest moon , titan , and on frozen enceladus , which seems to shoot jets of ice .	行星科學家卡羅琳.帕羅科將影像從卡西尼航行到土星 , 把焦點放在它最大的衛星上 , 土衛六 , 和土衛六上 , 似乎會射出冰面噴射機 。
nasa , design , exploration , science , space , technology , universe , visualizations	nasa , 設計 , 探索 , 科學 , 空間 , 科技 , 宇宙 , 視覺化圖像 。
carolyn porco flies us to saturn	carolynporco飛給我們土星上的土星
in the next 18 minutes , i'm going to take you on a journey .	在接下來的18分鐘裡 , 我要帶各位踏上一段旅程 。
and it's a journey that you and i have been on for many years now , and it began some 50 years ago , when humans first stepped off our planet .	這趟旅程是你和我已經進行了很多年的旅程 , 它從50年前開始 , 人類第一次踏出我們的星球 。
and in those 50 years , not only did we literally , physically set foot on the moon , but we have dispatched robotic spacecraft to all the planets all eight of them and we have landed on asteroids , we have rendezvoused with comets , and , at this point in time , we have a spacecraft on its way to pluto , the body formerly known as a planet .	在這50年裡 , 我們不僅僅是登上月球 , 我們還把機器人飛行器移到所有行星上 , 我們已經降落在小行星上 , 我們已將彗星視為是彗星 , 此時 , 我們有一艘太空船 , 前所知的冥王星 。
and all of these robotic missions are part of a bigger human journey: a voyage to understand something , to get a sense of our cosmic place , to understand something of our origins , and how earth , our planet , and we , living on it , came to be .	所有這些機器人的任務都是更大的人類旅程的一部分:一趟旅程 , 去了解某件事 , 去了解我們的宇宙 , 去了解我們的起源 , 以及地球、我們的星球 , 而我們 , 活在它上面 , 來到了 。
and of all the places in the solar system that we might go to and search for answers to questions like this , there's saturn . and we have been to saturn before we visited saturn in the early 1980s but our investigations of saturn have become far more indepth in detail since the cassini spacecraft , traveling across interplanetary space for seven years , glided into orbit around saturn in the summer of 2004 , and became at that point the farthest robotic outpost that humanity had ever established around the sun .	在太陽系中所有我們可能去的地方 , 尋找答案 , 像這樣的問題 , 有土星 。 我們在1980年代初造訪土星之前 , 曾到過土星 , 但自從卡西尼號太空船之後 , 我們對土星的調查變得更加深刻 , 在星際空間中旅行了七年 , 在2004年夏天時 , 滑入土星軌道 , 成為人類在太陽中所建立的最遙遠的機器人接觸點 。
now , the saturn system is a rich planetary system .	現在 , 土星系統是豐富的行星系統 。
it offers mystery , scientific insight and obviously splendor beyond compare , and the investigation of this system has enormous cosmic reach .	它提供了神秘、科學的洞見 , 以及顯然超越了比較 , 這個系統的調查有著巨大的宇宙到達 。
in fact , just studying the rings alone , we stand to learn a lot about the discs of stars and gas that we call the spiral galaxies .	事實上 , 光是單獨研究光環 , 我們就有很多關於星星和氣體的圓盤 , 我們稱之為螺旋星系 。
and here's a beautiful picture of the andromeda nebula , which is our closest , largest spiral galaxy to the milky way .	這張漂亮的圖片是andromedanebula , 這是我們最接近的 , 最大的螺旋星系到銀河系 。
and then , here's a beautiful composite of the whirlpool galaxy , taken by the hubble space telescope .	再來 , 這是個很漂亮的複合體 , 由哈伯太空望遠鏡所拍攝 。
