so the journey back to saturn is really part of and is also a metaphor for a much larger human voyage to understand the interconnectedness of everything around us , and also how humans fit into that picture .	所以 , 回到土星的旅程其實是其中的一部分 , 也是人類旅程的比喻 , 來了解周遭所有事物的相互連結 , 以及人類如何融入那張圖片 。
and it pains me that i can't tell you all that we have learned with cassini .	這讓我很痛苦 , 我無法告訴各位我們對卡西尼學過的所有知識 。
i can't show you all the beautiful pictures that we've taken in the last two and a half years , because i simply don't have the time .	我無法向你們展示我們過去兩年半所拍攝的美麗照片 , 因為我就是沒有時間 。
so i'm going to concentrate on two of the most exciting stories that have emerged out of this major exploratory expedition that we are conducting around saturn , and have been for the past two and a half years .	所以 , 我將集中在兩個最令人興奮的故事裡從這次重大的探索探險隊展開 , 展開我們在土星周圍進行 , 過去兩年半的歷史 。
saturn is accompanied by a very large and diverse collection of moons .	土星和非常大且多樣化的月球組合在一起 。
they range in size from a few kilometers across to as big across as the u . s .	它們的範圍從幾公里寬到相當大的全美 。
most of the beautiful pictures we've taken of saturn , in fact , show saturn in accompaniment with some of its moons . here's saturn with dione , and then , here's saturn showing the rings edgeon , showing you just how vertically thin they are , with the moon enceladus .	我們所拍攝的土星大部分美麗的圖片 , 事實上 , 與其它的衛星與土星相容 。 這是土星 , 與dione , 然後 , 這裡是土星 , 呈現出環形邊緣 , 讓你看到它們的垂直薄弱度 。 土星是土衛二的 。
now , two of the 47 moons that saturn has are standouts .	現在 , 土星47個月球中有兩個是站著的 。
and those are titan and enceladus . titan is saturn's largest moon , and , until cassini had arrived there , was the largest single expanse of unexplored terrain that we had remaining in our solar system .	這些是土衛六和土衛六 。 土衛六是土星最大的衛星 , 直到卡西尼號抵達那裡 , 是目前尚未被探索的最大單一地形 。 我們還留在太陽系中 。
and it is a body that has long intrigued people who've watched the planets .	它是一個長期以來都對行星有感興趣的人體 。
it has a very large , thick atmosphere , and in fact , its surface environment was believed to be more like the environment we have here on the earth , or at least had in the past , than any other body in the solar system .	它有很大、很厚的大氣層 , 事實上 , 它的表面環境被認為比較像是我們在地球上的環境 , 或至少在過去 , 比起在太陽系中的任何其他身體 。
its atmosphere is largely molecular nitrogen , like you are breathing here in this room , except that its atmosphere is suffused with simple organic materials like methane and propane and ethane .	它的大氣主要是分子氮 , 就像在座各位所呼吸的 , 只不過它的大氣層充斥著簡單的有機物質 , 如甲烷、丙烷、乙烷 。
and these molecules high up in the atmosphere of titan get broken down , and their products join together to make haze particles .	這些分子會在土衛六的大氣層中被打破 , 它們的產品會一起結合製造出霧狀粒子 。
this haze is ubiquitous . it's completely global and enveloping titan .	這種霧狀物是無處不在的 。 它完全是全球性的 , 並且包覆著土衛六 。
and that's why you cannot see down to the surface with our eyes in the visible region of the spectrum .	這就是為什麼你不能用我們的眼睛看表面 , 在可見光的區域 。
but these haze particles , it was surmised , before we got there with cassini , over billions and billions of years , gently drifted down to the surface and coated the surface in a thick organic sludge .	但這些霧狀粒子 , 被嚇到了 , 在我們和卡西尼號到達之前 , 數十億年來 , 溫和地漂到海面 , 以厚厚的有機泥塊覆蓋表面 。
so like the equivalent , the titan equivalent , of tar , or oil , or what we didn't know what .	所以就像土衛六一樣 , 土衛六相當於焦油 , 或石油 , 或我們不知道的 。
but this is what we suspected . and these molecules , especially methane and ethane , can be liquids at the surface temperatures of titan .	但這是我們懷疑的 。 而這些分子 , 尤其是甲烷和乙烷 , 可以在土衛六表面溫度上保持液態 。
and so it turns out that methane is to titan what water is to the earth .	結果發現 , 甲烷是用來霸凌地球上的水 。
it's a condensable in the atmosphere , and so recognizing this circumstance brought to the fore a whole world of bizarre possibilities . you can have methane clouds , ok , and above those clouds , you have this hundreds of kilometers of haze , which prevent any sunlight from getting to the surface .	它在大氣中是可以凝結的 , 所以意識到這種情況 , 導致了整個奇異的可能性 。 你可以有甲烷雲 , 好 , 在那些雲之上 , 你有數百公里的霧狀物 , 這可以防止任何陽光照射到表面 。
the temperature at the surface is some 350 degrees below zero fahrenheit .	表面的溫度是華氏零下350度 。
but despite that cold , you could have rain falling down on the surface of titan .	但儘管如此寒冷 , 你還是可以讓雨落在土衛六表面 。
and doing on titan what rain does on the earth: it carves gullies ; it forms rivers and cataracts ; it can create canyons ; it can pool in large basins and craters .	在土衛六上 , 雨在地球上所做的事:雕刻好幾何 ; 它形成河流和白內障 ; 它可以造峽谷 ; 它可以在大型盆地和隕石坑中水池 。
it can wash the sludge off high mountain peaks and hills , down into the lowlands . so stop and think for a minute .	它可以把污水從高山和山丘上沖下 , 下到低地 。 所以停下來思考一下 。
try to imagine what the surface of titan might look like .	試著想像土衛六的表面會是什麼樣子 。
it's dark . high noon on titan is as dark as deep earth twilight on the earth .	它很黑暗 。 在土衛六上的高中午 , 和地球上那麼深的地球暮光一樣黑 。
it's cold , it's eerie , it's misty , it might be raining , and you might be standing on the shores of lake michigan brimming with paint thinner .	它很冷 , 很糟糕 , 可能會下雨 , 你可能會站在密西根湖岸上 , 用油漆稀薄的油漆來生長 。
that is the view that we had of the surface of titan before we got there with cassini , and i can tell you that what we have found on titan , though it is not the same in detail , is every bit as fascinating as that story is .	這是土衛六在我們到達卡西尼號之前的景象 , 我可以告訴你們 , 我們在土衛六上所發現的 , 雖然它的細節並不相同 , 但故事的確如此引人入勝 。
and for us , it has been like the cassini people it has been like a jules verne adventure come true .	對我們來說 , 這就像卡西尼族一樣 , 過去就像是賈爾凡爾納的冒險成真 。
as i said , it has a thick , extensive atmosphere .	就像我說的 , 它有很厚、很廣的大氣層 。
this is a picture of titan , backlit by the sun , with the rings as a beautiful backdrop .	這是一張土衛六 , 太陽的後照 , 光環是美麗的背景 。
and yet another moon there i don't even know which one it is . it's a very extensive atmosphere .	但在那裏的另一個月球我甚至不知道它是哪一個 。 它是一個非常廣泛的大氣層 。
we have instruments on cassini which can see down to the surface through this atmosphere , and my camera system is one of them .	我們在卡西尼號上有儀器 , 它可以透過這個大氣層看到水面 , 我的相機系統是其中之一 。
and we have taken pictures like this .	我們也拍了這樣的照片 。
and what you see is bright and dark regions , and that's about as far as it got for us .	而你看到的是明亮且黑暗的區域 , 這大約是它給我們帶來的 。
it was so mystifying: we couldn't make out what we were seeing on titan .	實在太神秘了:我們無法在土衛六上看到的東西 。
when you look closer at this region , you start to see things like sinuous channels we didn't know . you see a few round things .	當你靠近一點看這個區域 , 你會開始看到一些東西 , 像是無數的通道我們不知道 。 你看到了一些圓形的東西 。
this , we later found out , is , in fact , a crater , but there are very few craters on the surface of titan , meaning it's a very young surface .	這個 , 我們後來發現 , 事實上是個隕石坑 , 但土衛六表面上只有極少的隕石坑 , 意味著它是個很年輕的表面 。
and there are features that look tectonic .	還有看起來像板塊的特徵 。
they look like they've been pulled apart .	它們看起來已經被拉開了 。
whenever you see anything linear on a planet , it means there's been a fracture , like a fault .	每當你在一個星球上看到任何線性的東西 , 就表示已經有斷裂 , 像是斷層 。
and so it's been tectonically altered .	所以在地圖上已經有了改變 。
but we couldn't make sense of our images , until , six months after we got into orbit , an event occurred that many have regarded as the highlight of cassini's investigation of titan .	但我們無法理解我們的影像 , 直到我們進入軌道的六個月後 , 發生了一場事件 , 許多人認為卡西尼號探測土衛六的高峰期 。
and that was the deployment of the huygens probe , the europeanbuilt huygens probe that cassini had carried for seven years across the solar system . we deployed it to the atmosphere of titan , it took two and a half hours to descend , and it landed on the surface .	那就是惠更斯號探測器的部署 , 歐洲的惠更斯號探測器 , 卡西尼號已經載運了七年的太陽系 。 我們將它部署到土衛六的大氣層 , 花了兩個半小時到後 , 降落在地表上 。
and i just want to emphasize how significant an event this is .	我只想強調這是多麼重要的事件 。
this is a device of human making , and it landed in the outer solar system for the first time in human history .	這是人類製造的裝置 , 它在外太陽系中首次登陸人類歷史上 。
it is so significant that , in my mind , this was an event that should have been celebrated with ticker tape parades in every city across the u . s . and europe , and sadly , that wasn't the case .	這件事很顯著 , 在我看來 , 這個事件應該是被讚頌的 , 在美國和歐洲的每個城市 , 不幸的是 , 並非如此 。
it was significant for another reason . this is an international mission , and this event was celebrated in europe , in germany , and the celebratory presentations were given in english accents , and american accents , and german accents , and french and italian and dutch accents .	這是另一個原因 。 這是個國際使命 , 這個事件在歐洲、德國都被慶祝 , 慶祝在英文口音、美國口音、德語、法語、義大利和荷蘭口音 。
it was a moving demonstration of what the words " united nations " are supposed to mean: a true union of nations joined together in a colossal effort for good .	它是一場動人的展示 , 展示了 「 聯合國 」 應該說的意思:一個真正的聯合國加入 , 為了好而努力 。
and , in this case , it was a massive undertaking to explore a planet , and to come to understand a planetary system that , for all of human history , had been unreachable , and now humans had actually touched it .	在這個案例中 , 要探索一個星球是一項巨大的考驗 , 要了解一個行星系統 , 在人類歷史上 , 它是不可思議的 , 現在人類已經摸到它了 。
so it was i mean , i'm getting goose bumps just talking about it .	所以 , 我是說 , 我只是在談它 。
it was a tremendously emotional event , and it's something that i will personally never forget , and you shouldn't either .	那是個極度情緒化的事件 , 也是我個人永遠不會忘記的事 , 你也不該這樣做 。
but anyway , the probe took measurements of the atmosphere on the way down , and it also took panoramic pictures .	但不管怎樣 , 探測器在向下的路上測量了大氣層的量測 , 同時也拍了全景照片 。
and i can't tell you what it was like to see the first pictures of titan's surface from the probe . and this is what we saw .	我無法告訴各位 , 第一次看到土衛六表面的照片是怎樣的 。 這是我們所看到的 。
and it was a shocker , because it was everything we wanted those other pictures taken from orbit to be .	這真是令人震驚 , 因為那是我們希望那些從軌道上拍攝的其他照片 。
it was an unambiguous pattern , a geological pattern .	那是一種不明確的模式 , 地質的模式 。
it's a dendritic drainage pattern that can be formed only by the flow of liquids .	它是一種獨立的排水模式 , 只能由液體的流動形成 。
and you can follow these channels and you can see how they all converge .	你可以追蹤這些頻道 , 你可以看到它們是如何匯聚的 。
and they converge into this channel here , which drains into this region .	他們匯聚到這個管道中 , 流入這個區域 。
you are looking at a shoreline .	你看到的是一條海岸線 。
was this a shoreline of fluids ? we didn't know .	這是流體的海岸線嗎 ? 我們不知道 。
but this is somewhat of a shoreline .	但這有點像海岸線 。
this picture is taken at 16 kilometers .	這張照片是在16公里拍的 。
this is the picture taken at eight kilometers , ok ? again , the shoreline .	這是在八公里長的海岸線拍的照片 。
okay , now , 16 kilometers , eight kilometers this is roughly an airline altitude .	好 , 現在 , 16公里 , 8公里--這大約是一個航空公司的高度 。
if you were going to take an airplane trip across the u . s . , you would be flying at these altitudes .	如果你要搭飛機橫越美國 , 你會在這些高度飛行 。
so , this is the picture you would have at the window of titanian airlines as you fly across the surface of titan .	這張照片是你在土衛六航空公司的窗口飛過土衛六的表面 。
and then finally , the probe came to rest on the surface , and i'm going to show you , ladies and gentlemen , the first picture ever taken from the surface of a moon in the outer solar system .	最後 , 探測器來到表面休息 , 我要給你們看 , 各位 , 各位先生 , 第一次從外太陽系一個月球表面拍攝的照片 。
and here is the horizon , ok ?	這裡是地平線 , 好嗎 ?
these are probably water ice pebbles , yes ?	這些可能是水冰卵石 , 對嗎 ?
and obviously , it landed in one of these flat , dark regions and it didn't sink out of sight . so it wasn't fluid that we landed in .	很顯然 , 它落在其中一個平坦、黑暗的區域 , 它沒有從視線下沉 。 所以它不是我們降落的液體 。
what the probe came down in was basically the titan equivalent of a mud flat .	探測器的結果基本上是等同於泥巴的土衛六 。
this is an unconsolidated ground that is suffused with liquid methane .	這是一片未解的地 , 上面充滿了液態甲烷 。
and it's probably the case that this material has washed off the highlands of titan through these channels that we saw , and has drained over billions of years to fill in lowlying basins .	可能是這樣 , 透過我們看到的這些管道 , 把土衛六的高地沖洗掉 , 數十億年來 , 用來填補低窪的盆地 。
and that is what the huygens probe landed in .	這就是惠更斯探測器降落的樣子 。
but still , there was no sign in our images , or even in the huygens' images , of any large , open bodies of fluids .	但是 , 我們的影像中仍然沒有任何標誌 , 或甚至惠更斯的影像 , 任何大型、開放的液體 。
where were they ? it got even more puzzling when we found dunes .	他們在哪裡 ? 當我們發現沙丘時 , 情況更加令人困惑 。
ok , so this is our movie of the equatorial region of titan , showing these dunes . these are dunes that are 100 meters tall , separated by a few kilometers , and they go on for miles and miles and miles .	好 , 這是我們在土衛六赤道地區的電影 , 展示這些沙丘 。 這些沙丘有一百公尺高 , 被幾公里長隔開 , 它們持續了數英里和數英里 。
there's hundreds , up to a 1 , 000 or 1 , 200 miles of dunes .	有數百人 , 到達一千或一千兩百英里的沙丘
this is the saharan desert of titan .	這是土衛六的撒哈拉沙漠
it's obviously a place which is very dry , or you wouldn't get dunes .	這顯然是一個非常乾燥的地方 , 或者你不會得到沙丘 。
so again , it got puzzling that there were no bodies of fluid , until finally , we saw lakes in the polar regions .	所以 , 再一次 , 它令人困惑的是沒有液體的存在 , 直到最後 , 我們看到極地地區的湖泊 。
and there is a lake scene in the south polar region of titan .	在土衛六南極地區有一個湖泊場景 。
it's about the size of lake ontario .	大約跟安大略湖一樣大
and then , only a week and a half ago , we flew over the north pole of titan and found , again , we found a feature here the size of the caspian sea .	然後 , 僅僅一個星期半前 , 我們飛過土衛六北極 , 發現 , 同樣地 , 我們找到了一個特徵 , 就是卡斯皮亞海的大小 。
so it seems that the liquids , for some reason we don't understand , or during at least this season , are apparently at the poles of titan .	所以 , 似乎液體 , 由於某些我們不了解的原因 , 或至少在這個季節 , 很明顯地在土衛六的極限 。
and i think you would agree that we have found titan is a remarkable , mystical place . it's exotic , it's alien , but yet strangely earthlike , and having earthlike geological formations and a tremendous geographical diversity , and is a fascinating world whose only rival in the solar system for complexity and richness is the earth itself .	我想你會同意我們發現土衛六是一個很了不起、很神奇的地方 。 它是外星人 , 也是外星人 , 但又像地球一樣奇怪 , 地質的形成和極大的地理多樣性 , 一個令人著迷的世界 , 這個太陽系只適合複雜而豐富的世界 , 就是地球 。
and so now we go onto enceladus . enceladus is a small moon , it's about a tenth the size of titan . and you can see it here next to england , just to show you the size . this is not meant to be a threat .	所以現在我們來到土衛二 。 土衛二是個小衛星 , 它大約是土衛六的十分之一 。 你可以看到它旁邊是英格蘭 , 只是給你看大小 。 這不是威脅 。
and enceladus is very white , it's very bright , and its surface is obviously wrecked with fractures .	而土衛二非常白 , 非常明亮 , 它的表面很明顯是用裂痕來破壞的 。
it is a very geologically active body .	它是一個地質活躍的身體 。
but the mother lode of discoveries on enceladus was found at the south pole and we're looking at the south pole here where we found this system of fractures .	但在土衛二上的發現之母在南極找到了 , 我們看到的是南極點 , 在那裡 , 我們發現了破裂的系統 。
and they're a different color because they're a different composition .	而它們是不同的顏色 , 因為它們是不同的組成 。
they are coated . these fractures are coated with organic materials .	它們是外層 。 這些裂痕被有機物質包覆著 。
moreover , this whole , entire region , the south polar region , has elevated temperatures . it's the hottest place on the planet , on the body .	此外 , 這整個、整個南極區域 , 溫度也升高了 。 這是地球上最熱的地方 , 在身體上 。
that's as bizarre as finding that the antarctic on the earth is hotter than the tropics .	這就像發現地球上的南極比熱帶地區還要熱 。
and then , when we took additional pictures , we discovered that from these fractures are issuing jets of fine , icy particles extending hundreds of miles into space .	然後 , 當我們拍下額外的圖片時 , 我們發現從這些裂痕上噴射出精緻的冰粒 , 延伸到數百英里外的太空 。
and when we colorcode this image , to bring out the faint light levels , we see that these jets feed a plume that , in fact , we see , in other images , goes thousands of miles into the space above enceladus .	當我們把圖像編碼出來 , 讓微弱的光線升高時 , 我們看到這些噴射流會吸收到一個圓頂 , 事實上 , 在其他影像中 , 我們可以看到 , 在土衛二上方幾千英里的太空中 。
my team and i have examined images like this , and like this one , and have thought about the other results from cassini .	我和我的團隊已經檢視過像這樣的影像 , 像這張 , 並思考過卡西尼號的另一項結果 。
and we have arrived at the conclusion that these jets may be erupting from pockets of liquid water under the surface of enceladus .	我們得出的結論是 , 這些噴射流在土衛二表面下可能是液態水的爆發 。
so we have , possibly , liquid water , organic materials and excess heat .	所以 , 我們有的 , 可能是液態水、有機物質 , 以及過熱 。
in other words , we have possibly stumbled upon the holy grail of modern day planetary exploration , or in other words , an environment that is potentially suitable for living organisms .	換句話說 , 我們可能偶然發現了現代地球探索的聖杯 , 或者說 , 一個可能適合生物居住的環境 。
and i don't think i need to tell you that the discovery of life elsewhere in our solar system , whether it be on enceladus or elsewhere , would have enormous cultural and scientific implications .	我不認為我需要告訴各位 , 在太陽系其他地方的生命的發現 , 不論是在土衛二或其他地方 , 都會有巨大的文化和科學涵義 。
because if we could demonstrate that genesis had occurred not once , but twice , independently , in our solar system , then that means , by inference , it has occurred a staggering number of times throughout the universe and its 13 . 7 billion year history .	因為如果我們能證明在我們的太陽系中 , 基因發生的次數不只一次 , 而是兩次 , 在我們的太陽系中獨立 , 那就表示 , 根據推斷 , 它發生了驚人的次數 , 遍及整個宇宙 , 以及它的137億年歷史 。
right now , earth is the only planet still that we know is teeming with life .	目前 , 地球是唯一一個我們知道是生命結合的星球 。
it is precious , it is unique , it is still , so far , the only home we've ever known .	它很珍貴 , 它是獨一無二的 , 到目前為止 , 它仍然是我們所知的唯一一個家 。
and if any of you were alert and coherent during the 1960s and we'd forgive you , if you weren't , ok you would remember this very famous picture taken by the apollo 8 astronauts in 1968 .	如果在座有人在1960年代被警示和連貫 , 我們會原諒你 , 如果你不是 , 好的 , 你們會記得1968年由阿波羅8號太空人拍下的這張著名照片 。
it was the first time that earth was imaged from space , and it had an enormous impact on our sense of place in the universe , and our sense of responsibility for the protection of our own planet .	那是第一次 , 地球從太空中被拍攝出來 , 它對我們在宇宙中的位置產生了巨大的影響 , 以及我們對地球保護的責任感 。
well , we on cassini have taken an equivalent first , a picture that no human eye has ever seen before .	嗯 , 我們在卡西尼號拍過一幅人類從未見過的照片 。
it is a total eclipse of the sun , seen from the other side of saturn .	它是太陽的全日全食 , 從土星的另一端看到 。
and in this impossibly beautiful picture , you see the main rings backlit by the sun , you see the refracted image of the sun and you see this ring created , in fact , by the exhalations of enceladus .	在這張不可能美麗的圖片中 , 你看到的是太陽的主要光環 , 你看到太陽的折射影像 , 你看到這個光環 , 事實上 , 由土衛二的呼吸所產生 。
but as if that weren't brilliant enough , we can spot , in this beautiful image , sight of our own planet , cradled in the arms of saturn's rings .	但 , 就好像那還不夠聰明 , 我們可以看見 , 在這個美麗的影像中 , 看見我們自己的星球 , 擠在土星光環的臂彎中 。
now , there is something deeply moving about seeing ourselves from afar , and capturing the sight of our little , blueocean planet in the skies of other worlds .	現在 , 有件事深深地移動著 , 看我們自己從遠處看 , 並捕捉到我們在其他世界的小型藍cean星球的視野 。
and that , and the perspective of ourselves that we gain from that , may be , in the end , the finest reward that we earn from this journey of discovery that started half a century ago .	而那 , 以及我們從中所獲得的觀點 , 可能是 , 最後 , 我們從這趟半個世紀開始的發現中得到最好的獎賞 。
as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped . this slows the delivery of aid after a disaster and hides the economic potential of unused lands and unknown roads . in this short talk , google's lalitesh katragadda demos map maker , a group mapmaking tool that people around the globe are using to map their world .	到2005年 , 只有15%的世界地圖繪製 。 這場災難之後 , 減緩了救援的遞送 , 隱藏了未經使用的土地和未知的道路的經濟潛力 。 在這場短短的演講中 , 谷歌已故的卡拉加達示意圖 , 一個全球各地人們使用地圖來繪製他們的世界 。
collaboration , design , map , technology	合作、設計、地圖、科技、科技、
lalitesh katragadda: making maps to fight disaster , build economies	已晚期的katragada:製作地圖來對抗災難 , 建立經濟 。
in 2008 , cyclone nargis devastated myanmar .	2008年 , 西隆納基斯破壞了緬甸 。
millions of people were in severe need of help .	數百萬人處於急需協助的狀態 。
the u . n . wanted to rush people and supplies to the area .	聯合國想要趕人和供應到該地區
but there were no maps , no maps of roads , no maps showing hospitals , no way for help to reach the cyclone victims .	但沒有地圖 , 沒有道路的地圖 , 沒有地圖顯示醫院 , 沒有辦法協助到達網路受害者的地圖 。
when we look at a map of los angeles or london , it is hard to believe that as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped to a geocodable level of detail .	當我們看到洛杉磯或倫敦的地圖時 , 很難相信到2005年 , 世界上只有15%的地圖被繪製成可編碼的細節 。
the u . n . ran headfirst into a problem that the majority of the world's populous faces: not having detailed maps .	聯合國提出了一個問題 , 一個世界上大多數人口普及的臉孔問題:沒有詳細的地圖 。
but help was coming .	但 , 協助來了 。
at google , 40 volunteers used a new software to map 120 , 000 kilometers of roads , 3 , 000 hospitals , logistics and relief points .	在google , 40個志願者使用了一個新的軟體 , 繪製120 , 000公里的道路 , 3000間醫院 , 物流和救災點 。
and it took them four days .	而且花了他們四天的時間
the new software they used ? google mapmaker .	他們使用的新軟體 ? googlemapmaker
google mapmaker is a technology that empowers each of us to map what we know locally .	googlemapmaker是一個讓我們每個人都能繪製我們所知的地圖的科技 。
people have used this software to map everything from roads to rivers , from schools to local businesses , and video stores to the corner store .	人們用這套軟體繪製所有東西 , 從道路到河流 , 從學校到當地企業 , 以及視訊商店到角落商店 。
nobel prize nominee hernando de soto recognized that the key to economic liftoff for most developing countries is to tap the vast amounts of uncapitalized land .	諾貝爾獎的諾貝爾得主赫南多德索托發現 , 對大部分發展中國家而言 , 經濟升遷的關鍵在於採用大量無人駕馭的土地 。
for example , a trillion dollars of real estate remains uncapitalized in india alone .	舉例來說 , 光是在印度 , 就有一兆美元的房地產仍然是不可疑的 。
in the last year alone , thousands of users in 170 countries have mapped millions of pieces of information , and created a map of a level of detail never thought viable .	光在去年 , 170個國家就有數以千計的使用者繪製了數以百萬計的資訊 , 並創造了一幅從未想過的細節地圖 。
and this was made possible by the power of passionate users everywhere .	這是由各地熱情使用者的力量所實現的 。
let's look at some of the maps being created by users right now .	我們來看看一些現在使用者所創造的地圖 。
so , as we speak , people are mapping the world in these 170 countries .	所以 , 正如我們說的 , 在這170個國家中 , 人們正在繪製這個世界 。
you can see bridget in africa who just mapped a road in senegal .	你可以看到在非洲的橋樑 , 剛剛在塞內加爾繪製了一條道路 。
and , closer to home , chalua , an n . g . road in bangalore .	而且 , 離家更近 , chalua是班加羅爾的n.g.道路 。
this is the result of computational geometry , gesture recognition , and machine learning .	這是計算幾何學、手勢辨識、機器學習的結果 。
this is a victory of thousands of users , in hundreds of cities , one user , one edit at a time .	這是數以千計的使用者的勝利 , 在數百個城市中 , 一個使用者 , 一次一個編輯 。
this is an invitation to the 70 percent of our unmapped planet .	這是我們70%未被開發的星球的邀請 。
welcome to the new world .	歡迎來到新世界
in 2003 , the palestinian village of budrus mounted a 10monthlong nonviolent protest to stop a barrier being built across their olive groves . did you hear about it ? didn't think so . brazilian filmmaker julia bacha asks why we only pay attention to violence in the israelpalestine conflict and not to the nonviolent leaders who may one day bring peace .	2003年 , 巴勒斯坦村莊布德鲁斯村以十個月長的非暴力抗議阻止一場障礙發生在他們的橄欖爐上 。 你聽說了嗎 ? 不這麼認為 。 巴西的電影製作人朱莉亞•巴察問為什麼我們只關注以色列人的暴力衝突 , 而不是非暴力領袖有一天可能會帶來和平 。
arts , communication , compassion , entertainment , film , peace , violence , war	藝術、溝通、同情、娛樂、電影、和平、暴力、戰爭、戰爭 。
julia bacha: pay attention to nonviolence	juliabacha:請注意非暴力事件
for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	過去8年來 , 我致力於記錄以色列人和巴勒斯坦人的作品 , 他們試圖用和平的方式來結束衝突 。
when i travel with my work across europe and the united states , one question always comes up: where is the palestinian gandhi ?	當我在歐洲和美國旅行時 , 有一個問題總是出現:巴勒斯坦甘地在哪裡 ?
why aren't palestinians using nonviolent resistance ?	為什麼巴勒斯坦人不用非暴力抗爭 ?
the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	當我聽到這個問題時 , 我面臨的挑戰是 , 通常我剛從中東回來 , 在那裡我花時間拍攝了數十位巴勒斯坦人使用非暴力手段來捍衛他們的土地和水資源 , 來自以色列士兵和定居者 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領導人試圖鑄造一個大規模的非暴力運動 , 來終結該地區的佔領 , 並在該地區建立和平 。
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	然而 , 大部分的人可能從來沒有聽過他們 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	這種在地面上發生的事和在國外發生的事之間的分裂 , 也是我們還沒有成功的巴勒斯坦和平抗爭運動的關鍵原因之一 。
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	所以 , 今天我在這裡要談談注意力的力量 , 你的注意力的力量 , 以及非暴力運動的出現和發展 , 在西岸、加薩和其他地方 , 但今天 , 我的個案研究將會是巴勒斯坦 。
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信 , 大多缺少非暴力增長的 , 並不是為了巴勒斯坦人開始採用非暴力手段 , 而是為了我們開始關注那些已有的人 。
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	讓我用布德鲁斯村來說明這一點 。
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前 , 他們面臨絕種 , 因為以色列宣佈它會建造出分離的障礙 , 而部分的障礙會建在村落的上面 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	他們會失去40%的土地 , 然後被包圍 , 所以他們會失去到西岸其他地方的自由 。
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	透過當地領導人的鼓舞 , 他們發起了一場和平抗爭活動 , 來阻止這件事發生 。
let me show you some brief clips , so you have a sense for what that actually looked like on the ground .	讓我給你們看一些短片 , 所以你們可以感受到在地面上實際的樣子 。
palestinian woman: we were told the wall would separate palestine from israel .	巴勒斯坦女人:我們被告知牆會將巴勒斯坦和以色列分開 。
here in budrus , we realized the wall would steal our land .	在布德鲁斯村這裡 , 我們了解到牆會偷走我們的土地 。
israeli man: the fence has , in fact , created a solution to terror .	以色列人:事實上 , 圍籬創造了恐怖的解決方案 。
man: today you're invited to a peaceful march .	男子:今天你被邀請去一場和平的遊行 。
you are joined by dozens of your israeli brothers and sisters .	你是數十位以色列兄弟姐妹加入的 。
israeli activist: nothing scares the army more than nonviolent opposition .	以色列積極分子:軍隊除了非暴力的反對者之外 , 沒有什麼比非暴力的反對者更嚇人 。
woman: we saw the men trying to push the soldiers , but none of them could do that .	女子:我們看到男人試圖推動士兵 , 但沒有一個人能做到 。
but i think the girls could do it .	但我認為女孩們可以做到
fatah party member: we must empty our minds of traditional thinking .	法塔赫派對成員:我們必須要把我們心中的傳統思想給打開 。
hamas party member: we were in complete harmony , and we wanted to spread it to all of palestine .	哈馬斯派對成員:我們處於完全和諧的狀態 , 我們想要把它傳播到所有巴勒斯坦 。
chanting: one united nation .	控告:一個聯合國
fatah , hamas and the popular front !	法塔赫、哈馬斯和大眾的前線 !
news anchor: the clashes over the fence continue .	新聞主播:圍籬的搖擺持續著 。
reporter: israeli border police were sent to disperse the crowd .	記者:以色列邊界警察被派去散佈群眾 。
they were allowed to use any force necessary .	他們被允許使用任何必要的力量 。
man: these are live bullets .	男子:這些是現場的子彈
it's like fallujah . shooting everywhere .	像是wallujah , 到處開槍
israeli activist: i was sure we were all going to die .	以色列激進份子:我確信我們都快死了 。
but there were others around me who weren't even cowering .	但在我身邊有一些人甚至不曾相識 。
israeli soldier: a nonviolent protest is not going to stop the [unclear] .	以色列士兵:非暴力抗議不會阻止[不清楚]
protester: this is a peaceful march .	抗議者:這是和平的遊行 。
there is no need to use violence .	不需要使用暴力 。
chanting: we can do it ! we can do it !	陳腔濫調:我們可以做到 ! 我們可以做到 !
julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	朱莉亞•巴哈:當我第一次聽到布德鲁斯村的故事時 , 我很驚訝 , 國際媒體並沒有報導這一連串非凡的事件 , 那是發生在七年前 , 2003年的事 。
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更令人驚訝的是布德鲁斯村成功的事實
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	居民 , 在十個月的和平抗爭後 , 說服以色列政府 , 將障礙的路線移到他們的土地上 , 移到綠線上 , 也就是國際認可以色列與巴勒斯坦領土之間的界線 。
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	布德鲁斯村的抗爭從此蔓延到西岸的村落 , 到耶路撒冷的巴勒斯坦社區 。
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	但媒體仍然對這些故事保持沉默 。
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種沉默帶著深刻的後果 , 造成非暴力可能會成長的可能性 , 甚至在巴勒斯坦存活下來 。
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力抗爭和非暴力抗爭共有一個很重要的共通點 ; 它們都是戲院形式在尋求觀眾的理由 。
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	如果暴力演員是唯一不斷得到頭版的 , 並吸引國際注意到巴勒斯坦的議題 , 那就很難讓非暴力領導人來為他們的社區做個案 , 讓公民不服從是可行的選項 , 來處理他們的困境 。
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	注意力的力量 , 可能對房間裡的父母來說 , 一點都不意外 。
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	要讓你的孩子發出更大聲的聲音 , 最好的方法就是讓他第一次丟出一個適合的聲音 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	tantrum將成為兒童心理學家所謂的功能性行為 , 因為孩子已經知道 , 他可以從中得到父母的注意力 。
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母可以單單給予孩子的注意力或獎勵或獎勵行為 。
but that's true for adults too .	但對成年人也是如此 。
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區和國家的行為都能受到影響 , 取決於國際社會在哪裡選擇把注意力集中在哪裡 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信 , 在結束中東地區的衝突的核心 , 並為我們帶來和平 , 讓我們能把非暴力行為轉變為一種功能性行為 , 做法是給予現今在地面上更加關注非暴力的領導人 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	在拍攝我的影片的過程中 , 在西岸的村落 , 在加薩和東耶路撒冷 , 我看到即使是一部紀錄片也能影響轉變 。
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	在一個叫做瓦拉耶的村落裡 , 居民非常靠近耶路撒冷 , 社區正面臨著類似的困境 。
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們會被包圍 , 失去很多土地 , 且沒有取得自由 , 要不就是西岸或耶路撒冷 。
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	他們已經使用非暴力行為大約兩年了 , 但自從沒人注意過之後 , 卻漸漸不知所措 。
so we organized a screening .	所以我們組織了一份篩檢
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一個禮拜後 , 他們舉辦了最好、最有紀律的示範 , 去約會 。
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	創辦人說 , 村民看到布德鲁斯村的故事 , 記錄在一部電影中 , 覺得確實有人在追隨他們所做的事 , 人們在乎 。
so they kept on going .	所以他們繼續前進 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	在以色列這邊 , 有一種新的和平運動 , 叫做索里達里特 , 意思是希伯來語中的團結 。
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這項運動的領導者一直在使用布德鲁斯村作為他們主要的招募工具之一 。
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們報告說 , 以色列人以前從未活動過 , 在看電影時 , 了解非暴力的力量 , 並開始加入他們的活動 。
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	華納jeh和索利達里特運動的例子顯示 , 即使是小型的預算獨立製片也能扮演一個角色 , 將非暴力轉變成一種功能性行為 。
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	現在 , 想像一下 , 大型媒體播放者能夠擁有的力量 , 如果他們開始報導非暴力的示威發生在村落中 , 像是比利、尼德林、華拉 , 在耶路撒冷附近的耶路撒冷 , 如謝赫•賈拉 , 和silwan , 非暴力的領導人會在工作上變得更明顯、更有價值、更有效 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信 , 最重要的是要了解 , 如果我們不注意這些努力 , 它們是看不見的 , 彷彿它們從來沒有發生過 。
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但我先看過如果我們這麼做 , 它們會相乘 。
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	如果它們相乘 , 它們的影響力就會在以色列巴勒斯坦的衝突中成長 。
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	而他們的影響力終於可以解開局面 。
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領導人已經證明了非暴力在布德鲁斯村這種地方行得通 。
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	讓我們給予他們注意 , 讓他們可以在任何地方證明它是可行的 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	西蒙.塞克有個簡單但強而有力的領導模式 , 都是從一個金色圓圈開始的 , 還有 「 為什麼 ? 」 他的例子包括蘋果 , 馬丁.路德.金 , 以及萊特兄弟......
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	bullseye , 企業家 , 企業家 , 領導力 , 銷售 , 銷售 , 成功的銷售 。
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	西蒙.史提克:偉大領導人如何激發行動 。
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	你如何解釋當事情不如我們假設時
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或更好的是 , 你要如何解釋當其他人能夠達成似乎可以否定所有假設時 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	例如:為什麼蘋果電腦如此創新 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	年復一年 , 年復一年 , 他們比所有的競爭對手都更有創意 。
and yet , they're just a computer company .	然而 , 他們只是一家電腦公司 。
they're just like everyone else .	他們和其他人一樣 。
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們有相同的才能、相同的機構、相同的顧問、相同的媒體 。
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	那為什麼他們似乎有所不同 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼馬丁•路德•金主導民權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一一個在美國受過事前權侵害的人 , 他肯定不是當時唯一偉大的演說家 。
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	為什麼萊特兄弟能夠想出控制權、有權力的人飛行 , 當肯定有其他隊伍更有資格、更有資金的時候......
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	他們沒有達成權力飛機 , 萊特兄弟打敗他們 。
there's something else at play here .	這裡還有其他東西在玩 。
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三年半前我做了一個發現
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	這個發現深深地改變了我對於我認為世界如何運作的看法 , 它甚至深深地改變了我在其中運作的方式 。
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	結果發現 , 有一種模式
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	結果發現 , 世界上所有偉大且鼓舞人心的領導者和組織 , 不論是蘋果或馬丁•路德•金恩或是萊特兄弟 , 他們都認為 , 採取行動 , 並用相同的方式溝通 。
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	而且完全與其他人相反
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我所做的只是抄寫它 , 大概是世界上最簡單的想法 。
i call it the golden circle .	我稱它為黃金圈 。
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 怎麼做 ? 什麼 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這個小小的點子解釋了為什麼有些組織和一些領導人能夠激發他人不在的地方 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我很快地定義一下術語 。
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	地球上每一個人 , 每一個組織都知道他們做什麼 , 百分之百 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有些人知道他們怎麼做 , 不論你稱它為你不同的價值主張 , 或你的專屬過程或你的usp 。
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但 , 非常少數的人或組織知道他們為什麼要做他們的工作 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	根據 「 為什麼 」 , 我指的不是 「 要賺取利潤 」 。
that's a result . it's always a result .	那是結果 。 結果總是 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	到 「 為什麼 」 , 我的意思是:你的目的是什麼 ?
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的原因是什麼 ? 你的信念是什麼 ?
why does your organization exist ?	為什麼你的組織會存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	你為什麼早上下床 ?
and why should anyone care ?	還有為什麼有人要在乎 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	結果 , 我們的思考方式 , 我們的行動方式 , 我們的溝通方式來自外在 。
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	這是顯而易見的 。 我們從最清晰的東西到最模糊的東西 。
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但受啟發的領導者和受啟發的組織 , 不論他們的大小 , 不論他們的產業都認為 , 採取行動 , 並從內部向外溝通 。
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我用蘋果是因為它們很容易理解 , 大家都懂 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	如果蘋果電腦和其他人一樣 , 來自它們的行銷訊息可能聽起來像這樣: 「 我們製造出很棒的電腦 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	他們設計得很漂亮 , 很簡單 , 可以使用和使用者友善 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想買一個 ? " 梅 "
and that's how most of us communicate .	而這也是我們大多數人溝通的方式 。
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	大部分的行銷就是這樣做 , 大部分的銷售都是這樣做 , 大部分的人都是這樣互相溝通的 。
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們說我們做了什麼 , 我們說我們如何不同 , 或我們如何更好 , 期待某種行為、購買、投票等等 。
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	這是我們的新法律公司:我們和最大的客戶有最好的律師 , 我們總是為我們的客戶做生意 。
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的新車:它有很大的氣體里程序 , 它有皮革座椅 , 買我們的車 。
here's how apple actually communicates .	蘋果電腦實際上是這樣溝通的 。
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	「 我們所做的一切 , 我們相信挑戰現狀 。
we believe in thinking differently .	我們相信用不同的方式思考 。
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰現狀的方式 , 是讓我們的產品優美地設計 , 簡單地使用和使用者友善 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們只是恰巧做出了很棒的電腦 。
want to buy one ? "	想買一台嗎 ? 」
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	完全不一樣吧 ? 你準備好向我買台電腦了 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的就是把資訊的順序倒過來 。
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	它向我們證明的是 , 人們不買你做什麼 ; 人們買你的為什麼 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做 。
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋了為什麼在場的每一個人都很舒適地從蘋果電腦買一台電腦
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但我們也很舒適地買了蘋果電腦的mp3播放器 , 或是蘋果電腦的手機 , 或是來自蘋果電腦的dvr 。
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	但 , 如我之前所說 , 蘋果電腦只是一家電腦公司 。
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	沒有什麼能將他們與任何競爭者區別開來
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭對手都同樣有資格做出所有這些產品 。
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們試過
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , gateway推出了平面螢幕電視
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	他們很明顯有資格製作平面螢幕電視
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	他們多年來一直在做平面螢幕監視器 。
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	迪爾帶著mp3播放器和pda一起出櫃 , 他們製造出很棒的品質產品 , 他們可以做出完美設計良好的產品 , 沒有人買一個 。
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 現在談到它 , 我們甚至無法想像從dell買一台mp3播放器 。
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	為什麼你會向電腦公司買mp3播放器 ?
but we do it every day .	但我們每天都在做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做 。
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標不是和所有需要你的人一起做生意 。
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目標是要和相信你所相信的人做生意 。
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	最棒的部分是:我告訴你們的都不是我的意見 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	都在生物學的主張之中根基 。
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學 , 生物學
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果你看人腦的一個橫切面 , 從上往下看 , 你看到的是人腦實際上被分成三個主要元素 , 與黃金圈完美地相關 。
our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們最新的大腦 , 我們的智人大腦 , 我們的新皮層 , 與 「 什麼 」 等級相對應 。
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	新皮層負責我們所有的理性和分析的想法和語言 。
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間兩個部分組成了我們的邊緣大腦 , 我們的邊緣大腦負責我們所有的感覺 , 像是信任和忠誠 。
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	它也負責所有人類的行為 , 所有的決策 , 它沒有語言的能力 。
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們從外界溝通時 , 是的 , 人們可以理解大量複雜的資訊 , 像是特徵、好處、事實和數字 。
it just doesn't drive behavior .	它只是沒有驅動行為 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們能從內部溝通 , 我們就直接和大腦控制行為的那部分說話 , 然後我們讓人們將它合理化 , 用我們說和做的事 。
this is where gut decisions come from .	這就是腸道決策的來源
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	你知道 , 有時候你可以給一個人所有的事實和數字 , 他們會說: 「 我知道事實和細節是怎麼說的 , 但感覺還是不對 。 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	為什麼我們要用那個動詞 , 它沒有 「 感覺 」 對嗎 ?
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為控制決策的腦部的那部份無法控制語言 。
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	我們能做的最好就是: 「 我不知道 , 感覺不對 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	或者有時你說你在帶著內心 , 或帶領你的靈魂 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	嗯 , 我很討厭把它分給你 , 那些不是其他身體部位在控制你的行為 。
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	這一切都發生在你的邊緣大腦中 , 控制決策而非語言的那部分 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道為什麼要做你所做的事 , 大家會回應為什麼要做你所做的事 , 那你要如何讓人們為你投票 , 或是向你購買一些東西 , 或 , 更重要的是 , 要忠誠 , 並想要成為你所做的一部分 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	同樣的 , 目標不只是賣給需要你擁有的人 ; 目標是賣給那些相信你所相信的人 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標不只是僱用需要工作的人 ; 而是僱用那些相信你所相信的事的人 。
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是說 , 你知道 , 如果你雇用人 , 只因為他們能做一份工作 , 他們會為你的錢工作 , 但如果你雇用那些相信你所相信的人們 , 他們會為你工作 , 他們會帶著血汗和淚水 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	沒有其他地方比萊特兄弟更好的例子 。
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大多數人不知道samuelpierpontlangley
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	回到二十世紀初期 , 追求權力的人飛行就像是當時的網路網路 。
everybody was trying it .	大家都在嘗試 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	而samuelpierpontlangley有我們假設的成功秘訣 。
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	我的意思是 , 即使是現在 , 你問人們: 「 為什麼你的產品或為什麼你的公司會失敗 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	人們總是給你相同的三件事:被忽略、錯誤的人、不良的市場狀況 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	總是相同的三件事 , 所以讓我們來探究一下 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	samuelpierpontlangley得到了五萬美元的戰爭部門來弄清楚這台飛行機器
money was no problem .	錢沒有問題 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他在哈佛舉辦一個座位 , 在史密森尼工作 , 當時他非常了解當時的所有大頭腦 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他雇用了最好的心靈金錢 , 市場狀況很棒 。
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	紐約時報跟著他到處跑 , 每個人都為langley而紮根 。
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	那為什麼我們從來沒有聽過samuelpierpontlangley ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	距離俄亥俄州的華盛頓特區 , 奧維爾和威爾布爾萊特幾百英里外 , 他們都沒有我們所認為的成功秘訣 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢 , 他們用腳踏車商店的成績來支付夢想 ; 沒有一個在萊特兄弟學院的人有大學教育 , 甚至不是奧維爾或威爾布爾 ; 紐約時報跟著他們到處走 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	差別在於 , 奧維爾和威爾布爾被一個原因所驅使 , 一個目的 , 一個信念 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信 , 如果他們能弄清楚這台飛行機器 , 它就會改變世界的軌道 。
samuel pierpont langley was different .	samuelpierpontlangley是不同的 。
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想要變得富有 , 他想要成名 。
he was in pursuit of the result .	他在追求結果 。
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他在追求富人 。
and lo and behold , look what happened .	你看 , 看看發生了什麼事 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	那些相信萊特兄弟的夢想的人和他們一起工作 , 帶著血汗和淚水 。
the others just worked for the paycheck .	其他人只為了支付而努力 。
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	他們會說故事 , 每次萊特兄弟出去時 , 他們就得先拿五組零件 , 因為他們要在供應供應商前墜毀的次數是多少 。
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	最後 , 1903年12月17日萊特兄弟起飛 , 沒有人在那裡體驗它 。
we found out about it a few days later .	我們在幾天後發現
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	進一步證明langley是錯誤的動機:萊特兄弟起飛的那一天 , 他放棄了 。
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可以說: 「 這真是太棒了 , 各位 , 我將改善你們的科技 。 」 但他沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	他不是第一個 , 他沒有變有錢 , 他沒有變有名 , 所以他退出 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做 。
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談到你相信的事物 , 你會吸引那些相信你所相信的事物的人 。
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但為什麼要吸引那些相信你所相信的人們呢 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	某項稱為 「 創新的擴散法則 」 , 如果你不知道法律 , 你絕對知道這個術語 。
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	前2.5%的人口是我們的創新者 。
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	接下來的13.5%的人口是我們早期的採用者 。
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	接下來的34%是你早期的大多數 , 晚期的大部分和產業 。
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	這些人買觸控式語音電話的唯一理由是因為你再也買不到手機了 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	我們都坐在這個規模的各個地方 , 但創新的擴散法則告訴我們 , 如果你想要大眾市場的成功或大眾市場接受一個想法 , 你不能擁有它 , 直到你達到了15%到18%的市場滲透率 , 然後系統就開始了 。
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我喜歡問企業: 「 你對新企業的轉換是什麼 ? 」
and they love to tell you , " oh , it's about 10 percent , " proudly .	他們很樂意告訴你: 「 喔 , 大概是10%吧 。 」 很驕傲的是 ,
well , you can trip over 10 percent of the customers .	嗯 , 你可以讓超過10%的顧客
we all have about 10 percent who just " get it . "	我們都有大約10%的 「 得到 」 。
that's how we describe them , right ?	我們就是這樣描述它們的 , 對吧 ?
that's like that gut feeling , " oh , they just get it . "	那就像是那種腸子的感覺 , 「 喔 , 他們就是懂的 。 」
the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:你要如何找到在你和他們做生意之前 , 而不是那些不懂的人 ?
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	正如傑佛瑞•摩爾稱之為 「 跨越隔閡 」 因為 , 你看 , 早期的大多數不會嘗試直到有人先試過了
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	而這些人 , 創新者和早期的採用者 , 他們很自在地做那些腸道決定 。
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們更自在地做出那些由他們所相信的世界所主導的直覺決定 , 而不僅僅是產品可取得的決定 。
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	這些人排隊 , 排隊了六個小時 , 第一次出櫃時可以買一支iphone , 下週你可能剛走進商店 , 買了架子上的一台 。
these are the people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on flat screen tvs when they first came out , even though the technology was substandard .	這些人在最初出櫃時花了四萬美金在平面螢幕電視上 , 即使科技是次級的 。
and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	順帶一提 , 他們沒有這麼做 , 因為這項技術太棒了 , 他們自己也這麼做了 。
it's because they wanted to be first .	是因為他們想要成為第一個
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it and what you do simply proves what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做 , 以及你做什麼 , 簡單地證明了你相信什麼 。
in fact , people will do the things that prove what they believe .	事實上 , 人們會去做那些證明他們所相信的事情 。
the reason that person bought the iphone in the first six hours , stood in line for six hours , was because of what they believed about the world , and how they wanted everybody to see them: they were first .	買iphone的原因在頭六個小時 , 排隊排隊排了六個小時 , 是因為他們相信這個世界 , 以及他們希望每個人如何看待他們:他們是第一個 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做 。
so let me give you a famous example , a famous failure and a famous success of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我舉一個有名的例子 , 一個有名的失敗以及一個有名的成功 , 關於創新的散播法則 。
first , the famous failure .	首先 , 著名的失敗
it's a commercial example .	這是個商業的例子
as we said before , a second ago , the recipe for success is money and the right people and the right market conditions , right ? you should have success then .	正如我們之前所說 , 一、二年前 , 成功的秘訣是金錢 , 而對的人和對的市場狀況 , 對嗎 ? 你應該要成功 。
from the time tivo came out about eight or nine years ago to this current day , they are the single highestquality product on the market , hands down , there is no dispute .	從八九年前到現在 , 提沃出現在市場上 , 他們是市場上最高品質的產品 , 手下 , 沒有爭議 。
they were extremely wellfunded .	他們非常有資金 。
market conditions were fantastic .	市場狀況很棒 。
i mean , we use tivo as verb .	我的意思是 , 我們用tivo作為動詞
i tivo stuff on my piece of junk time warner dvr all the time .	我隨時在垃圾時間華納的dvr上寫些東西 。
but tivo's a commercial failure .	但是tivo是一個商業失敗的
they've never made money .	他們從來沒有賺過錢 。
and when they went ipo , their stock was at about 30 or 40 dollars and then plummeted , and it's never traded above 10 .	當他們去ipo時 , 他們的股票大約是30到40美金 , 然後下跌 , 從來沒有在10以上交易 。
in fact , i don't think it's even traded above six , except for a couple of little spikes .	事實上 , 我不認為它在六個以上的交易 , 除了幾條小釘子之外 。
because you see , when tivo launched their product they told us all what they had .	因為你看 , 當tivo推出他們的產品他們告訴我們他們擁有的所有東西
they said , " we have a product that pauses live tv , skips commercials , rewinds live tv and memorizes your viewing habits without you even asking . "	他們說: 「 我們有一個產品 , 可以暫停現場電視、跳過廣告、重播現場電視、背誦你的觀看習慣 , 不用你問 。 」
and the cynical majority said , " we don't believe you .	而憤世嫉俗的大多數人說: 「 我們不相信你 。
we don't need it . we don't like it .	我們不需要 , 我們不喜歡
you're scaring us . "	你嚇到我們了 。 」
what if they had said , " if you're the kind of person who likes to have total control over every aspect of your life , boy , do we have a product for you .	如果他們說: 「 如果你是那種喜歡完全控制你生活的各個層面的人 , 男孩 , 我們是否有產品給你 。
it pauses live tv , skips commercials , memorizes your viewing habits , etc . , etc . "	它會暫停現場 , 跳過廣告 , 記住你的觀看習慣 , 等等 。 」
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it , and what you do simply serves as the proof of what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做 , 而你所做的就是證明你所相信的事 。
now let me give you a successful example of the law of diffusion of innovation .	現在讓我給你一個成功的例子 , 說明創新的散播法則 。
in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people showed up on the mall in washington to hear dr . king speak .	在1963年夏天 , 有25萬人出現在華盛頓的商場上 , 去聽金恩博士演講 。
they sent out no invitations , and there was no website to check the date .	他們派出不出任何邀請函 , 當時沒有網站去查看日期 。
how do you do that ?	要怎麼做呢 ?
well , dr . king wasn't the only man in america who was a great orator .	金恩博士並不是美國唯一一個偉大的演說家 。
he wasn't the only man in america who suffered in a precivil rights america .	他不是在美國唯一一個受過過過事前權事務的人 。
in fact , some of his ideas were bad .	事實上 , 他的一些想法很糟糕 。
but he had a gift .	但他有個禮物 。
he didn't go around telling people what needed to change in america .	他沒有到處告訴人們在美國需要什麼改變 。
he went around and told people what he believed .	他四處走動告訴人們他所相信的
" i believe , i believe , i believe , " he told people .	「 我相信 , 我相信 , 我相信 , 」 他告訴人們 ,
and people who believed what he believed took his cause , and they made it their own , and they told people .	而相信他所相信的人們取了他的理由 , 讓他們自己做出來 , 告訴別人 。
and some of those people created structures to get the word out to even more people .	其中一些人創造了結構 , 讓文字傳達給更多人 。
and lo and behold , 250 , 000 people showed up on the right day at the right time to hear him speak .	你看 , 25萬人在對的時間出現在對的日子裡 , 聽到他說話 。
how many of them showed up for him ?	有多少人為他出席 ?
they showed up for themselves .	他們為自己顯現 。
it's what they believed about america that got them to travel in a bus for eight hours to stand in the sun in washington in the middle of august .	這是他們所相信的美國 , 讓他們在公車上行駛八個小時 , 站在華盛頓的中央 。
it's what they believed , and it wasn't about black versus white: 25 percent of the audience was white .	這是他們所相信的 , 不是關於黑人與白人:25%的觀眾是白人 。
dr . king believed that there are two types of laws in this world: those that are made by a higher authority and those that are made by man .	金恩博士相信在這個世界上有兩種法律:那些由更高權威人士所制定的法律 , 以及由男人所制定的法律 。
and not until all the laws that are made by man are consistent with the laws that are made by the higher authority will we live in a just world .	直到所有由男人所制定的法律都和那些由更高權威制定的法律一致 , 我們生活在一個公正的世界 。
it just so happened that the civil rights movement was the perfect thing to help him bring his cause to life .	民權運動非常完美 , 幫助他帶來人生的成就 。
we followed , not for him , but for ourselves .	我們跟隨 , 不是為了他 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and , by the way , he gave the " i have a dream " speech , not the " i have a plan " speech .	順帶一提 , 他給了 「 我有一個夢想 」 演講 , 而不是 「 我有一個計畫 」 的演講 。
listen to politicians now , with their comprehensive 12point plans .	現在聽政治人物 , 用他們全面的十二點計劃 。
they're not inspiring anybody .	他們不鼓舞任何人 。
because there are leaders and there are those who lead .	因為有領導者 , 也有領導者 。
leaders hold a position of power or authority , but those who lead inspire us .	領導者持有權力或權威的立場 , 但那些領導的人激勵我們 。
whether they're individuals or organizations , we follow those who lead , not because we have to , but because we want to .	不論是個人或組織 , 我們都會追隨那些領導的人 , 不是因為我們必須 , 而是因為我們想要 。
we follow those who lead , not for them , but for ourselves .	我們跟隨那些領導的人 , 不是為了他們 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and it's those who start with " why " that have the ability to inspire those around them or find others who inspire them .	正是那些從 「 為什麼 」 開始的人有能力去啟發他們周圍的人 , 或去找激勵他們的人 。
how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你怎麼記得你把車子停在哪裡 ? 你怎麼知道如果你往正確的方向前進 ? 神經科學家尼爾博士研究了繪製我們周圍空間的神經機制 , 以及它們如何連結到記憶和想像 。
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索、神經科學、科學、
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	neil會燒掉:你的大腦如何告訴你你在哪裡 。
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們停在大型停車場時 , 我們如何記得我們停車的地方 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	荷馬所面臨的問題是
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	然後我們會試著去了解他大腦裡發生了什麼事 。
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	我們先從海馬體開始 , 以黃色表示 , 這是記憶的器官 。
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果你在那兒有損傷 , 比如阿茲海默症 , 你不記得事情包括你停車的地方 。
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	它以拉丁文的 「 海底 」 命名 , 和它相似 。
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	和大腦的其他部分一樣 , 它是由神經元構成的 。
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	所以人腦有大約一千億個神經元
and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	而神經元會彼此溝通 , 藉由透過互相連結的小脈衝或尖刺傳送電流 。
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	海馬體是由兩片細胞所組成 , 非常密集的相互連結 。
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家開始了解空間記憶如何運作 , 透過記錄老鼠在覓食或探索環境中尋找食物的個別神經元 。
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	所以 , 我們要想像我們是從這隻老鼠的海馬體內單一個神經元錄下來的 。
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	當它發出一個電的尖刺時 , 會有一個紅點和一個點 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	所以我們看到 , 這個神經元知道老鼠何時進入到環境中的某個特定位置 。
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	它藉由發送一個小小的電流刺激大腦的訊號
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	我們可以把神經元的發射速率當作動物的位置 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們從許多不同的神經元中記錄下來 , 我們會發現當動物在環境中不同部位時 , 不同的神經元會發出訊號 , 就像這個正方形的盒子 。
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	所以他們組成了大腦的地圖 , 持續地告訴大腦: 「 我現在在我的環境中在哪裡 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	位置細胞也被記錄在人類身上 。
so epilepsy patients sometimes need the electrical activity in their brain monitoring .	所以癲癇患者有時需要腦部監測的電活動 。
and some of these patients played a video game where they drive around a small town .	其中有些病人玩電玩遊戲 , 他們開著小鎮到處開車 。
and place cells in their hippocampi would fire , become active , start sending electrical impulses whenever they drove through a particular location in that town .	海馬迴的位置細胞會被激發 , 活躍起來 , 開始發送電脈衝 , 每當它們開車經過那個小鎮的特定位置時 , 都會發出電脈衝 。
so how does a place cell know where the rat or person is within its environment ?	所以 , 一個位置細胞如何知道老鼠或老鼠在其環境中的位置 ?
well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	這兩個細胞告訴我們環境的界限是特別重要的 。
so the one on the top likes to fire sort of midway between the walls of the box that their rat's in .	所以 , 上面的那個比較喜歡在老鼠所在的盒子中間的隔膜中間發射 。
and when you expand the box , the firing location expands .	而當你把盒子擴大 , 發射地點就會擴大 。
the one below likes to fire whenever there's a wall close by to the south .	下面的那一面就喜歡火 , 當南邊有一面牆靠近時 。
and if you put another wall inside the box , then the cell fires in both place wherever there's a wall to the south as the animal explores around in its box .	如果你把另一面牆放進盒子裡 , 那麼細胞兩者都會在盒子裡 , 到達南邊 , 當動物在盒子裡探索 。
so this predicts that sensing the distances and directions of boundaries around you extended buildings and so on is particularly important for the hippocampus .	所以這預測了感知你周圍的界限和方向 , 延伸出去的建築物等等 , 對海馬體尤其重要 。
and indeed , on the inputs to the hippocampus , cells are found which project into the hippocampus , which do respond exactly to detecting boundaries or edges at particular distances and directions from the rat or mouse as it's exploring around .	的確 , 在海馬體的輸入上 , 細胞在海馬體中找到了哪些項目 , 它的確會在特定的距離和邊緣 , 在它四處探索時 , 確切地偵測到界線或邊緣 。
so the cell on the left , you can see , it fires whenever the animal gets near to a wall or a boundary to the east , whether it's the edge or the wall of a square box or the circular wall of the circular box or even the drop at the edge of a table , which the animals are running around .	所以 , 左邊的細胞 , 你可以看到 , 只要動物接近一面牆 , 或是向東邊界線 , 不論是方形的邊緣 , 或方形的牆壁 , 或圓形的外牆 , 或甚至是桌子的邊緣 , 哪些動物會跑來跑去 。
and the cell on the right there fires whenever there's a boundary to the south , whether it's the drop at the edge of the table or a wall or even the gap between two tables that are pulled apart .	右邊的細胞會發出火花 , 只要有一條界線到南邊 , 不論是桌子邊緣、牆壁 , 或甚至兩張桌子間的鴻溝都會被拉開 。
so that's one way in which we think place cells determine where the animal is as it's exploring around .	這就是我們認為位置細胞在探索時 , 會決定動物在哪裡 。
we can also test where we think objects are , like this goal flag , in simple environments or indeed , where your car would be .	我們還可以測試我們認為物體的位置 , 像是這面目標旗幟 , 在簡單的環境或確實地 , 你的車子會在哪裡 。
so we can have people explore an environment and see the location they have to remember .	所以我們可以讓人們探索一個環境 , 看到他們必須記住的位置 。
and then , if we put them back in the environment , generally they're quite good at putting a marker down where they thought that flag or their car was .	然後 , 如果我們把它們放回環境中 , 一般來說 , 它們非常擅長放下他們認為旗幟或車子的位置 。
but on some trials , we could change the shape and size of the environment like we did with the place cell .	但在某些試驗中 , 我們可以改變環境的形狀和大小 , 就像我們用定位細胞做的一樣 。
in that case , we can see how where they think the flag had been changes as a function of how you change the shape and size of the environment .	在那個情況下 , 我們可以看到他們認為旗幟的位置是如何改變你如何改變環境的形狀和大小 。
and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	舉例來說 , 如果你看到旗幟位在小方形的環境中 , 然後如果你問人們在哪裡 , 但你讓環境變大了 , 他們認為旗幟的長度和位置細胞激發的情況完全相同 。
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	這就好像你記起旗幟的位置 , 在那個位置儲存你所有的位置細胞的模式 , 然後你就可以通過移動來回到那個位置 , 這樣你最好符合你所在位置細胞發射的模式 。
that guides you back to the location that you want to remember .	那會引導你回到你想要記住的位置 。
but we also know where we are through movement .	但我們也知道我們透過移動來到哪裡 。
so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以 , 如果我們把一些外界的路徑放到停車場上 , 我們就知道了 , 因為我們自己的運動 , 我們就能整合這條路徑 , 大約是前進的方向 。
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	位置細胞也會得到這種路徑整合 , 由一種叫做 「 網格細胞 」 的細胞所組成 。
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	現在 , 網格細胞又被發現了 , 在海馬體的輸入上 , 它們有點像位置細胞 。
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	但當老鼠四處探索時 , 每個個體細胞會在一連串不同的位置上發射 , 這些位置在一個驚人的三角形網格中 。
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	如果你用不同顏色的網格細胞來紀錄 , 每一個細胞都有一個類似網格的激發模式 , 橫跨整個環境 , 每個細胞的網格狀發射模式 , 都和其他細胞比較 。
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	紅色的會在這個格子上開火 , 綠色的這個 , 藍色的在這個格子上 。
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	所以 , 這就好像老鼠可以放置一個虛擬的發射地點在它的環境中 , 有點像是地圖上找到的緯度和長路線 , 但用的是三角形 。
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	當它四處移動時 , 電流活動可以從其中一個細胞傳遞到下一個細胞 , 來持續追蹤它的位置 , 讓它可以用自己的動作 , 知道它在它的環境中的位置 。
do people have grid cells ?	人們有網格細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	因為所有的網格激發模式都有相同的對稱性 , 相同的格子方向 , 在這裡用橘色顯示 , 表示網格的所有網格細胞在大腦特定部位的活動 , 應該會根據我們是否沿著這六個方向跑 , 或沿著兩者之間的六個方向跑 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	所以我們可以把人放進核磁共振造影掃描儀 , 讓他們做一個小小的電玩遊戲 , 就像我剛剛給你們看的一樣 , 並尋找這個訊號 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	的確 , 你在人類的大腦中也看到它 , 這跟你在老鼠身上看到網格細胞的同一部份 。
so back to homer .	回到荷馬 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他可能還記得他的車子位於距離和方向的位置來延伸建築物和邊界在他停車的地方
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	那會是由有限偵測細胞的發射而來的 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他也記得他從汽車公園裡走出來的路 , 這條路會以網格細胞的激發方式呈現 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	現在這兩種細胞都可以讓位置細胞發射
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	他可以藉由移動來回到他停車位的位置 , 來找出目前他腦中位置細胞的發射模式 , 與他停車的位置模式相符 。
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	這引導他回到視覺暗示的位置 , 像是他的車子是否真的存在 。
maybe it's been towed .	可能已經被鎮壓了 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道它在哪裡 , 所以他知道要去找它 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	所以 , 除了空間記憶之外 , 如果我們在整個大腦中尋找這個網格狀的激發模式 , 我們會在一系列的地點看到它 , 當我們在做各種自傳記憶的任務時 , 總是很活躍 , 就像你上次去參加婚禮一樣 。
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以 , 可能是代表我們周圍空間的神經機制也被用來產生視覺影像 , 這樣我們才能重現場 , 至少 , 在我們想要想像的時候發生在我們身上的事件 。
so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	所以 , 如果發生這種事 , 你的記憶可以從密集的相互連結開始 , 然後重新啟動邊界細胞 , 創造出你觀點周圍的空間結構 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	而網格細胞可以透過這個空間移動這個觀點 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另一種細胞 , 頭部方向細胞 , 是我還沒提到的 , 它們像指南針一樣 , 會根據你面對的方向 , 像指南針一樣開火 。
they could define the viewing direction from which you want to generate an image for your visual imagery , so you can imagine what happened when you were at this wedding , for example .	他們可以定義出你想要為你的視覺影像產生的看法 , 所以你可以想像當你在婚禮時發生了什麼事 , 比如說 。
so this is just one example of a new era really in cognitive neuroscience where we're beginning to understand psychological processes like how you remember or imagine or even think in terms of the actions of the billions of individual neurons that make up our brains .	這只是在認知神經科學中新時代的一個例子 , 我們開始了解心理的過程 , 像是你如何記住、想像 , 甚至是以數十億個神經元的行為來思考 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝 。
imagine a global security driven by collaboration among agencies , government , the private sector and the public . that's not just the distant hope of opensource fans , it's the vision of james stavridis , the supreme commander of nato , who shares vivid moments from recent military history to explain why security of the future should be built with bridges rather than walls .	想像一下 , 由機構、政府、私營部門和大眾所驅動的全球安全 。 這不僅僅是開放式電扇的遙遠希望 , 更是北約熱內盧的最高指揮官 , 他們共同分享鮮明的時刻 , 來解釋為什麼要用橋樑來建造 , 而不是牆壁 。
collaboration , global issues , opensource , peace , politics , social media , violence , war	合作、全球議題、開放資源、和平、政治、社交媒體、暴力、戰爭、戰爭 。
james stavridis: how nato's supreme commander thinks about global security	詹姆斯•史特拉迪斯:北約最高指揮官是怎麼看待全球安全的 。
i'm gonna talk a little bit about opensource security , because we've got to get better at security in this 21st century .	我要談一下開放原始碼的安全 , 因為我們必須在21世紀的安全上更好 。
let me start by saying , let's look back to the 20th century , and kind of get a sense of how that style of security worked for us .	讓我先說 , 讓我們回顧二十世紀 , 了解安全的風格對我們是如何運作的 。
this is verdun , a battlefield in france just north of the nato headquarters in belgium .	這是verdun , 一個在法國的戰場 , 就在比利時北方的北方 。
at verdun , in 1916 , over a 300day period , 700 , 000 people were killed , so about 2 , 000 a day .	在verdun , 1916年 , 超過300天的時間 , 七十萬人被殺害 , 所以一天大約有兩千人被殺害 。
if you roll it forward 20thcentury security into the second world war , you see the battle of stalingrad , 300 days , 2 million people killed .	如果你把它推向二十世紀的安全 , 進入第二次世界大戰 , 你就會看到史達林級的戰役 , 300天 , 殺害了200萬人 。
we go into the cold war , and we continue to try and build walls .	我們進入冷戰 , 繼續嘗試建造牆壁 。
we go from the trench warfare of the first world war to the maginot line of the second world war , and then we go into the cold war , the iron curtain , the berlin wall .	我們從第一次世界大戰的戰場 , 到第二次世界大戰的馬吉諾斯戰線 , 然後進入冷戰、鐵幕、柏林圍牆 。
my thesis for us today is , instead of building walls to create security , we need to build bridges .	我今天的論點是 , 與其建造牆壁來創造安全性 , 我們需要建造橋樑 。
this is a famous bridge in europe .	這是歐洲著名的橋樑 。
it's the bridge over the drina river , the subject of a novel by ivo andrić , and it talks about how , in that very troubled part of europe and the balkans , over time there's been enormous building of walls .	它是這座流過飲料河的橋樑 , 它是伊佛•安德里奇小說的主題 , 它談到如何 , 在歐洲和巴爾幹地區非常困擾的地區 , 隨著時間過去 , 已經有了巨大的圍牆 。
more recently , in the last decade , we begin to see these communities start , hesitatingly , to come together .	更近期 , 在過去的十年 , 我們開始看到這些社區開始 , 猶豫著 , 團結起來 。
i would argue , again , opensource security is about connecting the international , the interagency , the privatepublic , and lashing it together with strategic communication , largely in social networks .	我認為 , 同樣地 , 開放式安全就是把國際、介入性、私人公共的連結 , 和策略性溝通連結在一起 , 主要是在社交網路上 。
so let me talk a little bit about why we need to do that , because our global commons is under attack in a variety of ways , and none of the sources of threat to the global commons will be solved by building walls .	所以 , 讓我稍微談談為什麼我們需要這麼做 , 因為我們的全球公有物在各方面受到攻擊 , 沒有一個威脅到全球公有物的來源 , 會透過築牆來解決 。
now , i'm a sailor , obviously .	現在 , 我是個水手 , 顯然
this is a ship , a liner , clipping through the indian ocean .	這是一艘船 , 線條 , 翻遍印度洋 。
what's wrong with this picture ?	這張照片有什麼問題 ?
it's got concertina wire along the sides of it .	它沿著它的側邊有協奏曲線 。
that's to prevent pirates from attacking it .	也就是防止海盜攻擊它 。
piracy is a very active threat today around the world . this is in the indian ocean .	海盜是現今世界各地都很積極的威脅 。 這是在印度洋 。
piracy is also very active in the strait of malacca .	盜版在馬拉卡河水峽也很活躍 。
it's active in the gulf of guinea .	活躍於幾內亞灣
we see it in the caribbean .	我們在加勒比海看到的
it's a $10billionayear discontinuity in the global transport system .	在全球交通系統中 , 持續了10億美元 。
last year , at this time , there were 20 vessels , 500 mariners held hostage .	去年 , 在這個時候 , 有20艘船 , 500個船員舉辦人質 。
this is an attack on the global commons .	這是對全球公有物的攻擊 。
we need to think about how to address it .	我們需要考慮如何處理
let's shift to a different kind of sea , the cyber sea .	讓我們轉移到另一種海、網路海、
here are photographs of two young men .	這裡有兩位年輕男子的照片 。
at the moment , they're incarcerated .	目前 , 他們被監禁了 。
they conducted a credit card fraud that netted them over 10 billion dollars .	他們進行了一項信用卡詐欺 , 淨資超過100億美金 。
this is part of cybercrime which is a $2trillionayear discontinuity in the global economy .	這是網路犯罪的一部分 , 它是全球經濟的2兆年不連續性 。
two trillion a year .	一年兩兆
that's just under the gdp of great britain .	那只是在大英國的國內生產總值之下
so this cyber sea , which we know endlessly is the fundamental piece of radical openness , is very much under threat as well .	所以 , 這個我們無止境地知道的網路海 , 是激進式開放的基本元素 , 也受到威脅 。
another thing i worry about in the global commons is the threat posed by trafficking , by the movement of narcotics , opium , here coming out of afghanistan through europe over to the united states .	在全球公有物中 , 我擔心的另一件事是人口販賣所造成的威脅 , 鴉片類藥物的運動 , 來自阿富汗 , 透過歐洲到美國 。
we worry about cocaine coming from the andean ridge north .	我們擔心從andeanridge北部來的可卡因 。
we worry about the movement of illegal weapons and trafficking . above all , perhaps , we worry about human trafficking , and the awful cost of it .	我們擔心非法武器和人口販賣的運動 。 最重要的 , 也許 , 我們擔心人口販賣 , 以及它的可怕成本 。
trafficking moves largely at sea but in other parts of the global commons .	人口販賣主要在海上移動 , 但在全球公有物的其他地方 。
this is a photograph , and i wish i could tell you that this is a very hightech piece of us navy gear that we're using to stop the trafficking .	這是一張照片 , 我希望我能告訴你們 , 這是美國海軍陸戰隊的高科技片段 , 我們用它來阻止人口販賣 。
the bad news is , this is a semisubmersible run by drug cartels .	壞消息是 , 這是毒品販的半潛水服 。
it was built in the jungles of south america .	建於南美叢林中
we caught it with that lowtech raft — — and it was carrying six tons of cocaine .	我們用那低科技的木筏抓到它 , 它帶著六噸的可卡因 。
crew of four . sophisticated communications sweep .	四個船員 。 精密的溝通掃過 。
this kind of trafficking , in narcotics , in humans , in weapons , god forbid , in weapons of mass destruction , is part of the threat to the global commons .	這種販賣 , 在毒品、人體、武器中 , 上帝禁止 , 在大規模毀滅性武器中 , 是全球公有物威脅的一部分 。
and let's pull it together in afghanistan today .	讓我們今天在阿富汗一起拉近 。
this is a field of poppies in afghanistan .	這是阿富汗的一片洋芋片田
eighty to 90 percent of the world's poppy , opium and heroin , comes out of afghanistan .	世界上百分之八十到九十的嬉皮、鴉片和海洛因 , 來自阿富汗 。
we also see there , of course , terrorism .	我們也在那裡看到 , 當然 , 恐怖主義
this is where al qaeda is staged from .	這是基地組織的階段 。
we also see a very strong insurgency embedded there .	我們也看到有一股強烈的暴動 , 嵌在那裏 。
so this terrorism concern is also part of the global commons , and what we must address .	所以 , 這種恐怖主義的擔憂也是全球公有物的一部分 , 我們必須要處理的 。
so here we are , 21st century .	所以 , 現在 , 21世紀 ,
we know our 20thcentury tools are not going to work .	我們知道二十世紀的工具是行不通的 。
what should we do ?	我們該怎麼做 ?
i would argue that we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我認為 , 我們不會只靠槍支的桶子來提供安全保障 。
we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我們不會只靠槍支的桶子來提供安全保障 。
we will need the application of military force .	我們需要軍事力量的應用 。
when we do it , we must do it well , and competently .	當我們這樣做時 , 我們一定做得很好 , 而且有能力 。
but my thesis is , opensource security is about international , interagency , privatepublic connection pulled together by this idea of strategic communication on the internet .	但我的論點是 , 開放式安全是關於國際、跨部門、私人的聯繫 , 被這個網路上策略性溝通的想法所拉扯在一起 。
let me give you a couple of examples of how this works in a positive way .	讓我舉幾個例子來說明這是如何用正面的方式
this is afghanistan . these are afghan soldiers .	這是阿富汗 。 這些是阿富汗士兵 。
they are all holding books .	他們都拿著書
you should say , " that's odd . i thought i read that this demographic , young men and women in their 20s and 30s , is largely illiterate in afghanistan . "	你應該說: 「 這很奇怪 。 我以為我讀到這個人口統計數據 , 二十歲和三十多歲的年輕男女 , 在阿富汗大都不識字 。 」
you would be correct .	你是正確的 。
eightyfive percent cannot read when they enter the security forces of afghanistan .	85%進入阿富汗的安全部隊是無法讀取的 。
why ? because the taliban withheld education during the period of time in which these men and women would have learned to read .	為什麼 ? 因為塔利班在這個時期 , 在這些男人和女人都會學會閱讀的時候 , 會受到教育 。
so the question is , so , why are they all standing there holding books ?	所以問題是 , 為什麼他們都站在那裡拿著書呢 ?
the answer is , we are teaching them to read in literacy courses by nato in partnership with private sector entities , in partnership with development agencies .	答案是 , 我們正在教導他們閱讀 , 在北約和私營機構合作的課程中 , 和發展機構合作 。
we've taught well over 200 , 000 afghan security forces to read and write at a basic level .	我們已經教了超過二十萬名阿富汗安全部隊以基本的水準閱讀和寫作 。
when you can read and write in afghanistan , you will typically put a pen in your pocket .	當你可以讀和寫在阿富汗時 , 你通常會把一支筆放在口袋裡 。
at the ceremonies , when these young men and women graduate , they take that pen with great pride , and put it in their pocket .	在典禮上 , 當這些年輕男女畢業時 , 他們帶著那筆很棒的驕傲 , 把它放在口袋裡 。
this is bringing together international — there are 50 nations involved in this mission — interagency — these development agencies — and privatepublic , to take on this kind of security .	這使得國際上有50個國家參與這項使命 , 跨部門這些發展機構 , 私人公開 , 採取這類的安全措施 。
now , we are also teaching them combat skills , of course , but i would argue , opensource security means connecting in ways that create longer lasting security effect .	當然 , 我們也在教他們戰鬥技巧 , 但我認為 , 開放式安全意味著連結 , 創造更長久的安全性效應 。
this is a us navy warship .	這是美國海軍戰艦 。
it's called the comfort .	所謂的舒適感
there's a sister ship called the mercy .	有一艘叫做慈悲的姐妹船 ,
they are hospital ships .	他們是醫院的船隻 。
this one , the comfort , operates throughout the caribbean and the coast of south america conducting patient treatments .	這一個 , 舒適 , 在整個加勒比海和南美洲海岸進行病人治療 。
on a typical cruise , they'll do 400 , 000 patient treatments .	一般來說 , 他們會做40萬個病患的治療 。
it is crewed not strictly by military but by a combination of humanitarian organizations: operation hope , project smile .	它不是嚴格的軍隊 , 而是人道組織的結合: 「 希望 」 , 專案微笑 。
other organizations send volunteers .	其他組織發送志願者
interagency physicians come out .	跨部門的醫師出來 ,
they're all part of this .	它們都是這個的一部分 。
